# Pyreon — Signal-Based UI Framework

## Overview

Full-stack UI framework with fine-grained reactivity (signals). SSR, SSG, islands, SPA.
All packages under `@pyreon/*` scope.

**Open work**: This file (`CLAUDE.md`) is the single source of truth — feature status, shipped patterns, and open gaps are tracked inline next to the code they describe. The prior `.claude/plans/open-work-2026-q3.md` index was retired after it accumulated multiple stale "ready to execute" entries for already-shipped work (rocketstyle collapse tail, T2.2 doc-examples typecheck, iOS counter CI smoke — each documented as open while their CI / source artifacts proved otherwise). Capturing status next to the code makes drift visible at the point of edit. For prioritization across multiple open items, ask the user — the engineering bar is "do it properly, not quickly," not "burn down a backlog."

## Benchmark Results (Chromium via Playwright)

**Pyreon (idiomatic JSX — what users actually write) is the fastest FRAMEWORK on this synthetic row-list benchmark**, after the 2026-06 *objectivity pass* (see Methodology). On the proven pooled run below it wins **7 of 9 framework verdicts outright**, ties Solid on `select`, and Solid edges it on `remove` (7.20 vs 7.30ms) — every margin is honest (Pyreon competes on equal footing with the others; there is no manufactured "compiled" tier — see "One Pyreon entry" below). The robust, defensible signals: Pyreon sits in a **tight cluster with Vue and Solid** on small ops + create-1k (it leads that cluster by a few hundred µs); it holds a **genuine 2.4–3.0× edge over React/Svelte/Preact at bulk-create (10k) scale**; a large lead on React's keyed `swap` (7.1ms — ~10×) and Vue/Svelte's `append` (3.2–4.1×); and the `select`/`partial` ops where signal frameworks update O(changed) while VDOM re-runs render to diff O(total). Its only measurable cost vs optimal **Vanilla** is bulk-create (~7% at 1k, ~6% at 10k — per-row signal allocation + cleanup closure + keyed-For map); small mutations are tied-or-faster vs Vanilla within noise. On **retained memory** Pyreon is mid-pack (3.14MB — only Vue heavier), the one dimension it does NOT lead.

**One Pyreon entry — no manufactured tiers.** Earlier revisions of this benchmark shipped TWO Pyreon columns ("Pyreon" raw `h()`/JSX + "Pyreon (compiled)" hand-written `_tpl()`) and let only the hand-tuned one compete in rankings. That was a measurement artifact two ways: (a) the Pyreon compiler ALREADY lowers idiomatic JSX to the same `_tpl()` cloneNode + fine-grained-binding output a hand-written `_tpl()` impl produces, so they were never really two tiers; (b) a real **compiler inefficiency** masked the equivalence — the compiler emitted a wasteful per-row `_bind()` renderEffect for static item-property reads like `{String(row.id)}` in a `<For>` callback (it misregistered the callback's `row` param as reactive props), so idiomatic JSX paid 1k–10k unnecessary effect allocations + disposers per list. **PR #1501 fixed that** (`<For>`/render-callback item params are runtime values, not reactive props → bare property reads bake to static `textContent`); idiomatic JSX now emits byte-identically to hand-tuned `_tpl` and measures equal-or-faster. So the benchmark now shows ONE honest `Pyreon` entry = the idiomatic JSX users ship, competing in every ranking.

**The earlier "4–8× faster than everyone on small-list ops" claims were ALSO a measurement artifact, fixed in the same objectivity work.** Two harness bugs inflated them: (a) async frameworks (React/Vue/Preact) paid an `rAF` commit wait *inside the timed region*, folding a full animation-frame of browser scheduling latency (~4–6ms) into every small-list number; (b) the `select` and `clear` benches had **no reset hook**, so only the first of 21 runs did real work and the median of `[real, 0, 0, …]` was 0µs. The fix replaced the `rAF` waits with the tightest commit each framework allows (`flushSync` for React/Svelte, one microtask for Vue/Preact, nothing for the synchronous signal frameworks) and added per-run reset hooks, so every run measures real work and the comparison is close to pure framework CPU. It also fixed a non-idiomatic Solid text binding (hand-written `createRenderEffect(() => td.textContent = …)` → Solid's real compiler output `insert()`).

Numbers below are a **proven `--repeat 5` pooled run** (100 samples per op, 5 full passes with **independently reshuffled framework order each pass** so position-dependent confounds average out) of `examples/benchmark`'s `bench:fair` harness (**Apple M3 Max, 14 cores, 96 GB, Chromium 148** — the harness prints this machine stamp with every run). Per-framework page isolation (fresh `page.goto`), `--js-flags=--expose-gc` + per-iteration forced GC, adaptive warmup (5–15 iters, stops when rolling p90 stabilises within 10%), median + 95% bootstrap CI + CV across the pooled samples. Real Chromium via Playwright on the production `vite build`, DOM-verified renders, genuine `react@19` / `solid-js@1.9` / `vue@3.5` / `svelte@5` / `preact@10` deps. **Tightest-commit timing** (no `rAF` scheduler latency) + **per-run resets** on every op. **9 krausest-canon ops** (create/replace/partial/select/swap/remove/clear/create-10k/append-1k-to-10k). Wall-clock ms is machine-dependent — the column-to-column *ratios* are the signal. Reproduce: `cd examples/benchmark && bun bench:fair --repeat 5`.

| Benchmark          | Vanilla JS | **Pyreon** | Vue 3    | SolidJS  | React 19 | Svelte 5 | Preact   | Framework verdict + honest read |
| ------------------ | ---------- | ---------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | ------------------------------- |
| Create 1,000 rows  | 8.40ms     | **9.00ms** | 10.00ms  | 10.40ms  | 11.60ms  | 12.60ms  | 13.90ms  | 🥇 Pyreon outright (frameworks); ~7% over Vanilla |
| Replace 1,000 rows | 8.50ms     | **9.00ms** | 9.90ms   | 10.20ms  | 11.30ms  | 12.90ms  | 13.80ms  | 🥇 Pyreon outright; same shape as create |
| Partial update     | 800µs      | **700µs**  | 1.60ms   | 4.50ms   | 1.10ms   | 2.30ms   | 1.30ms   | 🥇 Pyreon outright — now *beats* Vanilla (700 vs 800µs); `_bindText` direct-subscriber ~6× leaner than Solid's effect-based `insert` (real architectural diff) |
| Select row         | 0µs        | **0µs**    | 700µs    | 0µs      | 300µs    | 400µs    | 400µs    | 🤝 tied Solid=Pyreon at 0µs (timer floor); VDOM pays 0.3–0.7ms to diff all 1000 children |
| Swap rows          | 800µs      | **700µs**  | 1.40ms   | 800µs    | 7.10ms   | 2.40ms   | 1.10ms   | 🥇 Pyreon outright (700µs vs Solid/Vanilla 800µs); React 7.10ms = keyed-list O(n) reconcile (~10×) |
| Remove row         | 6.90ms     | **7.30ms** | 8.40ms   | 7.20ms   | 7.50ms   | 8.80ms   | 7.80ms   | 🥇 SolidJS outright (7.20 vs Pyreon 7.30ms) — Pyreon's sole loss; most architecture-neutral op (6.9–8.8ms band) |
| Clear rows         | 100µs      | **200µs**  | 400µs    | 500µs    | 1.00ms   | 400µs    | 800µs    | 🥇 Pyreon outright; VDOM unmount 0.4–1.0ms |
| Create 10,000 rows | 89.80ms    | **95.00ms**| 110.50ms | 115.50ms | 226.20ms | 237.70ms | 288.20ms | 🥇 Pyreon outright at 1.058× Vanilla; Vue 1.16×, Solid 1.22×, React 2.38×, Svelte 2.50×, Preact 3.03× slower |
| Append 1k→10k rows | 20.90ms    | **22.40ms**| 92.30ms  | 23.80ms  | 24.70ms  | 72.10ms  | 28.30ms  | 🥇 Pyreon outright; Vue 4.12× / Svelte 3.22× pay a full keyed-reconcile on the grow |

(Vanilla JS is the no-framework baseline, held OUT of the framework verdict. `Pyreon` = the idiomatic JSX impl (`pyreon.tsx`) — what users write. Median of 100 pooled samples (`--repeat 5`, 2026-06-17 run, Apple M3 Max / Chromium 148.0.7778.96); full CI95 + CV in the live harness output. Pyreon is **leader or tied-leader in 8 of 9 framework verdicts — 7 outright** (create/replace/partial/swap/clear/create-10k/append), ties Solid on `select`, and **Solid takes `remove` outright** (7.20 vs 7.30ms — Pyreon's only outright loss, the most architecture-neutral op).)

**Retained JS heap after suite (post-GC, MB) — the one dimension Pyreon does NOT lead:** Preact 2.18 < Solid 2.26 < Svelte 2.45 < React 2.57 < Vanilla 2.59 < **Pyreon 3.14** < Vue 3.97. Per-row signal allocation + cleanup closures cost Pyreon more retained memory than the VDOM frameworks; the benchmark measures and reports this honestly instead of only showing the wall-clock wins. (The PR #1501 compiler fix shaved this from ~3.33 → ~3.15MB by dropping the wasteful per-row `_bind` effects; the 2026-06-11 optimizations left retained heap unchanged within noise.)

**2026-06-11 create-path optimizations (now IN the table above — the run is post-optimization).** Two shipped changes attack the one place Vanilla still led (bulk-create): (1) `createSelector` inline-first-subscriber storage (the signal `_d1` trick on the selector's per-key buckets — a 10k-row create previously allocated 10k single-entry Sets; PR #1537) and (2) the compiler's **baked text placeholder** (sole-dynamic-text children ship `' '` in the template HTML + bind via `.firstChild` instead of per-row `createTextNode+appendChild`; both backends byte-identical; PR #1540). Measured by **interleaved A/B/A/B replication** (both changes flipped together within one tree, cool machine, Vanilla stable across all four runs, bundle shapes verified per state): **create-10k gap vs Vanilla 8.5/9.0ms → 5.5/6.5ms (−3ms, −31%, replicated across both flips)**, append trending −1ms; create-1k effect ≤300µs (below cross-run resolution — an earlier hot-machine pairing overclaimed "gap → 0" there). A third candidate (hoisted bind function) measured as a **null result** under proper pairing and is recorded as do-not-re-propose. Full methodology + profiles: `.claude/audits/create-path-perf-2026-06-11.md`; the SSR-side campaign (escapeHtml charCode scan, key-marker fast paths, attr-name memo — blog-shaped pages −10%, 1k-row tables −13% per render, A/B/A/B-replicated) is at `.claude/audits/ssr-throughput-2026-06-11.md`.

**What this means in practice:** After the 2026-06 objectivity pass (per-pass-reshuffled order, ONE honest Pyreon entry, retained-heap dimension, +2 krausest ops, the PR #1501 compiler fix), the honest picture is *Pyreon (idiomatic JSX) is the fastest framework on this synthetic row-list benchmark, with mid-pack retained memory* — strong, but NOT "infinitely faster." **Pyreon does not win literally everything:** **Solid takes `remove row` outright** (7.20 vs 7.30ms — the most VDOM-neutral op, a hair's-width margin), `select` is a **tie** with Solid (both at the 0µs timer floor), and on **retained heap Pyreon is 6th of 7** (3.14MB; only Vue heavier). **The real, robust advantages:** (1) bulk-create at 10k — Pyreon 95.0ms vs Vue 110 / Solid 116 / React 226 / Svelte 238 / Preact 288 (the VDOM 2.4–3.0× is genuine reconciliation cost); (2) `append-1k→10k` where Vue (4.12×) and Svelte (3.22×) pay a full keyed-reconcile while Pyreon edges Solid (22.4 vs 23.8ms); (3) React's keyed `swap` (7.10ms — O(n) reconcile, ~10× Pyreon's 700µs); (4) `partial update` where Pyreon's `_bindText` direct-subscriber (~8µs/update) beats even Solid's idiomatic `insert()` (~42µs/update) — the one place Pyreon clearly out-fine-grains Solid; (5) `select`/`partial` O(changed)-vs-VDOM-O(total). Against **Vanilla**, Pyreon's only measurable cost is bulk-create (~7% at 1k, ~6% at 10k — per-row signal allocation + cleanup closure + keyed For-loop map); the small mutations are tied-or-faster within noise, and after PR #1501 idiomatic JSX no longer carries per-row `_bind` overhead for static item reads. **This run measures close to pure framework CPU** (tightest commits) — *not* React's default async path, so real-world async latency would sit higher.

Earning a legitimate broad "fastest" claim still requires either (a) the compiler-pass collapse for rocketstyle (see "Compile-time rocketstyle collapse" section below — no other framework has Pyreon's multi-dimensional theme system to compile away) or (b) a **real-app** head-to-head, which genuinely does not exist yet: the `examples/cpa-pw-app-{react,solid,vue,preact,svelte}` ports run on Pyreon's compat shims (Pyreon runtime, not the real frameworks), so they cannot serve as a fair Pyreon-vs-React real-app comparison. Building real-framework app ports is tracked, multi-day work — **deliberately not faked here**. The honest scope for that work, written out so future contributors can pick it up:

1. **Canonical app**: TodoMVC (industry-standard reference) OR a thin blog-with-routes (covers SSR, navigation, hydration — closer to what real Pyreon users ship). TodoMVC is faster to bootstrap; blog gives more representative coverage. Recommend starting with TodoMVC.
2. **Real-framework ports (5)**: Pyreon, React 19 + react-dom, SolidJS, Vue 3, Svelte 5. Each in its OWN `examples/real-bench/<framework>/` directory with the framework's idiomatic build setup (Create React App for React, Vite-Solid for Solid, etc.). NO Pyreon-compat shim — each uses the actual framework runtime via real npm-published deps. Preact is optional (a Preact port mostly duplicates the React shape; lower priority).
3. **Benchmark scenarios** (real-app shape, not synthetic): (a) cold-start to interactive (TTI), (b) toggle 100 todos completed, (c) filter all/active/completed cycle, (d) add 10 todos in rapid succession, (e) clear completed × 50 todos, (f) drag-reorder 20 todos. Each scenario is one timed region; same methodology as `bench:fair` (per-framework page isolation, GC between iterations, adaptive warmup, 20 timed runs, median + CI95).
4. **Methodology discipline**: same `commit?`-hook per-framework wait pattern as `bench:fair` (sync frameworks no `commit`, async frameworks supply their scheduler wait). Each app must use its framework's idiomatic state management (Pyreon → signals; React → useState/useReducer; Solid → createSignal; Vue → ref/reactive; Svelte → $state). NO cross-framework patterns (don't make React use signals, etc.).
5. **Bundle-size delta** alongside wall-clock: real apps trade off framework overhead AND bundle weight. Report gzipped main bundle per framework next to the perf medians — closes the second half of the "fast in real apps" claim.
6. **Time estimate**: 3-5 days. 1 day per framework port + 1 day on the harness + 1 day on validation/results. The harness can be lifted directly from `examples/benchmark/bench-fair.ts` — same Playwright loop, same per-page isolation, same JSON output shape. The work is in writing the apps themselves, not the runner.

**Why this matters**: the current benchmark shows Pyreon (idiomatic JSX) leading or tying every framework on the synthetic row-list wall-clock ops (and clearly faster than React/Vue/Svelte/Preact on bulk-create + append + partial), but those are isolated DOM operations against contrived 1k-row data — and Pyreon is mid-pack on retained memory, which the suite now reports. A real-app head-to-head closes the credibility gap — and may surface NEW bottlenecks (router cost, form input latency, large form re-render) that the synthetic benchmark doesn't exercise. Until it lands, "fastest" claims stop at the synthetic benchmark's evidence and don't extrapolate to real apps. **The single biggest remaining objectivity gap is the author-judge problem** (the framework author writes + judges the benchmark) — only an upstream submission to the independent krausest/js-framework-benchmark fully resolves it; the 2026-06 op-set alignment is the prerequisite.

**Methodology — designed for objectivity:**
- ✓ **Per-framework page isolation** — each framework runs in its OWN fresh `page.goto('?framework=<name>')` so no cross-suite memory pressure / heap bias / JIT cache poisoning from earlier suites. (Previous all-frameworks-one-page method gave first-run frameworks a measurable advantage.)
- ✓ **Forced GC between iterations** — Chromium launches with `--js-flags=--expose-gc`; `runner.ts` calls `globalThis.gc()` between iterations. Removes the dominant source of inter-run variance (heap growth from prior iteration running unsynchronised collection during the next timed region).
- ✓ **Adaptive warmup** — keeps warming until the JS engine reaches steady state (rolling p90 of last 3 samples within 10% of the prior 3). Bounded `WARMUP_MIN=5`, `WARMUP_MAX=15`. Strictly more objective than a fixed warmup — React's MessageChannel scheduler reproducibly needs 10-15 iterations; signal frameworks usually stabilise in 5-7.
- ✓ **20 timed runs, median + 95% bootstrap CI + CV** — bootstrap (1000 resamples) is non-parametric so it doesn't assume normal distribution (timing data is right-skewed by GC outliers). CV (stddev/mean) tells you how stable the measurement was: <10% is tight, >20% means jittery and the median should be read with caution.
- ✓ **CI95-overlap tied-within-noise detection** — `bench-fair.ts` output flags each test with a `🤝` marker listing every framework whose CI95 overlaps with the leader's. Removes the "is a 5% difference real?" judgement call from the reader.
- ✓ Real Chromium via Playwright on production `vite build` output (not happy-dom, not dev mode).
- ✓ DOM verification per iteration (`expectRows(N)` / `expectRowsWithSelected`) — frameworks that "win" by not committing **throw**, not pass.
- ✓ Seeded mulberry32 RNG with per-framework reset — every framework sees identical row labels.
- ✓ Real published deps (`react@19.2.4`, `solid-js@1.9.11`, `vue@3.5.x`, `svelte@5.x`, `preact@10`) — no in-house ports.
- ✓ **Tightest-commit-per-framework, no rAF (objectivity pass)** — each impl uses the smallest commit that still passes DOM verification, so the timed region isolates framework work: **React + Svelte 5** `flushSync()` (synchronous, zero scheduler wait); **Vue** `await nextTick()` + **Preact** `await Promise.resolve()` (one microtask — their real flush boundary, no rAF); **Vanilla / Pyreon (raw + compiled) / Solid** nothing (synchronous DOM/signal writes). The earlier `rAF + setTimeout(0)` for React/Preact folded a full animation-frame of browser scheduling latency into their timed region (~4–6ms) and inflated every small-list number — the single biggest fairness bug, now removed. Trade-off: `flushSync` is not React's default async path, so these are CPU-objective numbers, not real-world-async-latency.
- ✓ **Per-run reset hooks on EVERY op (objectivity pass)** — `select`/`clear` previously had none, so only the first of 21 runs did real work (select re-selected the already-selected row; clear cleared the already-empty list) and the median was a meaningless 0µs. Each op now resets untimed before each timed run (clear repopulates 1000 rows; select deselects), so all 21 runs measure real work. The old `rAF` wait had masked this by adding a constant ~5ms to every run regardless.
- ✓ **Idiomatic per-framework impls, verified** — each uses its framework's real compiler output / best-practice API: React/Preact `memo` + keys, Solid `template()` + `insert()` + `createSelector` + `For` (the non-idiomatic `createRenderEffect(() => td.textContent=…)` text binding was fixed to `insert()`), Svelte `$state` runes + `flushSync`, Vue keyed `v-for` + `ref`, Vanilla cached node refs. No competitor is sandbagged; audited file-by-file.
- ✓ **Optional CPU throttling** — `bun bench:fair --throttle 4` enables 4× slowdown via CDP `Emulation.setCPUThrottlingRate` (mimics mid-tier devices). Off by default; the uncongested numbers are the reference.
- ✓ **Randomized framework execution order (2026-06 objectivity pass)** — `bench-fair.ts` Fisher-Yates–shuffles the run order each process (printed as `[bench-fair] run order: …`) so thermal/JIT-warmth ordering bias can't favour whichever framework happens to run first or last. The OUTPUT tables keep a fixed canonical column order regardless. Prior to this, every run executed frameworks in declaration order, which gave the first-run framework a small but systematic edge on the very first op of its suite even with per-page isolation.
- ✓ **Machine stamp printed with results (2026-06)** — every run prints CPU model + logical cores + RAM + OS + the exact Chromium version (`browser.version()`) before the tables, so absolute-ms numbers are reproducible/attributable instead of floating context-free. (The representative table below was an Apple M3 Max / Chromium 148 run.)
- ✓ **Per-pass reshuffled execution order (2026-06)** — a single fixed order pins every framework to the same slot every `--repeat` pass, so position-dependent confounds (CPU thermal drift across a sweep, JIT/heap state inherited from the prior framework's page) bias the SAME framework the SAME way every pass and pooling never averages it out. The harness now reshuffles the order INDEPENDENTLY each pass (`aggregateRepeated` keys by framework NAME, not positional index), turning slot into noise the 100-sample pool cancels. The single-pass order is still randomized. This was a real harness bug: an earlier `--repeat` shuffled once per process.
- ✓ **Retained-heap metric (2026-06 — closes the "still missing memory" gap)** — Chromium launches with `--enable-precise-memory-info`; after each framework's full suite completes (DOM already cleaned), the harness forces GC 3× and reads `performance.memory.usedJSHeapSize`, printed as a "Retained JS heap after suite (post-GC, MB)" table. Honestly captioned as framework-runtime + post-cleanup retention (NOT the krausest after-create metric). **This is the dimension where Pyreon does NOT lead** — the proven run: Preact 2.19 < Solid 2.26 < Svelte 2.44 < React 2.57 < Vanilla 2.59 < **Pyreon 3.15** < Vue 3.97 MB. Pyreon sits 6th of 7: per-row signal allocation + cleanup closures cost more retained heap than the VDOM frameworks, and the benchmark now says so out loud.
- ✓ **One Pyreon entry — no manufactured tiers (2026-06 — supersedes the prior two-entries caveat)** — the benchmark previously shipped a raw `Pyreon` JSX entry AND a hand-written `Pyreon (compiled)` `_tpl()` entry, ranking only the latter. That was doubly artifactual: the compiler already lowers idiomatic JSX to the same `_tpl()` cloneNode output, AND a compiler inefficiency (wasteful per-row `_bind()` for static `<For>`-item reads, fixed in **PR #1501**) was the only thing keeping idiomatic JSX measurably behind hand-tuned `_tpl`. With that fixed, the two emit byte-identically and measure equal-or-faster, so the hand-tuned impl was deleted. The single `Pyreon` entry IS the idiomatic JSX users ship, competing head-to-head with Solid's compiled `template()` / Svelte's `.svelte` output / React 19 — apples-to-apples, no informational footnote sleight-of-hand.
- ✓ **Two new krausest-canon ops (2026-06): `remove row` + `append 1,000 to 10,000 rows`** — brings the op set to 9 and closes the gap vs the upstream js-framework-benchmark canon (single-row delete + incremental large-list append, the two ops most likely to expose keyed-reconcile cost). Both are idiomatic per framework (targeted DOM removal / immutable-or-mutable state append matching each lib's convention) and DOM-verified. `remove row` is the most VDOM-neutral op so far — every framework lands 6.9–8.8ms (a single keyed splice forces a full-list reconcile in every architecture), and **Solid edges Pyreon here** (7.20 vs 7.30ms); `append` is high-CV (GC + layout under a 10k→11k grow) and Pyreon edges Solid (22.4 vs 23.8ms) while Vue/Svelte pay a full reconcile.
- ⚠ `createSelector` for select-row in Pyreon/Solid vs `React.memo` for React — O(1) vs O(N). Each is idiomatic for its framework but is a genuine architectural advantage signal frameworks have over VDOM-diff.
- ⚠ Numbers are machine-dependent (developer-class hardware). CI / lower-spec machines will produce different absolute ms; the *ratios* + the CI95 intervals are the portable signals.
- ✓ **(was ⚠, now fixed) Pure-CPU-ish timing** — the prior methodology measured time-to-visible-commit incl. an `rAF` wait that inflated async frameworks' small-list numbers; the objectivity pass switched to `flushSync`/microtask so the timed region is close to pure framework CPU. Residual caveat: this is CPU-objective, NOT real-world-async-latency — React's default (non-`flushSync`) path would show higher wall-clock for users.
- ⚠ **Pyreon vs Solid is close on most ops, with real Pyreon edges.** Both are compiled fine-grained signal libs (cloneNode template + per-row signal + `createSelector` + keyed `For`), tied on `select` within noise, Pyreon edges `swap` (700 vs 800µs); Solid edges `remove` (7.20 vs 7.30ms). Pyreon's reproducible advantages: (1) `partial update` — Pyreon's `_bindText` direct-subscriber text binding (~8µs/update) vs Solid's idiomatic `insert()`/`createRenderEffect` (~42µs/update), a genuine ~5× per-update primitive difference confirmed after switching Solid to its real compiler output; (2) `create 1k` (9.00 vs 10.40ms) + `create 10k` (95.0 vs 115.5ms). These are real, not impl artifacts — and now that PR #1501 removed the per-row `_bind` for static item reads, idiomatic-JSX Pyreon emits the same `_tpl()` output a hand-tuned impl would, so these edges hold for what users actually ship. The className binding is symmetric (both effect-based after the objectivity pass).
- ✓ **(was ❌, now partially addressed) Memory metrics** — the 2026-06 retained-heap table (above) surfaces post-suite allocation pressure per framework. Still missing the finer-grained version: *per-iteration* peak heap + GC-pause durations via CDP `HeapProfiler` (the retained-heap number is one post-GC snapshot per framework, not a per-op allocation trace).
- ⚠ **The deepest objectivity limit is structural, not fixable in-repo: the benchmark author IS the framework author.** Test SELECTION (these 9 row-list ops) is the js-framework-benchmark canon and is precisely where fine-grained signal frameworks shine; there is no op here where a VDOM architecture might win (deep prop-diffing through large component trees, concurrent rendering under input pressure). A slow Pyreon impl always gets optimized; a slow competitor impl needs someone to notice. The only real fix is **submitting a Pyreon entry to the independent krausest/js-framework-benchmark** where community maintainers review every implementation — the 2026-06 op-set alignment (`remove row` + `append`) is the prerequisite for that. Until then, "fastest" claims stop at this synthetic suite's evidence and the honest headline is "fastest framework on the row-list ops (wins 7/9 framework verdicts, ties Solid on select, Solid edges remove), mid-pack on retained memory, with a real bulk-create + partial-update edge over VDOM."

Key optimizations: `_tpl()` (cloneNode), `_bind()` (static-dep tracking), `TextNode.data`, zero-alloc mount pipeline (lazy hooks, lazy EffectScope, devtools gated on `__DEV__`, per-definition WeakMap caches in rocketstyle, dimension-prop memo at the rocketstyle wrapper, `$element` bundle interning + styler classCache extension), **`_bindText` single-subscriber fast path** (inline-slot `_d1` for the dominant per-row signal case — no Set allocation, no iterator overhead; promotes to `_d: Set` on second subscriber), **`_set` inline-batch direct dispatch** (unbatched writes open the batch window without a `batch(closure)` allocation and dispatch single-subscriber channels — `_d1`, `_s` size 1 — DIRECTLY instead of round-tripping through the pending queues; cascades/diamonds/multi-pass re-fire still drain through the shared two-tier flush. Single-subscriber notify ~131ns → ~16ns; set→effect rerun ~162ns → ~46ns; effect-propagation bench 5× — see `batch.ts:openInlineBatch`).

### Core micro-benchmarks (`scripts/bench/` — `bench:router` / `bench:reactivity` / `bench:head` / `bench:ssr` / `bench:server` / `bench:compiler` / `bench:sync`)

Bun-run cross-library micro-benchmarks, separate from the browser DOM suite above. **Honest standings (2026-06, post-objectivity fixes):**

- **Router (`bench:router`** vs find-my-way / Hono / radix3 / react-router / TanStack / vue-router / path-to-regexp**): Pyreon is the fastest at realistic table sizes** — 1.00× leader at 50 + 200 routes, ahead of radix3 at every size; Hono's all-routes-in-one-regex leads the 10-route toy table only (and measures ~4.5× SLOWER than Pyreon at 50+ routes). Achieved by the 2026-06 `resolveRoute` hot-path overhaul (see the router section).
- **Reactivity (`bench:reactivity`** vs `@preact/signals-core` + solid-js (browser build)**): honest mid-field on raw-primitive microbenches.** Pyreon beats Solid on signal create (48 vs 113ns), computed diamond (17.0 vs 43.8µs/100 updates) and deep chain; Solid leads effect-heavy paths (propagation 8.6 vs 35.6µs, fan-out); **Preact signals-core leads every row** (its versioned linked-list dependency tracking avoids the per-rerun dep-Set teardown/re-subscribe Pyreon pays). **Why this does NOT contradict the DOM benchmark's `partial update` win:** compiled Pyreon apps don't run raw `effect()` for text/attr updates — the compiler emits `_bindText`/`_bindDirect` direct-subscriber bindings (~8µs/update DOM-included vs Solid's effect-based `insert` ~42µs), so the microbench's effect-path gap is largely bypassed in real rendered apps. **Tracked candidate, not yet built:** versioned/linked-list dependency tracking for `effect()` (the Preact architecture) — a reactivity-core re-architecture, to be attempted only with a measured real-app-shape campaign (the earlier hybrid-Set subscriber experiment measured NULL real-app gains — characterize before prototyping).
- **Head (`bench:head`** vs unhead (Vue/Nuxt)**): Pyreon 4.9–7.2× faster** on SSR head serialization at 5/20/50 tags.
- **Real-app (`examples/real-bench`** — TodoMVC-shape vs REAL `react-dom@19`**): Pyreon ~5.7–16× faster** (2026-06-17 run, 20 samples — add-100: 500µs vs 8.20ms ≈ 16×; toggle-1000: 300µs vs 1.70ms ≈ 5.7×; clear-1000: 200µs vs 1.30ms ≈ 6.5×). These are µs-scale, high-CV measurements — the *magnitude* (per-row signal patch vs React's whole-list re-render) is the signal, not the exact ratio; the ratio wobbles run-to-run.
- **SSR / server / compiler**: Pyreon-only throughput sanity (350K empty renders/s; 162K req/s simple handler). The compiler's reactive pass costs ~2.3× over bare OXC at BUILD time — the price of the reactivity analysis no competitor performs; still ~10–30× faster than Solid's legacy Babel pipeline.
- **Sync (`bench:sync`** — Pyreon-only, CRDT→signal hot paths**): validates the signature claim (remote-op→signal ~5µs/write) + characterizes the two O(N)-per-change costs (µs-scale, high-CV/machine-load-dependent — the O(N) SHAPE + order of magnitude are the signal, not exact values). Awareness recompute is clean O(N), low single-digit µs at realistic peer counts (dozens), ~10–30µs only at 200–500 peers; syncedList `toArray` rebuild O(N), ~1–10µs for typical lists, ~tens of µs at 5000. **Two speculative optimizations were MEASURED + REJECTED (do-not-re-propose without a NEW real-app measurement):** incremental awareness (delta-track peers vs full snapshot per change) — at realistic live-cursor counts (dozens) the recompute is sub-3µs, only matters at 200+ simultaneous cursors which the package already documents as a v1 limit with the throttle-cursor-publishes mitigation, AND the `Signal<PeerState[]>` API still forces an O(N) array materialization so the win is smaller than it looks; syncedList delta-apply (splice vs `toArray()`) — the keyed `<For>` already keeps the DOM surgical and huge lists belong in `@pyreon/virtual`. The bench's lasting value is regression-guarding the O(N) characterization + the signature-path cost.

**Objectivity contract for `scripts/bench/` (two bugs this section guards against, both fixed 2026-06):** (1) every bench MUST force `NODE_ENV=production` BEFORE framework imports evaluate — Pyreon's dev mode keeps the reactive-devtools registry always-on (per-primitive `new Error()` capture + fire recording), so dev-mode benching measures the instrumentation, not the framework (signal create read 1.4M ops/s in dev vs ~21M in production); (2) competitor IMPORTS must resolve to the build that actually does the work — under Bun/Node resolution, bare `solid-js` resolves via the `node` condition to `dist/server.js`, the SSR build where signals/memos/effects are INERT stubs (every "Solid" number was a no-op loop, ~42ns for "100 updates"); the bench imports `solid-js/dist/solid.js` (browser production build) explicitly. Related Solid trap: `createEffect`'s FIRST run is deferred until the owning `createRoot` body completes — benching inside the root callback times writes against a not-yet-subscribed effect; create inside the root, bench AFTER it returns.

| `@pyreon/react-compat`   | Full hooks (incl. useReducer/useRef/useId/useSyncExternalStore/useTransition/useDeferredValue/useImperativeHandle/useActionState/useOptimistic/use), forwardRef, memo, lazy, Suspense, createContext, createPortal shims. Companion compat layers: `preact-compat`, `vue-compat`, `solid-compat`, `svelte-compat` — each at near-full public-API parity (see their docs pages for the per-framework limitation matrix) |

| `@pyreon/vitest-config`  | Private: `defineNodeConfig` / `defineBrowserConfig` — single canonical shape for every package's vitest config. Enforces merge order + per-category coverage defaults by construction. Locked in by `pyreon/vitest-config-uses-shared` lint rule. See `packages/internals/vitest-config/README.md`. |

### UI Component Library (packages/ui/)

| Package                 | Description                                                                                                                      |
| ----------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `@pyreon/ui-theme`      | Default theme (colors, spacing, typography, borders, shadows, transitions) + rocketstyle ThemeDefault/StylesDefault augmentation |
| `@pyreon/ui-components` | 67 rocketstyle components across 10 categories (Button, Card, Input, etc.)                                                       |
| `@pyreon/ui-primitives` | Headless behavior primitives (ComboboxBase, CalendarBase, etc.)                                                                  |

#### @pyreon/ui-components — Architecture

- Three base components: `el` (Element — structured layout), `txt` (Text — inline typography), `list` (List — flowing children)
- Factory at `packages/ui/components/src/factory.ts` re-exports `el`, `txt`, `list`, `rs` from `bases/`
- **Layout in `.attrs()`**: `tag`, `direction`, `alignX`, `alignY`, `gap`, `block` — these target Element's inner layout
- **CSS in `.theme()`**: colors, spacing, borders, shadows — these target the styled outer wrapper
- **Pseudo-states in `.theme()`**: `hover: {}`, `focus: {}`, `active: {}`, `disabled: {}` objects — bases generate `:hover`/`:focus-visible`/`:active`/`:disabled` CSS
- **`:hover` is unconditional** — applied to ALL components with hover theme, not just interactive ones. Only `cursor: pointer` is gated on `onClick`/`href`
- **CSS property naming**: unistyle convention (`borderWidthTop`) not CSS-spec (`borderTopWidth`)
- **useBooleans: false** is the rocketstyle default (both type-level and runtime) — dimension props accept string values (`state="primary"`, `size="level3"`), not booleans. Opt in with `rocketstyle({ useBooleans: true })` for vitus-labs-style boolean shorthand. Before April 2026 the type default was `true` while the runtime default was `false` — boolean props typechecked but were silently dropped at runtime. Fixed by aligning the type default (rocketstyle `init.ts`)
- Theme augmentation: `@pyreon/ui-theme` augments `ThemeDefault extends Theme` and `StylesDefault extends ITheme` — apps must NOT re-augment

### UI System — Key Technical Details

#### @pyreon/styler (CSS-in-JS)

- `styled('div')\`color: red\``→ returns`ComponentFn`
- `css\`...\``→ lazy`CSSResult`, resolved on use
- `keyframes\`...\`` → returns animation name string
- Theme: `ThemeContext` is a **reactive** context (`createReactiveContext<Theme>`); `useTheme()` returns a `Theme` snapshot at call time, `useThemeAccessor()` returns the raw `() => Theme` accessor for tracking inside effects. Whole-theme swaps (user-preference themes) propagate through the resolver effect in `styled()` DynamicStyled and re-resolve CSS + swap class names without remounting the VNode. `PyreonUI` wraps `enrichTheme(props.theme)` in `computed` so the enriched theme updates when `props.theme` changes
- `createGlobalStyle\`...\`` → inject global CSS
- Singleton `StyleSheet` with FNV-1a hashing, dedup cache, SSR support
- `createSheet()` for isolated sheet instances
- **`innerRef` → `ref` alias**: a `styled()` component accepts `innerRef` as a `ref` alias (uniform with `@pyreon/elements` Element, which has always supported `innerRef`). A styled component renders a single DOM node so plain `ref` already targets it; before this, `<Styled innerRef={fn}>` SILENTLY dropped the ref (not a forwarded DOM prop) — the callback never fired (e.g. a `@pyreon/virtual` scroll container's element was never captured → empty list). `aliasInnerRef` (in `styled.tsx`) normalizes at both `StaticStyled` + `DynamicStyled` entry: when `innerRef` is set and `ref` is not, it shallow-copies descriptors (preserving getter-shaped reactive props + symbol brands) with `ref` ← `innerRef` and `innerRef` dropped (so it never reaches the DOM as an invalid `innerref=` attribute). Explicit `ref` always wins; zero-alloc fast path returns `rawProps` unchanged when there's nothing to alias. Real-Chromium-locked (`styler.browser.test.tsx` — static + dynamic delivery, ref-wins, no-attr; bisect-verified: neutralizing the alias fails the two delivery specs).
- **SSR fast path in `DynamicStyled` (`styled.tsx`)**: a module-level `IS_SERVER = typeof document === 'undefined'` (same detection as `sheet.ts`). On the server, `DynamicStyled`'s reactive branch (fired when `$rocketstyle`/`$rocketstate` are accessors — i.e. EVERY rocketstyle component) used to allocate a `computed` subscription + a `ref` closure + a `renderEffect` per component. All three are client-only dead weight server-side: refs never fire during `renderToString`, and no signal changes within a single SSR pass — they subscribe + allocate but emit zero HTML. The fast path resolves the class once via `doResolve` and emits, skipping all three. The emitted className is **byte-identical** to the reactive path's initial value (proven), so hydration — where the client (`IS_SERVER` false → full reactive path) re-establishes the machinery — sees no mismatch. Measured (`renderToString` of 2,000 reactive styled components, 8-pair drift-controlled A/B): **~9.7ms → ~1.95ms (~5×, CI [+7.54, +7.91ms], 8/8 faster)** — the reactive-machinery allocation is ~80% of per-component SSR cost when the resolve is cached (repeated components); always positive. Bisect-locked by the node-env `src/__tests__/styled-ssr-fast-path.test.tsx` (reverting the fast path makes the server run the client branch, which attaches a `ref` function — the test asserts it's absent). Ported from vitus-labs/styler's IS_SERVER `DynamicStyled` variant split. The companion micro-opts in that vitus-labs commit (proxyCache Map→null-proto, staticComponentCache tuple-promote, CSSResult `= undefined` drop, hash 4× unroll) MEASURED as noise per vitus-labs's own audit and were NOT ported — only the structural SSR work-skip carries.

#### @pyreon/unistyle (Responsive Props)

- Single value, mobile-first array `[xs, sm, md, lg]`, or breakpoint object `{ xs: ..., md: ... }`
- 170+ CSS property mappings for responsive shorthand
- Unit utilities for consistent spacing/sizing
- **`themeToCssVars(theme, options?)` — CSS custom properties autogenerated from a plain theme JSON** (Phase 1 of the CSS-variables theming track). Returns `{ vars, css, registry }`: `vars` is the same-shape tree with every eligible leaf replaced by a plain `'var(--px-<path>)'` string (plain strings → flow through the ENTIRE value pipeline untouched; `stripUnit`'s css-number regex doesn't match `var(`/`calc(`, so `value()`/`values()`/edge/borderRadius/`styles()`/`makeItResponsive` pass them verbatim — promoted from incidental behavior to a TESTED contract in `__tests__/cssVariables-passthrough.test.ts`); `css` is a ready-to-inject `:root { … }` block; `registry` maps `varName → emitted value` for consumers that can't evaluate `var()` (document export, devtools). **Units are baked at EMISSION via the existing `value()` + rootSize** — `spacing.small: 8` emits `--px-spacing-small: 0.5rem`, so themes stay authored in px and downstream never converts a var. Default per-top-level-key policy: `spacing`/`fontSize`/`headingSize`/`elementSize`/`borderRadius` → rem, `borderWidth` → px, everything else verbatim (unitless scales like `lineHeight`/`zIndex`/custom `ratio` keys stay valid `calc()` multipliers); override via `units: { myScale: 'rem' }`. Excluded (kept raw): `breakpoints`/`rootSize`/`__PYREON__` (`@media` can't read `var()`), arrays, functions, booleans, null/undefined, empty strings, non-finite numbers. Proportional sizing is native CSS: `` `calc(${vars.spacing.small} * ${vars.ratio.medium})` ``. Pure (no injection) + WeakMap-cached by theme identity (same theme + options → SAME result object — load-bearing for downstream identity-keyed caches). Kebab-collision (`xSmall` vs `x-small`) throws loudly. Real-Chromium smoke locks: computed styles resolve emitted values, calc-over-vars computes, **`[data-theme="dark"]` attribute flip changes computed styles with ZERO class change** (the mechanism the parked Phase 2 builds on). **Phase 2 SHIPPED (same branch chain)**: `init({ cssVariables: true | { prefix, attribute } })` on ui-core's config singleton (`resolveCssVariables()` is the one defaulted accessor); PyreonUI tokenizes the enriched theme via `themeToCssVars`, injects the `:root` block once via styler `injectRules` (SSR-aware — rides `getStyleTag()` + stream flush, proven by a node-env renderToString test), provides the var-leaf tree, and renders a layout-neutral `display: contents` wrapper carrying the mode attribute (SERVER-RENDERED — SSR/SSG ship the right mode; nested `inversed` providers scope via the cascade, real-Chromium-proven); rocketstyle's `mode(a, b)` becomes a hashed deduped var-pair factory (`--px-m-<fnv1a>`, picked at the single `getThemeFromChain` injection site; numbers warn in dev — emitted verbatim, units can't apply), `_resolveRsEntry` neither READS the mode signal nor keys on it under the flag (cross-mode cache identity → styler's identity-keyed classCache skips resolution on flip), and `getThemeByMode` is skipped (no brands exist). **Measured lock (real Chromium, bisect-verified-with-restore)**: `rocketstyle/src/__tests__/css-variables-mode.browser.test.tsx` — a mode flip changes computed styles with ZERO className writes, `styler.resolve: 0`, `rocketstyle.getTheme: 0`; the flag-off control asserts the classic path DOES re-resolve. Flag off = byte-identical behavior (all pre-existing suites green untouched). **Phase 3 SHIPPED (same chain)**: styler dev-mode resolved-CSS validator in `sheet.insert` (warns once per finding on NaN / undefined / malformed `var()` concat, naming the declaration — the safety net for legacy arithmetic + string-concat on var tokens); coolgrid grid math var-aware (`isCssVarValue` branch emits native `calc()` for Row margins / Col gap-margin / Col width — pre-fix a var gap SILENTLY skipped all spacing and emitted the malformed `var(--x)px`; NOTE multiplication not division: `calc(x / -2)` invalidates the whole shorthand); `resolveCssVarReferences(value, registry)` in unistyle (inline var refs for non-CSS consumers — document export/devtools; calc inlined NOT evaluated); REAL `@pyreon/ui-components` Button + full default ui-theme proven var-safe in real Chromium (zero validator findings, flip keeps className — `ui-components.browser.test.tsx`); **measured (real-app, `examples/cssvars-bench` + `scripts/bench-cssvars.ts`): a 300-real-component theme toggle is ~1.9× faster (16.5ms→8.8ms), ~2.05× at 600 components, holding 1.89× under 4× CPU throttle — and vars does ZERO per-component re-runs on flip (`rocketstyle.dimensionMemo.hit` 12000→0) vs classic's full O(N) re-run, the deterministic signal. NOTE the headline is STEADY-STATE toggle (both modes warmed): classic does NOT re-resolve themes on a warmed flip (the `_rsMemo` caches both modes), so the win is not 'classic re-resolves' — it's that vars does NO component-level JS at all (one `documentElement` attribute write + native CSS-var recalc) while classic re-runs every component's accessor. The earlier 100-box micro-bench's bigger ratios were a COLD-first-flip measurement.**. **Phase 4 partial**: `_rsCollapse` single-class fast path SHIPPED (identical light/dark classes — what var-mode collapse produces — skip the mode binding entirely; zero-subscription browser-locked, bisect-verified). **The whole chain is ONE stacked branch — Phase 1 is PR #1518, Phases 2–4 are PR #1528 (based on #1518; auto-retargets to main + needs a rebase to trigger CI when #1518 merges).** **Phase 4b SHIPPED**: the dark/light FOUC fix is a **root-vs-nested PyreonUI split** — the ROOT provider writes the mode attribute to `document.documentElement` via a client effect (so it sits at `:root`, where the var rules cascade from AND where the pre-paint script writes), returning children UNWRAPPED; only NESTED / `inversed` providers render the `display:contents` wrapper that scopes an override to their subtree. This is the correct shape because a head script (the only placement guaranteed before first paint) runs before the in-body wrapper parses, and a wrapper would be a closer ancestor than `<html>` that would defeat it. `cssVariablesPrePaintScript({ attribute?, storageKey?, fallback? })` (exported from `@pyreon/ui-core`) builds the blocking `<head>` script that sets the attribute on `documentElement` from localStorage (`zero-theme`) / `prefers-color-scheme` before paint. **zero needs NO change** — its existing `themeScript` export already writes `documentElement.dataset.theme` and composes with the root provider; non-zero apps inject `cssVariablesPrePaintScript()`. The ONE uncovered case (documented, rare): a hardcoded `mode="dark"` SSR app with no stored preference — the mode lives only in the app JSX, unknown to a pre-paint script; stamp `<html data-theme="dark">` server-side for that. **Q2 SHIPPED (document export under cssVariables)**: `resolveModeVar(value, mode)` (exported from `@pyreon/rocketstyle`, backed by a `varName → {light,dark}` registry the mode-pair factory populates) resolves `mode(a,b)` pair vars; connector-document's `resolveStyles` + `extractDocumentTree` gained a decoupled `resolveVar?` hook (keeps the bridge dep-light — only `@pyreon/document`); `@pyreon/document-primitives`' `extractDocNode({ theme?, mode? })` AUTO-builds the resolver (composing `resolveModeVar` + unistyle's `resolveCssVarReferences` over a `themeToCssVars(theme).registry`) so PDF/DOCX/email export inlines `var(--px-…)` to raw values — doc primitives mostly emit raw literals (untouched), the resolver is the safety net for doc components that reference theme tokens / mode pairs under cssVariables. Theme authoring stays UNCHANGED in all phases (mode pairs remain component-level `mode(a, b)`; no theme-level mode shapes — explicitly rejected). **Perf-bug the benchmark caught + fixed**: `PyreonUI` provided the core context as an EAGER object (`{ theme: enrichedTheme(), mode: modeComputed(), … }`), so reading `.theme` transitively read `modeComputed()` and subscribed every theme-reading component to mode — defeating mode-free resolution (every component re-ran on flip even under cssVariables). Fixed by providing LAZY getters (`get theme(){…} get mode(){…}`): a `.theme`-only reader subscribes only to `enrichedTheme` (stable on flip → no re-run); classic resolution reading `.mode` still re-runs (correct). This is what turned the real-app steady-state toggle from 0.74× (slower!) to ~1.9× faster — without it the var-mode win is invisible in steady state. Reference: `packages/ui-system/ui-core/src/PyreonUI.tsx` coreContext provide; benchmark `examples/cssvars-bench/` + `scripts/bench-cssvars.ts`. **Retained heap is NEUTRAL** (measured, `bench-cssvars.ts --heap`, 300 real components post-GC): classic 10.57 MB vs cssVariables 10.51 MB — vars marginally LOWER (classic caches both light+dark `_rsMemo` entries; vars caches one mode-free entry + the var-pair registry — a wash). **Bundle cost ~2.2 KB gz** (the net-new modules, esbuild prod+gz: unistyle `cssVariables.ts` 1.6 KB + ui-core `cssVariablesPrePaint.ts` 0.6 KB; rocketstyle/PyreonUI deltas are small interleaved additions), within the locked per-package budgets; the styler dev validator tree-shakes out in prod. **Real-app dogfood + e2e gate**: `examples/cssvars-bench` is a human-openable interactive demo (visible dark/light toggle over real `@pyreon/ui-components` + `mode(a,b)` boxes); `e2e/cssvars-showcase.spec.ts` (`bun run test:e2e:cssvars`, own config on port 5211, wired into `scripts/e2e-affected.ts` so a ui-core/rocketstyle/unistyle/ui change runs it) proves the mode end-to-end in real Chromium: under `?vars=1` a toggle is ONE `documentElement[data-theme]` write, the cascade re-resolves the `mode(a,b)` sentinel color, and the Buttons' classNames DON'T churn; under `?vars=0` the same toggle re-resolves (classic) and writes NO documentElement attribute. **Why NOT dogfooded by flipping `ui-showcase` wholesale**: ui-showcase feeds `verify-modes` + the rocketstyle-collapse probe cells (`rs-collapse-*-probe` routes), and cssVariables changes collapse output (single class vs dual) → those gates would break; a URL-param approach hits SSR hydration mismatch (server renders classic, client re-resolves var). The dedicated client-mounted example dogfoods without destabilizing those gates. **ui-system-wide validation (are we sure it works everywhere?)**: a comprehensive audit + per-package var-mode coverage confirms it. The only bug class is JS arithmetic on a theme value (a `var()` string can't go through `gap / 2` → `NaN`) — and an audit of EVERY ui-system package found it ONLY in `coolgrid` (fixed: `isCssVarValue` → native `calc()`, browser-tested). Every package that CONSUMES theme values does so exclusively through the styler `css` + unistyle `value()`/`makeItResponsive` chokepoint (var()/calc() pass through untouched — the tested contract) and has a dedicated var-mode test: rocketstyle (measured flip), ui-core (mode + SSR), unistyle (pass-through contract + ReDoS), coolgrid (real gap), `@pyreon/elements` (var through the full Element component → styler → resolved 8px, zero validator findings — `elements/src/__tests__/css-variables.browser.test.tsx`), ui-components (real Button + full default theme). The remaining packages are ORTHOGONAL by construction — `@pyreon/kinetic` + `@pyreon/kinetic-presets` (animation; only runtime dep is `@pyreon/sized-map`, NO styler/unistyle/ui-core dep, styles via className-merge + literal-CSS presets — the flag has no code path in), `@pyreon/attrs` (prop plumbing), `@pyreon/ui-primitives` (headless behavior/ARIA) — all audit-clean for theme-value math. So a kinetic-under-cssVariables test would add a fake dep to flip a flag kinetic never reads; deliberately NOT written (hollow). The styler dev validator (`sheet.insert` NaN/malformed-var scan) is the runtime safety net that would surface any future undetected math-on-var site in dev. Reference: `packages/ui-system/unistyle/src/cssVariables.ts`, `packages/ui-system/ui-core/src/{config,PyreonUI}.tsx`, `packages/ui-system/rocketstyle/src/utils/theme.ts`, `packages/ui-system/styler/src/sheet.ts` (validator), `packages/ui-system/coolgrid/src/{Row,Col}/styled.ts`, `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/template.ts` (`_rsCollapse` fast path).

#### @pyreon/attrs (HOC Factory)

- `attrs(component)` → chainable builder
- `.attrs({ prop: value })` → inject default props
- `.config({ dimensions: {...} })` → rocketstyle config
- `.statics({ method: fn })` → attach static methods
- `.compose(enhancer)` → apply HOC wrapper

#### @pyreon/rocketstyle (Multi-State Styling)

- `rocketstyle(component)` → multi-dimensional styling engine
- Dimensions: `state`, `size`, `variant`, `theme`, + custom
- Dark/light mode via `useDarkMode` dimension
- Each dimension maps prop values to CSS via `styled()` templates
- **Per-definition caching architecture**: all caches are created once per `rocketComponent()` call (component definition) and shared across all instances via WeakMap:
  - `_dimensionsCache` — `getDimensionsMap` result keyed on dimension-themes object identity
  - `_reservedKeysCache` — `Object.keys(reservedPropNames)` keyed on keywords object identity
  - `_omitSetCache` — pre-built `Set<string>` for `omit()` keyed on reserved-keys array identity (avoids per-mount Set allocation)
  - `ALL_PSEUDO_KEYS` / `STATIC_OMIT_KEYS` — merged key arrays computed once
  - `LocalThemeManager` — WeakMap tiers for baseTheme, dimensionThemes, and per-mode resolved themes
  - `_rsMemo` — dimension-prop memo (2026-Q2 follow-up to E2's B-FINDING). `WeakMap<theme, Map<keyString, { rocketstyle, rocketstate }>>` keyed by `mode|dimensionPropTuple|pseudoState`. The two accessors `$rocketstyleAccessor` / `$rocketstateAccessor` share a single resolver that returns the SAME object identities on cache hit, which lets the styler's downstream `classCache` (also identity-keyed) skip the resolve pipeline entirely. Hit emits `rocketstyle.dimensionMemo.hit`; miss emits `rocketstyle.getTheme` (semantics changed: now counts FRESH resolutions, not accessor invocations). LRU bound at 128 entries per theme — sized for high-cardinality surfaces (data tables with state derived from row data, design systems with many tokens crossed with size/variant axes, dashboards rendering many small interactive components). Previously 32; raised in the rs-cap PR after the rs-precompute spike (closed PR #761) bisect-verified that a 60-unique-tuple Button mount loop had 45% cache-miss rate at cap=32 (888/2000 lookups) and 46% wall-clock regression vs the cap-fits-workload case. At cap=128 the cold-resolve count drops to 0 for that workload. Memory cost ~12KB per definition per theme (128 × ~100 bytes), negligible vs the wall-clock win. Regression lock: `packages/ui-system/rocketstyle/src/__tests__/memo-cap.test.ts` (64-tuple + 100-tuple warm-pass cold-resolves must be 0; 200-tuple control still evicts). Oldest-first eviction. Wall-clock measurement (E2 bench, 200 Buttons × 5 runs): baseline dropped from 8.80ms to 4.80ms (~45% improvement); per-Button styler.resolve dropped from 22 to 6 (~73% reduction — the residual 6 come from styled wrappers OUTSIDE the rocketstyle layer where the memo doesn't reach). Real apps must mount one shared `<PyreonUI>` provider for the memo to span instances — each provider mount creates a fresh `enrichedTheme` via `computed()`, which produces a different WeakMap key
- **getTheme in-place merge**: dimension slices merged directly onto `finalTheme` instead of creating a new `{}` target per `merge()` call. Pseudo-state defaults use a frozen shared `EMPTY_PSEUDO` object instead of 6 `{}` allocations per call
- **Dev guard**: uses `__DEV__` (backed by `import.meta.env.DEV`) — tree-shaken to zero bytes in production

#### @pyreon/kinetic (Animations)

- `kinetic(component)` → animation-enabled wrapper
- `.preset(fadeIn)` → apply preset from `@pyreon/kinetic-presets`
- `.enter({ opacity: 0 })` / `.enterTo({ opacity: 1 })` — enter animation
- `.leave({ opacity: 1 })` / `.leaveTo({ opacity: 0 })` — leave animation
- `.collapse()` — height-based collapse/expand
- `.stagger({ delay: 50 })` — staggered children
- `.group()` — TransitionGroup wrapper
- 4 modes: transition, collapse, stagger, group
- **SSR contract — initially-hidden Transitions render structural content.** `<Transition show={() => false}>` always emits children in SSR, with hidden-state classes inlined (`leaveTo` if defined, else `enterFrom`). Critical for SSG sites using the documented scroll-reveal pattern (`useIntersection` + sticky-signal) — IntersectionObserver can't fire on the server, so `show` is false at SSR; prior to this contract, the wrapped content was structurally absent from prerendered HTML. Matches Framer Motion / react-transition-group / react-spring ecosystem norm: content is structural, animation is visual. Implementation: `Transition` branches at setup on `props.show()` — initially-visible uses the original `<Show>`-gated mount (preserves runtime-unmount semantic); initially-hidden always renders children + the `watch(stage)` effect drives the enter animation on `show` flip true on the SAME element. **Trade-off**: for initially-hidden Transitions, `unmount: true` no longer triggers a true DOM removal after a later leave animation completes — the element stays in DOM with the leave-to class applied. Initially-visible Transitions keep the unmount semantic. Companion fix in `applyEnter`: made symmetric to `applyLeave`, clearing residual `leave`/`leaveFrom`/`leaveTo` classes at start so the SSR-baked hidden class doesn't fight `enterTo`. Reference: `packages/ui-system/kinetic/src/Transition.tsx` `wasInitiallyShown` branch + `Transition.ssr.test.tsx` (7 specs via real `renderToString`) + `kinetic.browser.test.tsx` (2 new specs for the client-side mount + enter-on-flip). Bisect-verified at the SSR layer: reverting the branch fails 6 of the 7 specs with `expected '' to contain '<section'`; the 7th (initially-visible no-regression) keeps passing.

#### @pyreon/kinetic-presets (120+ Presets)

- Framework-agnostic CSS transition objects
- `fade`, `slideUp`, `slideDown`, `slideLeft`, `slideRight`, `scaleIn`, + 100 more
- `compose(preset1, preset2)` — merge presets
- `withDuration(preset, ms)` — override duration
- Factory functions for custom parameterized presets

#### @pyreon/elements (Base Primitives)

- `Element` — base block with responsive style props
- `Text` — inline text with typography props
- `List` — list container (ul/ol/dl)
- `Overlay` — positioned overlay with backdrop
- `Portal` — renders children outside DOM hierarchy
- **Overlay focus restore (a11y)**: `useOverlay`'s `showContent` captures the active element (typically the trigger); `hideContent` returns focus to it on close **only** when focus is still inside the closing overlay (or was lost to `<body>`/null) — if the user deliberately moved focus to another control, it's left there. Modal overlays get this from native `<dialog>.showModal()`; non-modal (dropdown/popover/tooltip) needed it explicitly (pre-fix `_prevFocusEl` was declared but never used → keyboard focus dropped to the top of the document on dismiss). Real-Chromium regression-locked at `packages/ui-system/elements/src/__tests__/Overlay-focus-restore.browser.test.tsx` (bisect-verified — neuter the `prev.focus()` and the restore spec fails while the no-steal spec stays green).
- **Element simple-path fast path (2026-Q2)**: when the Element has no `beforeContent` / `afterContent` and the tag doesn't need the button/fieldset/legend two-layer flex fix, Element inlines the `Wrapper` helper directly into a single styled invocation. Skips one component invocation, one `splitProps` call, and one `mountChild` per Element. Real-Chromium wall-clock benchmark (`packages/ui-system/elements/src/__tests__/perf-stress.browser.test.tsx`): 31-45% faster across all shapes — 500-child single-tree mount drops from 2.90 ms to 1.60 ms (−45%), 5000-mount stress from 31.80 ms to 19.70 ms (−38%). Compound elements (with before/after content) and needsFix tags still go through the original Wrapper for backward compat. The downstream contract change: simple-element rendered VNode now exposes the HTML tag as `props.as` and layout fields under `props.$element.{direction, alignX, alignY, block, equalCols, extraStyles}` instead of flat `props.{tag, direction, …}`. Tests reading these read both shapes via a `getLayoutProps()` helper; production styled-components consumers see no behavior change since `as` is the styled-components canonical tag selector.
- **`$element` bundle interning (2026-Q2 follow-up to PR #344)**: every `<WrapperStyled $element={{...}}>` call site (Element fast path + Wrapper helper's 4 paths + the **Content helper's compound before/after slots**) routes through `internElementBundle()` (`packages/ui-system/elements/src/helpers/internElementBundle.ts`). Same primitive-value tuple → same object identity, which lets the styler's `elClassCache` hit and skip the resolve pipeline entirely. (Content was the one consumer originally missed — it allocated a fresh bundle per mount → guaranteed `elClassCache` miss → a full `styler.resolve` per slot per mount on the compound `beforeContent`/`afterContent` path; the wrap drops 20 compound-Element mounts from 183 `styler.resolve` to <20, bisect-locked by `packages/ui-system/elements/src/__tests__/content-intern.test.tsx`.) Bail when any value is a function (signal accessor) or a non-string object (CSSResult / css callback). LRU bound at 256 entries; oldest-first eviction. Companion change in `@pyreon/styler/styled.tsx`: the existing `($rocketstyle, $rocketstate)`-keyed `classCache` is paired with a new single-key `elClassCache: WeakMap<$element, Map<$childFix, className>>` for non-rocketstyle styled components. E2 bench (200 Buttons × 5 runs, real Chromium): wall-clock 4.80 ms → **3.60 ms** (−25% vs PR #344, **−59% vs pre-memo baseline**); per-1000-mount `styler.resolve` collapses to **0** (was 6000) because every cached path returns before the styler's CSS template runs. The Element-only probe is even cleaner: TWO same-shape Elements drop from 6 → **0** styler.resolve.

#### @pyreon/ui-core — PyreonUI (Unified Provider)

- `PyreonUI` — single provider replacing 3 separate providers (theme, mode, config)
- Props: `theme` (theme object), `mode` (`"light"` | `"dark"` | `"system"`), `inversed` (boolean, flips mode)
- `mode="system"` — auto-detects OS dark mode via `prefers-color-scheme` media query
- `useMode()` — hook returning current resolved mode as a signal (`"light"` or `"dark"`)
- `enrichTheme(theme)` — utility from `@pyreon/unistyle` that merges user theme with default breakpoints/spacing
- `init()` is preserved for custom environments — `PyreonUI` calls it internally but apps can still call `init()` directly
- **`init({ cssVariables: true })` — opt-in CSS-variables theming mode (ui-system-wide)**: PyreonUI autogenerates `--px-*` custom properties from the theme JSON, provides a var-leaf theme tree, and renders a `display: contents` wrapper carrying `data-theme` (configurable via `{ prefix, attribute }`); dark/light flip = ONE attribute write (zero re-resolution / className churn — measured + bisect-locked in rocketstyle's `css-variables-mode.browser.test.tsx`); component-level `mode(a, b)` pairs become hashed var pairs; boot-time contract (set before first render). Flag off = byte-identical classic behavior

Engine-neutral seam + Yjs engine (`/yjs`), IndexedDB persistence, cross-tab + WebSocket transport, collaborative text/lists, ephemeral presence + live cursors (`syncedAwareness`), relay server with authz (`/server`) |
| `@pyreon/a11y`        | Accessibility primitives — `announce()` screen-reader live regions (zero setup, no provider, SSR-safe), `<VisuallyHidden>`, `createA11yId` for ARIA relationships. The shared foundation other packages build on for out-of-the-box a11y |

### Zero (Full-Stack Meta-Framework)

| Package                | Description                                                                                                                                                          |
| ---------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `@pyreon/zero`         | Full-stack meta-framework: file-system routing, SSR/SSG/ISR/SPA, API routes, server actions, theme, fonts, image optimization, SEO, adapters                         |
| `@pyreon/zero-content` | Content layer for markdown-driven Pyreon sites: compile-time `.md` → Pyreon JSX, typed collections (zod), MDX components scanned from `src/mdx/`, tight zero coupling |

#### @pyreon/zero — Key Features

- Client-safe main entry: `@pyreon/zero` exports only client-safe code (components, theme, middleware). Server-only code at `@pyreon/zero/server`
- Server import stubs: importing server-only APIs from the main entry gives clear error messages instead of silent failures
- Deployment adapters: Vercel (`vercelAdapter()`), Cloudflare Pages (`cloudflareAdapter()`), Netlify Functions (`netlifyAdapter()`) — in addition to Node, Bun, static
- CSP middleware: `cspMiddleware({ directives })` with `useNonce()` for inline scripts
- Env validation: `validateEnv({ PORT: 3000, DEBUG: false, API_KEY: String })` with `schema()` for custom parsers, `publicEnv()` for client-safe subset
- Request logging: `loggerMiddleware()` with configurable format and levels
- AI integration: `aiPlugin()` — generates llms.txt, JSON-LD inference metadata, AI plugin manifest
- `useRequestLocals()` — bridge middleware locals into component tree
- **Per-route render modes / hybrid rendering (Phase 2 of the render-modes plan)**: `export const renderMode = 'ssg' | 'spa' | 'isr' | 'ssr'` on any route file (or layout — cascades to descendants) overrides the app-level `mode`, which becomes the default for undeclared routes. ONE resolver (`packages/zero/zero/src/route-modes.ts:resolveRenderModeForPath` — leaf-first matched-chain walk + layout cascade + app default) drives BOTH the build and the runtime so they can never disagree. Inside `mode: 'ssr' | 'isr'`: 'ssg' routes are prerendered at build (ssgPlugin joins the plugin array BEFORE ssrPlugin — ordering is load-bearing so prerendered files exist when adapter staging copies the client dir) and served static-first by the emitted node/bun servers via the `_pyreon-ssg-paths.json` manifest (boot-time read) + excluded from the Cloudflare worker via `_routes.json`; 'spa' routes get the CSR shell at request time (built template, placeholders blanked, GET-only; no template → SSR fallback); 'isr' routes route through a shared SWR cache handler; 'ssr' under an 'isr' app = per-route cache bypass. Inside `mode: 'ssg'`: 'spa' routes emit the shell; 'ssr'/'isr' declarations are a BUILD ERROR (`assertModesSupported` — a static deploy has no server; the error names each route + the fix). The runtime dispatch (`entry-server.ts:wirePerRouteModes`) returns the plain app-level handler when no route declares a divergent mode — the zero-change path. The hybrid SSG pass skips 404 emission + the kind-'ssg' adapter invocation (the server/ssrPlugin own those) and no-ops without an SSR sub-build when no route declares a static mode (cheap file-scan pre-check). Static-first proof in e2e: `hybrid-static.ts`'s loader bakes a timestamp; two production requests return the SAME value (`e2e/ssr-node.spec.ts`). Reference: `route-modes.ts`, `ssg-plugin.ts` (hybrid gate + partition), `adapters/{node,bun}.ts` (manifest boot-read), `adapters/cloudflare.ts` (worker excludes), probe routes `examples/ssr-showcase/src/routes/hybrid-{static,spa}.ts`.
- Locale-aware favicons: `faviconPlugin({ locales: { de: { source: "./icon-de.svg" } } })` — per-locale favicon generation. Generates the full set (`.ico`/`.svg`/16/32/apple-touch/192/512/`site.webmanifest`) from one source + auto-injects all `<head>` tags. `sharp`-backed (opt install: `bun add -D sharp`). **Missing-`sharp` is a hard `vite build` error when a `source` is configured** (dev stays a soft warning) — never silently ships a faviconless production site. Documented in `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md` → Favicons.
- OG image generation: `ogImagePlugin({ templates, locales })` — build-time OG image rendering
- Reactive favicon switching: dual light/dark PNG/ICO **and SVG** with theme-synced `media` attribute swap. **Bug class fixed — a browser-preferred static asset bypassing the reactive opt-in attribute.** Pre-fix, an SVG source emitted a single static `<link rel=icon type=image/svg+xml href=/favicon.svg>` with NO `data-favicon-theme`; browsers prefer an SVG favicon over PNG, and the theme-swap script / `initTheme()` only toggle `[data-favicon-theme]` links — so the favicon never followed the theme in any SVG-capable browser (dev or prod), silently defeating the whole feature, while the `darkSource` JSDoc documented an unimplemented `prefers-color-scheme` mechanism. Fix: when `darkSource` is set, `transformIndexHtml` + `faviconLinks` (SSR) emit two theme-aware SVG links (`/favicon-light.svg` `data-favicon-theme=light`, `/favicon-dark.svg` `data-favicon-theme=dark media="not all"`) carrying the SAME contract the PNG dual-variant uses; build emits both variant files alongside the wrapped `favicon.svg` (kept as the no-JS / direct-ref OS-`prefers-color-scheme` fallback only); dev `configureServer` serves them (locale-aware, dev-badge on the active light variant). No-dark / PNG sources unchanged. The general lesson: any asset a browser auto-prefers (SVG favicon over PNG, source-order overrides, etc.) MUST carry the reactive opt-in attribute itself, or the toggle silently can't reach it. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/favicon.ts` (`transformIndexHtml` / `faviconLinks` / `generateFaviconSet` / `configureServer`); bisect-verified `favicon-plugin-hooks.test.ts` + `favicon.test.ts`.
- Meta completion: og:image:width/height, og:video, og:audio, noIndex, ogTemplate, favicon prop on Meta component
- `<Icon>` + `createIcon` — renders a FULL loaded SVG (4th member of the Image/Link/Script family). Does NOT synthesize an `<svg>` around `<path>` children — you load a complete svg and Icon makes it container-sizable + theme-aware. Two source props: `as` (imported `./x.svg?component` → rendered DIRECTLY, no host wrapper, svg attrs forward — recommended) or `svg` (imported `./x.svg?raw` markup string → inlined via ONE unavoidable `<span>` host). Container-fill defaults (`fill="currentColor"`, `display:block;width:100%;height:100%`) spread-overridable; no fixed size (consumer wrapper sizes it). Two layers (`createIcon(source)` per-glyph factory + `Icon` one-off); intentionally NO `useIcon` hook. Exports: `Icon`, `createIcon`, `IconProps` (extends `SvgAttributes`), `SvgComponent`. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/icon.tsx`; tests `src/tests/icon.test.ts` (real-`h()` happy-dom: component + raw-string + createIcon).
- `iconsPlugin` + `createNamedIcon` — folder → strictly-typed icon set. `iconsPlugin({ dir | sets, out?, mode? })` (from `@pyreon/zero/server`) scans `*.svg` (kebab name from filename), writes a gitignored generated `icons.gen.tsx` that calls `createNamedIcon(REGISTRY)` so `keyof typeof REGISTRY` IS the typed `name` surface (autocomplete + go-to-definition, zero per-app wiring; regenerates on add/unlink in dev, idempotent write). **Named multi-set form** `iconsPlugin({ sets: { ui: { dir }, brand: { dir, mode } } })` (XOR with `dir`, throws if both/neither) emits one file with a strictly-typed component PER set under NAMESPACED names so they never clash — `ui` → `<UiIcon>` + `type UiIconName`, `brand` → `<BrandIcon>` + `type BrandIconName`; per-set binding prefixes (`ui_check` / `brand_check`) keep two sets sharing a glyph filename collision-free; `mode` is per-set. Writes a REAL file (not a virtual module) because the published `@pyreon/zero` can't `import` a plugin virtual module — same Rolldown import-ordering constraint as islands' `hydrateIslandsAuto(registry)`. Two render modes (colorful-vs-system split): `mode: 'inline'` (default — system icons; `?raw` markup inlined via `Icon`, `currentColor`-themeable, recolorable via CSS `color`) and `mode: 'image'` (colorful / brand icons; svg emitted as a static asset, rendered `<img>`, NO mutation, original colors preserved). `createNamedIcon<R>(registry, { mode? })` is the runtime half (typed by `keyof R`). **Inline mode emits TWO shapes (the tree-shaking fix): (1) per-icon PascalCase components — `export const CheckCircle = /*#__PURE__*/ createIcon(checkCircle)` (multi-set: set-namespaced `UiArrowLeft` / `BrandLogoMark`) — the PREFERRED surface; `import { CheckCircle } from './icons.gen'` drops every unused icon AND the runtime registry via standard ESM dead-code elimination. The `/*#__PURE__*/` is load-bearing — it lets the bundler drop the unused cross-package `createIcon` / `createNamedIcon` calls it can't prove pure on its own. (2) `<Icon name="…" />` — the `registry[name]` runtime lookup, kept as the escape hatch for DYNAMIC / data-driven names (`<Icon name={cmsKey} />`), which necessarily retains the whole set. `componentNameFromIconName(name)` (`check-circle` → `CheckCircle`; leading-digit → `Icon1password`) is the new exported helper. Image-mode sets stay registry-only (`createIcon` renders `?raw` markup, not an `<img>`) and image-mode generator output is byte-identical to before — minimal blast radius. The bigger byte win than per-icon SVGO minification: a real app declares far more icons than it renders, so dropping the unused ones (100% elimination) dominates shaving the used ones (~10-30%). Why tree-shaking and not async/lazy-load per icon: icons are tiny, numerous, above-the-fold and instant-by-nature — lazy-loading them emits dead chunks + adds an async paint (FOUC/CLS) + a request waterfall, the wrong tradeoff for this asset class; async is the right tool only for an unbounded data-driven set, which is exactly what the `<Icon name={…}>` registry escape hatch serves.** Exports: `iconsPlugin`, `iconNameFromFile`, `scanIconDir`, `generateIconSetSource`, `componentNameFromIconName`, `componentNameFromSetKey`, `IconsPluginConfig` (server entry); `createNamedIcon`, `createIcon`, `Icon`, `IconMode`, `NamedIconProps` (client entry). Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/icons-plugin.ts` + `icon.tsx:createIcon`/`createNamedIcon`; tests `src/tests/icons-plugin.test.ts` (pure scanner/generator + per-icon export shape) + `icons-treeshake.test.ts` (real Vite/Rolldown build proves an unused icon's bytes are dropped — bisect-verified via an opaque-side-effect `@pyreon/zero` stub so the `/*#__PURE__*/` annotation, not the bundler's purity guesswork, is what's exercised) + `icon.test.ts` (createIcon/createNamedIcon real-`h()`, both modes). **NOT YET: per-icon tree-shakeable exports for `mode: 'image'` (needs an image-icon factory — `createIcon` renders `?raw` markup, not `<img>`) + SVGO `?optimize` minification for SVG (excluded from the imagePlugin optimize pipeline; SVGO is not a dep) + monorepo package-sourced sets + copy-to-public — explicit follow-ups.**
- **Image optimization — bi-modal `<Image>` + `createImageRegistry` + `<NoOptimize>` (PRs #1353/#1357/#1363).** `<Image src={…}>` is **bi-modal**: `src` accepts a `?optimize` `ProcessedImage` descriptor (Shape A — width/height/srcset/formats/placeholder inferred, supply only display props) OR a runtime string URL (Shape B — `width`+`height` REQUIRED at the type level so a remote/signal-driven URL can't silently cause CLS). The `optimize?: boolean` prop opts out (`false` → bare `<img>`, bypass pipeline) or forces optimization back ON inside an outer `<NoOptimize>` boundary (`true`). `<OptimizedImage source={descriptor} alt>` is the one-prop form (whole descriptor as a single prop — guards against the #1 real-world CLS cause, pulling just `hero.src` onto a raw `<img>`; the opt-in lint rule `pyreon/no-discarded-optimize-fields` flags that shape). `<NoOptimize>` / `useNoOptimize(): boolean` is a context-based subtree opt-out boundary — every `<Image>` inside renders a bare `<img>` unless it sets `optimize` to opt back in. `createImageRegistry(map)` builds a typed name→descriptor registry (autocomplete over imported assets). All built on `createImage(Base)` so consumers layer rocketstyle / custom wrappers without losing the pipeline. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/{image.tsx,image-registry.ts,no-optimize.tsx}`; docs `docs/src/content/docs/images-and-fonts.md`.
- **Resource-hint primitives — `usePreconnect` / `useDnsPrefetch` / `usePreload` (PR #1366).** Three typed `useHead` wrappers emitting `<link rel="preconnect|dns-prefetch|preload">`. `usePreconnect(origin, { credentials? })` opens DNS+TCP+TLS early (default `crossorigin="anonymous"`; `credentials: true` → `use-credentials`) — reserve for the 1-3 most-critical external origins. `useDnsPrefetch(origin)` is the cheaper DNS-only hint for likely-but-uncertain origins (pair both for old+modern browser coverage). `usePreload(href, { as, type?, crossorigin?, media?, imagesrcset?, imagesizes?, fetchpriority? })` is the typed critical-resource fetch hint — `as` is REQUIRED (the preload scanner ignores `<link rel=preload>` without it); deduped by `href` via `@pyreon/head`. Three separate helpers (not one mega-hook) because each has distinct typed semantics — preconnect always needs crossorigin, preload always needs `as`. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/use-resource-hints.ts`; docs `docs/src/content/docs/images-and-fonts.md` → Resource Hints.
- **Font preload + `?font` import — `usePreloadFont` / `fontImportPlugin` / `fontPlugin` (PRs #1359/#1360).** `usePreloadFont(href, opts?)` emits `<link rel=preload as=font crossorigin>` for a critical font, auto-inferring the MIME `type` from the extension via `inferFontMimeType(href)` (woff2/woff/ttf/otf). The `?font` Vite import (`fontImportPlugin`) turns `import Inter from './Inter.woff2?font'` into an auto-emitted `@font-face` + a hashed-URL `FontDescriptor` — one import wires BOTH the face declaration and the content-hashed asset URL. `fontPlugin` is the build-time companion; both auto-wire via `zero({ font })`. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/{use-preload-font.ts,font-plugin.ts,font-import-plugin.ts}`; docs `docs/src/content/docs/images-and-fonts.md`.
- **`zero({ image, font })` auto-wiring (PR #1356).** `imagePlugin` / `fontPlugin` are appended to the Vite plugin chain automatically when `zero({ image: {...}, font: {...} })` is configured — no separate `plugins: [imagePlugin(), fontPlugin()]` wiring needed.
- **`fontPlugin({ subsets })` — self-hosted Google Font subset scoping (opt-in).** By default self-hosting downloads EVERY subset Google returns (Ubuntu = 6: latin/latin-ext/cyrillic/cyrillic-ext/greek/greek-ext, each a separate `@font-face` + woff2), so a Latin-only site ships ~all of them. `subsets: ['latin','latin-ext']` narrows the emitted set (~−40% font weight on the example `Inter:wght@400;500;600;700;800` config). **Zero runtime change** — the browser already skips unrequested subsets via `unicode-range`; the win is build output / deploy size / static-host quota. **Mechanism (load-bearing): css2 IGNORES `&subset=`** (verified — `&subset=latin` still returns all 6), so the fix FILTERS the returned CSS by its per-subset comment labels (`filterCssBySubsets`, exported from `@pyreon/zero/font`) BEFORE `extractFontUrls` — one spot governs downloads + emitted assets + inlined CSS. **Opt-in** (omit = keep all; a `['latin']` default would silently break Cyrillic/Greek/Vietnamese pages); **self-host only** (no effect with `selfHost:false` / dev); **fail-safe** (an allowlist matching nothing, or a CSS with no labels, keeps all subsets — never a fontless build). The subset allowlist is folded into the `node_modules/.cache/zero-fonts` cache key so two configs differing only in `subsets` can't collide on a stale entry. **Companion fix (same PR): correct preload subset.** `collectGoogleFontTags` previously preloaded `selfHostedFontFiles.slice(0, familyCount)` = the FIRST file, which is css2's `cyrillic-ext` block (Google returns subsets cyrillic-ext→…→latin) — so a Latin site preloaded a Cyrillic woff2 AND failed to preload the latin one it actually renders.
