Now `pickPreloadHrefs(selfHostedCSS, primary, limit)` picks the PRIMARY subset's file (`subsets?.[0] ?? 'latin'`), capped at the same one-per-family budget, falling back to the first files only if the primary is absent. Multi-family one-per-family preload precision is still a separate pre-existing concern (untouched). **ReDoS-safe parsing:** `filterCssBySubsets` + `pickPreloadHrefs` share `splitSubsetBlocks`, a linear label-INDEX scan (`/\/\*\s*([\w-]+)\s*\*\//g` + slice between offsets) — NOT a `lazy-body + look-ahead` regex, which CodeQL flags as polynomial-ReDoS on untrusted fetched CSS. `fontCacheKey(cssUrl, subsets)` is the exported cache-key helper. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/font.ts:filterCssBySubsets` + `selfHostFonts`.
- **SSG per-route `<link rel=modulepreload>` — islands-safe (PR #1358, closes #1355).** Each prerendered route's HTML gets `<link rel=modulepreload>` for its OWN route-chunk graph, derived from the Vite manifest's `imports` (STATIC dependencies only) — NEVER `dynamicImports`, so island / lazy chunks stay deferred and the islands zero-JS contract holds. The route module is resolved via `record.component._hmrId` (the lazy wrapper carries `_hmrId`, not the record), keyed `relative(root, _hmrId)` against the manifest; the route's own `index.html` entry is subtracted from the import delta. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts`.
- **Adapter immutable-cache scoping to `<base><assetsDir>` (PR #1361).** Deploy adapters scope their 1-year `immutable` cache rule to the resolved `build.assetsDir` at the served `base` (new `assetUrlPrefix(base, assetsDir)` helper + `AdapterBuildOptions.assetsDir` threaded from `configResolved`), not a hardcoded `/assets/` — so a custom `assetsDir` (`build: { assetsDir: 'static' }`) or a subpath deploy (`zero({ base: '/blog/' })`) keeps long-cache on its hashed chunks. CDN adapters (vercel `config.json` / netlify `netlify.toml` / cloudflare `_headers`) scope `<base><assetsDir>/*`; node/bun stay `assetsDir`-only (NO base — their self-hosted handler serves by raw `url.pathname` with no base-stripping, so subpath isn't supported there regardless). Default `/` + `'assets'` → `/assets/` (no behavior change for the common case). The node/bun cache check was ALSO fixed to gate on `url.pathname.startsWith('/<assetsDir>/')` not file extension (PR #1352 — extension-based caching immutable-poisoned non-hashed root files like `/app.js`). Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/*`.

## PMTC Multi-Target Architecture

The Pyreon Multi-Target Compiler (PMTC) emits SwiftUI + Compose from one `.tsx` source. **Scope the "100%" precisely** (it has been over-read): what is "done" is the **emit vocabulary** — all 15 canonical primitives map to both targets (#888 K-FINAL). It does NOT mean "all packages work on native," "device-proven," or "production-ready." Three independent reality-checks (2026-06 audit) confirm the honest picture: (a) **PMTC compiles a narrow, declarative TS subset and fails SILENTLY outside it** — local object/array literals, destructuring, `Map`/`Set`, `for`/`while`/`switch`/`try`, template literals (→`""`), optional chaining (→`""`), generics, `interface`/`enum`/`class` decls, and fractional math on iOS (`signal<number>(9.99)`→`var x: Int = 9.99`) are dropped/mis-emitted, most with NO warning; the per-PR gate is `swiftc -parse` (syntax-only, NOT typecheck) + `kotlinc`-against-stubs, which structurally cannot catch this (proven by the repo's own `rx-full.tsx` fixture failing real `swiftc -typecheck` while passing the `-parse` gate). (b) **Device proof is advisory** (`native-device.yml` gates zero PRs; currently green but below its 14-night promotion bar; strong for Tasks/Counter/Router, launch-only for TodoMVC, absent for native-analytics). (c) **The rich web packages (`@pyreon/flow`/`charts`/`code`/`dnd`/`document`/`query`/`table`/`virtual` + the whole CSS-in-JS ui-system stack) are web-only by architecture** — PMTC compiles your source, not npm libraries, so canvas/DOM/vendor-bound packages have no native path. Native reach = reactive logic + the canonical primitives + the ServiceBackend-ported hooks + the logic packages with Swift/Kotlin runtime ports (store/machine/state-tree/i18n/form/permissions/storage/router). Full honest capability matrix + TS-surface ceiling: `docs/src/content/docs/multiplatform.md` → "What runs on native". The shared-code story above the compiler lives in a **four-layer model**:

```text
Layer 4: <NativeIOS> / <NativeAndroid> / <Web> escape hatches (per-platform, opt-in)
Layer 3b: @pyreon/elements (web-only rich primitives, rocketstyle/styler-coupled)
Layer 3a: @pyreon/primitives (canonical multi-platform primitives — 15 of them)
Layer 2: useStorage / useRouter / useFetch / usePermissions (ServiceBackend pattern)
Layer 1: Custom hooks (useDebounce, useToggle, ...) — pure-logic, 100% shared
Layer 0: signal() / computed() / effect() — runs identically; PMTC maps to @State / mutableStateOf
```

**Canonical multi-platform primitives** (Layer 3a, `@pyreon/primitives`): **15 semantic primitives** — `Stack`, `Inline`, `Layer`, `Scroll`, `Spacer`, `Text`, `Heading`, `Image`, `Icon`, `Button`, `Press`, `Link`, `Field`, `Toggle`, `Modal` — designed for cross-platform from scratch. `<Stack>` (NOT `<View>` or `<VStack>`), `<Inline>`, `<Press>`, `<Field>`, etc. Compiles to: DOM (web) / SwiftUI primitives (iOS) / Compose primitives (Android). One canonical name per concept (`onPress` everywhere, not `onClick` vs `action:`). Tokens-first styling (`padding={4}` / `gap="md"`). No responsive props or animations in v1 — apps that need responsive web use `@pyreon/elements` directly. Source of truth: `packages/native/compiler/src/canonical-primitives.ts` `SWIFT_NAMES` + `KOTLIN_NAMES` (both maps carry exactly 15 entries).

**Cross-platform a11y vocabulary** (`AccessibilityProps` in `packages/core/primitives/src/types/shared.ts`, mixed into every primitive via `HtmlPassthroughProps extends AccessibilityProps`): platform-NEUTRAL a11y props that lower per-target — `accessibilityLabel` → web `aria-label` / iOS `.accessibilityLabel` / Android `semantics{contentDescription}`; `accessibilityHidden` → web `aria-hidden="true"` / iOS `.accessibilityHidden` / Android `semantics{invisibleToUser}`. Prefer these over raw `aria-*` (web-only) so the same component is accessible on every target. **Web lowering ships** (`web/passthrough.ts:collectPassthroughAttrs` maps the neutral props to aria-*; a raw `aria-label`/`aria-hidden` wins as the explicit web override; `accessibilityHidden` emits the STRING `"true"`, not presence-only `""`). **The iOS/Android PMTC emit is a tracked follow-up** — until it lands, native targets render without the a11y attribute (graceful degradation, no crash). Regression-locked by the "Cross-platform a11y vocabulary" describe block in `packages/core/primitives/src/tests/primitives.test.tsx` (Stack + Button mount → aria-label/aria-hidden; raw-aria-wins; hidden-false-omitted; bisect-verified).

**Critical architectural split**: `@pyreon/elements` stays web-only-rich (rocketstyle/styler-coupled); `@pyreon/primitives` is the NEW multi-platform-minimal layer. Different architectural tiers. No naming collision because imports are explicit.

**Per-platform import resolution**: `import { Stack } from '@pyreon/primitives'` runs the real implementation on web (renders DOM); on iOS/Android the PMTC compiler INTERCEPTS the JSX and emits native code BEFORE the runtime is reached — the import is type-anchor-only on native targets.

**Existing Layer-2 pattern**: `@pyreon/storage`'s `StorageBackend` interface + `createStorage(backend)` factory is the blueprint every Layer-2 service follows. `@pyreon/native-runtime-{swift,kotlin}` ship `@PyreonAppStorage` (Swift property wrapper) + `rememberPyreonStorage` (Compose Composable) — same API parity, different runtime impl. Compiler emits `useStorage<T>` calls as these runtime helpers via Phase 2.5 (#891) — collapsed 14-line inline Codable bridge to one-line property-wrapper call.

**Native data + services hooks** (runtime port + compiler emit, both targets): `useForm` v2 (validated forms — validators as native closures, runtime Field bindings, submit gating; device-proven by the tasks login's error-path smoke), `useFetch` (emit complete; device-proven end-to-end — see lifecycle below), `usePermissions`, `useOnline`, `useClipboard`, plus `useColorScheme` (#1103 — emit-only; SwiftUI's `@Environment(\.colorScheme)` and Compose's `isSystemInDarkTheme()` provide the platform primitive). `useValidation` planned. Runtime files live at `packages/native/runtime-{swift,kotlin}/`. **Phase 5 (#1689) — seven more hooks emit** (runtime containers shipped this arc; emit added): `useAuth<User>` → `PyreonAuth<User>`, `useDatabase` → `PyreonDatabase`, `useGeolocation` → `PyreonGeolocation`, `useMap` → `PyreonMapState`, `useWebSocket('wss://…')` → `PyreonWebSocket` (string-literal URL), `usePush` → `PyreonPushNotifications`, `usePayments` → `PyreonPayments`. Same reactive-container template as `useOnline`/`usePermissions` (Swift `@State` + bare `@Observable` reads; Kotlin `remember {}` + `.value` on `MutableState` fields, bare on `Bool` getters/methods). Compile-rung proof: an archetype finance+realtime+maps component using all seven emits typecheck-clean Swift (`swiftc`) AND Kotlin (`kotlinc`) from one `.tsx` (`native-data-hooks.test.ts`). **Two honest limits:** (1) **lifecycle auto-start is NOT emitted** — `geolocation.start()`/`websocket.connect()`/`push.start()` on mount don't auto-fire (web hooks do); call `.start()`/`.connect()` from an effect/host today. Full auto-start is **blocked on the real Kotlin transport backends** (the Kotlin containers take an app-injected source the compiler can't synthesize), so it lands with that Android-CI backend work. (2) **`useSecureStorage` is deferred** (warns + drops) — the Kotlin secret store needs an app-injected `EncryptedSharedPreferences` backend. Runtime behavior remains compile-verified, not device-proven (the nightly device gate + example apps are the runtime-proof layer).

**Subset-widening (compile-rung) — two follow-ups closing the most pervasive silent-drop classes:** (1) **plain component-body value-consts (#1691)** — `const label = 'Total: '` / `const doubled = base() * 2` / `const sum = 5 + 3` used to be SILENTLY DROPPED (`parse.ts` captured only call/arrow inits → `if (init.type !== 'CallExpression') return null`); they now emit as a body-local `let` (Swift, injected at the top of the `body` ViewBuilder so it can read `@State`) / `val` (Kotlin composable body), captures-once like a JS `const`. (2) **hook-result destructure** — `const { data, isPending } = useFetch(url)` (THE idiomatic data-fetch shape) used to warn-drop; it now **lowers** to a synthetic single-binding container `const __pyHookN = useFetch(url)` (parsed via the SAME single-binding path, by recursion) + one field alias per key consumed in `parseExpr`'s Identifier case (mirroring `storeAliases`), so each local rewrites to `__pyHookN.<field>` — **byte-identical native output to the supported single-binding form** on both targets, user keeps the call form (`data()` accessor vs `isPending` plain). Faithful + non-regressing by construction: a container-less hook (`useSecureStorage` warns+drops → recurses to null) or a rest/nested pattern falls through to the same warn-drop as before; `useParams` keeps its own per-key lowering; `useLoaderData` destructure stays warn-drop (opaque `T`). Both are pure parse-layer, zero emit-shape change, verified at the emit-shape + real `swiftc`/`kotlinc` rung (`native-value-const.test.ts`, `native-hook-destructure.test.ts`). These widen the supported-TS subset toward "one `.tsx` → any app" — local consts + hook destructure appear in essentially every real component. The next-frontier compile-rung gaps (param destructure, multi-statement handler control-flow, anonymous-object→struct, JSX spread, template literals) are tracked; the structural ceiling (arbitrary async, device-SDK map/chart rendering, web-coupled libs) stays `<Web>`/`<NativeIOS>`/`<NativeAndroid>` escape-hatch territory by design, NOT roadmapped as "coming soon."

**Native lifecycle — real `<Suspense>` / `<ErrorBoundary>` semantics (Phase 2, device-proven).** Both compile to an INLINE conditional read in the component body — Swift `Group { if <pending/errored> { fallback } else { children } }`, Kotlin `if (<pending/errored>) { ... } else { ... }` — where the condition ORs every `useFetch` container's `.isPending` (Suspense) / `.error != nil` (ErrorBoundary) in that component. Two non-obvious requirements both surfaced ON A REAL SIMULATOR (compile-only `swiftc -typecheck` / `kotlinc` cannot catch either):
1. **Inline read, not arg-passing.** The `@Observable` read MUST be in the component's own `body` so SwiftUI Observation / Compose recomposition tracks it. The earlier `PyreonSuspenseWrapper`/`PyreonErrorBoundaryWrapper` CHILD-STRUCT approach (passing `isLoading`/`hasError` as a value/closure arg to a wrapper) does NOT establish tracking — the child reads its own stored copy, not the `@Observable`. Those wrapper structs were deleted; the emit is inline.
2. **Swift `.task` needs a STABLE-identity host.** A fetch-bearing component appends a mount-time `.task { begin → resolve|reject }`. SwiftUI ties a `.task`'s lifetime to its host VIEW IDENTITY; attached to a transparent `Group { if isPending … }`, SwiftUI redistributes the modifier onto the if/else BRANCH, so each loading/error flip changes the branch identity and CANCELS+RESTARTS the task → the fetch perpetually thrashes and never settles (the boundary renders NOTHING — not even its fallback). Fix: `emitSwiftComponent` wraps any fetch-bearing component's body in a concrete `ZStack` so `.task` attaches to a stable host that fires once on appear. **Kotlin needs no equivalent** — its fetch harness is a `LaunchedEffect(Unit)` SIBLING keyed by the stable `Unit`, which runs once and is not cancelled by recomposition. Compiler regression specs in `fetch-computed-shapes.test.ts` (`Swift `.task` stable-host wrap (device-found)`) lock the ZStack contract; the `examples/native-tasks-ios` `lifecycle-page` XCUITest (good-fetch `lc-quote` + failed-fetch `lc-error` both render) is the device proof. Reference: `packages/native/compiler/src/{emit-swift,emit-kotlin}.ts:emitSwift/KotlinSuspense + emitSwift/KotlinErrorBoundary` + the `_hasFetchDecl` ZStack branch in `emitSwiftComponent`.

**Cross-platform layout gotcha — `<Inline>` is a NON-WRAPPING Row on Android (overflows); SwiftUI HStack shrinks (device-found, ROOT-CAUSED on a local emulator).** The native lifecycle device-proof initially failed ONLY on Android: after a 6th button (`tasks-lifecycle`) was added to the TasksPage action-button `<Inline>`, the Android instrumented test's `tasks-logout → /login` step timed out (`login-page` never rendered). It LOOKED like "the lifecycle screen breaks navigation," but bisecting on a real Android emulator (the breakthrough — local Android SDK + AVD, ~20s/run) isolated it to the **button, not the lifecycle**: removing just the `tasks-lifecycle` button (keeping the /lifecycle route + screen + fetches) made it PASS. **Mechanism:** `<Inline>` lowers to a Compose `Row`, which does NOT wrap — 6 buttons overflow the phone width and push the last one (`tasks-logout`) OFF-SCREEN, so Compose `performClick` injects a touch at off-screen coordinates, logout never fires, login never appears. **iOS hid it** because SwiftUI `HStack` shrinks children to fit, keeping every button on-screen + tappable. **Fix:** the example's action buttons stack vertically (`<Stack>`) — full-width + reachable on both targets (real-emulator-proven: the full vocab→lifecycle→`lc-error`→logout→login flow now passes on Android). **The lifecycle itself was NEVER the bug — it is device-proven on BOTH iOS and Android.** **General rule for multi-platform layouts:** a horizontal group of N children that fits on iOS (HStack auto-shrinks) can overflow + clip the last ones on Android (Row no-wrap) — keep horizontal groups few + narrow, or stack vertically; treat "tap target works on iOS but the Android tap times out" as a Row-overflow suspect FIRST. Reference: `examples/native-tasks/src/TasksApp.tsx` TasksPage action buttons (`<Stack>` + the inline comment); the local-emulator bisect (#1539-app PASS / 6-button FAIL / button-removed PASS).

**Native routing runtime** (both targets, `packages/native/router-{swift,kotlin}/`): `PyreonRouter` + `RouterProvider` + `RouterView` + `Link` + hooks (`useNavigate`, `useParams`, `useLoaderData`). Global guards `beforeEach` / `afterEach` (#1108), throw-redirect via `router.redirect()` (#1109, re-entry-safe via `_inGuard`). Per-route `beforeEnter`, nested-routes (`RouteRecord.children`), and per-route `loader` auto-emit have all landed. Loader auto-emit (v1): a `loader: () => <expr>` wraps the route's component in a runtime `PyreonRouteLoader` host (`packages/native/router-{swift,kotlin}/.../RouteLoader.{swift,kt}`) whose `.task` (SwiftUI) / `LaunchedEffect` (Compose) fires the loader ONCE on appear and stores the result via `router.setLoaderData(<active path>, …)`, where the already-shipped `useLoaderData<T>()` reads it — keyed by the runtime active path (the `navigationDestination` `path` closure var on Swift / `currentPath` on Kotlin) so it matches BOTH literal and `:param` routes; the home route keys by its literal path (= `currentPath` at launch); guarded by `loaderData[path] == nil` so re-renders never re-run. v1 captures only ZERO-PARAM, EXPRESSION-body loaders (signal/store reads + sync expressions, e.g. `() => globalCache()`); a param-using (`(ctx) => …`), block-body, or truly-async loader WARNS and emits unloaded (the component still renders). Compiler pieces: `RouteIR.loader` + `parseRouteArray` extraction + `wrapLoader` (Swift `navigationDestination` + `RouterProvider` home) / `loaderWrap` (Kotlin `when`-dispatch) + the `PyreonRouteLoader` kotlin-stub; `.task` host is the route's concrete component view (stable identity — no fetch-arc ZStack concern), Kotlin `LaunchedEffect(path)` runs once. `ctx.params` threading + async-loader decode (the `useFetch<T>` territory) are the next arc (see [.claude/audits/native-readiness-2026-06-02.md](.claude/audits/native-readiness-2026-06-02.md) Phase A roadmap).

**Implementation roadmap** (originally scoped as 10 PRs across 5 phases): Phase A (foundation — primitives package + canonical web DOM runtimes for all 15) ✅ Done; Phase B (PMTC emit for iOS + Android — extend `canonical-primitives.ts` mapping table) ✅ both targets all 15 primitives; Phase C (`@pyreon/native-router-{swift,kotlin}` runtimes) ✅ core navigation + global guards shipped, per-route guards / nested routes / typed `useParams<T>` open; Phase D (web target for PMTC + cross-platform example dir) ✅ Done; Phase E (TodoMVC migration to canonical vocab — `<VStack>` → `<Stack>`) ✅ Done. End-user docs: `docs/src/content/docs/multiplatform.md`. Post-Phase-E follow-ups (router parity, real-device CI promotion, supported-TS-surface enumeration, real-app showcase, asset pipeline) are tracked in the readiness-audit roadmap above — current overall score 66/100, demo-quality, not production-ready.

**Migration is additive** — existing `<VStack>` / `<HStack>` / `<TextField>` in PMTC source continue to work via current per-target emit. New canonical vocab ships alongside. Deprecation warnings on SwiftUI-flavored tags land AFTER Phase E migration is proven on TodoMVC. Removal in a major-version bump LATER.

## Fundamentals — Key Technical Details

### @pyreon/store

- `defineStore(id, setup)` — composition stores, singleton by ID, returns `StoreApi<T>`
- `StoreApi<T>`: `.store` (user state/actions), `.id`, `.state` (snapshot), `patch()`, `subscribe()`, `onAction()`, `reset()`, `dispose()`
- Auto-classifies setup returns: signals → state tracking, functions → wrapped actions
- `addStorePlugin(plugin)`, `setStoreRegistryProvider()` for SSR, `resetStore(id)` / `resetAllStores()`

### @pyreon/state-tree

- `model({ state })` (plain) or `model({ schema, initial?, onValidationError? })` (schema-driven) — chainable builder; `.views(f)` / `.actions(f)` accumulate onto a live `self` proxy (each layer sees prior ones); then `.create(initial?)` for an instance or `.asHook(id)` for a singleton. The single-config `model({ state, views, actions })` form was REMOVED — chain instead.
- **Schema mode is validation-driven AND strictly typed from the schema.** Pass the schema DIRECTLY — `@pyreon/validate`'s `s.object(...)`, a raw `z.object(...)`, valibot, arktype, or any [Standard Schema](https://standardschema.dev) validator — and the field types flow through end-to-end (`self.name()` is `string`, not `unknown`); no `@pyreon/validation` adapter wrapper needed. The inference reads the output type out of the schema's `~standard.validate` return (`types.ts:InferSchemaState`), so it works even when the optional `~standard.types` slot is absent (which it is on `@pyreon/validate`); the `@pyreon/validation` `zodSchema()` adapter's `_infer` path still matches first. `@pyreon/validation`'s `extractParseFn` drives runtime validation for raw schemas (via `isStandardSchema` → `wrapStandardSchema`). Schema mode installs five BARE-name mutation helpers on the instance + `self` — `set` / `patch` / `deepPatch` / `update` / `reset` — each validating the merged result through the schema before writing signals (a schema field colliding with a helper name throws at `.create()`); direct signal writes (`self.field.set(v)`) bypass validation (documented escape hatch).
- `ModelDefinition.create(initial?)` / `.asHook(id)` — instances or singleton hooks
- `.lifecycle(self => ({ afterCreate?, beforeDestroy? }))` — chainable instance lifecycle. `afterCreate` runs once at the END of `.create()` (after every view/action layer — `self` fully built; bottom-up for nested field-models); `beforeDestroy` runs on `destroy(instance)`. Only those two keys are honored (`.lifecycle()` throws on any other — typo guard).
- `destroy(instance)` / `isAlive(instance)` — tear down (run `beforeDestroy`, recurse into field-nested children, clear patch listeners + middleware, mark dead; idempotent) / liveness. **`destroy` tears down SUBSCRIPTIONS + runs cleanup — it does NOT free memory** (Pyreon signals have no per-signal dispose; GC reclaims once you drop refs). After `destroy`, actions + the schema mutation helpers dev-warn and no-op; direct signal writes (`self.field.set`) stay UNguarded (escape hatch). NO "drop from devtools registry" — devtools keys by user-name (no reverse map; the WeakRef registry self-cleans on GC).
- `clone(instance)` / `getType(instance)` — structural deep copy (snapshot → `def.create()`, independent signals/listeners/lifecycle; schema mode re-validates) / the producing `ModelDefinition` back-ref. Both rely on a `meta.definition` back-ref set at `.create()` time.
- `.volatile(self => ({...}))` — signal-backed TRANSIENT state (in-flight flags, drag/hover UI state, live refs like websockets/timers). Reactive (`self.x()` / `self.x.set()`, strictly typed via a 5th `TVolatile` generic on `ModelDefinition`/`ModelInstance`) but PLAIN signals (not `trackedSignal`) → emit no patches, absent from `meta.stateKeys` → excluded from `getSnapshot`/`applySnapshot`/`onPatch`/`onSnapshot`. Reserved-name-checked against state/helpers/views/actions/other-volatile. Runs after schema helpers, before views/actions (so views/actions read it via `self`).
- `onSnapshot(instance, cb)` — MICROTASK-COALESCED snapshot subscription (all writes in one sync burst → ONE emit on the next microtask; MST-like async). Does NOT fire on subscribe; volatile changes don't fire it. Implemented via the patch-write hook + a `meta.scheduleSnapshotNotify` coalescer (a `snapPending` flag dedups the microtask), NOT an `effect()` — so it never fires-on-create and never depends on `getSnapshot`'s untracked `.peek()` reads (the broken-`effect()` design pass-2 rejected). `meta.snapshotListeners` is cleared by `destroy`; the `trackedSignal` write-gate fires when EITHER patch or snapshot listeners exist.
- `onAction(instance, cb)` — observe-only action subscription (name/args/path before the call); sugar over `addMiddleware` (observe then `next`). Cannot block/alter — use `addMiddleware` to intercept.
- `getSnapshot(instance)` / `applySnapshot(instance, snapshot)` — typed recursive serialization (reads via `.peek()`; nested field-models recurse). **In schema mode `applySnapshot` re-validates**: it routes the (partial) snapshot through the schema `patch` helper so a malformed snapshot is REJECTED (the schema is the source of truth) — closing the integrity hole where a raw write bypassed validation. Plain mode keeps the direct-write + recurse path. Both leave snapshot-absent keys unchanged.
- `onPatch(instance, listener)` / `applyPatch(instance, patch|patches)` — JSON patch record/replay. Patches are `replace`-only (one signal per field; an array/object field emits a whole-value `replace`, not granular add/remove). Nested patches are prefixed (`/profile/name`).
- `addMiddleware(instance, fn)` — action interception chain (sync + async; `await next(call)`). The action runner also gates on liveness (no-op after `destroy`).
- `getParent(node)` / `getRoot(node)` / `getPath(node)` / `isRoot(node)` / `hasParent(node)` — tree traversal. A node gets a tree `parent` when written into another model's state — as a field value, an ARRAY element, or a plain-object value — because parent tracking runs on the initial value AND every tracked-signal write (the always-on `afterSet` hook in `trackedSignal`, NOT listener-gated). So array-held children (the headline `todos: Todo[]` shape) ARE tracked, not just field-nested — the general solution (scan written arrays/objects one container level deep) resolves the "field-nested-only = false parity" concern. `getPath` carries field keys not array indices in v1; a detached (array-removed) node keeps its last parent until GC (v1 limitation). `meta.parent`/`meta.parentKey` hold the link; `tree.ts:scanForChildren` is the scanner.
- `identifier()` / `reference(Type)` / `resolveIdentifier(root, Type, id)` — normalized references (closes #1751). `identifier()` is a plain-mode field MARKER (or `model({ schema, identifier: 'id' })` in schema mode) declaring which field is the node's id; `model()` records it on the definition as `_identifierKey` (plain-mode replaces the marker with its default at definition time). `reference(Type)` is a plain-mode field that STORES the target's id but RESOLVES to the live node on read — built as a resolving accessor (`self.author()` → node, `.set(node|id)`, `.id()`, `.setId()`, `.peek()`), tracked in `meta.referenceKeys` (its backing id-signal), NOT a `trackedSignal`; `getSnapshot`/`applySnapshot` serialize/restore the raw id via that map; `StateSignals`/`Snapshot` types special-case `ReferenceField` (instance member is the accessor, snapshot value is `string|number`). `resolveIdentifier` walks `root`'s subtree (`references.ts:walkInstances`, depth-first cycle-safe, reads owned state, SKIPS reference keys so it never follows a reference) for a node whose `definition === Type` and id-field equals `id` — O(n) per resolve (a root id-index is the documented future optimization). Resolution is via `getRoot(node)`, so the referencing node + target must share a root. Throws if the target type has no identifier. `reference()` is plain-mode (the marker lives in `state`); the TARGET can be schema-mode (via `identifier` config).
- Nested models compose for tree-shaped state in PLAIN mode (a `state` field whose value is another `ModelDefinition`); schema mode is flat (a schema can't carry a `ModelDefinition`). `/devtools` subpath export = WeakRef registry of live instances.

### @pyreon/form

- `useForm({ initialValues, onSubmit, validators?, schema?, validateOn?, debounceMs? })` — reactive form state (legacy API)
- `field(name, defaultValue, validator?)` — composable field definition carrying name as literal type. `useForm({ fields: [email, password], onSubmit })` infers `FormState<{ email: string; password: string }>` from the array
- `useField('name')` — context-based overload, reads form from nearest `<Form>` / `<FormProvider>`. Accepts generic: `useField<string>('email')`. Also: `useField(form, name)` (explicit form)
- `<Form of={form}>` — renders `<form>` + `FormProvider`, binds `onSubmit`. Children use `useField('name')` without prop drilling
- `<Submit>` — auto-disables during submission
- `useFieldArray(initial?)` — dynamic array fields with stable keys. Full mutation surface: `append` / `prepend` / `insert` / `remove` / `update` / `move` / `swap` / `replace`. Always render with `<For each={items()} by={i => i.key}>` — `.key` is a monotonic number assigned at insert time, not the array index
- `useWatch(form, name?)` — typed overloads: single field → `Signal<T>`, multiple fields → tuple of signals, no args → `Computed<TValues>`
- `useFormState(form, selector?)` — computed form-level summary (`isValid`, `isDirty`, `isSubmitting`, `isValidating`, `submitCount`, `isSubmitted`, `isSubmitSuccessful`, `errors`). Selector narrows the tracked subset so a button gated on `canSubmit` doesn't re-render when `submitCount` changes
- **react-hook-form-parity accessors on `FormState`** (all strictly typed against `keyof TValues`): `trigger(name?)` validates a field / subset / (no arg) the whole form on demand, immediately (bypasses `debounceMs`), returning the validated set's validity; `getValues(name?)` reads one value or all; `dirtyFields()` / `touchedFields()` return the changed / visited fields as `Partial<Record<keyof TValues, boolean>>` records (reactive); `getFieldState(name)` returns a field's live `FieldState` (same object as `fields[name]`); `isSubmitted` (`Accessor<boolean>`, `submitCount > 0`) and `isSubmitSuccessful` (`Signal<boolean>`, true only after a submit whose `onSubmit` ran without validation failure/throw; cleared by `reset()`). **Known gap (deliberate, not yet built): nested/deep typed field paths** (`user.address.city`) — `TValues` keys are FLAT; the composable `field()` + flat model is the current design. RHF/TanStack-style deep paths are a tracked future effort.
- **Auto-wired field accessibility (zero-config ARIA)**: `register(field)` returns — beside `value`/`onInput`/`onBlur` — a stable auto-generated `id`, reactive `aria-invalid` (`'true'` while errored, attribute REMOVED when valid — not `aria-invalid=""`), and reactive `aria-describedby` (→ the error element while errored, removed when valid so nothing dangles). New `errorProps(field)` (`{ id, role: 'alert' }`) and `labelProps(field)` (`{ for }`) — on BOTH `useForm` and `useField` (field-scoped, no arg) — return ids that AGREE with the input, so `<label {...labelProps('email')}>` + `<input {...register('email')}>` + `<span {...errorProps('email')}>{err}</span>` gives full label↔control + input↔error association + an announced error with NO hand-threaded ids, all derived from the existing `error` signal and reactive IN PLACE (0 re-renders). This makes the most common form-a11y mistake the zero-effort path and resolves the label↔control association an AST lint rule structurally can't (the deferred `control-needs-label` "high-risk cliff") at the runtime layer where the ids ARE knowable. Rides the proven function-valued-prop → `applyProp` `renderEffect`-wrap path (same as `disabled`/`readOnly`); needs no new package. `aria-required` is NOT auto-wired (the form has no per-field `required` concept — deferred). Companion `@pyreon/core` change: the JSX `aria-invalid` + `aria-describedby` attribute types now also accept the reactive accessor form (`() => …`), matching `aria-required`/`aria-readonly` (additive). Tests: `form/src/tests/a11y-autowire.test.ts` (node — accessor values + id agreement) + `a11y-autowire-dom.test.tsx` (happy-dom mount — the real `<input {...register()}>` spread gets `aria-invalid`/`aria-describedby` reactively + the error element links). First slice of the ecosystem-wide a11y plan (`.claude/plans/a11y-dx-multiplatform.md`).
- **Performance (vs the most popular libs, benchmarked in `packages/fundamentals/form/bench/`)**: on the keystroke hot path Pyreon's per-field signal `.set` beats TanStack Form's store clone+notify by **~79×** (`update-field` 46ns vs 3.60µs), `reset` by ~7×, AND full-values `read` by ~1.3× (`form-bench.ts`, headless — the fairest direct peer comparison); TanStack edges Pyreon only on once-per-form `setup` (~1.3×) — the deliberate price of per-field fine-grained signals, which buy the ~79× write win (a dirty-count-inline attempt to close `setup` was measured + reverted: it regressed the keystroke path ~2× via V8 deopt of a larger `setValue`). **`values()` / `getValues()` are epoch-cached** — rebuilt only when a value-mutation method (`setValue`/`reset`/`setInitialValues`) bumps an internal `_valuesEpoch`; a clean read is an int-compare + cached-object return (`read-all-values` 109ns → ~6ns, beating TanStack's plain-object ~7ns), and the write path pays only one integer increment (no signal/subscriber → keystroke path untouched). Direct `fields.x.value.set()` bypasses the epoch (consistent with bypassing dirty/validation — use `setFieldValue`). **The keystroke path has NO per-field `effect()`** — auto-validation (change-mode + post-failed-submit live revalidation) is driven INLINE from `setValue` reading `submitCount.peek()`, not a per-field `effect()` tracking `valueSig`. The effect approach cost a per-field EffectScope at setup (the dominant per-field allocation) AND an effect flush on EVERY keystroke (a no-op in the default blur mode); removing it cut the hot path **242ns → 46ns (5.3×)**, setup ~17%, reset ~35% — all behavior-preserving (bisect-verified: dropping the `submitCount.peek()` trigger fails 3 post-submit-revalidation specs; dropping the change-mode setup-validation fails the change-mode spec). change-mode forms still validate initial values once at setup (a one-time `validateField` call in the `useForm` field loop, replacing the effect's setup-run). On re-renders (`form-rerender-bench.ts`, 10 keystrokes into 1 field of a 20-field form): **Pyreon 0 component re-renders** (signals patch the bound node, values still reactive) = react-hook-form's 0 (uncontrolled refs — but RHF gives up reactive value binding) < Formik's 10 (controlled — re-renders the form every keystroke). Competitors are devDeps (`@tanstack/form-core`, `react-hook-form`, `formik`, `react`/`react-dom`); run `bun bench/form-bench.ts` + `bun bench/form-rerender-bench.ts`.
- `FormProvider` / `useFormContext<TValues>()` — context pattern for nested components, no prop drilling
- Per-field fine-grained signals: `value`, `error`, `touched`, `dirty` are independent `Signal<T>` — reading one doesn't subscribe to others
- `validateOn: 'blur' | 'change' | 'submit'` — **default is `'blur'`**, not `'change'`, so users aren't scolded mid-keystroke. `showError` (from `useField`) always gates on `touched` so even `validateOn: 'change'` forms don't flash errors until first blur
- Async validators are version-tracked — stale results discarded if user types faster than the validator resolves. Combine with `debounceMs` to cut in-flight request count. `isValidating` signal true while any field has a pending async validation
- Server errors: `form.setFieldError(name, msg)` / `form.setErrors({ email: 'Taken' })` — does NOT touch `touched` state, so errors display immediately regardless of blur status
- Manifest-driven docs (T2.1 + T2.5.1): `packages/fundamentals/form/src/manifest.ts` is the single source for the `llms.txt` bullet + `llms-full.txt` section + MCP `api-reference.ts` region. 7 MCP entries generated from the manifest's enriched `api[]` (was 2 hand-written). Inline-snapshot test (`manifest-snapshot.test.ts`) locks the rendered output locally in addition to the CI `Docs Sync` gate.

### @pyreon/i18n

- `createI18n({ locale, messages, loader?, fallbackLocale?, pluralRules?, onMissingKey?, numberFormats?, dateFormats?, relativeTimeFormats?, formats? })`
- `t(key, values?)` — interpolation with `{{name}}`, **inline format specifiers** (`{{amount, currency}}`, `{{when, date}}`, `{{n, relativetime, day}}`), pluralization with `_one`/`_other`/`_zero` suffixes, **`context`** (gender/variant — i18next resolution order `key_male_one` → `key_male` → `key_one` → `key`), **`defaultValue`** (returned + interpolated when the key is missing), and **`$t(key)` nesting** (depth-capped at 4 to break cycles).
- **Intl formatters on the instance** (the 2026-Q3 reference-parity addition — apps previously hand-rolled `Intl` in ~10 example files): `n(value, options?)` (`Intl.NumberFormat` — currency/percent/units, or a named `numberFormats` entry), `d(value, options?)` (`Intl.DateTimeFormat` — accepts `Date`/epoch-ms/string, or a named `dateFormats` entry; bare inline `date`/`time`/`datetime` map to default styles), `rt(value, unit, options?)` (`Intl.RelativeTimeFormat`). All three READ `locale()` so they re-run reactively on locale change, and memoize the underlying `Intl.*Format` per `(locale, optionsKey)`. Named-format config (vue-i18n style, per-locale) + custom inline `formats` (named formatter fns) are resolved with fallback-locale support. The inline-spec resolver + formatter registry live in `formatters.ts` (`/core`-safe — `Intl` + reactivity only); `interpolate(template, values?, { format? })` gained an optional format-resolver param (bare `interpolate()` ignores specs).
- Namespace lazy loading with deduplication, `addMessages()` for runtime additions
- `<I18nProvider value={i18n}>` / `useI18n()` context (the prop is **`value`** — renamed from `instance` in the reference-parity PR to match `PermissionsProvider` + what the manifest already documented). `<Trans>` rich JSX interpolation now **auto-reads `t` from the nearest `<I18nProvider>`** via `useI18n()` — `t` is optional (pass it only to override the context instance or render provider-less). `components` values are `(children) => VNode` functions; the prop is `i18nKey` (NOT `key`, which JSX reserves).
- **Two entry points**: `@pyreon/i18n` (full — includes JSX `Trans`/`I18nProvider`/`useI18n`) and `@pyreon/i18n/core` (framework-agnostic — only `createI18n`, `interpolate`, `resolvePluralCategory`, types). The formatters (`n`/`d`/`rt`) are on the instance returned by `createI18n`, so they are available from BOTH entries. Use `/core` for backend translation pipelines, edge workers, or any non-JSX consumer. The `/core` entry transitively only depends on `@pyreon/reactivity` — zero JSX, zero `@pyreon/core`. The main entry has a `/** @jsxImportSource @pyreon/core */` pragma on `trans.tsx` so even bun runtimes without JSX-aware tsconfigs compile it correctly.

### @pyreon/query

- Full TanStack Query adapter: `useQuery`, `useMutation`, `useMutationState`, `useInfiniteQuery`, `useQueries`
- Prefetch: `usePrefetchQuery` / `usePrefetchInfiniteQuery` — warm the cache in component setup (cache-guarded, no re-fetch when already present) so a child's `useQuery` / `useSuspenseQuery` resolves with no loading flash
- Suspense: `useSuspenseQuery`, `useSuspenseInfiniteQuery`, `useSuspenseQueries` (aggregate — the result IS the `QuerySuspense` gate + a `data` array), `QuerySuspense` boundary
- SSR: `HydrationBoundary` — component that hydrates a server-dehydrated cache (`dehydrate(client)` blob) into the nearest `QueryClient` synchronously, before children render (`nativeCompat`-marked, complements the `dehydrate`/`hydrate` function re-exports)
- Error recovery: `QueryErrorResetBoundary` (component) + `useQueryErrorResetBoundary()` (hook returning `{ reset }`) — pair with a sibling `ErrorBoundary` so fallback retry clears errored queries
- **Offline persistence** (`@pyreon/query/persist` subpath): `PersistQueryClientProvider` (drop-in for `QueryClientProvider` that restores the cache from a persister on mount + persists on change), `useIsRestoring()` / `IsRestoringProvider` (reactive restore flag — exported from main too), and identity re-exports of TanStack's framework-agnostic persist engine (`persistQueryClient`/`persistQueryClientRestore`/`persistQueryClientSave`/`persistQueryClientSubscribe`/`removeOldestQuery`) + storage persisters (`createSyncStoragePersister` for localStorage/sessionStorage, `createAsyncStoragePersister` for IndexedDB/RN). **The fetch-gate**: all 6 query-reading hooks defer their first observer subscription (hence fetch) until `useIsRestoring()` flips false (via `subscribeWhenRestored` in `is-restoring.ts`) — so a restored cache is never clobbered by a redundant network fetch. No `<PersistQueryClientProvider>` → `isRestoring` is always false → hooks subscribe synchronously (byte-equivalent to before; SSR unaffected). The persist deps (`@tanstack/query-persist-client-core` + the two persisters) are subpath-only — tree-shaken from the main bundle.
- **In-app devtools** (`@pyreon/query/devtools` subpath, dev-only): `QueryDevtools` — a ~50-line `onMount` shim over `@tanstack/query-devtools`'s framework-agnostic `TanstackQueryDevtools` engine (the SAME panel React/Solid/Vue ship). Resolves the client from context or a `client` prop; mounts the engine into a host `<div>`, unmounts on cleanup; `nativeCompat`-marked. Import from `@pyreon/query/devtools` (NOT main) so the heavy engine tree-shakes out of production; gate render on `import.meta.env.DEV`. Config props read once at mount (reactive re-config is out of scope for v1). NOTE: a single `@tanstack/query-core@5.101.0` is pinned tree-wide via root `package.json` `overrides` so persist (pins 5.101.0) + devtools (resolves query-core) + the adapter share ONE query-core type (avoids the dual-version `#private`-brand mismatch).
- `useSubscription(options)` — reactive WebSocket with auto-reconnect, integrates with QueryClient for cache invalidation
- `useSSE(options)` — Server-Sent Events hook with QueryClient integration, same pattern as useSubscription but read-only. Updates `lastEventId()` on every incoming SSE `id` field. To resume across remount, pair `useStorage` with the new `initialLastEventId?: string | (() => string)` option and put the ID in the URL so the server reads it as a query param — `EventSource` has no API to set `Last-Event-ID` on the first connection. The seed is read once at mount; subsequent changes to the accessor are ignored (use the reactive `url` for runtime overrides).
- Global counters: `useIsFetching(filters?)` / `useIsMutating(filters?)` → `Signal<number>` for top-of-page spinners
- `useQueryClient()` — imperative access to the nearest `QueryClient` (throws if no provider mounted)
- TanStack core re-exports (identity-equal to `@tanstack/query-core`): `QueryClient`, `QueryCache`, `MutationCache`, all four observers (`QueryObserver`, `InfiniteQueryObserver`, `MutationObserver`, `QueriesObserver`), `dehydrate`, `hydrate`, `skipToken` (v5 sentinel — `queryFn: skipToken` type-safely disables a query), `keepPreviousData`, `hashKey`, `matchQuery`, `matchMutation`, `replaceEqualDeep`, `focusManager`, `onlineManager`, `notifyManager`, `isServer`, `isCancelledError`, `CancelledError`, `defaultShouldDehydrateQuery`, `defaultShouldDehydrateMutation` (+ all types: `QueryKey`, `QueryFilters`, `MutationFilters`, `Mutation`, `MutationState`, `QueryState`, `DehydratedState`, `HydrateOptions`, `InfiniteData`, `DefaultError`, `FetchQueryOptions`, `FetchInfiniteQueryOptions`, etc.) — consumers import everything from `@pyreon/query`. NOTE: `streamedQuery` / `experimental_streamedQuery` are NOT re-exported (not in the pinned query-core@5.101 surface); persistence (`@tanstack/query-persist-client-core`) and devtools (`@tanstack/react-query-devtools`) are separate TanStack ecosystem packages, out of scope for the adapter
- Fine-grained signals per field (data, error, isFetching independent) — each field-level read only subscribes to that field
- `useMutation({ invalidates: [['posts']] })` — auto-invalidates query keys on successful mutation. Preserves user `onSuccess` callback.
- `defineQueries({ user: () => opts, posts: () => opts })` — named parallel queries returning typed object instead of array
- **Options as a function**: `useQuery` / `useInfiniteQuery` / `useQueries` / `useSuspenseQuery` take options as a FUNCTION (not an object) so `queryKey` and other fields can read Pyreon signals — changing a tracked signal re-runs the observer options and refetches automatically. `useMutation` options are a plain object (mutations are imperative, no tracking needed).
- Manifest-driven docs (T2.1 + T2.5.1): `packages/fundamentals/query/src/manifest.ts` is the single source for the `llms.txt` bullet + `llms-full.txt` section + MCP `api-reference.ts` region. 25 MCP entries generated from the manifest's enriched `api[]` (was 2 hand-written). Inline-snapshot test (`manifest-snapshot.test.ts`) locks the rendered output locally in addition to the CI `Docs Sync` gate.

### @pyreon/table

- `useTable(options)` — reactive TanStack Table with signal-driven options, auto state sync
- `flexRender(component, props)` — renders column def templates (strings, functions, VNodes)

### @pyreon/virtual

- `useVirtualizer(options)` — element-scoped with reactive `virtualItems`, `totalSize`, `isScrolling`
- `useWindowVirtualizer(options)` — window-scoped variant with SSR-safe checks

### @pyreon/validation

- `zodSchema()` / `zodField()` — duck-typed Zod adapter (works with v3 and v4)
- `valibotSchema(schema, safeParseFn)` / `valibotField()` — Valibot standalone-function style
- `arktypeSchema()` / `arktypeField()` — ArkType sync adapter
- `wrapStandardSchema()` / `isStandardSchema()` / `extractParseFn()` — generic Standard Schema duck-typing (any spec-compliant validator including Zod 3.24+, Valibot 1.0+, ArkType 2.0+, Effect Schema, typia)

### @pyreon/validate

Pyreon's validator + DX layer on [Standard Schema](https://standardschema.dev). Two halves: (1) **DX helpers** (`withField` / `parseReactive` / `formatErrors`) that work on top of ANY spec-compliant validator (Zod 3.24+ / Valibot 1.0+ / ArkType 2.0+); (2) since v1, **Pyreon's own `s` validator runtime** — chainable + function-comp hybrid (`s.string().email()` / `pipe(string(), email())`), Standard Schema-native. **Tree-shaking is the bundle contract** (measured 2026-06): a DX-helpers-only import is ~0.5KB gz — the v1 runtime is pulled in only when `s` / primitives are imported (~3.9KB gz combined). The full main-entry budget measures 4.5KB gz because the budget script bundles the whole entry; real consumers pay per-import.

- `withField(schema, meta)` — attach `FieldMeta` (label / hint / placeholder / i18n keys / autoFocus / autoComplete / defaultValue) to any Standard Schema. The returned schema is the SAME REFERENCE — Pyreon mutates a Symbol-keyed non-enumerable slot. Mutation (not cloning) is required because ArkType's `Type` instances are callable functions whose `~standard.validate` does `this(input)` — a shallow clone is not callable and breaks that contract. Symbol-keyed non-enumerable mutation is invisible to `JSON.stringify` / `for…in` / `Object.keys` / structured clone / library-internal comparators. Re-wrapping merges (later keys win).
- `getMeta(schema)` — read attached metadata. Accepts both objects AND functions (callable schemas).
- `resolveMetaField(schema, field, t?)` — read a single field through optional i18n. `t('auth.email.label')` wins over `meta.label` when it resolves to a non-key string.
- `parseReactive(schema, source)` — returns `Computed<ParseResult>` that re-validates on signal changes. Sync.
- `parseReactiveAsync` — async variant for schemas with async refinements. Caller handles staleness via `watch`.
- `watchValid(schema, source, cb)` — fires only on validity flips, not every error change. Returns unsubscribe.
- `formatError` / `formatErrors` / `formatErrorsByPath` — resolve issues to strings via the `t` from `useI18n()`. Pyreon issues carry optional `{ key, params, fallback }`; bare StdSchema issues fall through to `message` (no overhead, no special-casing). `formatErrorsByPath` builds a per-field map keyed by issue path — compatible with `@pyreon/form`'s `Errors` shape.
- **v1 `s` validator runtime** — string/number/boolean/literal/enum primitives + object/array composition + optional/nullable/default/transform/refine/brand/describe modifiers + 20+ built-in checks. Opt-in by import; third-party validators (Zod / Valibot / ArkType / typia) remain fully supported through the same DX helpers. Existing `zodSchema()` / `valibotSchema()` / `arktypeSchema()` adapters in `@pyreon/validation` remain unchanged.
- **Object algebra** — `.pick` / `.omit` / `.partial` / **`.required`** (inverse of partial — unwraps `.optional()`/`.nullish()` fields back to required) / `.extend` / `.merge` / `.keyof` + unknown-key policy (`.strip` default / `.strict` / `.passthrough` / **`.catchall(schema)`** — validates every unknown key against `schema` and keeps it; takes precedence over strip/strict/passthrough; preserved through pick/omit/partial/extend/merge). `.required`/`.catchall` closed the two open follow-ups flagged in `v1.ts`. **JIT-correctness note**: `.catchall` disqualifies an object from the JIT plain-object inline path (`jit.ts:isPlainObject` checks `!s._catchall`) — otherwise the shape-only inline loop would silently strip unknown keys without validating them; a catchall object (root or nested) falls back to the interpreter, which is correct. Bisect-locked in `object-algebra.test.ts` (the nested-catchall-under-JIT spec).

### @pyreon/validate — Performance vs Zod / Valibot / ArkType

Benchmarked by `bun run bench:validate` (`scripts/bench/core/validate.ts` — custom warmup+timed-ops harness, `NODE_ENV=production`, a correctness gate asserts all four libs agree valid/invalid before timing, idiomatic schema per lib). Representative run (Bun 1.3, Apple Silicon, ops/sec; the column *ratios* are the signal):

- **Error/invalid-input path — `@pyreon/validate` WINS every shape**: small-object 8.0M ops/s vs Valibot 3.2M (2.5×) / Zod 0.21M (39×) / ArkType 0.20M (40×); nested 5.9M (3.6× Valibot, 40× Zod, 50× ArkType); array-of-20 0.87M (2.6×/8×/18×); discriminated-union 15.3M (3.5× Valibot, 18× ArkType, 30× Zod). The `s` runtime early-exits on the first failing op; Zod + ArkType allocate rich structured error objects (their cost), Valibot is closer but still behind.
- **Valid-input path — `s` is 2nd, behind only ArkType's JIT, and FASTER than Zod + Valibot**: small-object 14.1M ops/s (ArkType 22.8M is 1.62× faster; Valibot 6.7M / Zod 6.0M are 2.1–2.3× SLOWER than `s`); nested 10.4M (ArkType 1.40×; `s` 2.3–3.5× faster than Valibot/Zod); array-of-20 0.89M (ArkType 1.43×; `s` 2.3–3.3× faster than Valibot/Zod); discriminated-union 25.3M (ArkType 1.83×; `s` faster than Zod 17.8M + Valibot 4.7M).
- **The valid-parse gap to ArkType is the documented JIT frontier** — ArkType compiles each type to one flat monomorphic `new Function` predicate (see "what is ArkType JIT"); Pyreon's `core/jit.ts` does the same recursively for object/array/primitive trees but still does per-field `path.push/pop` on the valid path (ArkType defers path construction to the error path), and the **discriminated-union root currently isn't JIT'd** (falls to the interpreter — the widest valid-parse gap at 1.83×, the clearest tracked perf follow-up). Beating ArkType on valid-parse is the open frontier `v1.ts` notes; the bench quantifies exactly where.
- **Known remaining feature gaps** (vs Zod, honest completeness audit): `.catch(fallback)` (error-fallback value), `.readonly()` (freeze output), `.pipe`-with-descriptor-actions (Valibot-style, for tree-shaking), and the longer-tail string formats (datetime / ip / cidr / base64 / emoji / ulid). Core primitive/composition/object-algebra surface is at Zod parity after `.required`/`.catchall`.
- **Compiler-emit (SHIPPED, end-to-end)** — `@pyreon/compiler:analyzeValidate(code)` parses each `const X = s.<schema>` into a typed IR (`ValidateNode`, conservative `unsupported` bail) and `emitValidator(node)` lowers an emittable IR to an inlined monomorphic validator source string (typia-class: straight-line `typeof`/regex/comparison, no op-array traversal). A cross-runtime emit-equivalence gate (`validate/src/tests/emit-equivalence.test.ts`) builds each corpus schema BOTH as runtime `s` and via `analyzeValidate→emitValidator` and asserts verdict parity. The runtime half is `Schema.is(input)` + the internal `_attachCompiledVerdict(fn)` hook. The build wiring is **opt-in `pyreon({ compileValidators: true })`** in `@pyreon/vite-plugin`: production builds append `X._attachCompiledVerdict((v) => { try { return (<emitValidator>)(v).length === 0 } catch { return false } })` to every MODULE-LEVEL, fully-emittable `const X = s.<schema>` (gated on `ValidateSchemaInfo.topLevel` — a function/block-scoped attach at module end would ReferenceError), so `X.is(v)` runs the inlined verdict instead of `X.parse(v).ok`. Build-only (dev keeps the runtime path — already correct + HMR-reactive); runs for both `.ts` (esbuild-compiled after) and `.tsx` (verdict appended AFTER the JSX compile — BOTH paths transform-test-covered in `vite-plugin/src/tests/compiled-verdicts.test.ts`); byte-equivalent to the runtime (speed only); composed/aliased/unsupported schemas skip silently and fall back to runtime `.is()`. **MEASURED benefit (`bun run --filter=@pyreon/validate bench:compiled-verdict`, 500k×7, 3× replicated): compiled `.is()` is 1.6–3.0× faster than `parse().ok`** — biggest on cheap schemas (number 2.9×, array 3.0× — Result-alloc + parse-machinery overhead dominates), smallest on expensive ones (email regex 1.6×, object 1.8× — the regex/field work is shared). **Honest scope: it's NANOSECONDS (~20ns/call) — only matters in a hot `.is()` loop (filtering/gating large arrays); `.parse()` (the common form/request path) is UNCHANGED, and only module-level fully-emittable schemas qualify.** The codegen lives in `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/compiled-verdicts.ts` (internal `buildCompiledVerdicts`), isolated in its own file + excluded from CodeQL (`.github/codeql/codeql-config.yml` paths-ignore — a build-time generator whose input is the app's OWN schema source is a false positive for `js/bad-code-sanitization`, same accepted pattern as the validate runtime JIT). Reference: `packages/core/compiler/src/validate-emit.ts`, `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/compiled-verdicts.ts`, `packages/fundamentals/validate/bench/compiled-verdict.ts`.

### @pyreon/feature

- `defineFeature({ name, schema, api })` — schema-driven CRUD primitives
- Auto-generates: `useList`, `useById`, `useSearch`, `useCreate`, `useUpdate`, `useDelete`, `useForm`, `useTable`, `useStore`
- Composes `@pyreon/query`, `@pyreon/form`, `@pyreon/validation`, `@pyreon/store`, `@pyreon/table`

### @pyreon/charts

- `useChart<TOption>(optionsFn, config?)` — reactive ECharts bridge with lazy loading
- `<Chart />` component with event binding, auto-detects chart types and dynamically imports
- `@pyreon/charts/manual` entry for tree-shaking control
- **tslib alias is required in BOTH tests AND consumer Vite apps**: ECharts imports `tslib` for TypeScript helpers (`__extends`, `__assign`, etc.). tslib's `./modules/index.js` ESM entry destructures named helpers from a `__toESM(require_tslib())` default — the helpers live as top-level vars on the CJS factory, so the destructure reads `undefined` and the page throws `TypeError: Cannot destructure property "__extends"` the moment ECharts loads. The fix is `resolve.alias: { tslib: '<path-to>/tslib.es6.js' }` — that file is a flat ESM module with proper named exports. **Consumer Vite apps**: `import { chartsViteAlias } from '@pyreon/charts/vite'`, then spread it into `resolve.alias` (`alias: { ...chartsViteAlias() }`). It resolves the right path via echarts itself, falls back to walking up `node_modules` for hoisted layouts, and returns `{}` when tslib isn't reachable so apps that don't use Charts don't break. **Browser tests**: `tslibBrowserAlias(import.meta.url)` from `vitest.browser.ts` does the same job for vitest configs. Helper unit tests for the test-side variant live in `packages/internals/test-utils/src/tests/vitest-browser-helpers.test.ts`. Two helpers exist because Vite config files run under Node's `node` condition (so they need the package's `lib/vite.js` build artifact), while vitest browser configs are loaded inside the test runner's bundler context (so they can reach the repo-root `vitest.browser.ts` directly). Reference: `examples/fundamentals-playground/vite.config.ts`, `examples/app-showcase/vite.config.ts`, `packages/fundamentals/charts/vitest.browser.config.ts`. Tracking upstream: [microsoft/tslib#189](https://github.com/microsoft/tslib/issues/189).

### @pyreon/storage

- `useStorage(key, default, options?)` — reactive signal backed by localStorage, cross-tab synced
- `useSessionStorage`, `useCookie`, `useIndexedDB`, `useMemoryStorage` — backend variants
- `createStorage(backend)` — factory for custom backends (encrypted, remote, etc.)
- All return `StorageSignal<T>` — extends `Signal<T>` with `.remove()`
- **`StorageOptions.writeDebounceMs?` (opt-in, local/session)** — coalesce the synchronous `JSON.stringify` + `setItem` so a high-frequency setter (persist-as-you-type drafts) doesn't pay main-thread I/O per `.set`. The signal still updates SYNCHRONOUSLY (UI reactive); only the persist write is debounced (latest value wins). A pending write is flushed on `pagehide`/`beforeunload` via ONE shared idempotent listener (a module-level `pendingFlushes` set — NOT a per-signal listener, avoiding the event-listener pile-up leak class), and `.remove()` cancels any pending write so the timer can't resurrect a removed entry. Default (omit / `0`) = synchronous write, byte-identical to prior behavior. The IndexedDB backend already debounced async writes (`debounceMs`); this is the synchronous-backend analog. Reference: `packages/fundamentals/storage/src/local.ts` (`scheduleWrite` / `flush` / `ensureUnloadFlush`).
- **Wrapper-signal contract**: each storage factory wraps a base `signal()` with a callable that delegates `.direct` / `.subscribe` / `.peek` / `.set` AND forwards the internal `_v` field via getter. The `_v` forwarding is load-bearing for the compiler-emitted `_bindText` fast path — `_bindText(theme, textNode)` reads `theme._v` directly (skipping the function call), so without the getter the binding wrote `''` on initial render AND on every subsequent subscriber notification. Pre-fix shape (pre-2026-05-13): SSR rendered correctly but post-hydration text nodes went empty across every storage backend. See `packages/fundamentals/storage/src/{local,cookie,custom,indexed-db}.ts` for the canonical `Object.defineProperty(storageSig, '_v', { get: () => sig._v, configurable: true })` shape and `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` "Signal-like wrapper callables missing the internal `_v` field" for the general contract.

### @pyreon/hotkeys

- `useHotkey(shortcut, handler, options?)` — component-scoped, auto-unregisters on unmount
- `useHotkeyScope(scope)` — activate a scope for a component's lifetime
- Supports `mod` (⌘ on Mac, Ctrl elsewhere), scope-based activation

### @pyreon/permissions

- `createPermissions(initial?)` — reactive permissions instance, callable as `can(key, context?)`
- `can.not(key)` / `can.all(...keys)` / `can.any(...keys)` — inverse and multi-checks
- `can.assert(key, context?, message?)` — throw-on-deny (a custom `message`, or `[Pyreon] permission denied: '<key>'` by default) for loaders / route guards / server actions; evaluates predicates + wildcards exactly like `can()`
- `can.set(map)` / `can.patch(map)` / `can.clear()` — replace / merge / wipe permissions reactively
- `PermissionsProvider` prop is **`value`** (`<PermissionsProvider value={can}>`) — iter-2 renamed it from `instance` to match the documented/conventional name (the code had drifted from the docs/MCP which always said `value`)
- **Wildcard matching (most-specific-first):** `'posts.*'` matches exactly ONE segment (`posts.read`, NOT `posts.read.title`); `'posts.**'` matches any depth strictly below `posts` (covers `posts.read` AND `posts.a.b.c`, but NOT the bare `posts` node); `'*'` matches everything. Resolution order: exact → `parent.*` → nearest-ancestor `**` (longest prefix first) → global `*` → denied. Because resolution is most-specific-first, an exact or `**` deny overrides a broader subtree grant (`'posts.**': true` + `'posts.admin.**': false` grants posts but denies the admin subtree) — the CASL `cannot`-over-`can` shape, in the flat-key idiom. (`*` global stays recursive-everything; `prefix.*` stays one-segment — both unchanged, `**` is the new recursive-subtree primitive.)
- `PermissionsProvider` / `usePermissions()` — context pattern for SSR/testing
- **Deliberately out of scope vs CASL** (the predicate model replaces the DSL): MongoDB-style condition matching → predicates `(context) => boolean` (arbitrary code, more flexible); rule packing/serialization + subject-type detection → not applicable to the flat-string-key model. Async permission checks → resolve into a signal the predicate reads (async offloaded to Pyreon primitives).

### @pyreon/machine

- `createMachine({ initial, states })` — constrained signal with type-safe transitions
- `machine()` — read state, `machine.send(event, payload?)` — trigger a transition; **returns the settled `TState`** (after any `always` cascade), or the unchanged state for an unhandled event / rejected guard
- `machine.matches(...states)`, `machine.can(event, payload?)`, `machine.nextEvents()`, `machine.isFinal()`
- Guards: `{ target: 'state', guard: (payload?) => boolean }` for conditional transitions. **Guards are throw-safe** — a guard that throws (e.g. reading a property of a missing payload) DENIES the transition rather than crashing `send`/`can` (consistent with `@pyreon/permissions` predicates)
- **`can(event, payload?)`** — predicts `send(event, payload)` EXACTLY: it evaluates the guard (throw-safe → denied) with the given payload, or `undefined` if none is passed. (Iter-2 breaking change: previously a guarded event with no payload reported `true`; now it evaluates the guard, so `can('LOGIN')` with no payload against a payload-reading guard reports `false`.)
- **Eventless `always` transitions** (`states.X.always: target | { target, guard } | [...]`) — fire SYNCHRONOUSLY on entering a state (and for the initial state at creation / on `reset()`), cascading until none apply; the first unguarded entry or first passing guard wins. Guards receive NO payload (read external signals). Transient/condition states (`check → pass | fail`) are never observed by `machine()` or reactive readers. A self-looping `always` throws after 1000 steps (config-error guard). Eventless transitions are the synchronous-transition-logic part of the statechart model — distinct from "async, use effects" which Pyreon offloads to signals/effects.
- **Final states** — `states.X.final: true`; `machine.isFinal()` (reactive) reads true in any final state; `machine.onDone(cb)` fires (with the triggering event) when a final state is entered, including via an `always` cascade. Pyreon does NOT freeze final states (a final state's `on` transitions still fire if declared — omit `on` for true terminals).
- **Lifecycle listeners** — `onEnter(state, cb)` / `onExit(state, cb)` / `onTransition(cb)` / `onDone(cb)`, all returning an unsubscribe; `dispose()` clears all. On each transition they fire in state-chart order: `onExit(from)` (machine still reads `from`) → `onTransition(from, to, event)` → `onEnter(to)` (machine reads `to`) → `onDone` if `to` is final. `onExit` pairs with `onEnter` for per-state setup/teardown — e.g. start a timer on enter, clear it on exit (the idiomatic delayed-transition pattern; Pyreon has no built-in `after`, by design — async/timers use Pyreon primitives).
- **Deliberately out of scope vs XState** (offloaded to Pyreon primitives, per the package philosophy): extended-state/context → signals; invoked actors/services → effects + signals; hierarchical/parallel states → compose multiple machines; delayed `after` → `onEnter` + `useTimeout`/`setTimeout` + `onExit` cleanup. The package is "a constrained signal with statechart transition semantics," not an XState clone.

### @pyreon/flow

- `createFlow<TData>({ nodes, edges, ...config })` — generic over node `data` shape. `createFlow<MyData>(...)` returns `FlowInstance<MyData>` so `node.data.kind` narrows correctly without an `[key: string]: unknown` index signature on consumer types. Defaults to `Record<string, unknown>` if no generic supplied.
- `useFlow<TData>(config)` — component-scoped wrapper around `createFlow` that auto-disposes the instance on unmount. Use inside a component body; use `createFlow` directly only for app-store / singleton flows that outlive the component tree.
- Node/edge CRUD, selection, viewport (zoom/pan/fitView), auto-layout via elkjs (lazy-loaded)
- Components: `<Flow nodeTypes={{ custom: MyNode }}>`, `<Background>`, `<MiniMap>`, `<Controls>`, `<Handle>`, `<Panel>`. JSX components are NOT generic at the call site (`<Flow<MyData> />` is invalid JSX); `FlowProps.instance` is typed as `FlowInstance<any>` so typed consumers can pass `FlowInstance<MyData>` without casting.
- Edge paths: `getBezierPath()`, `getSmoothStepPath()`, `getStraightPath()`, `getStepPath()`
- **Configurable edge markers (arrowheads)**: `MarkerType.ArrowClosed` (filled `<polygon>`, the default) / `MarkerType.Arrow` (open `<polyline>`), set per-edge via `markerStart` / `markerEnd` (a bare `MarkerType`, a full `EdgeMarker` `{ type, color?, width?, height?, strokeWidth? }`, or `null` for explicit no-marker) and graph-wide via `FlowConfig.defaultMarkerEnd` (`null` → arrowless by default). `markerEnd: null` is the opt-out that overrides the default; OMITTING it inherits the default. Helpers in `edges.ts` (`resolveMarker` / `markerId` / `resolveEdgeMarkers` / `collectEdgeMarkers`) are pure + exported; the `<defs>` set is deduped by a config-keyed `markerId` and rebuilt reactively as edges change. One `<marker orient="auto-start-reverse">` def serves both ends. Reference: `packages/fundamentals/flow/src/edges.ts` + `components/flow-component.tsx:MarkerDef`; tests `tests/markers.test.ts` (13 unit) + `tests/flow.browser.test.tsx` (2 real-Chromium: deduped shapes/colors + reactive defs).
- **Render virtualization**: `FlowConfig.onlyRenderVisibleElements` (default OFF) culls nodes whose screen rect (± a 200px margin) doesn't intersect the viewport, and edges with no visible endpoint; the rendered set re-filters reactively on pan/zoom (the `<For each>` accessors read `viewport()` + `containerSize()`). A 0×0 pre-measurement container renders all (guard). An edge spanning two off-screen nodes is culled even if its line crosses the viewport (matches React Flow). Reference: `flow-component.tsx:visibleNodeList`/`visibleEdgeList`; tests `tests/flow.browser.test.tsx` (real-Chromium cull + re-filter-on-pan + flag-off control, bisect-verified).
- **Object-snapping is opt-out for drag perf**: `FlowConfig.snapToObjects` (default `true` — no behavior change) gates the helper-line align-to-other-nodes scan in the drag pointermove handler, which is an O(N) pass over every node on EVERY frame (the *dominant* per-frame cost on large graphs — `getSnapLines` was ~75% of drag-frame work, measured). `snapToObjects: false` skips it: drag becomes the single immutable node-array update only. Measured 60-frame drag: N=1000 1.34ms→0.31ms, N=3000 3.36ms→0.78ms (~3-4×). Distinct from `snapToGrid` (grid quantization in `updateNodePosition`). Reference: `flow-component.tsx` drag `handlePointerMove` gate; tests `tests/flow.browser.test.tsx` (real-Chromium snap-on snaps / snap-off raw-position, bisect-verified).
- **Round-2 component-bug sweep (9 real bugs, several dormant because the components had NEVER rendered in a real Pyreon-compiled app).** `<Flow>` now injects its instance to MiniMap/Controls via a `FlowContext` (`components/flow-context.ts`) — the documented `<Flow instance={flow}><MiniMap/></Flow>` shape previously rendered NOTHING (children resolve `props.instance ?? useContext(FlowContext)`, explicit prop wins). That fix exposed two latent **compiler-template-ordering** bugs (static-element reactive refs computed via `.nextSibling` walks AFTER a sibling `_mountSlot` mutates the DOM): MiniMap threw `setAttribute is not a function` (`{nodes.map}` between two `<rect>`s → fixed with a static `<g>` wrapper) and Controls threw `replaceChild of null` (conditional buttons before the reactive zoom-% `<div>` → fixed with a `display:contents` wrapper). Also: edge markers rendered `[object Object]` in real apps (bare `{MarkerGlyph(m,pts)}` call under `<marker>` → use the element form `<MarkerGlyph/>`); NodeToolbar show-on-select was a static `return null` (now reactive `selected` accessor — accepts a value OR accessor); NodeResizer handle offsets were hardcoded `-4px` (now scale with `handleSize`); node drag swallowed clicks on in-node controls (now bails on `.pyreon-flow-node-toolbar`/`.nodrag`/`button,input,…`); drag-to-connect created no edge (pointer-capture made `pointerup`'s `e.target` the container → now `document.elementFromPoint`); `getAbsolutePosition` stack-overflowed on a cyclic `parentId` (visited-set guard). **The flow package's vitest-browser tests use a JSX transform that does NOT match the real `@pyreon/vite-plugin` compiler and MASKED the markers/MiniMap/Controls template bugs** (green-in-vitest, broken-in-real-app) — the real-compiler e2e is the only reliable gate; see `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` (`_mountSlot`-ordering + `{fn()}`-stringify entries). The remaining underlying compiler ordering bug (hoist all static `__eN` refs above `_mountSlot`) is documented there as a deferred deep fix. **Every flow feature is now exercised in `examples/app-showcase/src/routes/flow-features/` (the Flow Feature Matrix route)** + gated by `e2e/app-showcase-flow-features.spec.ts` (7 real-Chromium specs). drag-to-connect is unit-covered (`tests/node-components.browser.test.tsx`) — the e2e canvas can't reliably synthesize the 8px-handle hit-test.
- Custom node renderers receive `NodeComponentProps<TData>`: `{ id, data: () => TData, selected: () => boolean, dragging: () => boolean }`. **All non-id props are reactive accessors** — read inside reactive scopes (JSX expression thunks, `effect()`, `computed()`) so the node patches in place when any underlying state changes. Each node mounts EXACTLY ONCE across the lifetime of the graph regardless of how many drags, selection clicks, or `updateNode` data mutations happen. Internally `<Flow>` uses `<For>` keyed by `node.id` plus per-node/per-edge reactive accessors that read live state via `instance.nodeMap()` / `instance.edgeMap()` — `Computed<Map<id, entry>>` lookups, O(1) per access, each map rebuilt once per `nodes()` / `edges()` change. **A drag writes the whole `nodes()` array every pointermove frame, which notifies EVERY node + edge style/class/path thunk (they all subscribe to the one `nodes()` signal) — so per-frame work is O(N) total (one map rebuild + N O(1) gets), NOT the O(N²) it was before these maps existed.** Pre-`nodeMap` the accessors did an O(N) `instance.nodes().find()` (and edges 2× O(N) for source/target) inside each thunk → O(N²) + O(E×(2N+E)) per drag frame, contradicting this O(1)-per-accessor contract; the `nodeMap`/`edgeMap` computeds (added on `FlowInstance`) restore it. Bisect-locked by `packages/fundamentals/flow/src/tests/drag-frame-complexity.test.ts` (a 60-node/40-edge drag frame: 460 `Array.prototype.find` calls pre-fix → ~0 post-fix; count must not scale with graph size).
- Custom edge renderers receive `EdgeComponentProps`: `{ edge, sourceX: () => number, sourceY: () => number, targetX: () => number, targetY: () => number, selected: () => boolean }`. Same accessor-based contract — each custom edge mounts once and recomputes path coordinates reactively when source/target nodes move. The default edge renderer (when no custom edge type is registered) uses inline reactive thunks for `d`, `stroke`, `stroke-width`, and `class`.
- `flow.toJSON()` / `flow.fromJSON()` for serialization round-trips, `flow.layout('layered', { direction, nodeSpacing, layerSpacing })` for elkjs auto-layout
- **`LayoutOptions` algorithm applicability** (verified empirically by running each algorithm twice with different option values): `direction` applies to `layered` and `tree`; `layerSpacing` and `edgeRouting` apply to `layered` only; `nodeSpacing` is the only field respected by every algorithm. The other algorithms (`force`, `stress`, `radial`, `box`, `rectpacking`) accept the option in `LayoutOptions` (so it typechecks) but silently ignore it at layout time. Use `layered` or `tree` if you need a directional layout.
- **Dev-mode safety net**: `flow.layout()` (and the underlying `computeLayout`) emits a `console.warn` in dev mode when an option is set on an algorithm that ignores it (e.g. `direction: 'RIGHT'` on a force layout). The dev gate uses bare `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` — the bundler-agnostic library convention used by React, Vue, Preact, Solid. Every modern bundler (Vite, Webpack/Next.js, Rolldown, esbuild, Rollup, Parcel, Bun) auto-replaces `process.env.NODE_ENV` at consumer build time and tree-shakes the dev warning to zero bytes in production. **Do NOT use `typeof process !== 'undefined' && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`** (the typeof guard is dead in Vite browser builds) **and do NOT use `import.meta.env.DEV`** (Vite/Rolldown-only — dead in Webpack/Next.js, esbuild, Rollup, Parcel, Bun). `flow/src/layout.ts:warnIgnoredOptions` is the reference implementation. The full monorepo migration (~30 files across `reactivity`, `core`, `runtime-dom`, `router`, `ui-system/*`, `fundamentals/{store,storage}`, `tools/{react-compat,solid-compat,svelte-compat}`) is complete. The lint rule `pyreon/no-process-dev-gate` enforces this codebase-wide; any new code introducing `import.meta.env.DEV` or the typeof-process compound fails CI.

  **Pattern × bundler outcome.** The bundler-agnostic standard is the only pattern that fires correctly across every bundler Pyreon ships to:

  | Source pattern                                                            | Vite prod   | Webpack/Next.js | esbuild     | Rollup      | Parcel      | Bun         | Verdict               |
  | ------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------- | --------------- | ----------- | ----------- | ----------- | ----------- | --------------------- |
  | `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` (bare)                            | tree-shaken | tree-shaken     | tree-shaken | tree-shaken | tree-shaken | tree-shaken | ✅ universal          |
  | `typeof process !== 'undefined' && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` | dead code   | dead code       | dead code   | dead code   | dead code   | dead code   | ❌ broken everywhere  |
  | `import.meta.env.DEV` (and `(import.meta as ViteMeta).env?.DEV === true`) | tree-shaken | undefined       | undefined   | undefined   | undefined   | undefined   | ❌ Vite/Rolldown only |

  Bundle-level regression test: `flow/src/tests/integration.test.ts` feeds `layout.ts` to esbuild with the defines every modern bundler uses (`'process.env.NODE_ENV': '"production"'` for prod) and asserts dev-warning strings are absent. This proves the bundler-agnostic claim empirically per migration.

  **Enforced by `pyreon/no-process-dev-gate`** (auto-fixable). The companion rule `pyreon/dev-guard-warnings` recognises `if (process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production') return` as a valid early-return guard so `console.warn` calls in the function body don't fire spuriously. Server-only packages (`zero`, `runtime-server`, `server`, `vite-plugin`) are exempt — they always run in Node where `process` is real.

- No D3 — pan/zoom via pointer events + CSS transforms
- **Peer dep**: `@pyreon/runtime-dom` is required because the JSX templates emit `_tpl()` calls — declare it in consumer apps' deps
- **MCP api-reference is manifest-driven (T2.5.1)**: the flow region in `packages/tools/mcp/src/api-reference.ts` regenerates from the same manifest's `api[]`. Eight entries today (`createFlow`, `useFlow`, `Flow`, `Background`, `Controls`, `MiniMap`, `Handle`, `Panel`) — a strict superset of the previous hand-written surface, covering all child components. First real consumer of the marker-based `<gen-docs:api-reference:start/end @pyreon/<name>>` region protocol — `query` / `form` / `hooks` flip to the same protocol in follow-up PRs as their manifests are enriched to MCP density.

### @pyreon/code

- `createEditor({ value, language, theme, minimap, lineNumbers, foldGutter, onChange, ... })` — reactive editor instance
- `editor.value` is a writable `Signal<string>` — `editor.value()` reads, `editor.value.set(next)` writes back into CodeMirror
- `editor.cursor` / `editor.selection` / `editor.lineCount` are computed signals
- `<CodeEditor instance={editor} />`, `<DiffEditor>`, `<TabbedEditor>` — mount components, auto-cleanup on unmount
- `minimapExtension()` — canvas-based code overview
- `loadLanguage(lang)` — lazy-load 19 language grammars (`json`, `typescript`, `python`, etc.)
- **Two-way binding via `bindEditorToSignal({ editor, signal, serialize, parse, onParseError? })`** — replaces the recurring loop-prevention flag-pair boilerplate from PRs #191 + #192. Accepts a `Signal<T>` or any `SignalLike<T>` and round-trips through user-supplied `serialize`/`parse` functions. Internal flags break the format-on-input race; parse failures call `onParseError` and leave the external state at its last valid value. Returns `{ dispose }` for cleanup. Both directions are loop-safe and the editor itself also has internal CM↔signal loop guards.
- Built on CodeMirror 6 (~250KB vs Monaco's ~2.5MB)
- **Peer dep**: `@pyreon/runtime-dom` is required because `<CodeEditor>` JSX emits `_tpl()` calls

### @pyreon/document

- `render(node, format, options?)` — render document node tree to any format
- `createDocument(props?)` — builder: `.heading()`, `.text()`, `.table()`, `.toPdf()`, `.toEmail()`, etc.
- JSX primitives: `Document`, `Page`, `Heading`, `Text`, `Table`, `Image`, `List`, `Code`, `Divider`, etc.
- 20 output formats: HTML, PDF, DOCX, XLSX, PPTX, email, Markdown, text, CSV, SVG, Slack, Teams, Discord, Telegram, Notion, Confluence, WhatsApp, Google Chat, JSON, JSONL
- Heavy renderers lazy-loaded — chunks only load when `render(doc, '<format>')` is invoked. Approximate chunk sizes (vendored): PDF ~3MB (pdfmake + fonts), DOCX ~700KB, XLSX ~1.1MB, PPTX ~400KB. The 14MB published `lib/` is the trade-off for a single-install batteries-included experience; apps tree-shake at the consumer level so unused renderers don't ship to end users.

### @pyreon/document-primitives

- 18 rocketstyle components — `DocDocument`, `DocPage`, `DocSection`, `DocRow`, `DocColumn`, `DocHeading`, `DocText`, `DocLink`, `DocImage`, `DocTable`, `DocList`, `DocListItem`, `DocCode`, `DocDivider`, `DocSpacer`, `DocButton`, `DocQuote`, `DocPageBreak`
- **Same component tree renders in browser AND exports to 20 formats** — primitives carry `_documentType` static markers; `extractDocumentTree(vnode)` from `@pyreon/connector-document` walks the tree and produces a `DocNode` for `@pyreon/document`'s `render()` to consume
- **`extractDocNode(templateFn)`** — one-step alias that replaces `createDocumentExport(templateFn).getDocNode()`. Most consumers should use this. The two-step form is still exported for callers that need to pass the helper object around
