- **Reactive metadata via accessor props**: `DocDocument` accepts `title?: string | (() => string)`, `author?: string | (() => string)`, `subject?: string | (() => string)`. Function values are stored in `_documentProps` and resolved by `extractDocumentTree` at extraction time, so each export click reads the LIVE value from any underlying signal — no `const initial = get()` workaround needed
- **Framework fix in `extractDocumentTree`**: real rocketstyle primitives' metadata is invisible on the JSX vnode because `_documentProps` only appears AFTER the rocketstyle attrs HOC runs — the JSX vnode's props only contain the user-supplied props (`{ title, author }`). PR #197 fixed this by invoking the full component to read post-attrs `_documentProps` (a workaround that depended on attrs purity). PR #321 (T3.1) replaced that workaround with a hoisted-attrs fast path: `@pyreon/rocketstyle` now exposes the accumulated `.attrs()` callback chain on the component function as `__rs_attrs`, and `extractDocumentTree` runs the chain directly via `attrsResult = chain.reduce(Object.assign, {})` — no styled wrapper invocation, no JSX tree creation, no dimension resolution. The non-rocketstyle Path B (full component invocation) stays as a fallback for hand-rolled test fixtures. The latent bug class is the same as before — `_documentProps` lives behind the attrs HOC — but the fast path now sidesteps the per-export cost
- `createDocumentExport(templateFn)` — kept for backward compat; internally delegates to `extractDocNode`
- Layout props live in `.attrs()` (not `.theme()`): `direction`, `gap`, `alignX`, `alignY`. Element accepts `direction: 'inline' | 'rows' | 'reverseInline' | 'reverseRows'` — `'row'` is invalid
- For fine-grained reactivity in templates that drive a live preview, pass a signal accessor (not its resolved value) and read it inside the template body via per-text-node thunks: `<DocText>{() => store.field()}</DocText>` — components run once, so reading the signal at the top of the template captures only the initial value
- Rocketstyle `.attrs<P>()` generic is the **public** prop type — runtime-filled fields like `tag` and `_documentProps` belong in the callback body, never in the generic, or they leak as required JSX props
- **Watch for prop names that collide with read-only HTML element properties.** `HTMLTableElement.rows` and `.columns` are read-only `HTMLCollection` getters — if a prop with that name reaches the DOM forwarding step, the runtime crashes with `Cannot set property rows of [object Object] which has only a getter`. Use rocketstyle's `.attrs(callback, { filter: ['rows', 'columns', ...] })` second argument to strip export-only props before they reach the DOM. `DocTable` uses this pattern. Other risky names: `style` (writable but reserved), `cells`, `tHead`, `tBodies` on table elements; `form` on form-associated inputs.

### @pyreon/storybook

- `renderToCanvas(context, canvasElement)` — core renderer for Storybook
- `Meta<TComponent>` / `StoryObj<TMeta>` — typed story definitions
- Preset: `framework: "@pyreon/storybook"` in `.storybook/main.ts`

### @pyreon/rx

- Signal-aware reactive transforms — every function overloaded: `Signal<T[]> → Computed`, `T[] → plain`
- 37 functions across 6 categories:
  - **Collections (21):** `filter`, `map`, `sortBy`, `groupBy`, `keyBy`, `uniqBy`, `take`, `skip`, `last`, `chunk`, `flatten`, `find`, `mapValues`, `first`, `compact`, `reverse`, `partition`, `takeWhile`, `dropWhile`, `unique`, `sample`
  - **Aggregation (8):** `count`, `sum`, `min`, `max`, `average`, `reduce`, `every`, `some`
  - **Operators (5):** `distinct`, `scan`, `combine`, `zip`, `merge`
  - **Timing (2):** `debounce`, `throttle`
  - **Search (1):** `search`
- `pipe(source, op1, op2, ...)` — compose transforms left-to-right
- Signal inputs produce `Computed` outputs that auto-track and re-derive when the source signal changes

### @pyreon/toast

- `toast(message)` — imperative toast creation, returns toast ID
- `toast.success(msg)`, `toast.error(msg)`, `toast.warning(msg)`, `toast.info(msg)`, `toast.loading(msg)` — preset variants
- `toast.update(id, options)` — update an existing toast (e.g., loading → success)
- `toast.dismiss(id?)` — dismiss one or all toasts
- `toast.promise(promise, { loading, success, error })` — auto-transitions through states
- `<Toaster />` — render component with Portal, CSS transitions, auto-dismiss, pause on hover
- Accessibility: `role="alert"`, `aria-live="polite"` on toast elements
- **Render layer was structurally broken until the reactive-rows + portal-delegation fix (the package's first browser test caught it — `toaster.tsx` had been coverage-excluded with zero DOM coverage; the node store suite passes because it reads the signal directly, never the rendered DOM).** Two independent bugs, both invisible to mount-only checks:
  1. **Stale rows (the `<For>` W22 contract).** `ToastItem` read `message`/`type`/`state` STATICALLY off the snapshot the `<For by={id}>` callback receives. Same-key item-object replacement does NOT re-render a keyed row, so `toast.update`, `toast.promise` transitions, AND the `entering→visible` promotion never reflected — toasts rendered stuck `--entering` (opacity:0 = invisible) and `update`/`promise` text never changed. **Fix:** `<For>` keys on the toast IDs (structure only); each row reads its live fields via a `_toastMap` computed (`id→Toast`, the `@pyreon/flow` `nodeMap` pattern) inside reactive thunks — so one update patches only that row's text node / className, 0 component re-renders. `action`/`dismissible` (immutable per toast) are read once at mount; `message`/`type`/`state` reactively.
  2. **Portal'd buttons dead.** `click` (and `submit`/`focusin`/`focusout`/…) are DELEGATED events — Pyreon installs ONE delegation listener on the mount container and stores per-element handlers as expandos. The Toaster portals into the body region, OUTSIDE the mount container, so a click on the dismiss `×` / action button bubbled `button→body` and never through the mount root → the handler never fired (dismiss, action, AND pause-on-FOCUS were all silently dead). **Fix:** the Toaster renders into a per-instance host element appended to `document.body` and calls `setupDelegation(host)` (exported from `@pyreon/runtime-dom`) — scoping delegation to the toast subtree so the buttons fire WITHOUT double-firing the app's own delegated handlers (a listener on `document.body`, an ancestor of the mount root, would catch app clicks too). Mirrors `@pyreon/elements`' per-instance Portal wrapper. **The same class affects any `@pyreon/core` `<Portal>` content with delegated handlers** (elements' overlays, dnd) — see the anti-patterns "Portal'd delegated-event handlers" entry; the broader core/elements fix is tracked separately.
  - Reference: `packages/fundamentals/toast/src/{toast.ts:_toastMap, toaster.tsx}`; regression locks: real-Chromium `src/tests/toaster.browser.test.tsx` (8 specs, bisect-verified 6-fail-on-revert) + node `src/tests/toast-map.test.ts`.
- **Benchmark (`bench/toast-bench.ts`, `bun run --filter=@pyreon/toast bench`) — fastest store dispatch vs react-hot-toast.** Headless store-op throughput (NODE_ENV=production, happy-dom for the React lib's import, median ns/op over 9 runs): **Pyreon is ~3.0–4.5× faster than react-hot-toast** — create+dismiss ~117ns vs ~357ns (3.0×), update-by-id ~79ns vs ~340ns (4.3×), create-10+clear ~0.93µs vs ~3.6µs (3.8×) (Apple M3, Node 24; stable across runs — the ratios are the portable signal). **Honest scope (deliberately NOT overclaimed):** (1) **react-hot-toast** is the fair headless peer — both have a hard, headless removal path so the store stays bounded across the timed loop. (2) **sonner is EXCLUDED from the headless bench** — its `dismiss` is animation-coupled (a dismissed toast is only removed once a MOUNTED `<Toaster>` finishes the exit animation), so headless the array grows unboundedly → O(N²); reporting that would be a benchmark artifact, not sonner's real per-op cost. (3) **No cross-lib COMMIT (wall-clock-to-render-an-update) number is published** — a happy-dom wall-clock harness measured react-hot-toast at a non-credible ~285× (its per-toast `getBoundingClientRect` height measurement is pathologically slow under happy-dom, NOT a real-browser cost) and sonner ~tied with Pyreon, so that bench was dropped rather than ship a misleading magnitude; a fair cross-lib commit comparison needs a real-browser (Playwright) harness — deferred. The **architectural** update advantage (Pyreon patches only the changed toast's text node — 0 component re-renders, independent of stack size — vs the React libs re-rendering the `<Toaster>` + reconciling every mounted toast item per update) is real-Chromium-proven by `toaster.browser.test.tsx` (update reflects via in-place patch, row mounts once), not by a contaminated wall-clock.

### @pyreon/url-state

- `useUrlState(key, defaultValue)` — returns `UrlStateSignal` synced to URL search params
- Schema mode: `useUrlState({ page: 1, sort: "name" })` — multiple params from a single call
- Auto type coercion (numbers, booleans, arrays), uses `replaceState` (no history spam)
- Configurable debounce for high-frequency updates, SSR-safe (reads from request URL on server)

### @pyreon/sync

Local-first / collaborative sync built on reactivity — a synced value IS a `Signal` (via `wrapSignal`), so a remote op becomes one `signal.set` → one fine-grained DOM update, never a re-render. Three entry points: `@pyreon/sync` (core bridge, universal, depends only on `@pyreon/reactivity`), `@pyreon/sync/yjs` (real Yjs engine — keeps `yjs` out of the core entry), `@pyreon/sync/server` (Node/Bun relay — imports `ws` + `node:http`, never enters a client bundle).

- `syncedSignal({ doc, key, initial })` — bind a `Signal<T>` to a scalar CRDT map entry. **Create-if-missing**: `initial` is written only if the key is absent (a persisted/peer value is authoritative). v1 scope is scalars (string/number/boolean).
- `syncedStore(initial, { doc })` — a flat store of synced fields over one map; `store.field()` reads, `store.field.set(v)` writes. A single-key change writes exactly one base signal (others early-return on `Set.has`).
- **The update loop (single source of truth, load-bearing):** `.set(v)` writes ONLY the CRDT; the map `observe` is the ONE writer of the base signal and fires for BOTH local and remote commits; the local echo is an `Object.is` no-op. **The network loop is prevented in the TRANSPORT** (it re-broadcasts `LOCAL_ORIGIN` updates and applies inbound ones as `REMOTE_ORIGIN`, never re-broadcasting a remote update) — NEVER by gating the observer on origin (that would drop the local UI update). `LOCAL_ORIGIN` / `REMOTE_ORIGIN` are `unique symbol` exports.
- **Engine seam:** `CrdtAdapter` / `CrdtDoc` / `CrdtMap` (engine-neutral) keep `syncedSignal`/`syncedStore` engine-free; `FakeCrdtAdapter` + `connectFakeDocs(a, b)` are the in-memory test double (no state-vector merge — can't model offline-reconnect; use the Yjs adapter for that). The seam ports the client bridge, NOT the wire format — persistence/transport/relay are Yjs-coupled.
- **`@pyreon/sync/yjs`:** `createYjsDoc(yDoc?)` (`.yDoc` exposes the Y.Doc); `syncedText(doc, key)` (`Y.Text` character-merge — `.insert`/`.delete` positional, `.set` is a prefix/suffix diff; concurrent edits keep BOTH, unlike scalar LWW); `syncedList(doc, key)` (`Y.Array` positional merge — render with keyed `<For>`); `syncedAwareness(doc, initial?)` (EPHEMERAL presence + live cursors over the Yjs awareness protocol — a SEPARATE channel from doc updates, NEVER persisted; returns reactive `local`/`others`/`states` signals + `setLocal`/`setLocalField`; `PeerState<T> = { clientId, state, isLocal }`; **create it BEFORE connecting** a transport — the transport peeks for the doc's awareness at connect via `peekDocAwareness`, so apps that never use presence pay zero awareness overhead; uses `y-protocols`); `persistViaIndexedDB(doc, dbName)` (browser-only, `await .whenSynced` BEFORE seeding); `connectViaBroadcastChannel(doc, name)` (same-origin cross-tab); `connectViaWebSocket(doc, url, opts?)` (cross-device, auto-reconnect, uses global `WebSocket` / `WebSocketImpl`, token in URL query — browser WS can't set headers, 4401 close = authz reject, terminal). **Awareness rides BOTH transports on a `MSG_AWARENESS` (=2) frame and is applied under the SHARED `REMOTE_ORIGIN`** so a received presence is never re-sent by the sibling transport (the cross-transport WS↔BroadcastChannel loop guard — same tag the doc-update echo guard uses). BroadcastChannel replays local presence on an inbound `sv` (the cross-tab analog of the relay's join-state, since BC delivers only to current subscribers). **Awareness lifecycle is DOC-owned, not view-owned**: the `Awareness` is one-per-`Y.Doc` (`WeakMap`, shared by every transport + every `syncedAwareness` view). A view's `dispose()` detaches ONLY that view's `'change'` observer — it must NOT `aw.destroy()` the shared instance (doing so strands the transports + any sibling view, and via `onCleanup` a single component unmount would silently kill the whole doc's presence). The DOC owns teardown: `YjsCrdtDoc.destroy()` → `destroyDocAwareness(doc)` (announce departure + `aw.destroy()` + WeakMap-delete); departure on disconnect is the transport's job (`removeAwarenessStates(aw, [aw.clientID], 'local')`) and the relay's socket-close purge is the real ghost-cursor guarantee. (Bug fixed 2026-06: `syncedAwareness().dispose()` originally did the full destructive teardown — listener-only now; bisect-locked by the multi-view + `doc.destroy()` specs in `awareness.test.ts`.) Presence recompute is O(N) in peer count (full snapshot rebuild + every `others()` consumer re-runs per change) — throttle cursor publishes; fine for dozens of collaborators, a v1 limit for large swarms.
- **`@pyreon/sync/server`:** `createSyncServer({ port?, server?, authorize? })` — one authoritative `Y.Doc` per room, broadcasts to other clients, GC's empty rooms (ephemeral — no persistence). The `authorize({ room, token, req })` hook is the per-room/per-doc gate (return false/throw → close 4401 before any data). **Default allows everything (dev only) — production MUST supply it.** Pass `server` to attach to an existing `http.Server`. **Awareness-stateful** (a deliberate departure from the otherwise-stateless doc relay): each room holds a `y-protocols` `Awareness` + a `socketClients: Map<WsSocket, Set<clientId>>`; a single `awareness.on('update')` handler is the ONE broadcast path (covers relayed client updates AND `removeAwarenessStates` removals — fans to all-but-origin-socket, or to ALL when origin is the `'disconnect'` string); a NEW client is sent the room's current presence on connect (instant join-presence — the relay filters its OWN clientId so no phantom relay-self leaks); a socket close PURGES that socket's clientIds + broadcasts the removal (the GUARANTEE a crashed client's cursor disappears even with no clean departure announce). `MSG_AWARENESS` frames are NEVER applied to the room doc.
- **Honest limits:** CRDTs prevent lost UPDATES, not semantic conflicts (scalar LWW drops the loser; text/list keep both ops but may interleave nonsensically — never market "never lose data"); a synced app ships ~60KB+ gz (`yjs`+`y-indexeddb`+WS client); authz is table-stakes; native/PMTC sync out of near-term scope (seam keeps the Loro-via-FFI door open).
- Manifest-driven docs: `packages/fundamentals/sync/src/manifest.ts` feeds `llms.txt` / `llms-full.txt` / MCP `api-reference`. Full reference: `docs/src/content/docs/sync.md`.

### @pyreon/lint

- `lint(options?)` — programmatic API: lint files, returns `LintResult` with counts
- `lintFile(filePath, sourceText, rules, config)` — lint a single file
- `listRules()` — returns metadata for all 91 rules
- `applyFixes(sourceText, diagnostics)` — apply auto-fixes
- `loadConfig(cwd)` — load `.pyreonlintrc.json` / `package.json` `"pyreonlint"` field
- `createIgnoreFilter(cwd)` — load `.pyreonlintignore` + `.gitignore` patterns
- `AstCache` — FNV-1a hash-keyed AST cache for repeat runs
- `watchAndLint(options)` — file watcher with 100ms debounce, re-lints changed files
- CLI: `pyreon-lint [--preset recommended|strict|app|lib|best-practices] [--fix] [--format text|json|compact] [--quiet] [--list] [--watch] [--config path] [--ignore path] [--rule id=severity] [path...]`
- **CLI colors follow the Pyreon brand handoff (#651), CLI spec §6.5** — `reporter.ts` uses the self-contained `lint/src/ansi.ts` (mirrors `@pyreon/cli`'s `doctor/render/ansi.ts`; no shared dep — both packages deliberately avoid a runtime ANSI lib). Brand tokens → nearest **xterm-256** 8-bit SGR (`38;5;N`); the handoff mandates "256-color must survive (no truecolor-only)", so no `38;2;r;g;b`. Mapping: error→ember-core (202), warning→ember-warm (220), info→cyan (45); glyphs `✗`/`!`/`ℹ`; file path `bold`, loc/ruleId `dim`. Ember stays scarce (only error/warning severities). Also closed a pre-existing gap: the reporter previously emitted raw ANSI unconditionally — `ansi.ts` adds the standard `NO_COLOR` / `FORCE_COLOR` / `isTTY` gate (parity with the doctor renderer). `--format json|compact` unchanged (machine formats, no color).
- 91 rules across 18 categories: reactivity (14), jsx (11), lifecycle (6), performance (6), ssr (4), architecture (10), store (3), form (4), styling (4), hooks (3), accessibility (3), router (5), ssg (3), frontend (11), query (1), rx (1), i18n (1), storage (1)
- **Opt-in best-practice rules** (`meta.optIn`): the `frontend` (a11y/CLS — `require-img-alt`, `img-requires-dimensions`, `no-positive-tabindex`, `prefer-zero-image`, `no-discarded-optimize-fields`, `no-autofocus`, `no-redundant-role`, `anchor-is-valid`, `heading-order`, `color-contrast`), `query` (`query-options-as-function`), `rx` (`rx-prefer-pipe`), `i18n` (`i18n-prefer-trans-for-rich-jsx`), `storage` (`no-storage-write-as-call`) categories + form's `no-signal-in-form-initial-values` + router's `prefer-typed-search-params` default **off** in `recommended`/`strict`/`app`/`lib`; the `best-practices` preset enables them wholesale, or enable per-rule in `.pyreonlintrc.json`. Library-scoped opt-in rules **auto-gate on `package.json` deps** via `utils/project-deps:isProjectDependency` (a project without `@pyreon/query` / `@pyreon/storage` never sees those rules — zero config, zero noise). Each carries a prescriptive AI-actionable fix message; `no-positive-tabindex`, `no-autofocus`, `no-redundant-role`, `no-storage-write-as-call` AND `query-options-as-function` are **auto-fixable** (`--fix`). `query-options-as-function` is ALSO a proactive MCP `validate` detector (`@pyreon/compiler` `detectPyreonPatterns`, PR #633) — an AI agent sees the fix BEFORE commit, not just after running lint.
  - **2026-Q2 frontend a11y additions**: `pyreon/no-autofocus` (autoFocus/autofocus attr disorients SR/keyboard users — fixable, removes the attr; skips `autoFocus={false}`), `pyreon/no-redundant-role` (a `role` that duplicates the element's implicit ARIA role — conservative tag→role map, `a`→`link` only with static `href`, dynamic/component skipped — fixable, removes the attr), `pyreon/anchor-is-valid` (`<a>` with no `href` or `href` of `""`/`#`/`javascript:` — not fixable, intent is ambiguous; `href={dynamic}` skipped). `control-needs-label` deliberately deferred: label/aria-label association needs cross-element id/scope resolution an AST walker can't do without false positives — the explicit "high-risk cliff" the codebase avoids.
  - **2026-Q2 `storage` category**: `pyreon/no-storage-write-as-call` (dep-gated `@pyreon/storage`) — `useStorage`/`useSessionStorage`/`useCookie`/`useIndexedDB`/`useMemoryStorage` return a `StorageSignal`; `s(next)` reads-and-discards like any signal call. Same proven conservative shape as the `signal-write-as-call` detector (tracks the `const s = useStorage(...)` binding, fires only on a bare-identifier call with ≥1 arg, skips `.set`/`.update`/`.remove` and zero-arg reads). Fixable: `s(x)` → `s.set(x)`.
- New in 2026-05: `pyreon/no-heavy-import-only-in-handler` (performance, warn) — flags a statically-imported heavy module (`@pyreon/charts|code|flow|document`, + configurable `heavyModules`) referenced ONLY inside JSX `on*` event handlers or post-setup/teardown lifecycle callbacks (`onMount`/`onUnmount`/`onCleanup`). The static import forces the heavy chunk into the initial bundle even though nothing touches it until the user interacts; the fix is a dynamic `await import()` inside the handler. The PRECISE counterpart to the blunt info-level `pyreon/no-eager-import` (which fires on EVERY heavy static import incl. render-time ones) — this one fires only when EVERY reference is provably deferred, so the fix is unambiguous and there is no "but I need it at render" false positive. Conservative by construction (any eager reference suppresses the report). **`effect` / `renderEffect` are deliberately NOT treated as deferred** — their callbacks run synchronously during component setup (the `no-imperative-effect-on-create` shape), so a heavy module used in an effect body is a render-time dependency, not a deferrable one. That exclusion was surfaced by the real-corpus e2e (`examples/app-showcase/.../LivePreview.tsx` calls `@pyreon/document`'s `render` inside an `effect` — a legit reactive render, not a defer opportunity; treating `effect` as deferred made the rule false-positive there). Distilled from the Tier-2 resumability spike's L3 heavy-import detection — the one part of that analysis with zero false-positive risk; the runtime thesis didn't survive measurement, this defensive lint use of the same detection did. Own-recursion `Program` walk (oxc passes no parent/exit), `JSXIdentifier` element-name handling so `<Chart/>` counts as a render-time use. 14 specs, bisect-verified (disabling the eager-guard collapses it to `no-eager-import` — 4 conservative DOES-NOT-FIRE specs fail); validated against all 577 example `.ts(x)` files → zero false positives.
- New in 2026-Q2: `pyreon/no-process-dev-gate` (architecture, error, auto-fixable) — flags bundler-coupled dev gates: `typeof process !== 'undefined' && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` (dead in Vite browser bundles) AND `import.meta.env.DEV` / `(import.meta as ViteMeta).env?.DEV === true` (Vite/Rolldown-only — undefined and silent in Webpack/Next.js, esbuild, Rollup, Parcel, Bun). Auto-fixes both to bundler-agnostic `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`, the universal library convention used by React, Vue, Preact, Solid. The companion `pyreon/dev-guard-warnings` recognises `if (process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production') return` as a valid early-return guard.
- New in T1.1 Phase 4: `pyreon/require-browser-smoke-test` (architecture, error, in `recommended`/`strict`/`lib`, off in `app`) — every browser-categorized package must ship at least one `*.browser.test.{ts,tsx}` file under `src/`. Locks in the T1.1 smoke harness so new browser packages can't quietly ship without coverage. `additionalPackages` option opts new packages in, `exemptPaths` opts out.
- New in 2026-05: `pyreon/storage-signal-v-forwarding` (reactivity, error) — flags a wrapper callable that delegates `.direct` to a base signal without forwarding the internal `_v` field via getter. The compiler-emitted `_bindText` fast path reads `source._v` directly (skipping the function call) for the JSX shape `{() => signal()}`, so a callable that has `.direct` but not `._v` silently binds to `undefined` — initial render and every subsequent subscriber notification write `''` to the textNode. Catches the bug class fixed in PR #546 (where `@pyreon/storage`'s 5 reactive primitives shipped this shape from inception for ~9 months). Per-function scope, no false positives on plain `signal()` implementations (their `.direct = _direct` RHS is a bare Identifier, not a delegate). The rule's tests serve as both contract documentation and bisect-verify canary against the canonical `createStorageSignal` shape. Locked into `recommended` / `strict` / `app` / `lib` automatically via `buildRecommended` reading `allRules` severities — no per-preset wiring needed.
- 4 presets: `recommended`, `strict` (warns→errors), `app` (lib rules off), `lib` (strict + architecture)
- Powered by `oxc-parser` — ESTree/TS-ESTree AST with Visitor
- **Per-rule options** via ESLint-style tuple form in config — `"pyreon/no-window-in-ssr": ["error", { "exemptPaths": ["packages/core/runtime-dom/"] }]`. Rules that support path-based exemption read `options.exemptPaths: string[]`. Each rule declares its option shape in `meta.schema` (`Record<string, 'string' | 'string[]' | 'number' | 'boolean'>`); wrong-typed values disable the rule and surface an error on `LintResult.configDiagnostics`, unknown keys emit a warning. The Pyreon monorepo's `.pyreonlintrc.json` at repo root configures server-only / DOM-runtime / hook-foundation exemptions that were previously hardcoded in rule source. JSON Schema for the config file ships at `@pyreon/lint/schema/pyreonlintrc.schema.json` (reference via `"$schema"` for IDE autocomplete). CLI flag `--rule-options id='{json}'` passes options for a single run.
- **`no-window-in-ssr` precision.** Recognised safe contexts: `onMount`, `onUnmount`, `onCleanup`, `effect`, `renderEffect`, `requestAnimationFrame` (entire call arguments are safe). `watch(source, cb)` is handled precisely: only the 2nd arg (callback) is safe — the 1st (source) is evaluated at setup to track signals, so browser globals there still fire. Recognised typeof guards: `if (typeof X !== 'undefined')` body, ternary consequent, const-captured idiom (`const isBrowser = typeof window !== 'undefined'; if (isBrowser) { … }`), negated-form early returns (`if (typeof X === 'undefined') return` + OR-chained form), logical-and guards where either side is a typeof-derived const (`IS_BROWSER && active() ? <Portal target={document.body} /> : null`), and const bindings from AND-chains / ternaries where any term is a typeof check (`const useVT = _isBrowser && meta && typeof document.startViewTransition === 'function'`, `const handler = _isBrowser ? fn : null`). Identifiers in type position (`let x: Window`, `type T = Document`, etc.), member-expression property names (`x.addEventListener`), object-property keys, import-specifier names, **function-parameter names that happen to match a browser global** (`function push(location) { location.X }` — the parameter shadows `window.location`), and **module-level imports that shadow a browser global** (`import { history } from '@codemirror/commands'` — every later `history` references the import, not `window.history`; same for default and namespace imports) are all skipped. Test files (`__tests__/`, `*.test.*`) and `no-unbatched-updates` are both test-exemptable via `exemptPaths`. **oxc visitor gotcha**: oxc's walker does NOT pass `parent` — `VisitorCallback = (node: any) => void`. Rules needing parent context must use enter/exit depth counters or pre-mark child nodes via WeakSet on the way in. Inert `parent?.type === '…'` checks were the root cause of several silent false-positive clusters.
- **`no-imperative-navigate-in-render` precision.** Fires ONLY when `navigate()` / `router.push()` runs synchronously in the component function body (the actual infinite-render-loop case). Any nested function inside the component body — event handler (`const handleClick = (e) => router.push(…)`), `setTimeout`/`setInterval` callback, `requestAnimationFrame` callback, lifecycle hook, `.then()` callback — is deferred execution and doesn't fire. Previously only recognised `onMount`/`effect`/`onUnmount` by name; now tracks a nested-function depth counter that covers every deferred-execution shape.
- **`no-dom-in-setup` safe contexts.** `document.querySelector`/`getElementById`/etc. are silent inside `onMount`, `onUnmount`, `onCleanup`, `effect`, `renderEffect`, AND `requestAnimationFrame` (the callback always runs inside a browser frame post-setup). Also recognises early-return-on-typeof guards at function head (`if (typeof document === 'undefined') return|throw …`) — same heuristic as `no-window-in-ssr` — **AND the canonical `@pyreon/reactivity` SSR primitive: `if (isServer) return|throw` / `if (!isClient) return|throw`** (recognised by name, like `dev-guard-warnings`'s `__DEV__`). This last form is load-bearing for consistency with `pyreon/prefer-isserver`: that rule pushes the `typeof document` guards TO `isServer`, so `no-dom-in-setup` must accept `isServer` as the same guard or the two rules contradict (prefer-isserver says "use isServer", then no-dom-in-setup flags the now-"unguarded" DOM access). Surfaced during the prefer-isserver framework burn-down — migrating a guard to `isServer` introduced 5 false-positive `no-dom-in-setup` findings until the rule learned the primitive.
- **Universal `fetch`.** Removed from the `no-window-in-ssr` browser-globals set — `fetch` is universal in Node 18+, Bun, Deno, browsers, and edge runtimes. Code using it isn't browser-specific. (`XMLHttpRequest` and `WebSocket` remain DOM-only.)
- **`no-window-in-ssr` typeof-guard functions.** A function whose body is `return <typeof check>` (or AND-chain of typeof checks) counts as a typeof guard at its call sites — e.g. `function isBrowser() { return typeof window !== 'undefined' }` makes `if (!isBrowser()) return` an early-return guard for the rule. Both function declarations and `const fn = () => …` form are recognised. Conventional names `isBrowser` / `isClient` / `isServer` / `isSSR` are pre-seeded so cross-module imports work without follow-the-import analysis (same name-convention basis as `dev-guard-warnings` recognising `__DEV__`).
- **Early-return guard `throw` form.** Both `no-window-in-ssr` and `no-dom-in-setup` recognise `if (typeof X === 'undefined') throw …` as an early-return guard (in addition to `return`). Common in entry-point functions like `startClient` that hard-fail in SSR rather than silently no-op.
- **`no-bare-signal-in-jsx` skip allowlist.** Skips call-expressions in JSX text whose callee name is one of `use…`/`get…`/`is…`/`has…`/`[A-Z]…` (hook / component conventions) OR a framework VNode-producing helper: `render` (`@pyreon/ui-core`), `h` (`@pyreon/core` hyperscript), `cloneVNode` (`@pyreon/core`). Their JSX call sites always produce a VNode, not a signal value. User-defined signals named identically would slip through — rename to `rendered`/`hyperscript`/etc. if you hit that.
- **`dev-guard-warnings` dev-flag recognition.** Accepts `__DEV__`, `import.meta.env.DEV` / `import.meta.env?.DEV`, `&&`/ternary test expressions, early-return guards (`if (!__DEV__) return` at function head), and locally-bound consts (`const flag = import.meta.env.DEV === true`). Recognised identifier names: `__DEV__`, `IS_DEV`, `IS_DEVELOPMENT`, `isDev` — extensible per project via the `"devFlagNames": ["__DEBUG__"]` rule option (merged with built-ins). The rule can't follow cross-module imports, so the name is the contract — pick one of the four defaults (or the user-configured list) for imported flags.
- **Inline suppression comments.** Two equivalent syntaxes: `// pyreon-lint-ignore <rule-id>` (legacy / short) and `// pyreon-lint-disable-next-line <rule-id>` (long-form, matches several rules' docstrings). Both suppress diagnostics on the IMMEDIATELY following line. Omitting the rule ID suppresses all rules on the next line. The runner accepts both prefixes — earlier docs documented `disable-next-line` while only `ignore` was implemented; that gap is closed.

### @pyreon/router — New Features

- **`resolveRoute` hot path (2026-06 overhaul) — fastest router at realistic table sizes on `bench:router`** (vs find-my-way / Hono / radix3 / react-router / TanStack / vue-router / path-to-regexp): 1.00× leader at 50 + 200 routes, ahead of radix3 at every size; only Hono's mega-regex leads the 10-route toy table (and measures ~4.5× SLOWER than Pyreon at 50+). The shape, in priority order: (1) **identity memo + single WeakMap probe** for the per-`routes`-array index; (2) **null-prototype dictionary** `staticMap`/`segmentMap` (~3× faster hit than `Map`; hostile keys like `__proto__` are plain own props); (3) **`validateFn` precomputed per flattened route** at flatten time (leaf→root, most-specific wins) so resolves never walk the matched chain; (4) **offset-walking fast lane** for plain paths (no `%` / `//` / trailing slash, certified by a one-pass `scanCleanPath`) — static segments compare in place via `startsWith`-at-offset, only param values slice, no parts array; weird shapes route to the preserved split-based general lane, so edge semantics are unchanged by construction; (5) **per-bucket segment-count dispatch** (`BucketDispatch.exact[n]`) for all-fixed buckets — count-mismatch rejects disappear structurally; buckets containing splat/optional candidates return `null` and keep the ordered flat scan because **definition-order priority (first match wins) cannot be expressed count-indexed** (a splat defined before a same-bucket param route must keep winning — bisect-verified spec in `match-fastlane.test.ts`); (6) **frozen empty singletons** for no-params/query/search results (the `meta`-freeze precedent — mutation of an EMPTY result field throws instead of polluting a shared object; non-empty values stay fresh per resolve). Reference: `packages/core/router/src/match.ts` (`scanCleanPath` / `matchFlattenedFast` / `buildBucketDispatch` / `EMPTY_PARAMS`); specs `src/tests/match-fastlane.test.ts` (lane equivalence + priority + frozen contract + validateFn).
- **URL hash/query split follows WHATWG order** (fixed in the same overhaul): fragment = everything after `#`, query sits between `?` and `#`. Pre-fix, `?` split first — `/user/42?tab=posts#bio` leaked the hash into the query (`{ tab: 'posts#bio' }`) and a `?` inside a fragment was misread as a query separator. Two legacy specs had CODIFIED the wrong order (the "test codified the bug" trap) and were corrected.
- `useIsActive(path, exact?)` — returns reactive boolean for whether a path matches the current route
- Segment-aware prefix matching: `/admin` matches `/admin/users` when `exact` is false
- `useTypedSearchParams({ page: 'number', q: 'string' })` — typed search params with auto-coercion
- `useTransition()` — returns a reactive accessor `() => boolean` (call it: `useTransition()()`), true during route transitions. `useMiddlewareData()` likewise returns `() => Record<string, unknown>` — both are accessors, not destructurable objects
- Hash scrolling — navigating to `#id` auto-scrolls to the matching element
- Route error boundaries — `errorComponent` on route records catches render errors (not just loader errors)
- View Transitions API — auto-enabled for route navigations, opt out per route via `meta.viewTransition: false`
- Middleware chain — `RouteMiddleware` with `ctx.data` for passing data between middleware, `useMiddlewareData()` to read in components
- `Router<TNames>` generic — typed named navigation, compile-time checked (`createRouter<'home' | 'user'>({ routes })` → `router.push({ name: 'typo' })` is a TS error)
- `aria-current="page"` on active `RouterLink` (WCAG 2.1 accessibility)
- Query parsing decodes `+` as space per `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` spec
- `useTypedSearchParams` guards NaN — non-numeric strings coerce to `0` not `NaN`
- `_middlewareData` properly typed on `ResolvedRoute` (no `as any` casts)
- Prefetch cache capped at 50 entries to prevent unbounded memory growth
- `prefetch="intent"` (default) — prefetches on hover AND focus (keyboard + mouse, so keyboard / screen-reader users get the same head-start as mouse users). Also: `"hover"`, `"viewport"`, `"none"`. **`"viewport"` polish**: the IntersectionObserver uses `rootMargin: '200px'` (fetch starts before the link is fully on screen) and the prefetch is scheduled via `requestIdleCallback` (falls back to `setTimeout(1)`) so it never contends with the scroll the user is performing. The observer disconnects synchronously on first intersection before the idle callback is queued, so scroll jitter can't double-schedule. `RouterLink` prefetch is on by default — the discoverability gap (docs previously omitted `'intent'` and misdocumented the default as `'hover'`) was closed in the prefetch-DX PR; see `docs/src/content/docs/router.md` "Prefetch Strategies".
- `notFound()` + `NotFoundBoundary` — throw `notFound()` in a loader or component to trigger a 404 boundary. `isNotFoundError()` type guard for custom handling
- `redirect(url, status?)` — throw inside a route loader to redirect the navigation BEFORE the layout renders. SSR-side: `@pyreon/server`'s handler catches the thrown error and returns a real HTTP `302`/`307` `Location:` Response (no layout HTML leaks server-side). CSR-side: the router's loader-runner catches and propagates as `router.replace(target)` with redirect-depth bookkeeping. Default status is `307` (method-preserving). Companion guards `isRedirectError()` / `getRedirectInfo()` are exported for custom error boundaries that should let redirects pass through. **Replaces the fragile `onMount + router.push('/login')` workaround** for auth-gates under nested-layout dev SSR + hydration — the prior pattern would briefly render the auth-gated layout before redirecting, leaking authenticated UI structure to anonymous users.
- `LoaderContext.request?: Request` — populated only when a loader runs during SSR (via `prefetchLoaderData(router, path, request)`); `undefined` on every CSR navigation. Lets server-side loaders read cookies / auth headers and decide whether to `redirect()` BEFORE the layout renders. Closes the `request: Request` audit-types finding from the original 0.14.0 baseline (the field was previously typed but not populated by any runtime path).
- **Nested-absolute-path matched-chain fix in `match.ts`**: when fs-router emits absolute paths for nested children (e.g. parent `/app` with child `/app/dashboard`, NOT child `dashboard`), `flattenOne` previously concatenated parent segments with child's already-absolute segments, producing wrong staticPaths like `/app/app/dashboard`. The staticMap lookup missed and `resolveRoute('/app/dashboard')` returned `matched: []` — no SSR rendering happened for any nested-layout route. The fix detects "child path starts with `/`" as the absolute-path signal and uses the child's own segments directly. Relative children (`dashboard`, `:id`) continue to inherit the parent's segments via concatenation. PR #415 fixed this for the dispatcher's pattern-flattening; this PR closes the matching gap inside the router itself.
- `pendingComponent` per route — shown while loader runs, with `pendingMs` (delay before showing) and `pendingMinMs` (minimum display time). Signal-based state machine: hidden → pending → ready
- `validateSearch` per route — transform raw query strings into typed values. Accepts any `(raw: Record<string, string>) => T` function — works with Zod `.parse`, Valibot, or plain functions. Result available on `route.search` and via `useValidatedSearch<T>()`
- `useValidatedSearch<T>()` — reactive accessor for validated search params with structural sharing (shallow-equal check prevents re-renders when unrelated query params change)
- **Loader cache** — key-based caching with dedup and TTL. `loaderKey: ({ params }) => \`user-${params.id}\``controls cache identity.`gcTime`(default 5min) controls expiry.`router.invalidateLoader(key?)` clears cache entries. In-flight dedup prevents duplicate requests for the same key. SWR routes bypass cache for revalidation.

### @pyreon/hooks

- 36 signal-based hooks across 7 categories. Every hook is SSR-safe (browser API access guarded), self-cleaning (registers `onUnmount` for listeners/observers/timers), and signal-native: returns `Signal<T>` / `Computed<T>` / accessor objects, never plain values
- **State**: `useToggle`, `usePrevious`, `useLatest`, `useControllableState`
- **DOM**: `useEventListener`, `useClickOutside`, `useFocus`, `useHover`, `useFocusTrap`, `useElementSize`, `useWindowResize`, `useScrollLock`, `useIntersection`, `useInfiniteScroll`
- **Responsive**: `useBreakpoint` (theme-driven), `useMediaQuery` (raw escape hatch), `useColorScheme`, `useReducedMotion`, `useThemeValue`, `useSpacing`, `useRootSize`
- **Timing**: `useDebouncedValue`, `useDebouncedCallback`, `useThrottledCallback`, `useInterval`, `useTimeout`, `useTimeAgo`
- **Interaction**: `useClipboard` (auto-resets `copied` after 2s), `useDialog` (native `<dialog>`), `useKeyboard`, `useOnline`
- **Data**: `useFetch` — thin reactive JSON fetch (`{ data, error, isPending, refetch }`); the web half of the multiplatform `useFetch` contract (PMTC compiles the same call to native `PyreonFetch` containers)
- **Composition**: `useMergedRef`, `useUpdateEffect` (skips first run), `useIsomorphicLayoutEffect` (layout effect on client, no-op on SSR)
- **`useControllableState({ value, defaultValue, onChange })`** is the canonical controlled/uncontrolled pattern — every `@pyreon/ui-primitives` component uses it. Pass `value` and `defaultValue` as FUNCTIONS so signal reads track reactively. Reimplementing the `isControlled + signal + getter` shape by hand was the #1 anti-pattern across primitives before the helper landed
- **Never reach for `addEventListener` / `removeEventListener` directly in primitives** — use `useEventListener`. Same for observers (`useIntersection` / `useElementSize`) and timers (`useInterval` / `useTimeout`). The cleanup is the hook's job
- **`useBreakpoint` reads the theme**, `useMediaQuery` is raw — use the former for layout decisions tied to the design system, the latter for one-off queries (`(prefers-contrast: more)`, `(orientation: landscape)`, etc.)
- Manifest-driven docs (T2.1 + T2.5.1): `packages/fundamentals/hooks/src/manifest.ts` is the single source for the `llms.txt` bullet + `llms-full.txt` section + MCP `api-reference.ts` region. 14 MCP entries generated from the manifest's enriched `api[]` (was 0 hand-written — hooks had no MCP entries before). Inline-snapshot test (`manifest-snapshot.test.ts`) locks the rendered output locally in addition to the CI `Docs Sync` gate.

### Devtools

Stateful packages expose `./devtools` subpath exports with WeakRef-based registries for introspection. Tree-shakeable — zero cost unless imported. Available for: store, state-tree, form, i18n.

**`@pyreon/devtools` (private, `packages/tools/devtools`)** — the Chrome DevTools extension. `@pyreon/runtime-dom`'s `installDevTools()` (auto-run on first browser `mount()`) attaches `window.__PYREON_DEVTOOLS__` with `version` / `getComponentTree()` / `getAllComponents()` / `highlight(id)` / `onComponentMount(cb)` / `onComponentUnmount(cb)` / `enableOverlay()` / `disableOverlay()`; the extension's `page-hook` reads exactly that surface and bridges it through content-script → background service worker → the **Pyreon** DevTools panel (live component tree, click-to-highlight, inspector, **element-picker toggle** wired to `enable/disableOverlay`). Built via `vl_rolldown_build` to `dist/` (5 entry bundles + manifest/html/css/icons copy; `scripts/sync-manifest.ts` stamps the manifest version from `package.json`). Pure logic (`messages.ts` / `serialize.ts` / `tree.ts`) is unit-tested at 100% under happy-dom; the four browser-sandbox context files are coverage-excluded. `scripts/generate-icons.ts` is a dependency-free PNG encoder rendering the ember-on-ink brand mark. Not published (no npm consumer can load a Chrome extension) — built and loaded unpacked. The panel UI implements the **Claude-Design handoff** (`pyreon-devtools.jsx` + `tokens.css`): the `PxDevChrome` shell (traffic-light title bar w/ inspected origin, glyph+wordmark, ember-gradient active tab underline, breadcrumb + live status) and the `PxArtDevTree` Components split (depth-indented mono tree, hot-row ember **pulse** on fresh mount — the truthful signal-model analog of the design's RE-RENDERED state since Pyreon components mount once — + `SELECTED`-eyebrow inspector). Full design token system + JetBrains Mono/Space Grotesk, dark-default w/ a light block honoring DevTools' theme. The design's other five tabs (Graph/Signals/Effects/Profiler/Console) are implemented in the panel and consume the **reactive-devtools Foundation** — the opt-in `@pyreon/reactivity` registry surfaced as `__PYREON_DEVTOOLS__.reactive` (`activate`/`deactivate`/`getGraph`/`getFires`) by `@pyreon/runtime-dom` (merged: Foundation #703 + tabs #702 + real-app e2e #707). Signals (live node table), Graph (layered SVG dep diagram), Effects (per-node fire lanes), Profiler (100ms fire-frame buckets), Console (page-world eval bridge). The `reactive` field is consumed defensively (runtime-guarded) so a page running an older `@pyreon/runtime-dom` degrades to an explicit "needs the Foundation" notice — never a fake/empty surface (brand brief: honesty over theater). Pure presentation logic (graph layout, fire bucketing) lives in `reactive-view.ts` (100% unit-tested); `panel.ts` stays coverage-excluded (browser-only); polling runs only while a reactive tab is open. Verified at every layer: the component-surface drift lock in `framework-integration.test.ts` Omits `reactive` (it legitimately differed across the two-PR transition); `reactive-e2e.test.ts` drives real `@pyreon/reactivity` primitives through the real hook into the extension's own `layoutGraph`/`bucketFires` (end-to-end, plus a bidirectional drift lock vs `@pyreon/reactivity`'s exported `ReactiveGraph`/`ReactiveNode`/`ReactiveFire`); the `ReactiveDevtools` mirror is an exact structural copy of the Foundation's `PyreonReactiveDevtools`. Web fonts deliberately not loaded (MV3 panel CSP + offline-safety) — design font stacks degrade to system.

**Reactive devtools bridge** (`@pyreon/reactivity` `reactive-devtools.ts` → `__PYREON_DEVTOOLS__.reactive`): a **leak-free** introspection layer over the live signal/computed/effect graph. `activateReactiveDevtools()` / `deactivateReactiveDevtools()` / `isReactiveDevtoolsActive()` / `getReactiveGraph()` (nodes + dependency edges, derived fresh from the real subscriber `_s` Sets) / `getReactiveFires()` (bounded ring-buffer fire timeline), exported from `@pyreon/reactivity` and surfaced on the hook as `reactive.{activate,deactivate,getGraph,getFires}`. **Always-on in `__DEV__`, zero cost in production**: `_rdRegister` / `_rdRecordFire` run for every signal/computed/effect created in dev (so a devtools panel attached AFTER mount sees the full live graph immediately — the activate-after-creation user workflow). The caller-side `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` gate (locked by `reactive-devtools-treeshake.test.ts`, a minified-bundle bisect test) folds the entire chain to dead code in production. `_active` is now a READ gate: `getReactiveGraph()` / `getReactiveFires()` / `getFireSummaries()` return empty when no client has called `activateReactiveDevtools()` — non-attached consumers see nothing even though the registry is populated. `deactivateReactiveDevtools()` does NOT clear the registry (a close+reopen panel cycle re-exposes the live graph); test-only `__resetReactiveDevtoolsForTesting()` drops everything for cross-test isolation. `_captureCallerLocation` is ALSO always-on in `__DEV__` so signals/computeds/effects created BEFORE a devtools client attaches still get loc captured — the LPIH editor inlay-hint surfaces ("🔥 signal fired N×") work uniformly across the activate-after-creation user workflow. Cost is **deferred two-phase**: at capture time, a single cheap `new Error()` allocation (~0.14µs in V8/Bun — the stack is captured but not formatted). The expensive `.stack` formatting + `parseStackLine` is lazily resolved by `getReactiveGraph()` / `getFireSummaries()` at devtools-read time and the result is memoized on the `NodeRec` (Error object becomes GC-eligible after first resolve). Most app signals never have their loc read (LPIH inlay-hints only consume loc for hot lines the user has on screen), so the typical cost per signal is just the cheap Error allocation regardless of count. Most user signals additionally pay 0µs because `@pyreon/vite-plugin`'s `injectSignalLocations` rewrites `signal(0)` → `signal(0, { __sourceLocation })` at build time and the caller short-circuits to the injected value before invoking `_captureCallerLocation`. Verified end-to-end: 477/477 pre-existing signals in `examples/perf-dashboard` get loc populated (100%); 10k-signal runtime-fallback creation runs in ~40ms (9× faster than the eager-parse design, parity with the OLD `_active`-gated zero-cost baseline). Never retains a node (WeakRef + FinalizationRegistry; fire buffer holds only ids+timestamps). Same risk profile as the adjacent `_recordSignalWrite` / perf-harness counter calls. This is the **Foundation** that unblocks the devtools Signals/Graph/Effects/Console tabs (the Profiler tab additionally needs per-frame duration instrumentation — deferred). The opt-in design that shipped before this fix was structurally invisible for ALL user-side "open devtools after the app mounted" workflows — bisect-verified with a 4-scenario controlled experiment against `examples/perf-dashboard` (958 components, 477 live nodes): every scenario returned `0/0/0` pre-fix and `477/112/16-22` post-fix; the `@pyreon/devtools` `verify-extension.ts` step-4 reactive-graph assertion was upgraded from informational to hard `fail()` in the same PR (this is the gap that allowed PR #900's first verification to pass while shipping a broken Foundation against real-world apps).

**Live Program Inlay Hints (LPIH)** (`@pyreon/reactivity` `reactive-devtools.ts` + `lpih-bridge.ts` + `@pyreon/compiler` `lpih.ts` + `@pyreon/lint` LSP integration): surface live runtime data — signal fire counts, effect re-runs, subscriber counts — as **inlay-hint ghost text at the source line** in the editor. Same surface TypeScript uses for inferred types. **No reactive framework today shows runtime data at source lines** for any reactive framework; the data lives in a separate devtools panel that requires context-switching. LPIH closes that gap. Three layers: (1) **Runtime capture** — `signal()` / `computed()` / `effect()` creation captures source location via `new Error().stack` (parsed for V8/JSC/SpiderMonkey), stored alongside the existing devtools registry. New API: `getFireSummaries()` returns fires aggregated by `file:line:col` with `{count, lastFire, kind}`. (2) **Bridge** — at subpath export `@pyreon/reactivity/lpih`: `writeLpihCache(path)` atomically writes the snapshot to a JSON file (tmp + rename); `startLpihPolling(path, intervalMs)` writes repeatedly. Bridge is at the subpath (not main entry) because it depends on `node:fs/promises` (Node-only) and is dev-mode-only integration glue — separation keeps the core reactivity bundle smaller AND clarifies that LPIH writes are an opt-in side channel, not a core primitive (same pattern as `@pyreon/i18n/core`). (3) **LSP** — `@pyreon/lint`'s `textDocument/inlayHint` handler reads `PYREON_LPIH_CACHE` env var on every request, parses, and emits `🔥 <kind> fired N×` hints via the new `firesToCreationSiteFindings()` helper. Compiler side also exports `mergeFireDataIntoFindings()` for the rare case where reactive-read sites coincide with creation lines. **Zero production cost** — entire capture path tree-shakes under `NODE_ENV=production` (locked by the existing `reactive-devtools-treeshake.test.ts`). **Dev-mode opt-in cost**: ~2.2µs per signal creation when devtools active (measured: 100k signals + 10k computeds + 10k effects = 269ms total; per-session real-app cost 0.2-2.3ms — invisible). **Measured impact**: 0.32ms median LSP roundtrip, ~150ms user-perceived save→hint with debounce, **20× faster than the 3-5s devtools-panel workflow** for "is this signal firing?"-type questions. Workflow-step reduction: 9→2 ("which signal fires most?"), 8→2 ("is this effect over-running?"), 10→4 ("did memoization help?"). 60 tests across the three layers (15 source-location + 6 bridge + 24 compiler + 15 LSP integration), bisect-verified (stashing LSP wiring fails 11/15 integration tests). Bridge uses filesystem cache because LSP servers are stdio-only — can't directly IPC with a browser; filesystem is the universal lowest-common-denominator transport. Reference: `packages/core/reactivity/src/{reactive-devtools,lpih-bridge}.ts`, `packages/core/compiler/src/lpih.ts`, `packages/tools/lint/src/lsp/index.ts` (`_readLpihCache` + `liveFires` option). Future: `@pyreon/vite-plugin` build-time location injection eliminates the 2.2µs/creation overhead by replacing stack capture with compile-time literals. Future: VS Code / Neovim extension that auto-wires `startLpihPolling` + `PYREON_LPIH_CACHE` for zero-config setup.

**The framework registers components POST-ORDER** — `mount.ts` calls `registerComponent(id, name, el, parentId)` *after* a component's subtree has mounted, so children register before their parent. `registerComponent` only pushes a child into `parent.childIds` if the parent is already in the registry at that moment — which it never is under post-order. **Consequence: a parent entry's `childIds` is empty in `getAllComponents()` output; only `parentId` (captured from the mounting stack at mount *start*) is reliable.** The extension's `tree.ts:getChildren()` rebuilds the tree by indexing on `parentId`; the panel renders from that, never from `childIds`. This was caught by `src/tests/framework-integration.test.ts` (real `mount()` → live hook → extension's own `serialize`/`buildMap`/`getChildren`/`getRoots`), which also carries a compile-time bidirectional assignability lock between the extension's local `PyreonDevtools`/`DevtoolsComponentEntry` mirror (`src/types.ts`) and `@pyreon/runtime-dom`'s exported types — a framework API add/rename/remove fails `tsc` instead of the extension silently losing a capability. Any consumer reading `getAllComponents()` (not just this extension) must reconstruct child links from `parentId`, not trust `childIds`.

## Key Architectural Patterns

### Workspace resolution (no build needed for dev)

Each package.json has `"bun": "./src/index.ts"` in exports.
Root tsconfig has `"customConditions": ["bun"]`.

**Bootstrap on fresh worktree/clone + mtime drift detection**: the `postinstall` script (`scripts/bootstrap.ts`) automatically builds all packages if any `lib/` directory is missing OR if any package's source is newer than its `lib/` (stale build, e.g. after `git pull` that touches package sources). This is needed because Vite's config bundler hardcodes `conditions: ["node"]` and resolves `import: "./lib/index.js"` — which must reflect the current source. The bootstrap runs `bun run --filter='./packages/*/*' build` (~45s) when rebuild is needed, otherwise no-ops in ~30ms (single mtime walk). You do NOT need to run `bun run build` manually after cloning, creating a worktree, or pulling changes — `bun install` handles it. **If you change package source files locally and run an example build that fails with confusing errors (`MISSING_EXPORT`, missing files, unexpected route shapes), run `bun scripts/bootstrap.ts` to rebuild stale lib/** — this catches the case where you edited source mid-session without re-running `bun install`.

**Bootstrap fails loudly on partial state (post-#398 + gap #3 closure).** After the build subprocess returns, the bootstrap re-runs the dirty-detection check against each originally-dirty package. If ANY are still missing or stale, the script exits nonzero — even on the postinstall path. PR #398 made manual / CI invocations exit nonzero on full build failure, but the postinstall path still swallowed silently because "aborting bun install over a transient lib build is worse than continuing." Gap #3 closed the remaining hole: silent partial state is **worse** than a failed install, because devs running `bun run dev` use the bun condition → `src/` and never touch `lib/` — they don't notice missing `lib/` until production-build time, far from the cause. Escape hatch: `PYREON_BOOTSTRAP_SOFT=1` swallows the postcondition failure (the install completes but `lib/` stays incomplete; consumers see confusing build errors until you re-run bootstrap manually). Companion env var `PYREON_BOOTSTRAP_FORCE_FAIL=1` jumps straight to the failure path for end-to-end testing of exit-code behavior.

**Bootstrap content + retry (post gap-#6 / gap-#3 follow-up).** Two defensive layers added on top of the postcondition check:

1. **`lib/index.js` content sanity** — the original postcondition only verified `lib/` directory existed and src/lib mtime ordering. If a prior bootstrap run crashed mid-write, wrote a 0-byte file, or hit a transient resource issue, the file's presence and recent mtime both look fine — but consumers would hit `MISSING_EXPORT` errors at example-build time. The check uses a **50-byte floor**: real Pyreon `lib/index.js` entries are hundreds to thousands of bytes, even the smallest. A package whose `lib/index.js` is <50 bytes is structurally broken — flagged as `[stale]` in BOTH the dirty-detection (catches broken state from a prior run on the next bootstrap) AND the postcondition (catches a current-run build that emitted empty output).
2. **Single sequential retry pass** — if any packages are still dirty after the first build, the bootstrap retries ONLY those packages, one at a time, via per-package `bun run --filter='@pyreon/X' build`. Sequential per-package retry avoids the parallel-load issues that may have caused the first failure (topological-order race, file-handle limits, native-binary link race after `bun install`). **Capped at one retry** — never recurse, never infinite-loop. Logs a counter line on success: `[bootstrap] Retry recovered N package(s) (first-pass-failed: M, retry-fixed: N, still-dirty: K)`. If retry also fails, the original failure-surfacing path runs (exit nonzero with per-package detail). The `PYREON_BOOTSTRAP_FORCE_FAIL=1` injection short-circuits retry so the test harness can verify exit-1 termination without burning 2 min of build time.

**Troubleshooting bootstrap failures.** If `bun install` fails on the bootstrap step:

1. **Most common**: a single workspace package failed to build (transient race, missing dep, source error). Run `bun run --filter='./packages/<category>/<pkg>' build` for the named package to see the per-package output; the bootstrap's stderr output names which packages are still dirty.
2. **If you need to unblock `bun install` immediately** (e.g. about to install a new dep that's required for the bootstrap to succeed): `PYREON_BOOTSTRAP_SOFT=1 bun install`. This restores the pre-#435 swallow-on-postinstall behaviour for one run — the install completes, `lib/` stays partial, you must re-run `bun scripts/bootstrap.ts` to complete the build before your next example build / production deploy.
3. **If `git push` isn't running validation**: your `core.hooksPath` is set to a real custom location (husky / lefthook). The bootstrap installer doesn't clobber it. Either chain Pyreon's hook into your existing pre-push, OR `git config --unset core.hooksPath` and re-run `bun scripts/install-git-hooks.ts`. **Note**: if `core.hooksPath` happened to be set to the default `<git-dir>/hooks` location (an older bootstrap may have done this explicitly), the installer now recognises that as "no real override" and replaces it with `.githooks/` — you don't need to do anything manually.

### Signal implementation

`signal<T>()` returns callable function with `.set()` and `.update()`.
Direct subscribers use a single-subscriber inline slot (`_d1`), promoting to a `Set` only on the 2nd subscriber (the dominant `<For>`-row case allocates no Set); effect subscribers use a lazy `Set`. `createSelector`'s per-key buckets use the same inline-first-subscriber shape (PR #1537). Batch uses pointer swap.

### JSX & VNode

- JSX configured via `jsxImportSource: "@pyreon/core"` in root tsconfig (`jsx: "preserve"`)
- JSX automatic runtime: `@pyreon/core/jsx-runtime` (jsx, jsxs, Fragment)
- `h<P extends Props>(type, props, ...children)` — lower-level API, children stored in `vnode.children`
- Components must merge: `props.children = vnode.children.length === 1 ? vnode.children[0] : vnode.children`
- `ComponentFn<P> = (props: P) => VNodeChild`
- `VNodeChild = VNodeChildAccessor | VNodeChildAtom | VNodeChildAtom[]` — accessor-first so `{() => cond && <X />}` typechecks
- `VNodeChildAccessor = () => VNodeChildAtom | VNodeChildAtom[]` — reactive child expression
- `VNodeChildAtom = VNode | string | number | boolean | null | undefined` — `boolean` included so `&&` patterns work without ternary
- `<For each={items} by={r => r.id}>{r => <li>...</li>}</For>` — keyed list rendering
  - Prop is `by` (not `key`) because JSX extracts `key` as a special VNode reconciliation prop
- `class` prop accepts strings, arrays, objects, or nested mix — processed by `cx()`. In the compiled template fast path, a dynamic class binding emits `typeof v === "string" ? v : _cx(v)` (string passthrough, array/object → `cx`), mirroring the runtime `applyProp` path (`runtime-dom/src/props.ts`). Before the binding-fidelity fix the fast path assigned the raw value, so reactive `class={[...]}` rendered `"a,b"` and `class={{...}}` rendered `"[object Object]"`. The injected import is aliased — `import { cx as _cx } from "@pyreon/core"` — because `cx` is a PUBLIC export a hand-written component may already import (a bare `cx` injection would collide: "Identifier `cx` has already been declared", which broke the docs build).
- JSX index signature narrowed to `[key: \`data-${string}\`]` and `[key: \`aria-${string}\`]` only (catches typos)
- `TargetedEvent<E>` types `currentTarget` per element — no manual `as HTMLInputElement` casts
- New events: `onBeforeInput`, `onInvalid`, `onResize`, `onToggle`, `onFocusIn`, `onFocusOut`
- `onFocusIn` / `onFocusOut` are the **bubbling** focus events (vs non-bubbling `onFocus`/`onBlur`), so a handler on a container fires when focus moves to/from any descendant — e.g. pausing a `<Toaster>` region's auto-dismiss when a keyboard user tabs into a toast. Already in `DELEGATED_EVENTS` (the runtime delegated them since inception via the generic `on*` → lowercased event-name path — `onFocusIn` → `focusin`); this just adds the missing JSX types in `@pyreon/core` (`jsx-runtime.ts`). The `@pyreon/toast` Toaster uses them to mirror its pause-on-hover with pause-on-focus.
- `style` prop accepts both string (`style="color: red"`) and object (`style={{ color: "red", fontSize: "14px" }}`)
  - String: inlined as HTML attribute by compiler
  - Every compiled style binding (static object, reactive object, thunk, or string) emits `_setStyle(el, value)` — the runtime `applyStyleProp` helper exported from `@pyreon/runtime-dom`. So a compiled style binding normalizes IDENTICALLY to the `applyProp`/`h()` path: string → `cssText`; object → per-property `setProperty` with kebab-casing + `normalizeStyleValue` (number→px) + **stale-key removal** (a reactive object going `{color,fontSize}` → `{color}` drops `fontSize`); dynamic bindings are wrapped in a reactive `_bind`. Before the binding-fidelity fix, object styles took a one-shot `Object.assign` (static — `style={{ color: theme() }}` never updated, no number→px, no key-removal) and the `() => ({...})` thunk emitted `cssText = <object>` → `"[object Object]"` → **no styles at all**. Both class and style now match the runtime `applyProp` value-normalization in BOTH backends (JS + Rust native), locked by `native-equivalence.test.ts` + runtime DOM regression specs in `runtime-dom/src/tests/compiler-integration.test.tsx`.

### Props Utilities

- `splitProps(props, keys)` — split props object preserving signal reactivity
- `mergeProps(...sources)` — merge default props with component props, last source wins
- `removeUndefinedProps(props)` — copy props dropping keys whose DATA value is `undefined`, preserving getter-shaped reactive props verbatim (descriptor-copy, never value-copy). The filter every prop-forwarding HOC runs before `mergeProps`. `@pyreon/attrs` + `@pyreon/rocketstyle` previously hand-rolled this identically (one shipped a value-copy reactivity bug); both now re-export it from core
- `createUniqueId()` — SSR-safe unique ID generation
- `untrack(fn)` — alias for `runUntracked`, reads signals without subscribing
- **Component-JSX spread `<Comp {...rest}>` preserves reactivity end-to-end.** The compiler emits `<Comp {..._wrapSpread(rest)}>`, which re-brands getter-shaped reactive props as `_rp` thunks. `makeReactiveProps` converts them back to getters on the consumer side. No need to think about which props are reactive when forwarding through spread — it just works. Fast path: sources with no getters return unchanged (zero cost). Reference pattern: `docs/src/content/docs/patterns/reactive-spread.md` (MCP `get_pattern('reactive-spread')`).
- **Manual prop-merging helpers must copy descriptors, not values.** If you write a helper function that copies props in plain JS (not through JSX spread), use `Object.getOwnPropertyDescriptors` + `Object.defineProperty` rather than `result[key] = source[key]` — the latter fires getters at copy time and collapses reactive props to static snapshots. Better: just use `mergeProps` / `splitProps` / `removeUndefinedProps` from `@pyreon/core` (they preserve descriptors). The framework's own HOC pipelines (`@pyreon/rocketstyle`, `@pyreon/styler`, `@pyreon/ui-core`, `@pyreon/elements`) follow this rule.

### JSX Types

- `cx(…values: ClassValue[]): string` and `ClassValue` exported from `@pyreon/core`
- `PyreonHTMLAttributes`, `CSSProperties`, `StyleValue`, `CanvasAttributes` (typed `Ref<HTMLCanvasElement>`) exported from `@pyreon/core`
- `AriaRole` exported from `@pyreon/core` — the WAI-ARIA 1.2 role union the `role` attribute is typed as: `role?: AriaRole | (() => AriaRole | undefined)`. Gives `role="…"` literal autocomplete + discoverability; the union includes `(string & {})` so it stays OPEN (any string still assigns — custom/abstract roles, `role={dynamicString}`, future tokens). Non-breaking DX refinement (so it does NOT type-error on typos — autocomplete only). Mirrors React's `AriaRole`. Type-contract locked by `packages/core/core/src/tests/aria-role.types.test.ts` (bisect-verified: closing the union → the open-ness assertions fail tsc).

### Router

Context-based: `RouterContext = createContext<RouterInstance | null>(null)`.
`RouterProvider` provides the router via `provide()` (owner-based on the client; request-scoped stack on SSR) + sets module fallback.
Hash mode uses `history.pushState` (not `window.location.hash`) to avoid double-update.
View Transitions API integration: route changes wrapped in `document.startViewTransition()` when available.

**What `await router.push()` / `.replace()` waits for** — the ViewTransition object exposes three promises, and picking the wrong one is easy to re-break:

| Promise              | Resolves when                                          | Router awaits?       |
| -------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------- |
| `updateCallbackDone` | Callback (DOM commit) finished; new state is live      | ✅ yes               |
| `ready`              | Snapshot captured, pseudo-elements ready for animation | no — just `.catch()` |
| `finished`           | Full animation completed (typically 200-300ms)         | no — just `.catch()` |

The router awaits `updateCallbackDone` so callers can inspect the new route immediately after `await router.push()`. It does NOT wait for `.finished` because blocking every programmatic navigation on a 200-300ms animation is unacceptable. `.ready` + `.finished` get empty `.catch()` handlers so their `AbortError: Transition was skipped` rejections (fired when a newer navigation interrupts an in-flight transition) don't leak as unhandled promise rejections.

**Hook ordering changed alongside this fix** — `afterEach` hooks and `scrollManager.restore` now fire AFTER the VT callback completes (previously they fired after `commitNavigation` returned but BEFORE the VT callback ran, which meant hooks briefly saw the OLD route state). This is the correct behavior per the hook's documented semantics ("after-navigation hook") but it is a silent behavior change for any app that relied on hooks running pre-commit.
Middleware chain: `RouteMiddleware[]` runs before guards, `ctx.data` passed through, `useMiddlewareData()` reads in components.
Hash scrolling: after navigation, `#id` fragments auto-scroll to matching DOM element.

### SSR

`renderToString(vnode)` + `renderToStream(vnode)` with Suspense streaming.
**`renderToString` is a maybe-sync renderer (2026-06)**: the internal string-render family returns `string | Promise<string>` — fully-sync subtrees concatenate with ZERO promise hops; only a real `async function Component()` promotes its own subtree, with `.then` continuations preserving strict sibling order + provider visibility + trim-after-settle (contract specs: `runtime-server/src/tests/maybe-sync-order.test.ts`). The prior always-async walk paid ~90µs of promise machinery per 500-node page vs ~10µs of HTML work. Measured: renderToString +41-78% per scenario; zero's full handler +24-45% req/s (nested-5-deep 78.6K→114.1K). Public API unchanged (`Promise<string>`); `renderToStream` untouched.
`mergeChildrenIntoProps(vnode)` called before `runWithHooks` in both paths.
`runWithRequestContext(fn)` isolates context + store per request via ALS.
**`renderToString` / `renderToStream` INHERIT an active request context** (Phase 1 render-pipeline unification): inside `runWithRequestContext`, both renderers reuse the request's ALS stack + store so request-level `provide()` frames — `provideRequestLocals(ctx.locals)`, request-scoped DI — are visible to rendered components. Pre-fix they always opened a FRESH `_contextAls.run([], …)`, so the nested scope silently discarded every request-level provide and `useRequestLocals()` could only ever resolve its default inside a component (a shipped, documented-but-broken feature). Bare calls keep the fresh isolated stack. Bisect-locked by `runtime-server/src/tests/request-context-inherit.test.ts` + the locals spec in `server/src/tests/render-page.test.ts`.
**`renderPage()` (`@pyreon/server/src/render-page.ts`) is the ONE string-mode page pipeline** — preload (lazy components + loaders, `redirect()` catch) → render with head collection → CSS-in-JS collect (empty-tag skip) → loader-data inline script → status 404 via the `notFoundComponent` chain → `routeModules` (`component._hmrId`) for SSG modulepreload. Consumed by `createHandler` (string mode), zero's SSG prerender entry, AND zero's dev SSR middleware (loaded via `ssrLoadModule("@pyreon/server")` + a nested-package alias so it shares the user code's module graph — the dual-instance hazard). Template composition stays caller-specific by design (handler: precompiled parts; SSG: `injectIntoTemplate`; dev: Vite-transformed `index.html`); streaming keeps its own pipeline. The drift class this closes: styler tag missing from SSG, dual noindex call sites, serializer divergence — per-page concerns now land in all three consumers at once. Contract: the router must be a per-request instance created AT the path (`preload` warms, it does not navigate).
**The SSR handler resolves lazy route components BEFORE rendering** via `router.preload(path, req)` (not loaders-only `prefetchLoaderData`). `renderToString` is synchronous — an unresolved `lazy()` route component falls back to `RouterView`'s empty loading state, so the page renders BLANK inside the layout (status 200, the unfilled template shell). zero's fs-router emits every route as `lazy()`; `mode: 'ssr'`/`'isr'` shipped empty pages (0.30.0 regression) until the handler switched from `prefetchLoaderData` (loaders only) to `router.preload` (lazy components + loaders + request forwarding + redirect propagation) — the same path SSG already used. `prefetchLoaderData` stays loaders-only because it is also the RouterLink-prefetch path. See `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` → "SSR-rendering Mistakes" (pre-resolve lazy components).
Suspense streaming has a 30s timeout — if async children do not resolve within 30 seconds, the fallback remains.
XSS escape in Suspense swap templates — all template content is properly escaped.
`For` list SSR emits per-item key markers (`<!--k:key-->`) for precise hydration matching.

**Streaming SSR + `@pyreon/styler` — inline `<style>` flushing.** `renderToStream` calls `globalThis.__PYREON_STYLER_FLUSH__()` (registered by `@pyreon/styler`'s `sheet.ts` on SSR module init) (a) ONCE after the synchronous shell render → emits `<style data-pyreon-stream="shell">…</style>` inline at the top of the app body so shell content is correctly styled before any Suspense boundary resolves; (b) inside EVERY `streamSuspenseBoundary`, BEFORE the `<template>` element → emits `<style data-pyreon-stream="<id>">…</style>` so each boundary's resolved HTML arrives with its styles already applied to the page. Closes the FOUC where the final consolidated `<style>` tag would otherwise arrive AFTER the boundary content. No hard `runtime-server → styler` dependency — the runtime reads `globalThis.__PYREON_STYLER_FLUSH__` and no-ops when absent (mirrors `__pyreon_count__` perf-counter pattern, the SSG-plugin styler-tag lookup, and the `__PYREON_SSR_TEMPLATE__` cloudflare-adapter pattern). The styler side: `sheet.flushSSRPending()` returns rules added since the previous flush + advances a watermark; emits `@layer elements, rocketstyle;` on the FIRST flush only; resets cleanly on `reset()` / `clearAll()` / `resetSSRBuffer()` (per-request boundaries). `getStyleTag()` unchanged for SSG / non-streaming SSR. Reference: `packages/ui-system/styler/src/sheet.ts:flushSSRPending` + module-init `globalThis.__PYREON_STYLER_FLUSH__` registration; `packages/core/runtime-server/src/index.ts` (`renderToStream` post-shell flush + `streamSuspenseBoundary` per-boundary flush). Bisect-verified at two layers: 13 sheet unit specs (`__tests__/streaming-flush.test.ts` — watermark + `@layer` ordering + reset semantics) + 7 runtime-server integration specs (`tests/styler-stream-flush.test.ts` — shell + per-boundary ordering, `</style` escape, multi-boundary, no-hook graceful no-op). Observable in `examples/cpa-pw-app-solid` (`mode: 'ssr', ssr: { mode: 'stream' }`). Bundle cost: ~239 gz across the two packages.

### Island Architecture

`island(loader, { name, hydrate, prefetch? })` → async ComponentFn → `<pyreon-island>` element.

**Import `island()` from `@pyreon/server/client`, NOT the `@pyreon/server` main barrel, in any code that ships to the client (the dominant case: a route/component that is bundled client-side for hydration).** `island.ts` is fully client-safe (imports only `@pyreon/core` `h` + `./island-codec`), but the `@pyreon/server` *main barrel* also re-exports `createHandler` / `prerender`, which pull `node:fs/promises` / `node:path` / `node:async_hooks` AND the package's `registerSingleton`. A barrel import (`import { island } from '@pyreon/server'`) therefore drags the entire server module into the client/route bundle → (a) `node:*` externalized-for-browser in the client bundle, and (b) a SECOND `@pyreon/*` instance vs the build's node_modules copy → the singleton sentinel throws (`[Pyreon] Duplicate @pyreon/server detected`) during the SSG render of that route, AND the dual `@pyreon/core` instance splits the context graph so the hydrated island crashes (`Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'ref')`). This is the failure mode that made islands unusable inside `@pyreon/zero` routes (every zero route ships to the client). The fix: `island` (+ `IslandOptions`/`IslandMeta` types) is exported from the CLIENT-safe `@pyreon/server/client` subentry; `check-client-bundle-node-imports` now walks `/client` so it can never regress to pulling a `node:` import.

**Islands work natively in `@pyreon/zero` via a SELF-HYDRATING `island()`.** `@pyreon/zero` re-exports `island` (from `@pyreon/server/client`), so a zero app declares islands with `import { island } from '@pyreon/zero'` — no `@pyreon/server` dependency, `startClient({ routes })` only, no manual `hydrateIslandsAuto`. The runtime reconciliation problem this solves: `@pyreon/zero`'s route is a **reactive child of RouterView**, so on the client the SSR route DOM is **discarded + re-mounted** (`hydrateReactiveChild` → `mountChild`), NOT hydrated in place. That defeats the islands model two ways — (1) an `island()` that renders its component inline is **async**, and rendering an async component inside the host mount/`hydrateRoot` throws with no Suspense boundary (→ the route error boundary swallows it: "An error occurred while rendering this page"); (2) the one-shot external `hydrateIslandsAuto` scan races the async route mount (it runs once after `hydrateRoot`, before the lazy route + its marker mount). **Fix:** the client branch of `island()` (`typeof document !== 'undefined'`) renders ONLY the `<pyreon-island>` marker, then `onMount` dynamically imports `scheduleHydration`/`schedulePrefetch` from `@pyreon/server/client` and mounts the component INTO the marker per the `data-hydrate` strategy — the island OWNS its hydration lifecycle, robust whether the host hydrated or re-mounted. (Dynamic import = client-only → keeps the scheduler out of the SSR graph + avoids a static `client`↔`island` cycle.) **The marker render also captures `getContextOwner()` and `scheduleHydration` re-establishes it (`runWithContextOwner`) around the island's `hydrateRoot`** — under #1338's owner-based context the deferred mount has NO owner chain otherwise, so a `rocketstyle` component inside the island reads an undefined PyreonUI theme and crashes (`reading 'base'`). Capturing at the marker's render (owner active, links up through `_layout`'s PyreonUI) + restoring at hydrate time lets `useContext()` walk to the real provider; static-islands apps (no client owner) pass `null` → detached root, unchanged. 0.30.0 regression; see `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` → "Islands Mistakes" (deferred hydration must re-establish the captured owner). The SERVER branch is unchanged (async `loader()` → marker + content, for SEO/no-JS/first-paint). The static islands app is unaffected — there `island()` runs only at SSR and the client uses `hydrateIslandsAuto`, never this branch. Proven by `e2e/zero-islands.spec.ts` (real-Chromium: island hydrates with no wiring + signal click drives the DOM + zero console errors — Bug 3/F's `reading 'ref'` crash gone) and the 9 islands-showcase strategy specs staying green. Reference: `packages/core/server/src/island.ts` (the `typeof document` branch) + `client.ts` (`export`ed `scheduleHydration`/`schedulePrefetch`). **Follow-up (bundle):** the schedulers could be extracted to a dedicated `island-hydrate.ts` so an island chunk pulls only the scheduler, not the whole `@pyreon/server/client` (which statically imports `@pyreon/router`); deferred to keep this change low-risk.

Client: `hydrateIslands({ Name: () => import(...) })` — strategies: load, idle, visible, **interaction**, media, never. The `interaction` strategy hydrates on first user interaction (`focus` / `click` / `pointerenter` / `touchstart` / `submit` by default; customize via `'interaction(<events>)'` form). **Both click events AND form submits are replayed** post-hydration on the equivalent live element — click via a synthetic `MouseEvent('click')`, submit via a synthetic `SubmitEvent('submit')` re-dispatched on the live form (so the live submit handler reads current `FormData` with the user's input values, instead of the browser doing its full-page POST/GET before hydration).
