The pre-hydrate handler calls `preventDefault()` + `stopImmediatePropagation()` for both, closing the "user clicks/submits but nothing happens until they retry" UX trap AND the more severe "form silently navigates away before the island ever wakes up" data-loss trap. The replay path uses `data-testid` when present, falling back to a tag+child-index walk relative to the island root, which survives the DOM swap that hydrateRoot performs on mismatch / structural reshape. Reference: `packages/core/server/src/client.ts:scheduleInteractionHydration` (the `CapturedInteraction` discriminated union carries the event type so the post-hydrate `dispatchEvent` builds the right synthetic event).

**`hydrate: 'never'` islands MUST NOT have a registry entry.** The whole point of the strategy is shipping zero client JS — registering a loader in `hydrateIslands({ ... })` defeats it by pulling the component module into the client bundle graph. `hydrateIslands` short-circuits before the registry lookup for never-strategy islands so missing entries are silent (NOT a `data-island-error="no-loader"` flag). Reference: `packages/core/server/src/client.ts:hydrateIslands`.

**Island prop codec** (`packages/core/server/src/island-codec.ts`): roundtrip-preserving JSON encoder/decoder pair used by SSR's `serializeIslandProps` + the client's `hydrateIsland`. Replaces the naïve `JSON.stringify` path, which silently lost fidelity: `Date → ISO string`, `Map`/`Set`/`RegExp` → `{}`, `BigInt` → empty-props fallback, class instances → `{}` with no warning. The codec tags non-JSON-native types with an internal `__pyreon_t` marker (`'d'`/`'m'`/`'s'`/`'r'`/`'B'`); the inverse decoder on the client unwraps the marker to restore real `Date`/`Map`/`Set`/`RegExp`/`BigInt`. Plain objects without markers round-trip byte-identically. Objects whose OWN key is literally `__pyreon_t` get a transparent `'e'`-escape wrapping (decoder unwraps; user sees the original shape). **Fail-loud (was: silent `{}`)**: class instances, circular references, and >100-deep nesting emit `IslandPropEncodeError` with a `$.foo.bar`-style path + offender name + island name; the caller (`serializeIslandProps`) catches and falls back to empty props as before, BUT the dev-mode `console.error` now NAMES the offender instead of hiding it as a generic "BigInt or circular reference" message. Forward-compatible decoder: unknown tag values pass through verbatim so an older `client.ts` doesn't crash on a future-encoded type. Tests at `packages/core/server/src/tests/island-codec.test.ts` (21 roundtrip + escape + fail-loud + forward-compat specs) + 3 contract-update tests in `tests/server.test.ts` (BigInt now roundtrips, class instance fails loud, circular still falls back). **Contract change for consumers**: code that received `Date` props as ISO strings (e.g., `new Date(props.someDate)` to revive) still works (Date constructor accepts Date); `typeof props.someDate === 'string'` checks would need updating.

**Prefetch hint** (`prefetch: 'idle' | 'visible' | 'none'`, default `'none'`): pair a deferred-hydration strategy with a prefetch hint to pre-warm the chunk BEFORE the hydration trigger fires. With `hydrate: 'visible'` alone, scrolling into view kicks off both the chunk fetch AND the hydration — users see a blank island flash while the chunk arrives. With `hydrate: 'visible', prefetch: 'idle'`, the chunk is fetched during browser idle so the IntersectionObserver fires against an already-warm module cache. Independent scheduling: prefetch and hydration each register their own `requestIdleCallback` / `IntersectionObserver`, fire-and-forget the loader, and rely on JS's import-promise dedup to share the underlying module fetch. Suppressed (no `data-prefetch` attribute emitted) when `hydrate: 'load'` (loader runs synchronously) or `hydrate: 'never'` (defeats zero-JS). Reference: `packages/core/server/src/client.ts:schedulePrefetch`.

**Auto-registry** (`@pyreon/vite-plugin` `islands: true`, default-on as of post-#461 Tier 1). Eliminates the manual sync between `island()` declarations and the client `hydrateIslands({ ... })` call — typo / forgotten entry / registry drift was the #1 author foot-gun. Plugin pre-scans the source tree at `buildStart` for `island(() => import('PATH'), { name, hydrate })` calls (mirrors the existing `prescanSignalExports` pattern), emits a `virtual:pyreon/islands-registry` virtual module the user imports in `entry-client.ts` and passes to `hydrateIslandsAuto(registry)`. Never-strategy islands are deliberately omitted from the auto-registry so their components stay out of the client bundle. **Why the user passes the import explicitly** rather than `hydrateIslandsAuto()` resolving the virtual module itself: Rolldown's static-import analysis runs before plugin `resolveId` hooks for workspace package sources, so an `import 'virtual:...'` inside `@pyreon/server/client` would fail to resolve at build time. Putting the import in the user's `entry-client.ts` (where the plugin's `resolveId` fires natively) is the clean shape. Reference: `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/index.ts` (`prescanIslandDeclarations` / `scanIslandDeclarations` / `renderIslandsRegistry`); manual `hydrateIslands({ ... })` stays public for non-Vite consumers.

**Project-wide audit** (`pyreon doctor --check-islands` + MCP `audit_islands` tool, PR C of the islands DX roadmap). Walks `packages/` and `examples/` and runs five cross-file detectors that auto-registry can't reach AND PR G's per-file `island-never-with-registry-entry` detector misses (it only catches the same-file shape):

1. **`duplicate-name`** — two `island()` declarations with the same `name`. Runtime hydrates only the FIRST loader; every other declaration fails silently with no error flag.
2. **`never-with-registry-entry`** — project-wide cross-file version of PR G's per-file detector. Fires when ANY file's `hydrate: 'never'` declaration matches a key in ANY other file's manual `hydrateIslands({...})` call.
3. **`registry-mismatch`** — manual `hydrateIslands({ X })` entry where `X` has no matching `island()` declaration anywhere. Catches typos / removed islands / forgotten imports. Suppressed implicitly when consumers use auto-registry (`hydrateIslandsAuto()`) — there's nothing to manually sync.
4. **`nested-island`** — an `island()` whose loader-imported file ALSO contains an `island()` call. Outer's `hydrateRoot` would replace the inner subtree before its loader runs.
5. **`dead-island`** — an `island()` declared in a file that no other source imports (statically OR dynamically). Heuristic catches the common shape of "declared but never wired up." Auto-registry's `() => import('PATH')` counts as an import, so registered islands stay alive.

Each finding ships with file path + line/column + actionable fix suggestion. Both detectors emit JSON via `--json` for CI gates. Implementation: [packages/core/compiler/src/island-audit.ts](packages/core/compiler/src/island-audit.ts) — entirely syntactic (TypeScript compiler API, no type-check pass), bisect-verified per-detector in [tests/island-audit.test.ts](packages/core/compiler/src/tests/island-audit.test.ts) (19 tests cover broken + fixed shapes for each finding type, plus discovery + formatter + integration). Bisect-verified at the real-repo level too: planting a typo + a never-strategy registry entry in `examples/islands-showcase` produces both findings with correct line numbers + cross-file pointers.

**Real-app coverage**: `examples/islands-showcase` exercises one island per strategy (Counter / IdleClock / VisibleComments / MobileMenu / StaticBadge), with `VisibleComments` pairing `hydrate: 'visible'` + `prefetch: 'idle'` as the canonical pattern, and uses `hydrateIslandsAuto()`. Real-Chromium e2e gate at `e2e/islands-showcase.spec.ts` + `e2e/islands-showcase-mobile.spec.ts` (separate config `e2e-configs/islands-showcase.config.ts`, separate webServer boot — same isolation rationale as ui-regression / app-showcase / compat-layers). Per-package browser smoke at `packages/core/server/src/tests/islands.browser.test.tsx` covers each strategy in isolation under real `IntersectionObserver` / `requestIdleCallback` / `matchMedia` (the unit-level happy-dom suite at `client.test.ts` cannot exercise these), plus 3 prefetch specs proving the chunk warms BEFORE the hydration trigger fires. Auto-registry unit tests at `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/tests/islands-registry.test.ts` (10 specs covering scanner edge cases — prescan walk skips, never-strategy omission, duplicate-name dedup, missing-name skip, multiple files, stub mode).

### JSX Compiler

**Dual-backend architecture**: Rust native binary (napi-rs, 3.7-8.9x faster) with automatic JS fallback.

- **Rust path** (`packages/core/compiler/native/`): full reactive pass in Rust using `oxc_parser`/`oxc_ast` crates directly — zero JSON serialization, zero JS object traversal. Single-pass recursive walk with `FxHashMap`-cached `isDynamic` analysis. 2,800+ lines of Rust, compiled via `cargo build --release` to a ~1MB `.node` binary.
- **JS fallback** (`src/jsx.ts`): uses `oxc-parser` (Rust NAPI binding) for parsing + JS reactive pass. Activated automatically when the native binary isn't available (CI, WASM, wrong platform).
- **Auto-detection**: `transformJSX()` loads the native binary via `createRequire(import.meta.url)` (ESM-safe), falls back per-call with try/catch so a Rust panic doesn't crash the Vite dev server.
- **527 tests**: 347 original + 180 cross-backend equivalence tests verifying identical output between JS and Rust on Unicode, TypeScript syntax, control flow, classes, string collisions, circular refs, and real-world patterns.

**Dual-backend deep validation (2026-06) — text-vs-vnode classifier made generic (whole-class fix) + a component-prop registration fix; remaining gaps characterized.** The curated `native-equivalence.test.ts` fixtures all pass (380, byte-identical JS↔Rust), but a **644-file real-corpus byte-diff sweep** (every `.tsx`/`.jsx` in `examples/`+`docs/`+`packages/`, run through BOTH backends) surfaced Rust-only divergences the curated set missed. Two were in `contains_jsx_in_expr` (the text-vs-vnode child classifier) and one in component-prop registration. Reduction: 30 → 20 code-diffs, 14 → 4 REAL primitive-profile divergences. The fixes (`native/src/lib.rs`, locked by the `corpus-sweep regressions` describe block, bisect-verified 7/9 fail against the pre-fix binary):
  1. **Text-vs-vnode classifier rewritten to a GENERIC walk (whole-class fix).** The JS oracle (`jsx.ts:containsJSXInExpr`) is a generic recursive walk over EVERY child (`forEachChild`) — returns true if any descendant is a JSXElement/Fragment. The Rust `contains_jsx_in_expr` was a hand-rolled arm-by-arm PARTIAL mirror that drifted and mis-classified nested-JSX shapes as TEXT (`_bind .data` → renders `[object Object]`): `obj?.map(x => <jsx/>)` (JSX in a `ChainExpression`'s call args — hit `@pyreon/zero`'s `image.tsx` `img.formats?.map(f => <source/>)`) and IIFEs `(() => { … return <jsx/> })()` (JSX in the CallExpression CALLEE — hit `@pyreon/zero-content`'s `Playground.tsx`). Both were the SAME class: the partial walk missing a node shape. Rather than patch shapes one at a time, `contains_jsx_in_expr` now uses an `oxc_ast_visit::Visit` walker (a `JsxFinder` that flips a flag on `visit_jsx_element`/`visit_jsx_fragment`) — the trait's default walk IS `forEachChild`, so RS classification is **identical to the JS oracle BY CONSTRUCTION** (both visit every node). This kills the entire "RS misses a nested-JSX shape → `[object Object]`" class, including exotic shapes not present in the corpus. (`oxc_ast_visit = "0.126"` added as a direct dep — it was already a transitive dep of `oxc_parser`.) The component-detection walkers (`body_contains_jsx`/`expr_contains_jsx`/`stmt_contains_jsx`, used by `maybe_register_component_props`) are a SEPARATE concern and left untouched.
  2. **`.map`/any-CallExpression-argument callback param over-bound as reactive** (documented-contract violation + per-row perf). The Rust `in_jsx_child_callback` flag only suppressed component-prop registration for DIRECT JSX-child render callbacks, NOT nested CallExpression-arg callbacks (`items().map((item) => <div key={item.id}><span>{item.label}</span></div>)`), so RS emitted a wasteful per-row `_bind()` for `{item.label}` where JS bakes static `textContent`. Fixed by a new `in_callback_argument` Ctx flag set in the CallExpression arm when the argument is directly an arrow/function, consumed by the arrow/function arms alongside `in_jsx_child_callback` — mirrors JS `jsx.ts:1801` (`parent === CallExpression && arguments.includes(node)`). Attribute-value render fns (`renderItem={(p) => …}`) are NOT call-args → stay reactive props (parity preserved).

  **Remaining 4 code-divergences are STRUCTURAL, not renders-wrong (characterized, not fixed).** All four (`collab-board/CardPanel.tsx`, `zero/image.tsx`, two `_error.tsx`) are the **prop-derived-const inlining heuristic** differing between backends — JS and Rust make different decisions about WHEN to inline a `const` derived from `props.*` at a JSX use site, and the divergence is **bidirectional** (JS inlines `const editor = createEditor(props.x)` into a reactive `_rp(() => …)` where RS keeps the stable `instance={editor}` var — RS arguably safer there, doesn't re-run the factory; conversely RS inlines `const message = props.error…` into a reactive child where JS keeps `message` bare/static). Both backends render correct output for the common case; forcing byte-parity would require aligning the deep transitive-resolution heuristics (`resolveVarToString` ↔ `find_init_in_expression`) — high-risk, not a renders-wrong bug, deferred. The sweep also found **296 reactivity-LENS span-offset divergences** (RS lens spans drift from JS on complex files), but this is an **unconsumed sidecar**: `analyzeReactivity` (the only LSP-facing consumer) forces `transformJSX_JS`, and production codegen is byte-identical with the lens option on/off — so the lens drift has zero production/LSP impact (the `compareLens` gate covers 9 fixtures; a stronger gate is a low-priority follow-up). Reproduce the sweep: a throwaway dual-backend diff script over the corpus (no committed scratch — the `corpus-sweep regressions` fixtures are the permanent lock).

**Signal auto-call**: `const x = signal(...)` and `const x = computed(...)` declarations are tracked. Bare references in JSX are auto-called: `{x}` → `{() => x()}`. Scope-aware — shadowed variables (inner `const x = 'text'`, function parameters, destructured params) are NOT auto-called. Already-called signals (`x()`) are NOT double-called. Cross-module support via the Vite plugin's signal export registry (pre-scans all files in `buildStart`, detects `export const x = signal(`, separate `export { x }`, and `export default signal(`). The `knownSignals: string[]` option on `TransformOptions` seeds the compiler with imported signal names. **Both backends implement signal auto-call**: the Rust binary tracks `signal_vars` / `shadowed_signals` / `is_active_signal` with full scope-aware shadowing semantics, exercised by 15+ cross-backend equivalence tests in [`src/tests/native-equivalence.test.ts`](packages/core/compiler/src/tests/native-equivalence.test.ts) — JS and Rust paths produce byte-identical output for every signal-auto-call pattern.

`shouldWrap` only wraps if the fused `isDynamic` check finds a non-pure call, props/prop-derived access, or signal variable reference.
Static JSX nodes hoisted to module scope as `const _$h0 = ...`.
Template emission: JSX element trees with ≥1 DOM element emit `_tpl()` + `_bind()`.
Supports mixed element+expression children (via `childNodes[]` indexing), multiple expressions, and fragment inlining.
Reactive text writes `TextNode.data` (not `.textContent`). **Sole-dynamic-text children bake a `' '` placeholder text node into the template HTML and grab it via `.firstChild`** — no `createTextNode`/`appendChild` per instantiation (PR #1540; per ROW under `<For>`); mixed element+text content emits a `<!>` comment placeholder swapped via `createTextNode("") + replaceChild`.
Per-text-node independent binding: each text node gets its own binding (`_bindText` / `_bindDirect` / `sel.subscribe` fast paths; `_bind()` fallback) for fine-grained reactivity (instead of grouping all bindings).
**Element-conditional children keep the `_tpl` fast path**: a DOM wrapper around an inline element-conditional (`<div class="card">{() => open() ? <Panel/> : <Empty/>}</div>`, `<section>{n() > 0 && <List/>}</section>`, or a `.map(x => <li/>)` child) templatizes the wrapper (`_tpl("<div class=\"card\"><!></div>", …)`) and routes the conditional child through `_mountSlot` + a `<!>` placeholder — the SAME path `.map`-returning children and element-valued-`const` children already take. Previously the whole wrapper bailed to the jsx runtime (`h()`). The conditional's own reactive boundary (`mountChild` → `mountReactive`, which creates its own marker before the placeholder so `_mountSlot`'s placeholder-removal can't strand it) is unchanged — behaviour is identical, only the wrapper gains cloneNode. The distinction in `countChildForTemplate`: a DIRECT static JSX element/fragment child (`{<span/>}`) returns `-1` (keeps the cheaper static-hoist path); an expression that CONTAINS JSX but isn't directly one (ternary / `&&` / `.map`) returns `0` (templatable via `_mountSlot`). Inner JSX inside the conditional stays raw (compiled downstream by esbuild to `h()`), consistent with how ALL expression-nested JSX is handled (component props `_rp(() => …<x>)`, `.map` callbacks). Cross-backend byte-identical (JS `jsx.ts:countChildForTemplate` + `processOneChild`; Rust `lib.rs:count_child_for_template` + `process_one_child`); runtime contract locked by `runtime-dom/src/tests/element-conditional-tpl.browser.test.tsx` (reactive swap + disposal).
Pure static call detection: 40+ functions treated as pure (Math._, JSON._, Object.keys/values/entries, Array.isArray, etc.) — not wrapped in reactive getters.
Spread props on root element: when a root element has `{...props}`, emit `_tpl()` + `_applyProps()` instead of falling back to `h()` calls.
Reactive props inlining: the compiler auto-detects `const` variables derived from `props.*` or `splitProps` results and inlines them at JSX use sites. `const x = props.y ?? 'default'; return <div>{x}</div>` compiles to `_bind(() => { t.data = (props.y ?? 'default') })` — fully reactive. Transitive resolution is fully AST-based: `collect_prop_derived_idents` walks `IdentifierReference` nodes in the expression subtree (never string-scans source text). `const a = props.x; const b = a + 1` inlines `b` as `((props.x) + 1)`. Only `const` is tracked (`let`/`var` are mutable, unsafe to inline). Non-JSX usage (e.g., `console.log(x)`) stays static (uses captured value). **Circular references are safe**: cycle detection via `resolving` set breaks infinite recursion, leaving the cyclic identifier as-is (falls back to captured const value at runtime).

**Component-child stable-reference carve-out**: when the JSX parent is a COMPONENT (uppercase tag) AND the expression is a stable reference (bare `Identifier`, simple non-computed `MemberExpression` chain `obj.x.y`, OR any of the above wrapped in TS type-only layers `as T` / `satisfies T` / `!` / parens) AND the expression does NOT reference a tracked signal var, the compiler emits the inlined value BARE — without the `() => …` accessor wrap. The default for component children is otherwise wrap (`<Comp>{count()}</Comp>` → `<Comp>{() => count()}</Comp>` for reactive consumers). The carve-out prevents the silent footgun where a pass-through pattern (`const children = childHolder.children; <Inner>{children}</Inner>` after `splitProps`) delivered `props.children` as a FUNCTION instead of the expected `VNode | VNode[]` — libraries that iterated children directly or `cloneVNode`'d them saw `{type: undefined}` and the DOM rendered literal `<undefined>` tags. Reproducer was the kinetic Stagger + bokisch.com Intro shape (PR #731 shipped the library-side `resolveChildren` workaround; this compiler fix is the upstream root cause). The carve-out is complementary to the library-side fix — they each cover different shapes (stable refs vs CallExpression-inside-JSX-child like `cloneVNode(...)` calls). Signal references explicitly KEEP the wrap (`<Comp>{count}</Comp>` → `<Comp>{() => count()}</Comp>` so the receiving component subscribes reactively). Cross-backend (JS + Rust native binary) implemented byte-identically. Reference: `packages/core/compiler/src/jsx.ts:handleJsxExpression` + `isStableReference` + `unwrapTypeLayers`; tests at `packages/core/compiler/src/tests/component-child-no-wrap.test.ts` + cross-backend specs in `native-equivalence.test.ts`.

**`<For>`/render-callback item params are NOT reactive props**: a JSX-child render callback — `<For each={rows}>{(row) => <td>{String(row.id)}</td>}</For>` (also `<Index>`, `<Show>`, `<Switch>`) — receives a runtime ITEM the framework passes per row, NOT reactive component props. So a BARE property read (`row.id`) is provably static and the compiler bakes it as a one-time `textContent = String(row.id)` instead of a per-row `_bind(() => …)` renderEffect. (Reactivity in Pyreon is via signal CALLS — `row.label()` / `() => row.x` — which keep their own `_bindText`/wrap paths; only non-call property reads bake.) **Detection (`maybeRegisterComponentProps`)**: a function is registered as a component (first param = reactive `props`) ONLY if it returns JSX AND is NOT a `.map`/`.filter` CallExpression callback AND is NOT a JSX-child render callback (parent is a `JSXExpressionContainer` whose grandparent is a `JSXElement`/`JSXFragment`). Attribute-value functions (`component={(p) => …}`) are NOT skipped — those can be real inline components receiving props. **Impact**: a 1k–10k-row `<For>` previously allocated 1k–10k unnecessary `renderEffect`s + disposer closures (retained until unmount — a real per-row CPU + retained-heap cost); the compiler now matches hand-written `_tpl()` for the dominant `{item.id}` shape. Cross-backend byte-identical (JS `maybeRegisterComponentProps` JSX-child skip + Rust `Ctx.in_jsx_child_callback` flag set in `handle_jsx_expression_child`, consumed by the arrow/function `walk_expression` branches). **The JS skip also covers ANY CallExpression-argument callback** (`items().map((item) => …)`, `.filter`, etc. — `jsx.ts:1801` `parent === CallExpression && arguments.includes(node)`); the Rust port originally missed the NESTED `.map`-arg case (the `in_jsx_child_callback` flag was cleared by the outer `{() => …}` JSX-child callback, so the inner `.map((item) => …)` callback's param was re-registered as reactive props → a per-row `_bind` for `{item.label}` instead of static `textContent`). Fixed by the dedicated `in_callback_argument` Ctx flag (see "Dual-backend deep validation" above) — set in the CallExpression arm when the argument is directly an arrow/function. Reference: `packages/core/compiler/src/jsx.ts:maybeRegisterComponentProps` + `native/src/lib.rs:maybe_register_component_props_arrow` / `in_jsx_child_callback` / `in_callback_argument`; tests at `packages/core/compiler/src/tests/static-text-baking.test.ts` (`<For> render-callback item params` describe block) + `native-equivalence.test.ts` (`corpus-sweep regressions`), self-discriminating + bisect-verified.

### Compile-time rocketstyle collapse (opt-in — `pyreon({ collapse: true })`)

P0's vertical slice — shipped. A literal-prop rocketstyle call site
(`<Button state="primary" size="medium">Save</Button>` — every dimension
prop a string literal, no spread, static-text children) collapses from a
5-layer wrapper mount (rocketstyle → attrs HOC → Element → Wrapper →
styled) into ONE `_rsCollapse` cloneNode. E2 measured **44× wall-clock**,
`mountChild` 9→1, `styler.resolve` 22→0. **OFF by default** (zero
behaviour change); enable with `pyreon({ collapse: true })` or
`pyreon({ collapse: { sources, components, provider, theme, mode } })`.

**How it works (parity by construction — no chain reimplementation):**

- **Resolve** (`@pyreon/vite-plugin:createCollapseResolver`): ONE
  programmatic Vite-SSR server bound to the consumer's OWN `vite.config`
  renders the REAL component twice (`<Provider mode="light">` /
  `"dark"`), captures the root `class` per mode + the styler rule text
  via `sheet.getStyleRules()`, strips the root class → a `_tpl` template.
  Because it's the same `renderToString` + `@pyreon/styler` code path the
  app uses (styler's FNV-1a class hash is identical SSR vs DOM — its
  hydration contract), the resolved class is byte-for-byte the
  client-mounted class. Memoised; `closeBundle` disposes the server.
  Generalises beyond app-local — works cross-package too (the RFC's
  "sidecar manifest" deferral proved unnecessary).
- **Scan + detect** (`@pyreon/compiler:scanCollapsibleSites` +
  `tryRocketstyleCollapse`): a SINGLE shared `detectCollapsibleShape`
  bail catalogue used by BOTH the plugin scan (what to resolve) and the
  compiler emit (what to collapse) — keys cannot drift.
  `rocketstyleCollapseKey(localName, props, childrenText)` is the
  canonical, order-independent key both sides compute. Bail (keep the
  normal mount) on: any non-literal/`{expr}`/signal dimension prop,
  `{...spread}`, element/expression children, non-candidate component,
  or an unresolved key. Conservative — uncertain ⇒ no collapse.
- **Emit** (`TransformOptions.collapseRocketstyle`): replaces the JSX with
  `__rsCollapse(<templateHtml>, <lightClass>, <darkClass>, () =>
  __pyrMode() === "dark")` + a once-per-module idempotent
  `__rsSheet.injectRules(<rules>, <ruleKey>)` (RFC decision 1 dual-emit;
  decision 4 hoisted `_tpl`). Only the CLIENT graph collapses — the SSR
  graph keeps the real mount (renderToString needs the VNode tree, and
  the resolver itself SSR-renders). **Both backends emit collapse.** The
  port to Rust shipped all four variants (`__rsCollapse` full /
  `__rsCollapseH` on\*-handler partial / `__rsCollapseDyn` +
  `__rsCollapseDynH` dynamic-prop / element-child reusing `__rsCollapse`),
  each locked byte-for-byte against the JS path by the cross-backend
  equivalence suite. The old `transformJSX` force-route to the JS path
  (`if (options.collapseRocketstyle) return transformJSX_JS(...)`) was
  REMOVED once all variants landed: the dispatcher now lowers the
  `collapseRocketstyle` config from its `Set`/`Map` shape to the napi
  array/Record shape (`toNativeCollapse`) and threads it as `transformJsx`'s
  6th arg, so a collapse build gets the native backend's 3.7-8.x× transform
  speed (the JS path stays the graceful fallback when the native binary is
  absent). Verified end-to-end by the `verify-modes ui-showcase × spa`
  collapse cell building the rs-collapse / dyn / elem probes through native.
- **Runtime** (`@pyreon/runtime-dom:_rsCollapse`): one html-keyed `_tpl`
  cloneNode (shared parsed template across N mounts) whose class is
  reactively bound to the live mode accessor — a mode swap re-runs ONLY
  the className assignment on the SAME node (no remount). The styler
  injection is the emitted code's job (`@pyreon/styler:injectRules` —
  raw pre-resolved rule text, idempotent by key, NO re-hash since the
  class is already baked into the template); `runtime-dom` stays
  layer-pure (never imports styler/ui-core).

**Proven:** 5 layers tested — styler `injectRules` (3 browser specs),
`_rsCollapse` (4 real-Chromium specs: light class, mode-flip-no-remount,
children dispose, shared template), resolver vs REAL ui-components Button
via Vite SSR (8 specs incl. determinism + graceful bail), compiler
detection/emission/bail-catalogue/dedupe (13 specs, bisect-verified:
disable detection → 4 emission specs fail), end-to-end pipeline (real
Button → resolver → scanner → compiler emits `__rsCollapse` with the real
classes byte-for-byte). **SSR→hydrate seam closed + proven** (the prior
"thinnest unproven seam"): `_rsCollapse` returns a `NativeItem` via
`_tpl`, so under `hydrateRoot` it hits `hydrate.ts`'s `__isNative === true`
branch — the framework-wide, correctness-first `_tpl` hydration path
SWAPS the SSR (real 5-layer) subtree for the freshly-built collapsed node
(same final DOM, byte-for-byte class via the FNV-1a SSR↔DOM contract, NO
crash, NO mismatch warning, reactivity intact). NOT collapse-specific —
`_rsCollapse` inherits it from `_tpl` for free; no runtime change needed.
Proven by a real-Chromium e2 spec (`examples/experiments/e2-static-rocketstyle/e2.browser.test.ts`
— `SSR markup → hydrateRoot(_rsCollapse)`): real Button outerHTML placed
as the container's SSR DOM → `hydrateRoot` the collapsed `_rsCollapse` →
asserts (A) the in-DOM node is the swapped clone, not the SSR node, (B)
byte-for-byte SSR class parity + `isEqualNode` + identical computed style
+ zero hydration-mismatch `console.error`, (C) reactivity SURVIVES — a
post-hydrate mode flip patches `className` IN PLACE on the SAME node (no
remount). Bisect-verified-with-restore: neutralizing the `__isNative`
branch fails ONLY this spec with `expected <button> not to be <button>`
(no swap → still the SSR node); restored → 11/11. Additive: all 1079
compiler tests unchanged with collapse off. **Build-artifact gate closed + proven** (the prior deferred coverage item): a `verify-modes` `ui-showcase × spa` cell with `pyreon({ collapse: true })` builds a dedicated `examples/ui-showcase/src/routes/rs-collapse-probe.tsx` (canonical literal-prop `<Button state="primary" size="medium">Save</Button>` — ui-showcase's other Buttons all carry `onClick` and correctly bail) through the full plugin→resolver→compiler→bundle pipeline in a real production `vite build`, and asserts the emitted `rs-collapse-probe-*.js` chunk collapsed via MINIFICATION-STABLE, collapse-exclusive fingerprints (the baked-children template literal `…Save</span></button>` + the `=== "dark"` dual-emit mode accessor) — NOT the pre-minification `__rsCollapse(` identifier, which Vite renames in prod (`__rsCollapse`→`t`, `__rsSheet`→`e`) so a literal-identifier assertion can never match a real build (that was a real bug in the gate's first cut, caught by the build itself proving the feature works while the assertion didn't). Bisect-verified-with-restore: flipping the cell to `collapse: false` builds the real 5-layer Button → the probe chunk has neither fingerprint → the cell fails with `expected probe chunk … to be COLLAPSED (bakedChildren=false, modeAccessor=false)` while the plain `ui-showcase × spa` cell stays green; restored → 2/2 green. First proof of the fully-assembled production artifact (unit + e2 layers prove the pieces). **Build-only is now an EXPLICIT, intentional, tested contract — not a deferral.** The collapse block in `vite-plugin.ts:transform` is gated `if (collapseEnabled && isBuild && !isSsr)`. Dev (`command: 'serve'`) deliberately keeps the normal rocketstyle mount and the resolver is NEVER constructed (zero per-dev-process orphan nested Vite server). **Why this is correct, not a limitation:** the resolver freezes each site's class from a SEPARATE nested Vite-SSR module graph and caches it — in `vite dev` that frozen class would NOT react to the user's theme-source HMR edits, which is strictly *worse* than the normal mount (which IS reactive). So collapse trades dev-time theme-edit reactivity for production speed; dev must keep the normal mount. Pre-fix the block was gated only `&& !isSsr`, so it silently attempted to run in dev (per-transform nested-Vite spin + a frozen-against-HMR class). The plugin now surfaces the contract ONCE per dev process via `this.info('[Pyreon] collapse is build-only — …')` so an opted-in `vite dev` consumer isn't left wondering why nothing collapsed. Bisect-verified-with-restore (`packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/tests/rocketstyle-collapse-dev.test.ts`, stub resolver so the bisect is faithful locally with no `lib/`): remove the `&& isBuild` gate → serve-mode transform emits `__rsCollapse(` → the `command:serve` spec fails on `.not.toContain('__rsCollapse(')`; the companion `command:build` spec (same source, same stub) still collapses, proving the gate is the only difference; restored → 2/2. Reference: `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/rocketstyle-collapse.ts`,
`packages/core/compiler/src/jsx.ts` (`scanCollapsibleSites` /
`tryRocketstyleCollapse` / `rocketstyleCollapseKey`),
`packages/core/runtime-dom/src/template.ts:_rsCollapse`,
`packages/ui-system/styler/src/sheet.ts:injectRules`.

**Dynamic-prop partial-collapse — fully shipped.** Extension targeting the dynamic-prop bail bucket (15.4% of all real-corpus sites per the bail census, vs 7.8% for the `on*`-handler bucket). Two runtime helpers cover the dynamic-collapse surface, both layer-pure (no styler/ui-core imports; styler injection stays the emitted code's job via the existing `injectRules`):

- **`_rsCollapseDyn(html, classes, valueIndex, isDark, bind?)`** — generalises `_rsCollapse`'s 2-class dispatch to N-class for sites where ONE dimension prop is an enumerable dynamic expression. Canonical case: `<Button state={cond ? 'primary' : 'secondary'}>` — ternary of two literals.
- **`_rsCollapseDynH(html, classes, valueIndex, isDark, handlers, bind?)`** — combined helper for the handler-bearing variant (`<Button state={cond ? 'a' : 'b'} onClick={h}>`), the most common real-world shape. Structurally the union of `_rsCollapseDyn`'s class dispatch + `_rsCollapseH`'s canonical `_bindEvent` handler attachment. Closed the bulk of the 15.4% bucket the strict no-handler `_rsCollapseDyn` could only address at 0.2%.

Class layout for both: **stride-2, value-major** — index = `2 * valueIndex + (isDark ? 1 : 0)`. Both accessors are reactive — a value flip OR a mode flip patches className IN PLACE on the SAME node (no remount); handlers stay attached across both.

Compiler path: `detectDynamicCollapsibleShape` (ternary-of-two-literals on ≤1 dim prop; composes with `on*`-handler relaxation) → `scanCollapsibleSites` expands each dynamic site into TWO `CollapsibleSite` entries (one per literal) → the resolver pre-renders both via the existing SSR pipeline → `tryRocketstyleCollapse`'s fallthrough chain (full → on*-handler-partial → dynamic) emits `__rsCollapseDyn(...)` (no handlers) or `__rsCollapseDynH(...)` (with handlers) when both expanded sites resolve AND structural template parity holds. Conservative bail discipline at every layer: half-resolved sites bail, divergent templates bail, multi-axis bails (separable scope — 2^N value-set growth).

Out-of-range `valueIndex` coerces to empty className (graceful — never crashes); compiler is source of truth for the index domain. Bisect-verified at three layers: 7 real-Chromium specs for `_rsCollapseDyn` + 8 for `_rsCollapseDynH`; compiler detector + emit + scan specs (28 total); build-artifact `verify-modes ui-showcase × spa` cell with a dual-Button probe (`Dyn` + `DynH`) that asserts both the stride-2 class array fingerprint AND the handler-combined `===\`dark\`,{` 5-arg signature unique to `_rsCollapseDynH`. Reference: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/template.ts:_rsCollapseDyn` + `_rsCollapseDynH`, `packages/core/compiler/src/jsx.ts:detectDynamicCollapsibleShape` + `tryDynamicCollapse`, `examples/ui-showcase/src/routes/rs-collapse-dyn-probe.tsx`.

**Element-child collapse — fully shipped.** Extension targeting the element-child bail bucket (the largest remaining frontier at ~9.2% of all real-corpus sites; the recursively-static SAFE subset measured 3.0%, lifting addressed coverage 83.0% → **86.0%** per the bail census). **NO new runtime helper** — unlike partial (`_rsCollapseH`) and dynamic (`_rsCollapseDyn`/`DynH`), element-child reuses the EXISTING `_rsCollapse(html, light, dark, isDark)` UNCHANGED. Reason: the resolver SSR-renders the REAL component WITH its child subtree and bakes the FULL output HTML, so the cloned `_tpl` template already contains `<button class=X><span>…</span>Save</button>` and `_rsCollapse` clones the whole thing. The emit is byte-identical to full-collapse; only the detector + child-serialization + scanner-expansion + resolver-reconstruction are new.

- **Correctness boundary (recursively-static)** — `detectStaticElementChild` / `detectElementChildCollapsibleShape` (`@pyreon/compiler` `jsx.ts`) accept an element child iff, recursively: it's a **DOM element** (lowercase tag — a component child has its own setup/reactivity → hard bail), **every attribute is a string literal** (no `{expr}`, no spread, no boolean-shorthand, NO `on*` handlers — a child handler can't survive baking into a static clone), and **children are static text OR recursively-static elements**. Anything else bails (the site keeps its normal mount). Conservative by construction: a false-negative (missed collapse) is fine; a false-positive (baking reactivity) is the only real danger and the rule structurally prevents it.
- **Scan + serialize** — `scanCollapsibleSites` expands each static-element-child site into ONE `CollapsibleSite` carrying `childTree` (the structured `StaticChild[]` subtree) + `childrenText = serializeStaticChildren(childTree)` (the cache/key discriminator). `serializeStaticChildren` is deterministic — distinct subtrees produce distinct strings, so the `rocketstyleCollapseKey` (reused unchanged) can't collide across subtrees. Child text is normalized via the compiler's own `cleanJsxText` (verbatim if no newline; line-trim + single-space-join if multiline) so the baked subtree is byte-faithful to a real mount.
- **Resolver reconstruction** — `ResolveInput.childTree` channel + `buildChildVNodes(tree, h)` (`@pyreon/vite-plugin` `rocketstyle-collapse.ts`) rebuild the real child VNodes via `h()` (`typeof c === 'string' ? c : h(c.tag, c.props, ...buildChildVNodes(c.children, h))`) and render them as the component's children instead of `childrenText` as a string. The resolve cache key includes the child tree.
- **Emit** — `tryRocketstyleCollapse` falls through `tryPartialCollapse → tryDynamicCollapse → tryElementChildCollapse`; the element-child arm emits the UNCHANGED `__rsCollapse(...)` on key match. `StaticChild` / `StaticChildNode` are exported from `@pyreon/compiler`.

**Proven** at every layer (the resolver reconstruction was the genuine correctness risk — it's the only new render path): resolver real-Vite-SSR specs render the REAL `@pyreon/ui-components` Button WITH a `childTree` and assert the baked subtree appears in `templateHtml` — single element, mixed text+element ("Press `<kbd>`Enter`</kbd>` now"), and distinct-subtree-distinct-template (3 specs, bisect-verified: neutering the `childTree` branch fails exactly those 3); compiler detector + scan + emit specs (PR 1+2, bisect-verified); real-Chromium `rs-collapse.browser.test` specs proving the baked static subtree renders as real nested elements + survives a mode flip with root AND child node identity preserved (no remount) + a recursive 2-level subtree; build-artifact gate (`verify-modes ui-showcase × spa` cell + `examples/ui-showcase/src/routes/rs-collapse-elem-probe.tsx` — asserts the baked `<span class="elemico">ElemSave` subtree + the `=== "dark"` mode accessor in the route chunk; bisect-verified: collapse-off → no `=== "dark"` → fails); census reclassification (the element-child static-addressable sites now count toward the 86.0% TOTAL ADDRESSED headline). Reference: `packages/core/compiler/src/jsx.ts:detectStaticElementChild` + `detectElementChildCollapsibleShape` + `serializeStaticChildren` + `tryElementChildCollapse`, `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/rocketstyle-collapse.ts:buildChildVNodes`, `examples/ui-showcase/src/routes/rs-collapse-elem-probe.tsx`.

**Collapse coverage ceiling — 86.0% is the practical maximum (measured, not assumed).** The `collapse-bail-census` test measures the next-frontier go/no-go before any further build. As of the element-child PR, **86.0%** of 566 real `@pyreon/ui-components` call sites collapse end-to-end (full 72.8% + on\*-handler partial 7.8% + dynamic-prop 2.5% + element-child 3.0%). The ~14% un-addressed remainder is OUT OF SCOPE for **structural** reasons, not laziness — and the census distinguishes the two cases:
- **Structurally IMPOSSIBLE** (will never collapse): element-child where a child is a COMPONENT (it owns its own setup/reactivity/state — baking would freeze it); dynamic-prop that's non-enumerable (`state={fn()}` has no finite value set to pre-render); expression children (`{expr}` — dynamic, can't bake); spread (`{...x}` — unknown prop set, no resolvable class); boolean-attr (a valueless attr is ambiguous between a static HTML bool like `disabled` and a rocketstyle dimension shorthand like `primary` — the compile-time detector can't disambiguate without component introspection).
- **Bounded-but-DEFERRED** (could collapse, judged not worth it): **multi-axis-ternary** (≥2 ternary-of-two-literals dimension props → 2^k pre-renderable combinations). The census added a `multiAxisTernaryAddressable` counter for exactly this go/no-go — **measured 0 sites in the real corpus** (no component uses ≥2 ternary dims), so building dynamic-multi-axis collapse would address zero real sites. The counter is logged + locked in `collapse-bail-census.test.ts`; if the corpus ever grows such a site the number flips and the decision can be revisited. Until then, **86.0% is the ceiling and no further collapse work is warranted.**

**Element-child — SSR→hydrate + perf, CI-gated + MEASURED (the gates' final layer).** The SSR→hydrate seam and the perf win are proven against the runtime AND the real component in CI (the `examples/experiments/e2-static-rocketstyle` E2 file is a one-off, un-gated measurement; these are the gated equivalents):

- **`@pyreon/runtime-dom` `rs-collapse.browser.test.ts`** (real Chromium, CI `Test (browser)`): (1) SSR markup with a baked element subtree → `hydrateRoot(_rsCollapse(strippedTpl, …))` → the `__isNative` swap replaces the SSR node (in-DOM node ≠ the SSR node) with NO hydration-mismatch `console.error`, the baked `<span class="ico">` child is carried on the swapped-in node, and a post-hydrate mode flip patches the root class IN PLACE (same node, child subtree preserved) — the element-child SSR→hydrate seam (inherited from `_tpl`, proven for the baked-subtree shape). (2) **Perf signature** — a deliberately DEEP subtree (`<button>Press <kbd>…</kbd> <span class="w"><b>Hi</b></span></button>`) mounts with EXACTLY ONE `runtime.mountChild` + `runtime.tpl ≥ 1` regardless of depth (the whole subtree is ONE `cloneNode`). Counter read via a manual `globalThis.__pyreon_count__` sink (no perf-harness dep; counters fire under vitest's Vite DEV mode). Bisect-verified: replacing `_rsCollapse` with a per-element mount makes `mountChild` scale with depth.
- **`@pyreon/ui-components` `elem-child-collapse.browser.test.tsx`** (real Chromium, CI `Test (browser)`): real `<Button state size><span class="ico">Save</span></Button>` → capture outerHTML → strip root class → `_rsCollapse` → **byte-for-byte parity** (`isEqualNode` the real 5-layer mount, identical class + computed style + the nested `<span class="ico">` present as an element). **Perf MEASURED** (provider amortized for fairness): the real element-child Button fires **9** `runtime.mountChild`; the collapsed clone fires **1** (9× fewer) — and a wall-clock benchmark (N=150 × 5 runs) measures **~8.6 ms → ~0.8 ms (~11× faster)**. Counter delta is the deterministic CI lock; wall-clock asserts direction only (`collapsed < baseline`, robust under CI load) + logs the figure. Bisect-verified: replacing the collapsed mount with the real Button makes `collapsedMountChild` 9 → the `toBe(1)` assertion fails. (ui-components gained `@pyreon/runtime-dom` + `@pyreon/perf-harness` devDeps for these imports.)

### Reactivity Lens (experimental — surface the compiler's analysis back to the author)

The compiler ALREADY decides per-expression whether code is reactive (`isDynamic`/`shouldWrap`/`unwrapAccessor`'s `isReactive`), emits codegen, and discards the analysis. The Lens pipes that ground truth back to the editor so Pyreon's silent rule — "components run once; reactivity depends on WHERE you read a signal" — becomes **visible at the cursor**. Prevention upstream, not another downstream detector.

- **Additive, opt-in.** `TransformOptions.reactivityLens: true` populates `TransformResult.reactivityLens: ReactivitySpan[]`. Emitted `code` is **byte-identical** with the option on or off (asserted by an `additive` test across fixtures + all 1000 compiler tests passing unchanged). The lens is recorded at the SAME ~5 codegen-decision sites as the existing `replacements.push` — it never runs a second analysis pass.
- **Kinds** (each a faithful RECORD of a codegen branch, never an approximation): `reactive` (text `_bind`/`_bindText` / `() =>` wrap), `reactive-prop` (`_rp(() => …)`), `reactive-attr` (live attribute binding), `static-text` (the literal `else`-branch of the reactive text decision — baked once, the high-precision "this `{x}` is dead" signal), `hoisted-static` (`const _$h\d+ =` module hoist). **Absence of a span is "not asserted", never an implicit static claim** (asymmetric-precision commitment).
- **`analyzeReactivity(code, filename, { knownSignals? })`** (exported from `@pyreon/compiler`) → `{ findings: ReactivityFinding[], spans: ReactivitySpan[] }`. Merges the structural compiler facts with the EXISTING `detectPyreonPatterns` footgun detectors (`kind: 'footgun'`, carries the detector `code`) under one taxonomy — the Lens unifies the surface, it does not reinvent footgun analysis. `formatReactivityLens(code, result)` renders an annotated-source CLI/debug view. `analyzeReactivity` itself forces `transformJSX_JS` (the JS path is the oracle for the merged footgun+structural taxonomy), but **the raw `TransformResult.reactivityLens` sidecar is now emitted by BOTH backends** (Phase 3): `transformJSX(code, f, { reactivityLens: true })` carries the spans whether it dispatched to the Rust native binary (the ~80% path) or the JS fallback. The Rust binary mirrors the 6 `lens()` codegen-decision sites byte-for-byte (`native/src/lib.rs:Ctx::lens` + the napi `ReactivitySpan` struct; napi maps snake_case → camelCase so the JS shape is identical). Additive on the native path too — codegen is byte-identical with the option on or off. Proven by the `compareLens` cross-backend gate in `native-equivalence.test.ts` (9 fixtures, one per structural kind + mixed/multi-line/auto-call; asserts JS↔Rust span-set parity AND the additive guarantee; bisect-verified by removing any single `ctx.lens(...)` call).
- **Drift gate** (`packages/core/compiler/src/tests/reactivity-lens.test.ts`): per-fixture, the lens kind is asserted against the matching emitted token (`_bind`/`_bindText`/`_rp`/`_$h`). Bisect-verified-with-restore: reverting the `reactive` `lens()` call → `expected +0 to be 1`; restored → 12/12. Real-corpus sweep: 177 `examples/**/*.tsx`, 0 crashes, ~0.78ms/file.
- **LSP surface** (`@pyreon/lint`'s EXISTING server — no new server): `inlayHintProvider` capability + `textDocument/inlayHint` handler renders structural kinds as end-of-span ghost text (`live` / `static` / `live·prop` / `hoisted`); footguns publish as `source: 'pyreon-lens'` warning diagnostics. `computeReactivityHints(filePath, text)` is the pure testable core; `_handleMessage` is exported (underscore convention) for the JSON-RPC integration test (initialize → didOpen → inlayHint round-trip, real compiler, no mocks). `@pyreon/lint` gained a `@pyreon/compiler` workspace dep (acyclic — compiler is layer 3, standalone). Reference: `packages/core/compiler/src/reactivity-lens.ts`, `packages/tools/lint/src/lsp/index.ts`. Roadmap status: Rust parity SHIPPED (Phase 3); **manifest/llms enrichment SHIPPED** (dense `analyzeReactivity` entry in `packages/core/compiler/src/manifest.ts` + llms bullets); **body-scope `const {x}=props` SHIPPED** — `props-destructured-body` (#618, TS-compiler-API: PascalCase JSX component + bare `= props` first-param + top-of-body destructure) is surfaced by the lens via the `detectPyreonPatterns` merge and locked by `reactivity-lens.test.ts` ("body-scope … via the merge"; bisect-verified — neutering the merge fails it). The ONLY genuine remainder is a **rendered-editor (VS Code) inlay-hint e2e**, whose contract is already covered by `lsp-reactivity.test.ts`'s JSON-RPC `initialize → didOpen → inlayHint` round-trip against the real compiler — a low-value defer (real editor harness for marginal gain).

### Context providing pattern

Two context types:

- `createContext<T>(default)` — static context, `useContext()` returns `T`, safe to destructure
- `createReactiveContext<T>(default)` — reactive context, `useContext()` returns `() => T`, must call to read

`provide(ctx, value)` — provides a value for the current component's subtree; released automatically when the component unmounts (no manual cleanup).

**Resolution model — owner-based (client) / stack (SSR).** On the client each mounted component's `EffectScope` doubles as a context OWNER: `provide()` writes onto the current owner (`scope._contexts`), `useContext()` walks the owner chain (`scope._parent`, set by the renderer so it mirrors the component tree), and context is released when the scope is disposed. There is no global stack to grow and no frame to orphan — deferred boundaries (`<Show>`/`<For>`) just capture the owner reference (`getContextOwner()`) and restore it (`runWithContextOwner`) when they mount children later. This **replaced** a global mutable `Map[]` stack whose snapshot / restore / dedup / identity-removal machinery (`captureContextStack` / `restoreContextStack` / `removeContextFrame`, the 321k-frame-leak fixes) existed only to fake tree-position across deferred mounts; that entire bug class is now structurally impossible. SSR keeps the request-scoped stack (a synchronous top-down render needs no band-aids; `@pyreon/runtime-server` isolates concurrent requests via an AsyncLocalStorage-backed stack). `useContext()` resolves owner-chain-first, then falls back to the stack — so SSR and the `*-compat` layers' own stack-based provide/inject keep working. Reactivity exports `getContextOwner` / `setContextOwner` / `runWithContextOwner`; `EffectScope` carries `_parent` / `_contexts` + `provideContext` / `lookupContext`. Reference: `packages/core/reactivity/src/scope.ts` + `packages/core/core/src/context.ts` (236 lines, down from 425). The historical stack-leak entries below ("321k-frame leak", "restoreContextStack splices", "Effects that read context across re-runs") describe the SUPERSEDED stack model — kept for archaeology; the owner model deleted the band-aids they document.

For reactive values (mode, locale, etc.), always use `createReactiveContext`:

```tsx
const ModeCtx = createReactiveContext<'light' | 'dark'>('light')
// Provider: provide(ModeCtx, () => modeSignal())
// Consumer: const getMode = useContext(ModeCtx); getMode() // 'light'
```

### onMount signature

`onMount(fn: () => CleanupFn | void)` — callbacks can return nothing or a cleanup function.

### Compat-mode native marker contract

`@pyreon/{react,preact,vue,solid}-compat` ship a JSX runtime that wraps every user component in a `wrapCompatComponent` HOC — the wrapper relocates the render context so React/Preact/Vue/Solid-style component bodies (which expect a fresh render frame on every state change) work inside Pyreon's mount pipeline. **This wrapping is a problem for Pyreon framework components** that use `provide()` / `onMount()` / `onUnmount()` / `effect()` at component-body scope: their setup code lands inside the wrapper's accessor, not inside Pyreon's setup frame, so `provide()` writes land on a torn-down / wrong owner scope and `effect()` re-runs lose access to live signals.

**Solution: `nativeCompat(Component)` from `@pyreon/core`.** Marks a component so the four compat jsx() runtimes route it through `h(type, props)` directly — no wrapper, body runs in Pyreon's setup frame. The marker is a `Symbol.for('pyreon:native-compat')` property on the function (registry symbol → cross-package identity without import direction). 24 framework components ship marked today across 13 packages:

- **`@pyreon/core`**: `ErrorBoundary`
- **`@pyreon/runtime-dom`**: `Transition`, `TransitionGroup`, `KeepAlive`
- **`@pyreon/router`**: `RouterProvider`, `RouterView`, `RouterLink`
- **`@pyreon/head`**: `HeadProvider`
- **`@pyreon/query`**: `QueryClientProvider`, `QueryErrorResetBoundary`
- **`@pyreon/i18n`**: `I18nProvider`
- **`@pyreon/form`**: `FormProvider`, `Form`, `Submit`
- **`@pyreon/permissions`**: `PermissionsProvider`
- **`@pyreon/toast`**: `Toaster`
- **`@pyreon/ui-core`**: `PyreonUI`, `CoreProvider`
- **`@pyreon/unistyle`**: `UnistyleProvider`
- **`@pyreon/styler`**: `ThemeProvider`
- **`@pyreon/rocketstyle`**: `Provider`
- **`@pyreon/coolgrid`**: `Container`, `Row`
- **`@pyreon/elements`**: `Overlay`, `OverlayContextProvider`

The marker is internal infrastructure for framework components — user code in compat-mode apps doesn't normally need to call it. **Exception**: if you write your own Pyreon-flavored helper component using `provide()` / `onMount()` and use it in a compat-mode app, mark it: `nativeCompat(MyHelper)`. See `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` for the foot-gun catalog.

**Internal Provider components are also marked** even when they're `@internal` / `@deprecated` (CoreProvider, UnistyleProvider, RocketstyleProvider, OverlayContextProvider). Reason: PyreonUI's JSX body still routes through the active jsx() runtime in compat-mode apps — any unmarked Provider rendered inside PyreonUI gets wrapped, which swallows its `provide()` call before reaching descendants.

Test layering: per-compat marker-bypass unit tests in each `*-compat/src/tests/native-marker-bypass.test.tsx` (bisect-verified by removing the `if (isNativeCompat(type))` branch from each compat's `jsx-runtime.ts`), plus the cpa-app-compat e2e gate in `e2e/cpa-app-compat.shared.ts` (3 tests × 4 compat scaffolds — proves real-app shape including loader-driven routes work end-to-end). The unit tests catch jsx-runtime regressions; the e2e tests catch multi-render-cycle regressions (signal change re-fires the wrapper's accessor → `provide()` in re-run lands in stale stack — only visible against real router state).

Reference implementation: `packages/core/core/src/compat-marker.ts`.

### Code Splitting & Dynamic Components

- `lazy(loader)` — wraps dynamic import with Suspense `__loading` integration
- `Dynamic({ component, ...props })` — renders component by reference or string tag
- Re-exported from `@pyreon/react-compat` for compatibility

### Signal-Preserving HMR (Vite plugin)

- Top-level `signal()` calls rewritten to `__hmr_signal(moduleId, name, signal, initialValue)`
- `import.meta.hot.dispose` saves signal values to `globalThis.__pyreon_hmr_registry__`
- On hot reload, signals restore their previous values instead of reinitializing
- Virtual module `virtual:pyreon/hmr-runtime` serves the HMR helpers
- **Component-level fast-refresh (zero / router apps).** `injectHmr` emits `import.meta.hot.accept((m) => { const s = globalThis.__pyreon_hmr_swap__; if (typeof s === 'function' && m && s("<id>", m)) return; import.meta.hot.invalidate() })` — NOT a bare `accept()`. The bare form (pre-2026-05-16) re-evaluated the module but re-rendered nothing AND suppressed Vite's reload fallback → a component/JSX edit produced a **silently-stale UI until a manual refresh**. Now: `@pyreon/router` registers `globalThis.__pyreon_hmr_swap__` (dev+browser only, zero import coupling — same sink pattern as perf-harness) → `RouterInstance._hmrSwap(id, freshModule)`. It walks the active matched chain for any lazy record whose `_hmrId` matches `id` (`@pyreon/zero`'s fs-router `lazy(() => import("/abs/X"), { hmrId: "/abs/X" })`), sets `_componentCache[record] = freshModule.default`, and bumps `_loadingSignal`. `RouterView`'s `depthEntry` computed re-emits and (via its identity `equals`) re-renders ONLY that subtree **in place** — no page reload, so `__pyreon_hmr_registry__` survives and module-scope signals keep their values. Using the namespace Vite hands the accept callback (NOT a re-run of the lazy thunk) sidesteps the stale-`?t=` trap: the dynamic-import thunk lives in the non-invalidated virtual routes module, so re-importing it would return the OLD module. `_hmrSwap` returns falsy (edit outside the active route tree — nested non-route component, unrelated route, signal-only module — or no coordinator: plain `@pyreon/runtime-dom` app) → `import.meta.hot.invalidate()` → Vite propagates → an **automatic** full reload (still no manual refresh). Reference: `packages/tools/vite-plugin/src/index.ts:injectHmr`, `packages/core/router/src/router.ts:_hmrSwap` + `_hmrIdMatches`, `packages/zero/zero/src/fs-router.ts:nextLazy`. Real-Chromium gate: `e2e/zero-hmr.spec.ts` (`bun run test:e2e:zero-hmr`, own config + ssr-showcase dev boot on 5201) — edits `examples/ssr-showcase/src/routes/hmr-probe.tsx` mid-test, asserts the marker updates in place + a `window` sentinel survives (no reload) + the module-scope `count` signal keeps its value. Bisect-verified: reverting injectHmr to the bare `accept()` → the spec times out with `hmr-marker` stuck at `MARKER_V1` (the exact reported bug); restored → passes.

### Auto Signal Naming (Vite plugin, dev only)

- `const count = signal(0)` → `const count = signal(0, { name: "count" })`
- Applies to all signal() calls (module-scope and function-scope)
- Module-scope signals get names via `__hmr_signal`; function-scope via injected options
- Skips signals that already have an options argument
- Not applied in production builds (tree-shaken)

### Runtime DOM — SVG/MathML and Custom Elements

- SVG namespace: 67 SVG/MathML tags auto-detected, created via `createElementNS` with correct namespace URI
- **SVG/MathML attribute application**: SVG and MathML elements ALWAYS use `setAttribute()` for prop forwarding, never property assignment. Many SVG properties (`SVGMarkerElement.markerWidth`, `SVGMarkerElement.refX`, `SVGRectElement.x`, etc.) are read-only `SVGAnimatedLength` getters — `el[key] = value` would crash with `Cannot set property X of [object Object] which has only a getter`. Detected by `el.namespaceURI !== 'http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml'`. Standard React/Vue/Solid behavior.
- Custom elements: props set as properties (not attributes) on elements with a hyphen in the tag name — EXCEPT `data-*`/`aria-*`, which always go through `setAttribute` (the hyphenated-tag property branch broke `getAttribute`/`dataset`/CSS attribute selectors — the server-island marker bug, PR #1523)
- **Boolean `aria-*` attributes render as the STRING `"true"`/`"false"`, NOT presence-only `""`.** ARIA state/property attrs (`aria-checked`, `aria-selected`, `aria-expanded`, `aria-disabled`, `aria-pressed`, `aria-hidden`, …) are string enums — assistive tech does NOT read `aria-checked=""` (presence) as "true"; it falls back to the default → effectively unchecked. So `applyStaticProp` (client) and `renderPropValue` (SSR) BOTH check `typeof value === 'boolean' && key.startsWith('aria-')` BEFORE the generic boolean→presence branch and emit `String(value)`. **HTML boolean attrs (`disabled`/`hidden`/`checked`/…) keep presence semantics** (`disabled=""`), and `data-*` (author-defined) keeps presence — only `aria-*` booleans coerce to `"true"`/`"false"`. Both renderers do this identically so SSR markup matches client hydration. So a component author can write `aria-checked={isChecked()}` (boolean) and it renders correctly — explicit string `aria-checked={isChecked() ? 'true' : 'false'}` is also fine but no longer required. Reference: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/props.ts:applyStaticProp` + `packages/core/runtime-server/src/index.ts:renderPropValue`; regression tests in `runtime-dom/src/tests/props.test.ts` + `runtime-server/src/tests/ssr.test.ts` (bisect-verified — disabling either branch renders presence-only).
- Transition 5s timeout: if `transitionend`/`animationend` never fires, the transition completes automatically after 5 seconds
- Duplicate key production guard: duplicate `key` values in lists emit a one-time console warning in production (not just dev)
- **Subpath exports**: `@pyreon/runtime-dom/transition` (Transition + TransitionGroup) and `@pyreon/runtime-dom/keep-alive` (KeepAlive) for explicit opt-in. Main entry re-exports everything for backward compat.
- **URL-attribute injection guard (`setStaticProp` + the `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` sanitizer)**: URL-bearing attrs (`href`, `src`, `action`, `formaction`, `poster`, `cite`, `data`) are checked against `UNSAFE_URL_RE = /^\s*(?:javascript|data):/i` and dropped (dev-mode `[Pyreon] Blocked unsafe URL` warning; silent in prod). **`data:image/*` is allowed when the attribute is an image source (`src`/`srcset`/`poster`) on an image-context element (`<img>`/`<source>`/`<video>`)** — `isSafeImageDataUri`, single-sourced in `@pyreon/core` (see below). This is required because the framework's own `imagePlugin` ships `data:image/webp;base64,…` (blur) and `data:image/svg+xml,…` (color) placeholders that flow into `<Image>`/`<OptimizedImage>`'s `<img src={props.placeholder}>`; blocking them silently disabled the placeholder feature (functional regression fixed post-0.28.0). Raster types always pass; SVG is allowed only when it carries no `<script>`/`on*=` handlers (payload decoded for both base64 and url-encoded forms). `javascript:` stays blocked everywhere, `data:text/html` stays blocked on `<iframe>`/`<object>`/`<embed>`, and `data:` on navigable elements (`<a href>`, `<form action>`) stays blocked. **General rule when a framework feature emits a `data:` URI for an attribute: it MUST land on an image-context element/attr, or the runtime guard rejects it.** **The guard is single-sourced in `@pyreon/core` (`url-guard.ts`)** — `URL_ATTRS`, `UNSAFE_URL_RE`, and `isSafeImageDataUri(tagName, key, value)` are exported from core and imported by BOTH renderers: `@pyreon/runtime-dom`'s client `setStaticProp` + DOMParser sanitizer (passing `el.tagName`) and `@pyreon/runtime-server`'s SSR `renderProp` (passing the JSX `tag`; `renderProp` now takes the element tag so the guard can check image context). `tagName` is matched case-insensitively so both the uppercase DOM `Element.tagName` and lowercase JSX tag resolve. **This extraction exists because the two renderers previously carried independent copies that DRIFTED** — the client guard allowed `data:image/*` (0.28.1) while the SSR copy still stripped ALL `data:` URIs, so `renderToString`/`renderToStream` shipped prerendered/SSG static HTML with `<img>`/`<video>` that had no `src`/`poster` (a functional regression invisible to client-only tests; the original runtime-dom-only fix was PR #1212, the SSR mirror was #1314, and this extraction collapses both into one source so the drift class can't recur). The exhaustive allow/block matrix lives once in `packages/core/core/src/tests/url-guard.test.ts`; each renderer keeps a thin behavior test of its own wiring (`coverage-gaps.test.ts` client + `image-data-uri-guard.browser.test.tsx` real-Chromium + `runtime-server/src/tests/ssr.test.ts` SSR), and the full `<Image>` → SSR pipeline is locked by `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/image-ssr-placeholder.test.ts`. Reference: `packages/core/core/src/url-guard.ts`.

### Mount Pipeline Performance

The mount pipeline is optimized for zero unnecessary allocations in production:

- **Devtools gated on `__DEV__`**: `compId` generation (`Math.random`), `_mountingStack` tracking, `registerComponent`/`unregisterComponent` are all behind `if (__DEV__)` — Vite tree-shakes the entire devtools module from prod bundles. Zero production cost.
- **Lazy LifecycleHooks**: `mount`/`unmount`/`update`/`error` arrays start as `null`, allocated on first `onMount()`/`onUnmount()`/etc. call. Components with no hooks (80%+) skip all hook iteration.
- **Lazy EffectScope**: `_effects` and `_updateHooks` arrays start as `null`, allocated on first `add()`/`addUpdateHook()`. Components with no effects save 2 array allocations.
- **makeReactiveProps scan-first**: Scans for `REACTIVE_PROP`-branded functions before allocating the getter-backed result object. Static-only components (60%+) return the raw props object immediately — no allocation, no property copying.
- **Lazy mountCleanups**: Only allocated when an `onMount` callback actually returns a cleanup function.
- **Per 150-component page**: ~2,020 allocations + ~1,050 operations eliminated vs naive implementation.

### Memory characteristics — measured

Run `bun run measure-memory` (`scripts/measure-memory.mjs`, `node --expose-gc`, `NODE_ENV=production`) for reproducible **retained bytes per reactive primitive**. This fills the one instrumentation gap the other gates didn't cover — bundle-budgets gates *bundle* bytes (deterministic, CI-gated), perf-harness journeys gate *allocation counts*, leak-sweep gates *heap-growth slope*, but nothing measured per-primitive retained heap. It is a TOOL, not a CI gate (runtime heap is ±~10% noisy run-to-run; gating it would flake — use it for RELATIVE before/after checks on a reactivity change).

Production per-primitive cost (V8 heapUsed, N=100k, stable):

| primitive | retained bytes |
| --- | --- |
| `signal` | **~152 B** (≈ the ~170 B the in-browser perf-harness reads on `reactivitySignalCreate-100k ≈ 17 MB`; node V8 reads slightly leaner) |
| `signal + effect` | ~930 B (combined) |
| `signal + computed` | ~1.65 KB (combined — a computed is **~10× a signal**: dep tracking + recompute closure + value cache; prefer plain signals where derivation isn't needed) |
| `effectScope` | **~64 B** (the lazy-null-array design — `_effects`/`_updateHooks` start `null`; an empty scope is barely more than its object header) |

The signal struct is near its floor: 1 read closure + 5 fields, methods on a shared `SignalProto` via ONE `setPrototypeOf` (not 6 per-instance assignments; monomorphic + `instanceof Function` preserved), `_s`/`_d` lazy-null, single-subscriber inline `_d1` (no `Set` for the dominant `<For>`-row case). **Important: the measurement MUST run under `NODE_ENV=production`** — in dev the reactive-devtools machinery (per-primitive `new Error()` source-capture + always-on registry) dominates and OOMs at 100k; that overhead is real but prod-gated (tree-shaken), so it is not what consumers pay.

**`@pyreon/runtime-dom` bundle tree-shakes correctly** (`sideEffects: false`, pure modules — measured, esbuild prod+gzip): a `mount`-only import is **~7.4 KB gz**; core (`mount`+`hydrateRoot`+`mountChild`) ~8.6 KB; the full kitchen-sink (incl. `Transition`/`TransitionGroup`/`KeepAlive`) ~9.8 KB. The optional animation/keep-alive features (~1.2 KB) tree-shake OUT when unused AND have subpath exports — a minimal app ships ~7.4 KB, not the 12 KB kitchen-sink budget figure. No main-entry split is warranted (it would break back-compat for zero gain).

**App-level: virtualize large lists.** Fine-grained reactivity allocates per reactive node — a 10k-row `<For>` = ~10k signals (~1.5 MB) + cleanup closures + key map (the ~13%-over-Vanilla bulk-create cost; Solid pays it identically). The signal is already near its floor, so the lever is **`@pyreon/virtual`** (`useVirtualizer` renders only visible rows → only ~visible-count signals), not a smaller signal.

### Mount-loop closure hazards — reactive entry points read marker.parentNode live

Any framework primitive that (a) accepts `parent` as a setup arg, (b) inserts a marker into that `parent`, and (c) calls `parent.insertBefore(...)` from inside an effect re-run is structurally unsafe under `mountFor`'s frag-then-move pattern. `mountFor` builds its children into a `DocumentFragment` and commits via `liveParent.insertBefore(frag, tailMarker)` — the move carries markers and all sibling DOM along, but inner mount loops still hold the original (now-empty) fragment as `parent`. Next signal-driven re-run → `insertBefore(node, marker)` against the stale fragment → `NotFoundError` → child-loss.

Closed across two PRs in 2026-Q2:
- **#776** — `mountReactive` reads `marker.parentNode ?? parent` at each effect run. Surfaced by the For-of-`<Show>` batched-toggle journey in `scripts/leak-sweep.ts` (#772). CONTRACT regression: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/tests/show-of-for-batched-toggle.browser.test.ts`.
- **#783** — `mountKeyedList` reads `tailMarker.parentNode ?? parent` at each effect run, threads `liveParent` through `mountNewEntries` + `keyedListReorder` (which propagates to `applyKeyedMoves` → `moveEntryBefore`). Bug reachable only when a `<For>` child returns a function directly (`(i) => () => signal().map(...)`) so the inner keyed array lands in the For's frag — a `<div>` wrapper isolates from the frag-move. CONTRACT regression: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/tests/keyed-array-in-for-batched-toggle.browser.test.ts`.

Sibling primitives audited safe — no remaining instances of this class in runtime-dom:
- `mountFor` itself reads `startMarker.parentNode` at the top of its effect (pre-existing pattern; same shape as the post-#776/#783 fixes).
- `KeepAlive` / `TransitionGroup` / `Transition` use `containerRef.current` (live DOM-element refs that move atomically with the surrounding tree, never stale).
- `_bindText` / `_bindDirect` (template.ts) operate on text-node `.data` only — no `parent.insertBefore` from inside an effect.
- Hydrate paths inherit through `mountReactive`'s call.

General rule for framework code: any mount loop running inside an effect that accepts `parent` as a setup arg should compute the live parent from a marker at each re-run — `parent` is captured at setup and the DOM moves; markers move with the DOM, so their `parentNode` is the source of truth. Full anti-pattern entry in `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` under "Architecture Mistakes". Reproducer for the For-of-Show shape: `bun run perf:leak-sweep --app perf-dashboard --journeys domConditionalToggle-1000`.

### Dev-Mode Warnings (`__DEV__`)

- `mount()` validates container is not null/undefined
- Component output validation (must return VNode, string, null, or function)
- Duplicate `by` keys in `<For>` loops logged as warnings
- Passing raw signal (function) as child instead of calling it
- Devtools: component tree tracking, inspector overlay, highlight
- All guarded by `__DEV__` — tree-shaken in production builds

### Dev-mode perf counters (`@pyreon/perf-harness`)

Framework packages emit named call counters for perf-driven debugging (real-app-shape instrumentation, not synthetic benchmarks). The counter contract is:

```ts
// In a framework package's hot path — NO import from @pyreon/perf-harness.
interface ViteMeta {
  readonly env?: { readonly DEV?: boolean }
}
declare const globalThis: { __pyreon_count__?: (name: string, n?: number) => void }

if ((import.meta as ViteMeta).env?.DEV === true) globalThis.__pyreon_count__?.('styler.resolve')
```

- **Zero cross-package coupling.** Framework packages (styler, unistyle, rocketstyle, runtime-dom, reactivity, router) are published to npm; they must not depend on the private `@pyreon/perf-harness` package. The global sink lets them emit without an import.
- **Zero cost until opt-in.** `globalThis.__pyreon_count__` is `undefined` until a consumer calls `perfHarness.install()` or `perfHarness.enable()`. Optional-chaining short-circuits; prod tree-shakes the whole block via the `import.meta.env.DEV` gate.
- **Counter names live in ONE place**: `packages/internals/perf-harness/COUNTERS.md`. Adding a new counter means (a) adding the emit in source, and (b) adding a row to `COUNTERS.md`. The drift test (`catalog-drift.test.ts`) enforces both directions — emits without catalog entries fail CI, and catalog entries with no emitters also fail.
- **Instrumented layers (66 counters today)**:
  - `styler`: `resolve`, `sheet.insert`, `sheet.insert.hit`
  - `unistyle`: `styles`, `descriptor`, `descriptor.fallback-scan`
  - `rocketstyle`: `getTheme`, `dimensionsMap.hit`, `localThemeManager.hit`, `omitSet.hit`
  - `runtime`: `mount`, `unmount`, `mountChild`, `mountFor.lisOps`, `tpl`, `applyProp`, `applyEvent`, `bindText`, `bindDirect`, `mountReactive`, `cleanup`. Foundation PR added 6 new counters + 5 stress journeys + baselines for the rendering layer. **Counter scope notes**: `runtime.applyProp` fires per `applyProp(el, key, value)` call — i.e. the imperative-prop path used by `h()`-based code, prop spreads, and styled-component theme forwarding; NOT for JSX-compiled static templates (compiler bakes static props into `_tpl()` HTML) or compiler-emitted event delegation. `runtime.applyEvent` is a strict subset of `applyProp` for `on*` props — near-zero in pure-JSX-compiled code because the compiler emits `el.addEventListener(...)` directly, bypassing `applyProp`. `runtime.bindText` / `runtime.bindDirect` fire per compiler-emitted reactive binding setup — stable on a static page, spike during HMR. `runtime.mountReactive` fires per `<Show>` / accessor-child boundary mount. `runtime.cleanup` fires per registered mount cleanup that actually runs (gated on `hasCleanup` so the placeholder noop on first mountReactive run doesn't count). The 5 journey baselines (`domMount-1000`, `domShuffleLis-1000`, `domAppend-10k`, `domConditionalToggle-1000`, `domEventAttach-1000`) lock in the counter signatures: `domMount-1000` proves `mountChild × tpl × bindText × signalCreate` scale together (1000 each), `domShuffleLis-1000` pins worst-case `mountFor.lisOps` ≈ 999 (full reversal degenerates LIS to length 1), `domAppend-10k` proves the three-tier fast path's "extend" tier (`mountFor.lisOps` absent — 0), `domConditionalToggle-1000` shows `mountReactive ≈ 4000` + `cleanup ≈ 3003` for the 1000-Show × 2-cycle toggle pattern (catches the bug shape PR #505 fixed at root), `domEventAttach-1000` shows the JSX-compiled event path bypasses applyEvent (`runtime.applyEvent` absent in baseline — informational, not a regression).
  - `runtime-server` (SSR): `render`, `stream`, `component`, `escape`, `suspense.boundary`, `suspense.fallback`, `for.keyMarker`
  - `reactivity`: `signalCreate`, `signalWrite`, `effectRun`, `computedRecompute`. Five isolated stress journeys + baselines lock in per-primitive cost without folding it into the app-shaped cascade (form / query / rx / store). Each isolates ONE counter dimension so regressions can't hide:
    - **`reactivitySignalCreate-100k`** — 100k fresh signal allocations, no subscribers. Baseline: `signalCreate: 100_000`, others 0. Heap ~17MB. Diagnoses per-signal allocation overhead.
    - **`reactivitySignalWrite-100k`** — 1 signal, 100k unique-value writes (loop counter bypasses `Object.is`). Baseline: `signalCreate: 1`, `signalWrite: 100_000`. Diagnoses write-path cost in the no-subscriber fast path. Any non-zero `effectRun` / `computedRecompute` here = stray subscriber leak.
    - **`reactivityEffectFanout-1k`** — 1 signal, 1000 effect subscribers under one EffectScope, 10 writes. Baseline: `effectRun: 11_000` (1000 initial + 10 × 1000 cascades). `effectRun > 11_000` = batch dedup broken.
    - **`reactivityComputedDiamond-1k`** — 1 source → 1000 computeds all reading source → 1 effect reading all 1000 → 1 write. Baseline: `computedRecompute: 2000` (1000 cold + 1000 cascades), `effectRun: 2` (1 initial + 1 cascade — DEDUP WORKS, NOT 1000). The `effectRun: 2` count is the structural proof that the two-tier flush dedupes diamond-shaped dependencies correctly.
    - **`reactivityScopeDispose-10k`** — 10k effects in 1 scope, dispose scope, then write source once. Baseline: `effectRun: 10_000` (initial mounts only — post-dispose write fires ZERO cascades). Leak detector: `effectRun > 10_000` means `scope.stop()` left orphan effects attached to the signal.

    Reference: [packages/internals/perf-harness/COUNTERS.md](packages/internals/perf-harness/COUNTERS.md) + [examples/perf-dashboard/src/components/ReactivityStressSection.tsx](examples/perf-dashboard/src/components/ReactivityStressSection.tsx) + per-journey docstrings in [examples/perf-dashboard/src/journeys.ts](examples/perf-dashboard/src/journeys.ts).
  - `router`: `navigate`, `loaderRun`, `loaderCache.hit`, `prefetch`
  - `store`: `defineStore`, `pluginRun`, `patchKey`, `subscribeNotify`, `actionListenerNotify`, `actionCall` (foundation PR — baselines for 5 stress journeys (`storeMount-1000`, `storeAction-10k`, `storeWrite-10k`, `storeSubscribeNotify-1k`, `storePluginScale-1000`) recorded in `perf-results/`. The earlier "plugin-chain caching" follow-up was measured + REJECTED (2026-06): plugins are side-effecting per-instance initializers — each fresh store must run each plugin, so `storePluginScale-1000`'s `pluginRun: 5000` (5 plugins × 1000 stores) is the CORRECT signature, not a cache miss; a noop plugin costs ~0.2µs and the loop skips entirely in the zero-plugin common case.)
  - `rx`: `transform.signal`, `transform.raw`, `pipe`, `debounce.create`, `throttle.create` (foundation PR — baselines for 5 stress journeys (`rxFilterMap-10k`, `rxPipe-10k`, `rxSortBy-10k`, `rxAggregate-10k`, `rxDebounceRapid-1k`) recorded in `perf-results/`. The `transform.signal` / `transform.raw` pair is the structural diagnostic — non-zero `.raw` = consumer accidentally pre-resolved a signal where rx expected one. `rxPipe-10k` proves pipe collapses the chain into 1 computed: `rx.pipe: 1`, `rx.transform.signal: 0`, vs equivalent separate-call chain `rxFilterMap-10k`'s `rx.transform.signal: 2`.)
  - `query`: `useQuery`, `useMutation`, `observerNotify`, `setOptions`, `invalidate`, `isFetchingScan`. Foundation PR added the 6 counters + 4 stress journeys + baselines. **Lazy signal allocation follow-up**: each `useQuery` / `useMutation` / `useSuspenseQuery` / `useInfiniteQuery` previously allocated 8-13 fine-grained `Signal<T>` instances at setup AND wrote to all of them on every observer notify, but real consumers read 1-2 fields. The hooks now use a slot-bag with property getters that `??=` materialize each signal on first access; the subscribe callback only writes to materialized slots. Same `Signal<T>` identity is preserved across repeat property access (load-bearing for Pyreon's identity-keyed effect tracking). Baseline diffs (5-run median): `queryMount-1000` `signalCreate: 9000 → 0`, `signalWrite: 10006 → 6` (-99.9%), wall-clock -15%, heap -10.7%. `queryNotify-10k` `signalWrite: 20070 → 7` (-100%), wall-clock -22%. `mutationInvalidate-1000` `signalCreate: 908 → 0`, heap -25.8%. The journey numbers are the EXTREME case (the QueryAtScale stress component doesn't read any result fields → zero materialization); real apps reading 1-3 fields land in the 67-89% range. Bisect-verified in the PR by reverting just the `data` slot of `useQuery` to eager: `signalCreate: 0 → 10`, `signalWrite: 7 → 10005` (= 10 subs × 1000 events for that one field) — proving the optimization drives the counter drop. Lazy contract locked in by `tests/lazy-signals.test.tsx` (4 tests: same-signal-identity guarantee for both `useQuery` and `useMutation`, plus end-to-end "read field, await mutate, see updated value" round-trips). The 5th `queryReactiveKey-1000` journey (100 useQuery with shared reactive queryKey × 10 flips = 1000 setOptions runs) was originally deferred from the foundation PR; root cause turned out to be a missing `runUntracked` wrap around child mounts in `<For>` — see "Reactive-render entry point untracking" below.
  - **Reactive-render entry point untracking (post-#490 fix)**: `mountFor` / `mountKeyedList` / `KeepAlive` / `TransitionGroup` all wrap their child mount work in `runUntracked(() => ...)` — same pattern `mountReactive` already had.
