Without this, signals read during a child's setup (`useQuery`'s `new QueryObserver(client, options())` reading the queryKey signal at construction time, `useTheme` reads, etc.) leak their subscription up to the OUTER reactive primitive's effect. When the leaked signal flips, the OUTER effect re-runs → `runCleanup()` disposes ALL inner effects (the children's per-component effects), and the keyed-update path skips re-mount on unchanged keys → the children's reactivity is gone forever. This was the structural cause of PR #490's deferred `queryReactiveKey-1000` journey: 100 useQuery hooks under `<For>`, 10 flips of a shared reactive queryKey, expected 100 × 10 = 1000 setOptions runs, observed 0 across the 10 flips because `<For>`'s effect tore down all 100 setOptions effects on the first flip. Bisect-verified at unit level: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/tests/fanout-repro.test.tsx` fails with `expected 100 to be 0` against the unwrapped version. Post-fix baseline: `query.setOptions: 1100` (was 100 pre-fix), `effectRun: 1104` (was 104). Reference: `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/nodes.ts` (mountFor + mountKeyedList), `keep-alive.ts`, `transition-group.ts`.
  - `island` (`@pyreon/server` browser-side): `scheduled`, `hydrated`, `skipped.never`, `skipped.nested`, `skipped.no-loader`, `error`, `prefetch`. The `island` namespace is emitted from `@pyreon/server`'s browser-running `client.ts` (per-island hydration scheduling, prefetch warming, success/error tracking). `scheduled - hydrated` at steady state = islands still waiting on a deferred trigger (`idle` / `visible` / `interaction` / `media`); `skipped.no-loader` should be zero (registry drift); `error` should be zero (pair with `data-island-error="invalid-props"|"hydration-failed"` on the failing element to diagnose). Note: the special-case mapping in `catalog-drift.test.ts` recognises that the `server` package emits the `island.*` prefix — see `LAYER_PREFIX_OVERRIDE`.
  - `i18n`: `t`, `lookupKey`, `lookupKey.fallback`, `interpolate`, `pluralResolve`, `namespaceLoad`. Foundation PR added the 6 counters + 4 stress journeys + baselines. Pair `t` with `lookupKey`/`interpolate` for per-call cost breakdown. `localeFlip-100` journey shape (`i18n.t: 1100` = 100 initial mount + 100×10 flips) confirms the locale signal's fan-out works as expected. Plural journey's lookupKey count is 1000 (not the predicted ~2000) because the plural-suffix probe hits on first try (`items_one`/`items_other` exist in `en`) — no fallback path fires.
- **Gate shape differs by package category.** Browser packages (runtime-dom, router, styler, reactivity, etc.) use `import.meta.env.DEV` so the gate folds to `false` at Vite build time and the counter strings tree-shake out. Server packages (runtime-server) use `typeof process !== 'undefined' && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` because they don't run through a Vite bundle in production — the gate evaluates at runtime under Node and correctly short-circuits when `NODE_ENV=production`. Consequence: server-side counter strings remain in the bundle (few bytes) but the runtime cost is zero. Verified by `src/tests/runtime-server-runtime-gate.test.ts` in perf-harness.
- **Dev-mode overhead is trivial.** `src/tests/ssr-overhead.test.ts` measures a 1k-row SSR render three ways: NODE_ENV=production (~1.14ms baseline), NODE_ENV=development with no sink (~1.12ms — within noise), NODE_ENV=development with a no-op sink installed (~1.20ms — ~5% overhead). The gate + optional-chain is essentially free, and even fully-firing counters add only a few percent.
- **Consumer APIs**:
  - `perfHarness.snapshot()` / `perfHarness.reset()` / `perfHarness.record(label, fn)` / `perfHarness.diff(a, b)`
  - `perfHarness.overlay()` — in-page shadow-DOM panel with live counters, Ctrl+Shift+P toggle, reset/record/export buttons
  - `install()` attaches everything to `globalThis.__pyreon_perf__` so devtools console can use it directly
- **Tree-shake regression test**: `src/tests/treeshake.test.ts` in perf-harness Vite-production-bundles each instrumented file and asserts both the `__pyreon_count__` identifier and every counter name string are absent from the prod output. Proves the dev-gate folds to dead code across all five layers.
- **Automation**:
  - `examples/perf-dashboard` — single-page real-app-shape stress rig; auto-installs the harness in dev so counters are live from boot. Journeys exported from `src/journeys.ts`.
  - `bun run perf:record --app <name> --journey <name>` — Playwright drives the example through the journey, N runs (default 5), writes `perf-results/<sha>-<app>-<journey>.json` with median counters + wall-clock + heap
  - `bun run perf:diff <baseline> <current>` — compares two records, exits nonzero on regression (upward move > threshold, absolute floor max(3, before × threshold) prevents noisy rare-counter false positives)
  - `.github/workflows/perf.yml` — advisory-only workflow; runs on manual dispatch, nightly schedule, and `perf`-labelled PRs; posts a sticky comment with the diff when a baseline is committed

### exactOptionalPropertyTypes

Enabled in root tsconfig — optional properties need explicit `| undefined` when assigned from functions that may return undefined.

### Manifest-driven docs pipeline (T2.1 + T2.5.1)

One source of truth per package — `packages/<category>/<pkg>/src/manifest.ts` — feeds every generated doc surface. `bun run gen-docs` regenerates `llms.txt` (bullets), `llms-full.txt` (per-package sections), and `packages/tools/mcp/src/api-reference.ts` (MCP regions). CI `Docs Sync` job runs `bun run gen-docs --check` against all three.

- **llms.txt / llms-full.txt** are regenerated wholesale for every migrated package.
- **api-reference.ts** uses OPT-IN region markers per package: `// <gen-docs:api-reference:start @pyreon/<name>>` / `... end @pyreon/<name>>`. **Coverage is partial, not complete: as of this writing 42 of 63 published Pyreon packages have a `src/manifest.ts` and are on the pipeline** (PR #319 onward). The remaining 21 have NO manifest and NO api-reference region — they are simply ABSENT from the generated surfaces (this is NOT the same as a hand-written block; there are no hand-written MCP api-reference blocks left — un-migrated packages just produce nothing). **Before any "enrich package X's docs/MCP" task, `ls packages/<cat>/X/src/manifest.ts` first — if it's absent the task is a migration, not an enrichment.** Real-API backlog worth migrating (packages whose public API agents actually `get_api`): `rocketstyle`, `attrs`, `coolgrid`, `kinetic`, `kinetic-presets`, `connector-document`, `dnd`, `sized-map`. Tooling / scaffolding (`cli`, `zero-cli`, `create-zero`, `meta`, `storybook`, `vite-plugin`, `typescript`, the 5 `*-compat` shims) mostly has no `get_api`-shaped surface — exempt those explicitly rather than ship thin filler manifests. Adding a new package: drop a `src/manifest.ts` matching the `@pyreon/manifest` `defineManifest()` shape, add `@pyreon/manifest` as a `workspace:*` devDependency (the `@pyreon/lint` convention — `manifest.ts` is gen-docs-only, tree-shaken from published `lib/`), add the marker pair to `api-reference.ts`, run `bun run gen-docs`. Quality bar varies by package — `flow` / `query` / `form` / `hooks` are at MCP density (dense `summary`, 6+ `mistakes` per flagship API); the more recently migrated packages (head, server, ui-core, unistyle, lint, mcp, document-primitives) start with verbatim ports of the prior hand-written entries plus a few obvious omissions filled in (e.g. all 11 MCP tools and all 18 doc primitives now have entries).
- **Field mapping** (manifest `ApiEntry` → MCP `ApiEntry`): `signature` / `example` passthrough; `summary` → `notes` (with `[DEPRECATED]` / `[EXPERIMENTAL]` prefix when `stability` is set, plus `seeAlso: X, Y`, `Added in vX.Y.Z`, `Deprecated since vX.Y.Z` trailers); `mistakes[]` → `mistakes` (joined `- item` bullets). The `McpApiReferenceEntry` type in `@pyreon/manifest` is asserted structurally equal to MCP's real `ApiEntry` via a compile-time `Equal<...>` check in `packages/tools/mcp/src/tests/api-reference.test.ts` — any drift fails `tsc --noEmit` before the generator produces stale output.
- **Migration recipe** for flipping a package to the MCP pipeline: (1) enrich the manifest's `api[]` entries to MCP density — 2-3 sentence `summary` carrying architectural rationale + per-API foot-gun `mistakes[]` catalog (see flow's manifest for the quality bar); (2) wrap the existing hand-written block in `api-reference.ts` with the marker pair; (3) `bun run gen-docs`; (4) add `renderApiReferenceEntries(manifest)` spot-checks to the package's `manifest-snapshot.test.ts`.
- **MCP `validate` tool runs two detectors (T2.5.2)**: `detectReactPatterns` (from `@pyreon/compiler`) catches "coming from React" mistakes — `useState`, `useEffect`, `className`, `htmlFor`, `onChange` on inputs, `.value` writes on signals, React-package imports. `detectPyreonPatterns` (added 2026-Q2) catches "using Pyreon wrong" mistakes — 15 detector codes today (`for-missing-by`, `for-with-key`, `props-destructured`, `props-destructured-body`, `process-dev-gate`, `empty-theme`, `raw-add-event-listener`, `raw-remove-event-listener`, `date-math-random-id`, `on-click-undefined`, `signal-write-as-call`, `static-return-null-conditional`, `as-unknown-as-vnodechild`, `island-never-with-registry-entry`, `query-options-as-function`). `query-options-as-function` makes the `@pyreon/query` best-practice surface **proactive**: the same rule ships as the opt-in `@pyreon/lint` rule `pyreon/query-options-as-function` (reactive — seen after running `pyreon doctor`/`pyreon-lint`), and now ALSO as a compiler detector so MCP `validate({ code })` flags it BEFORE the code is committed — an AI agent calling `validate` sees the fix (`useQuery(() => (...))`) without running lint. Object-literal first arg to `useQuery`/`useInfiniteQuery`/`useQueries`/`useSuspenseQuery` only; `useMutation` excluded by design; identifier/call args stay silent (unprovable). `props-destructured-body` is the body-scope companion to `props-destructured` — it flags `const { x } = props` written synchronously in a component body (precise: PascalCase JSX components only, bare `= props` first-param identifier unwrapped through `as`/`satisfies`/`!`/parens, does NOT descend into nested functions since handler/effect/accessor destructures re-read per invocation). Both detectors are AST-based (TypeScript compiler API, same style as `react-intercept.ts`). The merged result is sorted by line + column so the MCP output reads top-down. Idiomatic Pyreon code hits neither detector — the combined zero-false-positive test in `packages/tools/mcp/src/tests/validate.test.ts` is the regression guard.
- **MCP proactive docs: `get_pattern` + `get_anti_patterns` tools (T2.5.3 + T2.5.4)**: `validate` is reactive (catches bad code). These two are proactive — AI agents call them BEFORE writing to see the canonical pattern or the anti-pattern catalogue. `get_pattern({ name })` serves `docs/patterns/<name>.md` from the monorepo; 16 foundational patterns ship today (`controllable-state`, `data-fetching`, `dev-warnings`, `dynamic-fields`, `event-listeners`, `form-fields`, `imperative-toasts`, `islands`, `keyed-lists`, `reactive-context`, `reactive-spread`, `routing-setup`, `signal-writes`, `ssr-safe-hooks`, `state-management`, `styler-theming`). `get_anti_patterns({ category?, name?, full? })` parses `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md`; each entry surfaces its `[detector: <code>]` tag inline so an agent can pair the catalog entry with the live static detector. **Token-frugal by default (mcp-token-slim PR):** no-arg returns a COMPACT INDEX — one line per entry (title + detector tag + one-sentence hook), ≈3.3K tokens vs the ≈14K full dump (a ~76% cut on the common orient call), keeping per-category `## <Heading>` markers so categories stay discoverable in one call. Drill in with `{ name }` (single entry full body — cheapest), `{ category }` (one category\'s full bodies — unchanged contract), or `{ full: true }` (entire catalog, explicit ≈14K opt-in). A `token-budget.test.ts` regression gate pins `tools/list` < 1,300 tokens and `get_anti_patterns({})` < 5,000, bisect-verified to fail if the full-dump default returns. Parser + loader + index formatter live in `packages/tools/mcp/src/anti-patterns.ts` and `.../patterns.ts`. Add a new pattern by dropping a new `docs/patterns/<slug>.md` file — the tool picks it up on next call, no code changes needed.
- **MCP `get_changelog` tool (T2.5.8)**: AI agents get recent release notes for any `@pyreon/*` package without scraping `git log` or raw markdown. Parses changesets-populated `packages/**/CHANGELOG.md` into version entries (`{ version, changes[], dependencyUpdates[], empty }`) and returns the N most recent substantive versions. Filters out ceremonial version bumps by default (pure dependency-update releases with no user-facing body) since they're noise for agent consumers. Accepts both `"query"` and `"@pyreon/query"`. Params: `limit` (default 5) controls depth; `includeDependencyUpdates` opts the dep bumps back in; `since` filters to versions strictly newer than a floor (`since: "0.12.0"` returns the delta — especially useful when an agent knows the version it was trained against). Loader walks up to the nearest monorepo root. Parser + loader in `packages/tools/mcp/src/changelog.ts`; 44 tests cover synthetic edge cases (ceremonial bumps, multi-line bullets, mixed Major/Minor/Patch sections), the real-repo discovery (40+ packages), the `compareVersions` / `filterSince` comparator (semver-ish with pre-release ordering), and the tool handler over JSON-RPC.
- **Test-environment audit (T2.5.7)**: scanner + formatter in `packages/core/compiler/src/test-audit.ts`, exported from `@pyreon/compiler` so both `@pyreon/mcp` and `@pyreon/cli` consume it without pulling in each other. Scans every `*.test.ts(x)` under `packages/` for mock-vnode patterns — tests that construct `{ type, props, children }` object literals (or a custom `vnode()` helper / call-site) instead of going through the real `h()` from `@pyreon/core`. The bug class that caused PR #197's silent metadata drop: mock-only tests pass while rocketstyle / compiler / attrs work stays unexercised. Three risk tiers (HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW) from the balance of `mockVNodeLiteralCount` + `mockHelperCount` (defs) + `mockHelperCallCount` (call-sites, the pervasiveness metric) + `realHCallCount` + `importsH`. Two consumer surfaces: MCP `audit_test_environment` tool (options `minRisk`, `limit`) and CLI `pyreon doctor --audit-tests [--audit-min-risk high|medium|low] [--json]`. 32+ tests cover synthetic fixtures per tier, real-repo sanity, the `.test.ts(x)` filename filter, node_modules skip, zod/CLI-flag rejection of invalid minRisk, and JSON output contract. Use before modifying an existing test to check if strengthening is warranted, or after a framework change to audit for regression.
- **Scanner false-positive heuristics (T1.2 sweep)**: three context-aware skips were added to keep the audit honest after the initial scanner caught 14 false positives out of 24 HIGH files. (1) **Helper-def discrimination**: `(const|let)\s+vnode\s*=\s*(\(|\{|function|async)` — RHS must be an arrow fn / inline object / function keyword. `const vnode = defaultRender(...)` and `const vnode = <span/>` are real-VNode bindings, not factory definitions, so they no longer count. (2) **Type-guard call-args skip**: literals passed as args to `is*(...)`, `has*(...)`, `assert*(...)`, `validate*(...)`, `check*(...)` (uppercase-suffix identifiers, type-guard convention) are skipped — the literal IS the test input for a duck-type check, not a mock-render input. Closes `utils-coverage.test.ts` and similar. (3) **Template-string masking**: `maskTemplateStrings(source)` blanks the inside of every backtick-delimited region (preserving positions for line/column reporting). Fixture content written to disk via a `writeFile()` call whose body is a template-literal source string no longer counts as code under audit — closes `cli/doctor.test.ts`, the audit tool's own test fixtures. All three are bisect-verified by `tests/test-audit.test.ts` — reverting any one of them fails specific tests.

## Docs Website

Pyreon-native documentation site at `docs/` (package `@pyreon/docs`) — powered by `@pyreon/zero` + `@pyreon/zero-content`. 176 doc pages covering all packages (incl. a "Why Pyreon" honest-positioning page, a consolidated **Accessibility** guide (`accessibility.md` — the out-of-the-box a11y map: form label/error auto-wiring, `announce()` / `<RouteAnnouncer>`, modal focus trap + restore, primitive keyboard navigation, the multiplatform `accessibilityLabel`/`accessibilityHidden` vocabulary, reduced-motion, typed roles, and the opt-in a11y lint rules), a Quickstart with a live no-install `<Example>`, 42 auto-generated per-package API-reference pages (460 symbols) emitted from `src/manifest.ts` by `docs/scripts/gen-reference.ts` (rendering Features + end-to-end Complete-example + **Parameters / Returns tables** when a manifest `ApiEntry` provides the optional structured `params` / `returns` fields — `@pyreon/reactivity`'s core primitives populated today, other packages incremental), a generated Troubleshooting reference (7 categories, 100 anti-patterns) emitted from `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` by `docs/scripts/gen-troubleshooting.ts`, an Examples gallery (42 runnable `<Example>`s grouped by topic) emitted by `docs/scripts/gen-examples-gallery.ts`, 12 in-depth task-oriented guides (`guides/*` — data-fetching, routing, forms, state, styling, animations, SSR/SSG/ISR, islands, performance, testing, deployment, reactivity-in-depth, each grounded in the real package source + embedding live `<Example>`s), a Recipes cookbook (`recipes.md` — copy-paste task solutions: auth gate, optimistic UI, infinite scroll, dark mode, debounced search, persisted state, server-side form errors, polling), "Coming from React / Solid / Vue / Svelte / Angular" migration guides, a guided 6-chapter concept Tutorial track (`tutorial/01-signals` … `06-build-something`, sequenced with prev/next, each with a live `<Example>`), and a "Build a Real App in 30 Minutes" tutorial whose every step is a live inline `<Example>`). **Dogfoods the framework end-to-end** — the docs site itself runs on Pyreon's signal-based reactivity, fs-router, SSG, and content pipeline. Ships the **`<Example>` primitive** — real `.tsx` files mounted inline with optional cross-mount signal-bridging via `share="key"` — proving cross-mount reactivity no MDX-flavor framework can replicate.

Replaces the legacy VitePress site that previously lived here. The migration from `<Playground>` → `<Example>` landed in PR #1448 across 30 pages; the production cutover (delete VitePress, move docs-zero into `docs/`) is this commit.

```bash
cd docs && bun run dev       # serve docs locally
cd docs && bun run build     # build static site to dist/
cd docs && bun run preview   # preview the built site

bun run --filter=@pyreon/docs dev    # same, from repo root
bun run --filter=@pyreon/docs build
```

### Authoring docs in `docs/`

The new site uses `@pyreon/zero-content`'s markdown pipeline. Authoring contracts:

- **Live examples** — `<Example file="./examples/<topic>/<slug>" />` in any `.md`. The component file lives at `docs/src/examples/<topic>/<slug>.tsx` and is a real default-exported Pyreon component. Two `<Example>` calls with the same `share="key"` receive the SAME `Signal<unknown>` via `getOrCreateSharedSignal` — proving cross-mount reactivity no MDX-flavor framework can replicate
- **Code blocks** — every fence is highlighted by Shiki at build time using BOTH light + dark themes inlined into ONE `<span>` tree. Page's `data-theme` swap flips the visible variant via CSS — zero JS cost. Meta string drives wrapping: `filename=`, `showLineNumbers`, `highlight=` (1-indexed line numbers)
- **Code groups** — `:::code-group` with each child fence carrying `[label]` after the language. Active tab is a signal; SSR ships tab 0 visible; client-side hydration enables tab switching with **zero per-mount cost** (tabs are CSS class swaps via `data-active`, not VNode reconciliation)
- **Callouts** — `:::tip` / `:::warning` / `:::note` / `:::danger` / `:::info` container directives → `<Callout type="…">`. Levenshtein "did you mean…?" suggestion for unknown names + unclosed-fence heuristic warning
- **`registerExamples(import.meta.glob('./examples/⁎⁎/⁎.tsx'))`** must be called from `entry-client.ts` (compile-time-resolved relative to where it's called). Side-effect import + glob in the consumer's source tree
- **`<Example>` rendering contract**: example components MUST accept `{ shared?: Signal<T> }` as the prop shape and fall back to a local signal when undefined. This lets the same component work with or without sharing
- **Migration tooling**: `scripts/migrate-playground-to-example.ts` + `scripts/batch-fix-example-types.ts` automated the 36-instance migration. Reusable for future docs ports
- **`@pyreon/zero-content/README.md`** covers every plugin behavior + diagnostic; `docs/src/content/docs/zero-content.md` is the user-facing reference. Single source of truth for `Example` API lives in `@pyreon/zero-content` `manifest.ts:api[]` and MCP `get_api('@pyreon/zero-content/Example')`

- Pyreon-native: built on @pyreon/zero (fs-router + SSG) + @pyreon/zero-content (markdown pipeline)
- Deployed via GitHub Pages
- Workspace member: `"docs"` in root `package.json` workspaces
- Has `lint` script (oxlint) + typecheck (`tsc --noEmit`)

63 published packages across 5 categories under `packages/`, plus 7 private support packages:

- `packages/core/` — 10 packages: reactivity, core, compiler, runtime-dom, runtime-server, router, head, server, primitives, sized-map
- `packages/fundamentals/` — 25 packages: a11y, store, state-tree, form, validation, validate, query, table, virtual, i18n, feature, charts, storage, hooks, hotkeys, permissions, machine, flow, code, document, rx, toast, url-state, dnd, sync
- `packages/tools/` — 11 published packages: cli, lint, mcp, vite-plugin, typescript, storybook, react-compat, preact-compat, vue-compat, solid-compat, svelte-compat; + `devtools` (private, not published — Chrome DevTools extension)

- `packages/zero/` — 6 packages: zero, zero-cli, create-zero, create-multiplatform, meta, zero-content

- `packages/ui/` — 3 packages: ui-theme, ui-components, ui-primitives (private, internal demo / app component library)

Plus: `docs/` (Pyreon-native docs site, package `@pyreon/docs`), `examples/` (example apps).

## Reactive vs Static — The Core Rule

In Pyreon, components run ONCE. What's reactive and what's static depends on WHERE you read a signal:

```tsx
// Component props with signal reads are REACTIVE — compiler wraps with _rp()
<MyComponent title={name()} />  // compiler → title: _rp(() => name()) → getter on props
// Reading props.title in an effect/accessor tracks the signal

// DOM text children are REACTIVE — compiler wraps in accessor
<div>{name()}</div>  // compiler → () => name() — re-evaluates on change

// Reactive accessor (explicit) — always reactive
<div>{() => `Hello ${name()}`}</div>

// Context reads — ReactiveContext returns () => T, regular Context returns T
const getMode = useContext(ModeCtx)  // ReactiveContext → () => ThemeMode
getMode()  // reactive read
```

Rule of thumb:

- **Component props** = reactive when expression contains signal reads (compiler wraps)
- **DOM children with signals** = reactive (compiler wraps)
- **Context reads** = ReactiveContext returns accessor, read it in reactive scope
- **Destructuring props** = captures once (static) — use `props.x` for reactivity
- **`const` from props in JSX** = reactive (compiler inlines `props.x` back at use site) — `const x = props.y; return <div>{x}</div>` is now reactive
- **`let`/`var` from props** = static (mutable variables are not inlined)
- **JSX spread on a component** = reactive (compiler wraps spread sources with `_wrapSpread`) — `<Wrapper {...rest} {...overrides}>` preserves every getter-shaped prop through to the receiving component, no matter how the source was constructed (`splitProps`, `mergeProps`, raw `props` of a parent). DOM-element spread `<div {...rest}>` is also reactive (template path's `_applyProps`). Manual `Object.assign({}, source)` or `{...source}` in plain JS (not JSX) is NOT covered — use `mergeProps` / `splitProps` for those.

## Memory Leak Classes

The 8-PR sweep across #725-#741 surfaced 5 distinct memory-leak classes with real bug instances. Each class is catalogued in `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` "Memory Leak Classes" section with: bug shape, fix shape, every PR that landed an instance, and static-analysis coverage. Read that catalog before introducing a new module-level cache / stack / registry. Classes seen in this sweep:

- **A** (position-based stack pop on shared state) — #725 / #729 / #733 vue-compat
- **C** (unbounded caches) — #733 lint AstCache / #737 createStore / #741 vite-plugin caches
- **D** (event-listener pile-up) — #734 initTheme / #739 svelte-compat ChildInstance
- **F** (Promise queue stale resolution) — #730 charts+storage / #737 createResource
- **H** (closure-captured snapshot retention) — #725 effect snapshots
- **I** (orphaned `Promise.race + setTimeout`) — #734 ISR / #735 ssg-plugin

Two preventative lint rules ship in the `recommended` preset for the classes with high static-analysis precision: `pyreon/init-fn-needs-idempotency` (Class D) and `pyreon/promise-race-needs-cleartimeout` (Class I). The other classes are caught at audit time by the leak-hunt subagent prompt.

## Common Issues & Fixes

- `ComponentFn<{ name: string }>` not assignable → solved by generic h()
- `@pyreon/reactivity` missing from deps → add to package.json + `bun install`
- `noNonNullAssertion` → use `if (!x) return` guard
- SSR empty render → forgot `mergeChildrenIntoProps` in renderComponent
- DOM tests need happy-dom preload (bunfig.toml in each package)
- Vite resolves `dist/` not `src/` → add `resolve.conditions: ["bun"]` to vite.config.ts
- `signal(5)` doesn't write → use `signal.set(5)` (dev mode warns)
- `onClick={undefined}` crashes in production → runtime now bails on non-function handlers
- Context destructuring loses reactivity → keep the object reference, access properties lazily
- Theme mode switching broken → PyreonUI now uses getter properties for reactive mode
- `mergeProps` throwing `Cannot redefine property` → a source's getter descriptor was created without `configurable: true`. `mergeProps` now forces `configurable: true` on copied descriptors, but when authoring your own `Object.defineProperty` on an object that may later be merged, always set `configurable: true` explicitly.
- Symbol-keyed props silently dropped by `splitProps` / `mergeProps` → now preserved. Both utilities use `Reflect.ownKeys` so symbol-keyed brands (e.g. `REACTIVE_PROP`) survive the split and merge.
- `RefProp<T> = Ref<T> | RefCallback<T>` — the old narrow `(el: T) => void` mount-only arm was removed. Callback refs ALWAYS receive `el | null` at runtime; if you need a mount-only handler, accept `T | null` and early-return when null. Pairs with #233's null-on-unmount fix.
- `<For>` SSR key markers (`<!--k:KEY-->`) now URL-encode the key and replace every `-` with `%2D` so user-controlled keys can never form `-->` and break out of the HTML comment.
- `<Show when={signal}>` / `<Match when={signal}>` no longer crash with `props.when is not a function`. The compiler's signal auto-call rewrites bare `when={mySignal}` to `when={mySignal()}`, which previously produced a value (boolean) where the framework expected an accessor. `Show` and `Match` now accept value OR accessor — `typeof === 'function'` check normalizes both shapes. Reactive cases still need `when={() => signal()}` so the framework can re-evaluate when the signal changes; the value form is for static booleans and the auto-call edge case.
- `<Element tag="hr" />` (and other void HTML elements: `input`, `img`, `br`, `link`, `area`, `base`, `col`, `embed`, `source`, `track`, `wbr`) no longer trip runtime-dom's "void element cannot have children" warning. The Wrapper helper used to leak an `undefined` child into the JSX slot via `{own.children}` even when Element correctly skipped passing children. Wrapper now drops the children slot entirely for void tags via `getShouldBeEmpty(own.tag)` — the same util Element uses to make the void/non-void decision.
- `@pyreon/styler` `insertRule` failures used to be silently swallowed in production. Earlier the dev gate was bare `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` (which read as dead code in real Vite browser bundles), then briefly `import.meta.env.DEV` (Vite/Rolldown-only — broken under Webpack/Next.js, esbuild, Rollup, Parcel, Bun). The current convention across the monorepo is bare `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` again — every modern bundler auto-replaces it at consumer build time. Reference: `packages/ui-system/styler/src/sheet.ts` uses a local `__DEV__` const derived from `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`. Same convention applied to `@pyreon/coolgrid` and `@pyreon/attrs`. Tree-shake regression test in `packages/ui-system/styler/src/__tests__/dev-gate-treeshake.test.ts` bundles `sheet.ts` through Vite production and asserts the warn strings are gone, plus a dev-mode bundle to assert they're preserved. Enforced by `pyreon/no-process-dev-gate`.
- Passing `layout` to `createApp` / `startClient` while ALSO using fs-router's `_layout.tsx` no longer double-mounts. fs-router emits `_layout.tsx` as a parent `RouteRecord` (children = page routes), so the matched route chain already wraps every page in the layout. Pre-fix, also passing the same component as `options.layout` to `startClient` added a second wrapper around App's RouterView — 3× `nav.sidebar` + 3× `main.content` rendered after hydration mismatch on the fundamentals-playground layout. `createApp` now detects collision (`options.routes.some(r => r.component === options.layout)`), drops the explicit option, and warns in dev. User-side: never pass `layout` to `startClient` when using fs-router's `_layout.tsx` (the SSR pipeline doesn't pass it either — they used to disagree). The 4 examples (`ssr-showcase`, `ui-showcase`, `app-showcase`, `fundamentals-playground`) all use `startClient({ routes })` only.
- `<RouterLink to={someExpr}>` with a compiler-emitted reactive expression (e.g. `to={props.path}` from a parent component) now renders the resolved URL as `href`. Pre-fix, two bugs combined to produce `<a class="active" href="() => props.path">` on the fundamentals NavItem layout: (1) `runtime-server` (SSR) and `hydrate.ts` skipped `makeReactiveProps` on the way into a component, so `props.to` was the raw `_rp` function instead of a getter — `${props.to}` stringified the function source. (2) `RouterLink` hard-overrode the user's `class` prop with its internal `activeClass` accessor instead of merging, silently dropping `class={() => isActive() ? 'active' : ''}`. Both fixed: `makeReactiveProps` is now wired through `runtime-server`'s `mergeChildrenIntoProps` and through `hydrate.ts`'s component setup (parity with `mount.ts`). `RouterLink` destructures `class` separately and composes the user-provided value with `activeClass` via `cx`, returned from a single accessor so `applyProp` wraps it once in `renderEffect`. The systemic SSR/hydrate fix closes a class of "any `<Comp prop={signalRead}>` produces wrong attribute in SSR" bugs that was masked elsewhere because most apps re-mount client-side rather than relying on hydrated values.
- `useStorage` / `useSessionStorage` / `useCookie` / `useMemoryStorage` / `useIndexedDB` no longer render empty post-hydration. Pre-fix, every `@pyreon/storage` reactive primitive wrapped a base `signal()` with a callable that delegated `.direct` / `.subscribe` / `.peek` / `.set` — but never forwarded the internal `_v` field that the compiler-emitted `_bindText` fast path reads. SSR rendered `<strong>light</strong>` correctly (server invoked `theme()` directly via the JSX expression) but post-hydration the `_bindText(theme, textNode)` fast path read `theme._v === undefined` → wrote `''` → subscribers fired on every `.set()` and re-wrote `''`. localStorage was updated correctly the whole time; only the DOM stayed empty. The bug shipped from package inception across every storage backend; no existing tests caught it because none exercised the compiler-emitted fast path against a storage signal. Fix: each storage factory now defines `_v` as a getter that forwards to the underlying `sig._v`, so the fast path reads the live value on every access. **General contract** for any callable that wraps a base signal: if you delegate `.direct`, you MUST also forward `_v` via getter (`Object.defineProperty(wrapper, '_v', { get: () => sig._v, configurable: true })`) — `_bindText` / `_bindDirect` skip the function call and read `_v` directly. The companion rule is documented under "Reactivity Mistakes" in `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md`. Other wrapper-signal packages (`@pyreon/url-state`, `@pyreon/machine`, `@pyreon/state-tree`'s patch.ts) audit clean — they don't delegate `.direct`, so they take the safe slow path through `renderEffect`. Reference: `packages/fundamentals/storage/src/{local,cookie,custom,indexed-db}.ts`. Regression tests at unit (`packages/fundamentals/storage/src/tests/bind-text-compat.test.ts`, 6 specs) and real-Chromium e2e (`e2e/fundamentals/storage-hydration.spec.ts`, 4 specs); both bisect-verified.
- `@pyreon/core` `ErrorBoundary` cleanup no longer pops the wrong handler when sibling boundaries unmount out-of-order. **Same bug class as #725's `popContext` (followed up while sweeping core for the same pattern).** `ErrorBoundary` pushed its handler onto a module-level `_errorBoundaryStack` at setup and registered `onUnmount(() => popErrorBoundary())` where `popErrorBoundary` did `stack.pop()` — position-based. That assumed strict LIFO between push and pop, but sibling boundaries unmount in whatever order the renderer drives (keyed `<For>` removing a non-last item, `<Show>` flipping the FIRST of N siblings, route nav unmounting an outer of nested routes). A non-last sibling's `onUnmount` therefore popped the LAST sibling's handler instead of its own — the surviving (innermost) boundary's handler was removed from the stack and the unmounted boundary's stale handler was orphaned at the top. Subsequent throws in the surviving boundary's children dispatched to the orphan handler; `error.set(err)` on a disposed signal is a no-op, so the error was silently swallowed AND the surviving boundary's fallback never rendered. Real-app shape: chat lists / dashboards / any `<For>`-rendered list where each row is wrapped in `<ErrorBoundary>` — remove a row and the remaining rows silently stop catching errors. Fix: `popErrorBoundary(handler)` accepts the handler reference and removes by IDENTITY via `lastIndexOf + splice`. `ErrorBoundary`'s `onUnmount` passes its own handler. `popErrorBoundary()` (no-arg) still does `stack.pop()` for back-compat. Reference: `packages/core/core/src/{component.ts:popErrorBoundary, error-boundary.ts:71}`. Bisect-verified: reverting the fix → `error-boundary-stack-leak-repro.test.tsx` FIRST-unmounted-sibling spec fails with `AssertionError: expected null to be truthy` (surviving fallback never renders); restored → 2/2 pass.
- **Tools leak-class sweep follow-up (post-#725/#729/#730):** three findings across the 12-package `packages/tools/*` audit. **[Findings (1)+(2) are SUPERSEDED on the CLIENT by the owner-based context model — the global `pushContext`/`popContext`/`removeContextFrame` stack they describe is now SSR-only; client `provide()` writes onto the component's EffectScope owner and dies with the scope, so there is no orphan-frame growth. Finding (3) AstCache is unaffected and stands.]** (1) **`@pyreon/vue-compat` `provide(key, value)` used position-based `popContext` — exact #725 shape.** Vue-compat's `provide` pushed a Map onto Pyreon's global context stack via `pushContext` (the low-level API) and registered `unmountCallbacks.push(() => popContext())` for cleanup. `popContext` is the documented-unsafe `stack.pop()` API that the core `provide()` fix in #725 already stopped using. Sibling components unmounting out-of-order (renderer-driven `<For>` removal, `<Show>` flipping a non-last sibling, route nav unmounting an outer of nested provider chains) caused the first sibling's `popContext` to pop the LAST sibling's frame — the surviving sibling's frame was orphaned at the top forever. (2) **`@pyreon/vue-compat` `createApp(C).provide(k, v).mount(el)` pushed app-level provisions without ever popping them.** `mount()` ran `pushContext(...)` per provision before mounting, but the returned unmount only ran `pyreonMount`'s VNode cleanup — leaving app-level frames on the global stack permanently, one per provision per mount cycle. Multi-test harnesses + SSG re-mount cycles compound this. **Fix for both**: capture the pushed frame at push time, register identity-based removal via `removeContextFrame` (newly-exported from `@pyreon/core` for compat-layer consumers). Reference: `packages/tools/vue-compat/src/index.ts:provide` (line ~881) + `createApp.mount` (line ~1064). Bisect-verified: revert `vue-compat/src/index.ts` → `provide-stack-leak-repro.test.ts` both specs fail (`expected length to be baseLen, got baseLen + N`); restored → 2/2 pass. (3) **`@pyreon/lint` `AstCache` was unbounded** — keyed by FNV-1a hash of source text with no eviction. Each entry holds a multi-MB oxc-parsed AST + `LineIndex`. A long-running LSP session or `pyreon-lint --watch` editing across many files would accumulate one entry per UNIQUE content snapshot ever seen — hundreds of MB heap after a workday of editing. **Fix**: LRU bound (default 256 entries) using `Map`'s insertion-order property (first key = oldest); `get`/`set` on an existing key refresh recency by re-inserting at the tail. Reference: `packages/tools/lint/src/cache.ts:AstCache`. Bisect-verified: 5 LRU regression specs in `tests/ast-cache-lru.test.ts`; revert → all 5 fail; restored → 5/5 pass. **New `@pyreon/core` export**: `removeContextFrame(frame: Map<symbol, unknown>): void` — purely additive, used by `provide()` internally + now available to compat layers / advanced consumers that call `pushContext` directly. Audit byproducts NOT bundled: solid-compat `createStore` per-path signal Map unbounded; solid-compat `createResource` Class-F stale-resolution race; svelte-compat ChildInstance `unmountCallbacks` discard; vite-plugin per-instance caches lack file-delete invalidation.
- **Fundamentals leak-class sweep follow-up (post-#725/#729):** three correctness bugs found in 2 packages of the 22-package fundamentals audit. (1) `@pyreon/hooks` `useDialog` crashed on every component unmount — `ref` typed its parameter as `(el: HTMLDialogElement) => void` but Pyreon's RefCallback contract fires the ref with `null` on unmount; the body called `el.addEventListener('close', ...)` unconditionally, throwing `TypeError: Cannot read properties of null`. Fix: null path cleans up the previous binding + early-returns; ref param typed `HTMLDialogElement | null`. (2) `@pyreon/storage` `useStorage` cross-tab listener was retained ONCE per unique-key signal creation, NOT per consumer — same-key cached returns skipped the retain. `.remove()` always released, driving the refcount below the actual consumer count. Real-app symptom: N components each `useStorage('theme', 'light')`, one calls `.remove()` → cross-tab listener detached AND registry entry deleted → surviving N-1 consumers orphaned from the cross-tab pipeline. Fix: same-key cached returns also retain (refcount matches consumer count); `.remove()` no longer deletes the registry entry — keeps it so the listener's dispatch table remains intact. Reference: `packages/fundamentals/storage/src/local.ts:useStorage + .remove()`. Bisect-verified: revert → `Expected: "dark", Received: "light"` on surviving-consumer cross-tab test; restored → pass. (3) `@pyreon/charts` `loadAndRegister` + `@pyreon/storage` `openDB` both cached `loader().then(...)` / `new Promise(...)` in module-level Maps. Without a `.catch` clearing the entry on rejection, a single transient failure (CDN blip / IndexedDB quota) cached the rejected promise forever — any subsequent retry of the same key got the same rejection until page reload. Bounded by ~50 module keys / unique DB-store pairs but a real correctness footgun. Fix: `.catch(err => { cache.delete(key); throw err })` (same shape both files). **General rule** mirroring #725/#729's identity-removal lesson: any framework `Map<key, Promise<T>>` cache should clear on BOTH settle paths (`.then` AND `.catch`), not just resolution. Audit byproducts NOT bundled: `@pyreon/code` `<CodeEditor>` does not call `instance.dispose()` on unmount (design question — user vs component owns lifecycle); `@pyreon/state-tree` `_hookRegistry` unbounded growth with dynamic IDs (uncommon usage shape); `@pyreon/rx` `distinct`/`scan` missing dispose vs `debounce`/`throttle` having it (API inconsistency).
- `@pyreon/core` context stack no longer leaks orphan provider frames under repeated reactive remounts. Reporter shipped a 1 GB heap snapshot showing the live context stack at 321,024 entries but only 47 distinct provider `Map` instances — the same providers re-referenced thousands of times each, with 33 in-flight effect snapshots each holding a ~10,000-frame shallow copy via `captureContextStack()` from inside `effect()`'s setup-time snapshot capture. **Root cause (two cooperating bugs)**: (1) `provide()` registered `onUnmount(() => popContext())` — but `popContext` pops `stack.pop()` (the last frame). `mountReactive`'s effect-re-fire flow runs the previous-mount subtree cleanup INSIDE the effect's snapshot-restore window, so the snapshot-pushed frames sit ABOVE the descendant's own provider frame when its `onUnmount` fires. `popContext` popped the snapshot push; the descendant's provider frame was orphaned on the live stack. (2) `restoreContextStack`'s finally used `stack.splice(insertIndex, snapshot.length)` to remove its pushes — position-based. Identity-based removal by a descendant (fix 1) shifts the snapshot pushes down, making `splice(insertIndex, …)` either no-op or pull the wrong frames. **Fix**: both layers use IDENTITY-based removal. `provide()` and `withContext()` capture the frame reference at push, register `onUnmount(() => removeContextFrame(frame))` where `removeContextFrame` does `stack.splice(stack.lastIndexOf(frame), 1)` — robust to "wrong frame on top" regardless of the live stack's mutation history. `restoreContextStack`'s finally iterates `snapshot` in reverse and removes each frame via `lastIndexOf + splice`. `popContext` stays public + position-based (used by `@pyreon/runtime-server.trimContextStack` for the strict-LIFO SSR-render path where the unbounded-mutation hazard doesn't apply). Geometric amplification — each iteration leaves 1+ orphan frames; nested boundaries × thousands of toggles produce the 321k-frame state. Reference: `packages/core/core/src/context.ts:provide` + `withContext` + `restoreContextStack` + `removeContextFrame`. Bisect-verified: reverting `context.ts` to pre-fix state → the nested-boundaries regression spec in `packages/core/runtime-dom/src/tests/ctx-stack-growth-repro.test.tsx` fails with `expected 502 to be less than 10` (502 orphan frames after 500 toggle cycles); restored → 4/4 specs pass. **General contract** for any framework helper that pushes onto the context stack: capture the pushed `Map` reference at push time, register identity-based removal at cleanup. Never use `popContext()` as the cleanup callback — reactive boundaries can push frames between your push and your pop.
- `@pyreon/reactivity` `wrapSignal(base, { set, update? })` — the canonical **writable-side-effect facade** primitive (PR #1345). Wraps a base `signal()` with a callable whose reads (`()` / `.peek` / `.subscribe` / `.direct`) AND the internal `_v` field delegate to `base` (the `_v` forwarding is load-bearing for the compiler's `_bindText` fast path — see the storage-signal contract), while `.set` runs your custom `set` handler (do the side effect, then call `base.set(value)` to commit; `update` optional, defaults to `set(fn(peek()))`). Retired the hand-rolled facades in `@pyreon/storage` (5 backends) and `@pyreon/state-tree`, and FIXED a latent state-tree bind bug they shared (the facades missed `_v` forwarding). The `pyreon/storage-signal-v-forwarding` lint rule is the proof the primitive was missing — any wrapper delegating `.direct` without `_v` is now caught. Reference: `packages/core/reactivity/src/wrap-signal.ts`.
- `@pyreon/head` `useHead({ script })` — external scripts (`src` set) **default to `defer`** for non-blocking page load (PR #1365). The default applies ONLY when ALL hold: `src` present, no `type`, no `async`, no `defer` already set. Module scripts (`type="module"`) are NOT given explicit `defer` (they defer by spec); import maps + inline scripts (`children`, no `src`) are NEVER touched (must run synchronously); `jsonLd` is unaffected (`type="application/ld+json"`). Opt out with an explicit `type: ''` or `async: ''`. The `ScriptTag` type carries the full attribute surface (`crossorigin` / `integrity` / `nomodule` / `referrerpolicy` / `fetchpriority` / …). Reference: `packages/core/head/src/context.ts:ScriptTag`; docs `docs/src/content/docs/head.md` → Script Tags & Defer Default.
- `@pyreon/runtime-server` SSR attribute mapping — an internal `SVG_ATTRIBUTE_MAP` (module-level const, NOT exported) translates camelCase JSX SVG attrs to their kebab/namespaced SSR form (`strokeWidth` → `stroke-width`, `viewBox` stays, `xlinkHref` → `xlink:href`, etc.), with expanded HTML attribute coverage so `renderToString` emits the same attribute spelling the client `runtime-dom` does — closing a class of SSR↔client attribute-name drift (PR #1362). Reference: `packages/core/runtime-server/src/index.ts:SVG_ATTRIBUTE_MAP`; docs `docs/src/content/docs/runtime-server.md` → HTML & SVG Attribute Mapping.
- `@pyreon/head` `HeadProvider` no longer silently shadows an outer `HeadContext`. Pre-fix the component resolved its ctx as `props.context ?? createHeadContext()` — it ALWAYS allocated a fresh ctx when no explicit prop was passed, even when an outer `HeadContext` was already in scope. That broke every consumer of the documented composition `renderWithHead(h(HeadProvider, null, h(App)))` and, structurally, the entire `@pyreon/zero` SSG/SSR pipeline: zero's `createApp` mounts `h(HeadProvider, null, …)` unconditionally with no `context` prop, so every `useHead()` call in the App subtree wrote tags into the inner ctx while `renderWithHead` resolved the outer ctx (still empty) — static `dist/<path>/index.html` files shipped with an EMPTY `<head>` despite Meta/JSON-LD/OG/useHead working correctly. Social scrapers and non-JS crawlers saw nothing; Googlebot saw the post-hydration values so the bug stayed invisible to standard SEO sweeps. Resolution chain is now `props.context ?? useContext(HeadContext) ?? createHeadContext()` — explicit prop wins, otherwise inherit an outer ctx if one is in scope, otherwise auto-create. Inherited semantics restore the framework-wide rule that `HeadContext` is a single per-request registry; explicit-isolation cases (iframe / micro-frontend boundaries) keep working by passing `context={createHeadContext()}` explicitly. Reference: `packages/core/head/src/provider.ts:HeadProvider`. Bisect-verified: reverting `useContext(HeadContext) ??` from the chain → 2/5 specs in `provider-inherits-context.test.tsx` fail — `expected '' to contain '<title>Page Title</title>'` (zero-shape) AND `expected '<title>Outer Title</title>' to contain 'name="inner"'` (nested-shadow). Restored → 5/5 pass.
- `@pyreon/zero` `imagePlugin` placeholder strategy is now honoured on every path. `PlaceholderStrategy` typed `'dominant-color'` from the plugin's inception but never implemented it (CDN / dev / build all fell through to blur), AND `placeholder: 'none'` was only respected in the CDN path — `processImage` (build) and `loadDevImage` (dev) hard-coded `generateBlurPlaceholder`. Classic typed-but-unimplemented bug class (`audit-types` territory). Fix: a single `generatePlaceholder(input, strategy, size)` dispatcher used by all three paths. New `placeholder: 'color'` implements the dominant-colour strategy for real — sharp `.stats()` histogram swatch (approximate by design: pure-red → ~`#f80808`) as a constant ~200-byte flat SVG data URI (zero decode, instant paint, fixed size regardless of source complexity). `'dominant-color'` kept as a deprecated alias of `'color'`. Also: `quality` now accepts `number | Partial<Record<ImageFormat, number>>` for per-codec tuning (`{ avif: 55, webp: 75 }`); the single-number form is unchanged (backward-compatible). No `<Image>` changes — `placeholder` stays an opaque string. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/image-plugin.ts:generatePlaceholder` / `generateColorPlaceholder` / `resolveQuality` / `normalizePlaceholder`; tests `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/image-plugin.test.ts` (sharp-backed dispatch + per-format-quality + alias-normalization specs).
- `@pyreon/zero` `imagePlugin` dev-mode `?optimize` no longer serves raw filesystem paths. **Bug class — a downstream path consumer not updated when an upstream resolver started producing absolute paths.** The `resolveId` fix made `rawPath` an absolute fs path for relative/aliased imports (`/Users/…/img.png`), but `loadDevImage` still decided the dev URL with `rawPath.startsWith('/') ? rawPath : '/@fs/'+absPath` — `startsWith('/')` is `true` for an absolute fs path, so `vite dev` served `http://localhost:5173/Users/…/img.png` → 404 / broken image. Build mode was unaffected (separate `processImage` path → hashed `dist/` assets). Fix: `loadDevImage` uses the SAME `existsSync(rawPath)` discriminator the `absPath` derivation already uses — a real on-disk file (relative/aliased import) → Vite `/@fs/` prefix; only an unresolved `/foo.png` public-dir web path is served as-is (Vite serves `public/` at the web root). Audited siblings: favicon (static `/favicon-*` web hrefs, build-emitted), icons-plugin (Vite's own asset pipeline / `?raw` inline), SVG-as-component (inlined, never a fetched URL) — none share the class. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/image-plugin.ts:loadDevImage`; bisect-verified test `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/image-plugin-resolve.test.ts` (both branches: absolute → `/@fs/`, public web path → unchanged).
- `@pyreon/zero` ships ambient types for its custom Vite import queries out of the box (`@pyreon/zero/image-types`). **Packaging gap, not a missing-types gap** — `src/image-types.d.ts` (the correct `declare module "*.{jpg,png,webp,avif,svg}?optimize"` → `ProcessedImage`, `"*.svg?component"` → `ComponentFn`, `"*.svg?raw"` → `string`) already existed and shipped via `files: src`, but there was no `exports["./image-types"]`, so the `/// <reference types="@pyreon/zero/image-types" />` the file itself documents could not resolve — every consumer had to hand-author + manually keep a `declare module "*?optimize"` in sync with `ProcessedImage` (silent drift). Ecosystem precedent: `vite/client`, `vite-imagetools/client`, `vite-plugin-pwa/client` all ship their query ambients. Fix: wire `./image-types` as a real build entry (`{ bun: ./src/image-types.ts, import: ./lib/image-types.js, types: ./lib/types/image-types.d.ts }`, mirroring `./client`) + switch the internal `import('./image-plugin')` → `import('@pyreon/zero/image-plugin')` (resolution-stable: the package self-ref resolves via the consumer's `./image-plugin` export → clean `lib/types` declaration, not the full src `.ts`). **Two interlocking constraints made the "just add a `.d.ts`" first cut wrong (caught by CI, not local typecheck):** (1) `vl_rolldown_build` derives a build ENTRY from every exports subpath → a hand-authored `src/image-types.d.ts` with no buildable `src/image-types.ts` failed the zero build with `[UNRESOLVED_ENTRY] src/image-types.ts`. So the source is a real `src/image-types.ts` that `vl_rolldown_build` compiles → empty `lib/image-types.js` + DTS-emits `lib/types/image-types.d.ts` (the ambients, verbatim). (2) The repo tsconfig sets `moduleDetection: force` → every `.ts` is a module, so `declare module '*.svg?raw'` in a `.ts` is read as an *augmentation* of a non-existent module (TS2664). `src/image-types.ts` is therefore **excluded from zero's own `tsc --noEmit`** (it carries zero logic; the build's DTS emit produces a real `.d.ts` which is always ambient + moduleDetection-exempt for consumers). Consumers add one line to a tsconfig-covered `.d.ts`. **General lesson: a Vite plugin introducing a custom import query MUST ship + EXPORT its query ambients — and "ship a `.d.ts`" is insufficient when the build derives entries from exports (needs a buildable `.ts` source) AND `moduleDetection:force` is in play (the `.ts` ambient source must be excluded from the local typecheck; only the emitted `.d.ts` is the ambient contract).** Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/image-types.ts` + `package.json` `exports["./image-types"]` + zero `tsconfig.json` `exclude`; test `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/image-types-export.test.ts`.
- `@pyreon/zero` no longer emits a `node:async_hooks` "externalized for browser compatibility" warning in a consumer's CLIENT build. **Bug class — a dynamic-import SITE for a `node:`-bearing module living in a client-reachable file.** `i18nRouting()` (a server-only Vite plugin) held `await import('./i18n-routing-als')` (als statically imports `node:async_hooks`), and it lived in `i18n-routing.ts` — which is client-safe and reachable from the main entry via `useLocale`/`setLocale`. A dynamic import always produces a code-split chunk, so Vite/Rolldown emitted the als chunk in the CLIENT build and warned (runtime-safe — the browser never loads the server-only chunk, `node:async_hooks` externalized — but real noise + a dead chunk + a smell). **A lazy `await import()` does NOT escape the client-bundle leak; it only downgrades a build ERROR to a build WARNING + a dead chunk.** Fix: split `i18nRouting()` + its `parseCookies`/`_parseCookiesForTesting` helpers into a new server-only `i18n-routing-plugin.ts`, exported ONLY from `@pyreon/zero/server` (the manifest already documented `i18nRouting` as server-only — this aligns the source with the contract; no public API change). `i18n-routing.ts` stays client-safe (`useLocale`/`setLocale`/`extractLocaleFromPath`/`buildLocalePath` + the `_setLocaleStoreReader` bridge), with no als reference — so the client graph never reaches the dynamic-import site. Same shape as the `island` → `@pyreon/server/client` split. The `check-client-bundle-node-imports` gate PASSED through this bug because it deliberately skips dynamic imports (can't distinguish a server-hook-gated one from a leak); the regression guard is a SCOPED reachability test (`packages/zero/zero/src/tests/i18n-routing-client-safe.test.ts`, walks the main entry following static + relative-dynamic imports, asserts `node:async_hooks` unreachable, bisect-verified). NOTE a real `vite build` INSIDE vitest does NOT reproduce (vitest's Vite context changes warning routing + tree-shaking vs a standalone consumer build) — the static reachability walk is the faithful, deterministic model. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/i18n-routing-plugin.ts` (new) + `i18n-routing.ts` + `server.ts`; anti-patterns.md → "node:\* module at module scope in a client-safe published package" (fix shape 3).
- `@pyreon/zero` `mode: "ssr"` and `mode: "isr"` now auto-build the SSR handler bundle at `dist/server/entry-server.js` AND auto-invoke `adapter.build({ kind: 'ssr', … })`. Same typed-but-unimplemented bug class as `mode: "ssg"` before it — `Adapter.build({ kind: 'ssr' })` was implemented for all 6 adapters (vercel/cloudflare/netlify/node/bun/static) but no production code path called it. SSR/ISR apps shipped only a client bundle; users had to bundle their own server entry by hand and wire the platform deploy config themselves. The new `ssrPlugin()` (auto-wired into `zeroPlugin()` when `mode === 'ssr' | 'isr'`) closes that gap, mirroring the `ssgPlugin` precedent exactly: separate plugin file, `apply: 'build'`, `enforce: 'post'`, per-mode env-flag gate (`PYREON_ZERO_SSR_INNER_BUILD`, distinct from SSG's `PYREON_ZERO_SSG_INNER_BUILD` so cross-mode flag-leak failure class is structurally impossible). **Synthetic-vs-user-entry contract**: when `src/entry-server.ts` exists, the plugin uses THAT file as the bundle entry (preserves user-authored `securityHeaders()` / `cacheMiddleware()` / `ssr.mode: 'stream'` overrides / `actions: { corsOrigins }` config). When absent, the plugin materializes the canonical 6-line shape (`import { routes } from "virtual:zero/routes"; … export default createServer({ routes, routeMiddleware, apiRoutes })`) and cleans it up after the build — same fallback the SSG plugin uses. The shared infrastructure between SSG and SSR/ISR (env-flag set/clear recipe, atomic-write helpers, mkdir-cache, template-injection, synthetic-entry materialization) lives in `packages/zero/zero/src/ssr-build-shared.ts` so the SSG and SSR plugins can never independently drift their cleanup contracts. The SSR plugin invokes `adapter.build({ kind: 'ssr', serverEntry, clientOutDir, outDir, config })` after the bundle lands; adapter throws are caught + logged (not rethrown) so a buggy adapter can't hide the successful SSR bundle from CI — the bundle stays on disk at `serverEntry` for hand-deploys. The recursive SSR sub-build is gated by `apply: 'build'` (never runs during `vite dev`) AND the env flag (so the inner build's plugin chain doesn't re-enter the outer closeBundle). **`zeroPlugin()` now returns `Plugin[]`** for every mode: `[mainPlugin]` for SPA, `[mainPlugin, ssgPlugin]` for SSG, `[mainPlugin, ssrPlugin]` for SSR/ISR — Vite's plugins array natively accepts nested arrays so consumer `plugins: [pyreon(), zero()]` keeps working. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssr-plugin.ts` + `packages/zero/zero/src/ssr-build-shared.ts`; SSG companion is `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts` (refactored to consume the shared helpers).

  **Inner build inherits asset-emission settings from the outer config.** The inner `buildSsrBundle` runs `configFile: false` (it must NOT re-load + re-run the user's whole `vite.config.ts` — that's what the reconstructed `[pyreon(), zeroPlugin(userConfig)]` chain is for), but that ALSO dropped the user's `build.assetsInlineLimit`, so the inner build fell back to Vite's 4 KB default. Result: a `<= 4 KB` image the client build emitted as a hashed file (`/assets/logo-HASH.png`) was inlined as a `data:` URI in the SSR/SSG-rendered HTML — the two builds disagreed on the `<img src>` of every small image (a hydration mismatch; and combined with the SSR URL guard, the reason small placeholders could vanish from static output entirely). Fixed by capturing `resolved.build.assetsInlineLimit` + `resolved.build.assetsDir` in each plugin's `configResolved` and threading them into the inner build via `buildInnerBuildOptions(options)` (`ssr-build-shared.ts`) — a PURE, exported function so the config is unit-asserted without spawning a real build. **Only asset-EMISSION settings are inherited** (`assetsInlineLimit`, `assetsDir`); the SSR-runtime-fixed settings (`target: 'esnext'`, ES output, `node:` externals) are deliberately NOT inherited from the user. Apps that never set `assetsInlineLimit` keep Vite's default (no behaviour change). Proven with a real Vite SSR build (default inlines a sub-4 KB PNG as `data:`; with `assetsInlineLimit: 0` propagated it emits a file reference). Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssr-build-shared.ts:buildInnerBuildOptions` + the `configResolved` capture in `ssg-plugin.ts` / `ssr-plugin.ts`; bisect-locked by `tests/ssr-build-shared.test.ts` (removing the propagation lines fails the 3 "propagates" specs).

  **SSR/ISR deploy artifact builds, runs, and HYDRATES (the staging + production-template fix).** Three latent bugs made `mode: 'ssr'` / `'isr'` unrunnable end-to-end — invisible until someone actually ran the emitted server (nobody could, because step 1 crashed). All exposed + fixed once the artifact ran:

  1. **Copy-into-self EINVAL in every deploy adapter.** The SSR plugin (`ssr-plugin.ts`) invokes each adapter with `clientOutDir === outDir === distDir` and the server bundle already at `distDir/server`. Every adapter then did `cp(clientOutDir, outDir/<subdir>)` — a copy of a directory into its own subtree → Node `fs.cp` throws `ERR_FS_CP_EINVAL` ("cannot copy … into itself"); the node/bun server copy `cp(distDir/server, distDir/server)` is the even more direct "src and dest cannot be the same". The throw was caught by the plugin and NOT rethrown (so a buggy adapter can't hide the SSR bundle from CI), which meant the deploy artifact was silently never staged — `node dist/index.js` (the runnable server) never existed. Fix: a single `materialize(src, dest, { preserve })` helper (`packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/stage.ts`) handling **same dir** (no-op — server already in place / static+cloudflare flat client), **dest inside src** (copy top-level entries INDIVIDUALLY into dest — each entry's source/dest are disjoint subtrees once the dest's own top segment is skipped, so no copy-into-self — PRESERVING the originals so the flat `outDir` still serves under `vite preview` / other tooling; a whole-dir `cp(src, dest)` is what would EINVAL), and **disjoint** (recursive copy). Wired into all SIX adapters (node, bun, static, vercel, netlify, cloudflare); each was independently broken because the client dest is always `outDir`-or-a-subdir-of-`outDir`. **Why the bug shipped: the pre-existing `adapters.test.ts` used a mock client dir DISTINCT from `outDir`, so it only ever hit the `cp` (disjoint) branch — it never exercised the `clientOutDir === outDir` shape the real plugin produces.** A same-dir regression block now covers all six adapters; bisect-verified — reverting `materialize` to a raw `cp` fails all six with the exact EINVAL.

  2. **`/` shipped the empty `<!--pyreon-app-->` shell + no HTTP wrapper.** Once staging works, the node/bun server's static-first branch served the SSR template `index.html` at `/` (it maps `/` → `index.html`, `.html` has an extension → served as a static file), shipping the UNFILLED template shell instead of server-rendering the home route — and the cp crash had also meant the `dist/index.js` HTTP wrapper was never written (the "entry-server.js not HTTP-wrapped" symptom). Fix: the emitted node/bun server now static-serves ONLY real assets (`if (ext && ext !== '.html')`, no `/` → index.html mapping); `/` and any `.html` path fall through to the SSR handler → server-rendered. (A static SPA shell at `/` is what `mode: 'spa'` / the static adapter are for; in SSR mode `dist/client/index.html` is the unfilled template, never a prerendered page.)

  3. **Production SSR shipped the DEV client entry → no hydration.** `createHandler` defaulted `clientEntry` to `/src/entry-client.ts` (a dev path Vite serves; in production there's no Vite and it 404s) + `DEFAULT_TEMPLATE` (no hashed `<script>`, no CSS). `createServer({ routes })` passed neither, so the production page server-rendered but the browser 404'd the dev entry → never hydrated, no styles. Fix (adapter-agnostic): the SSR build copies the built client `index.html` (which carries the hashed `<script type=module src=/assets/index-*.js>` + CSS `<link>` + the `<!--pyreon-app-->`/`<!--pyreon-head-->`/`<!--pyreon-scripts-->` placeholders) → `dist/server/template.html`; `createServer` reads that sibling via `readBuiltTemplate()` (`new URL('./template.html', import.meta.url)`) and uses it as the production template, suppressing the dev client-entry injection via a new `clientEntry: false` option on `createHandler`/`createServer` (the template already references the hashed entry). Every deploy adapter copies the WHOLE server dir, so `template.html` travels to node/bun/vercel/netlify/cloudflare alike. Dev/tests have no sibling → `readBuiltTemplate` returns `undefined` → the handler's defaults apply (dev SSR renders via the separate `renderSsr` path that reads the real `index.html`).

  Also fixed the `createServer` JSDoc example (`@pyreon/zero` → `@pyreon/zero/server` — the bare import throws the server-only guard; the actual create-zero template was already correct).

  **Proven end-to-end** at three layers: (a) unit — `stage.test.ts` (materialize same-dir/move/disjoint), `adapters.test.ts` (all six adapters' same-dir staging + the node/bun spawn-and-curl runtime contract now asserting `/` SSRs not the shell), `server.test.ts` (`clientEntry: false` suppression + single-script-no-duplicate); (b) build-artifact — `verify-modes` `× ssr` cells (ssr-showcase / app-showcase / playground) assert the staged `dist/{client/index.html, server/entry-server.js, server/template.html, index.js, package.json}` layout (the layout only exists if staging ran without EINVAL); (c) real-Chromium — the new `ssr-node` e2e gate (`e2e/ssr-node.spec.ts`, `bun run test:e2e:ssr-node`, own config on port 5203) builds ssr-showcase in `mode: 'ssr'` and runs the EMITTED `node dist/index.js`, asserting `/` + `/about` are server-rendered (no `<!--pyreon-app-->`), static assets serve, and the page hydrates + client-navigates. Bisect-verified: disabling `readBuiltTemplate` (production template) fails the e2e hydration + asset specs with the dev-entry 404 while the SSR-render specs stay green; reverting `materialize` to a raw `cp` fails the adapter same-dir tests with EINVAL. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/stage.ts` + the six `adapters/*.ts`, `packages/zero/zero/src/ssr-plugin.ts` (template.html copy), `packages/zero/zero/src/entry-server.ts` (`readBuiltTemplate` + `clientEntry: false`), `packages/core/server/src/handler.ts` (`clientEntry: string | false`).

  **ISR shares this whole path** (`mode: 'isr'` → same node-adapter staging + production template; the handler is additionally wrapped by `createISRHandler`). It is gated the same way: a `verify-modes ssr-showcase × isr` cell (staged-artifact + production template) + the `isr-node` real-Chromium e2e (`e2e/isr-node.spec.ts`, `bun run test:e2e:isr-node`, port 5207 — runs the emitted `node dist/index.js`, asserts `/` server-renders + hydrates + is **cache-consistent** across repeat requests). The ISR caching SEMANTICS (LRU / TTL / `cacheKey` / `revalidate`) are unit-covered by `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/isr.test.ts` (47 specs). Before this, ISR's end-to-end deploy had NO committed gate (only the unit caching tests) — `isr-node` + the verify-modes cell close that.

  **Cloudflare (workerd) SSR — the node-runtime template+singleton path breaks on workerd; two fixes make it hydrate.** The above `readBuiltTemplate()` (`new URL('./template.html', import.meta.url)` + `readFileSync`) and the `registerSingleton(..., import.meta.url)` self-registration both assume a Node-style runtime. The node/bun/vercel/netlify adapters run on Node, so they work. **Cloudflare runs in workerd**, which has NO filesystem and passes `undefined` for `import.meta.url` — so verified-in-real-workerd (`wrangler pages dev`) surfaced two breakages a Node-side test could never catch: **(1) startup crash** — `normalizeLocation(undefined).indexOf('?')` threw `Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'indexOf')` at module-eval (before any handler), taking down every `@pyreon`-based Worker; **(2) no hydration** — `readBuiltTemplate`'s `readFileSync` can't reach the staged `_server/template.html` sibling on workerd → caught → `undefined` → the page shipped the dev `entry-client.ts` (no hashed `<script>`) and never hydrated. Fixes: (1) `@pyreon/reactivity` `normalizeLocation` guards `typeof url !== 'string' || url.length === 0 → '<unknown>'` (the duplicate-detection key is the package NAME + location, so a single re-registering `<unknown>` instance is idempotent via the same-location early-return; the only degraded case — two genuinely-distinct `<unknown>`-located instances → missed duplicate — is the documented safe failure mode AND structurally unreachable in workerd's single bundle). (2) the **cloudflare adapter inlines** the built template (`dist/server/template.html`, with the hashed entry) into `globalThis.__PYREON_SSR_TEMPLATE__` in `_worker.js`, then **dynamic-imports** the handler (`const { default: handler } = await import('./_server/entry-server.js')`) so the global is set BEFORE `createServer → readBuiltTemplate` evaluates; `readBuiltTemplate` reads that global FIRST, falling back to the `readFileSync` sibling for Node runtimes. `JSON.stringify(template)` is safe — `_worker.js` is an ES module (no HTML tokenizer), so `</script>`/backticks/`${`/the `<!--pyreon-app-->` markers all survive byte-for-byte (the handler's marker `.replace` finds them). **`nodejs_compat` is load-bearing, not optional**: the SSR bundle statically imports `node:async_hooks` (`runWithRequestContext`, instantiated at module-eval) + `node:fs`, which workerd resolves ONLY with the flag — the create-zero cloudflare scaffold sets it (`wrangler.toml: compatibility_flags = ["nodejs_compat"]`). **Lessons (in `.claude/rules/anti-patterns.md` → Build Pipeline Mistakes):** any `import.meta.url` deref at module-init must guard for `undefined` (workerd); a filesystem read as the ONLY delivery path for a build artifact breaks no-fs runtimes — provide a `globalThis`-inlined fallback set before the consuming module evaluates. Verified: `wrangler pages dev --compatibility-flags nodejs_compat` → `/posts` 200, server-rendered, ships hashed `/assets/index-*.js`, hydrates. Locked by `singleton-sentinel.test.ts` (workerd undefined-url block, bisect-verified → `indexOf` TypeError) + `adapters.test.ts` (the `_worker.js` global-set-before-dynamic-import + hashed-template structural assertion, bisect-verified) — node-invoke smoke alone can't catch workerd breakage (it has fs + a real `import.meta.url`, so it's a false-positive for the CF runtime). Reference: `packages/core/reactivity/src/singleton-sentinel.ts:normalizeLocation`, `packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/cloudflare.ts` (template inline + dynamic import), `packages/zero/zero/src/entry-server.ts:readBuiltTemplate` (global-first). **Follow-up (deferred):** a real-workerd CI e2e (`wrangler pages dev`, mirroring `ssr-node`/`isr-node`) — wrangler downloads workerd (cacheable like Playwright Chromium); the committed structural `_worker.js` assertion is the regression lock until then.

- `@pyreon/zero` `mode: "ssg"` now actually generates per-route HTML at build time. Before this fix, `mode: "ssg"` and `ssg.paths` were typed in `types.ts` but had no runtime — the plugin had zero Rollup build hooks, so apps configured for SSG silently shipped a SPA shell with no per-route HTML. The new `ssgPlugin()` (auto-wired into `zeroPlugin()` when `mode === 'ssg'`) hooks `closeBundle`, runs a programmatic Vite SSR sub-build of a synthetic entry that imports `virtual:zero/routes` + zero's `createServer`, loads the resulting handler, and renders each path to `dist/<path>/index.html`. Path resolution: `ssg.paths` accepts `string[]`, `() => string[]`, or `() => Promise<string[]>`; if neither is set, the plugin auto-detects static paths from the fs-router tree (anything without `:param` or `*` segments). The recursive sub-build is gated by an env-var flag so it doesn't infinitely re-trigger itself. **Breaking change for `zeroPlugin()` consumers**: it now returns `Plugin[]` (`[mainPlugin]` for non-SSG modes, `[mainPlugin, ssgPlugin]` for SSG). Vite's plugins array natively accepts nested arrays, so `plugins: [pyreon(), zero()]` keeps working — but downstream test code that assumed `zeroPlugin()` returned a single Plugin needs `.[0]` or array-aware access.

  **`getStaticPaths` per-route export (PR A of the SSG roadmap).** Dynamic routes (`/posts/[id].tsx`) used to be silently skipped during auto-detect — users had to hand-list every value in `ssg.paths`. Now: any route file can `export const getStaticPaths: GetStaticPaths<{ id: string }> = () => [{ params: { id: 'a' } }, { params: { id: 'b' } }]` (sync or async, returns `Array<{ params: TParams }>`). The fs-router scanner picks up the export at build time; the SSG plugin's auto-detect calls each route's enumerator and expands the URL pattern (`/posts/:id` × `[a, b]` → `/posts/a`, `/posts/b`). Catch-all routes (`[...slug].tsx`) work via `{ params: { slug: 'a/b' } }` → `/blog/a/b`. Errors during enumeration (function throws, returns non-array, missing params) are captured into `PrerenderResult.errors` and the build continues for other routes — SSG never aborts on a single bad enumerator. The type helper `GetStaticPaths<TParams>` is exported from `@pyreon/zero/server`. Mirrors Astro's per-route convention. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/fs-router.ts:detectRouteExports` (scanner), `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:autoDetectStaticPaths` (expansion), `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:expandUrlPattern` (URL substitution). Real-app coverage: `examples/cpa-pw-blog/src/routes/blog/[slug].tsx` enumerates blog post slugs.

  **PR C — auto-emit `dist/404.html` from `_404.tsx` convention.** fs-router scans `_404.tsx` / `_not-found.tsx` and attaches the default export as `notFoundComponent` on its parent layout's `RouteRecord`. The synthetic SSG entry walks the routes tree at module-eval time, picks up the first `notFoundComponent` (depth-first, supports nested per-locale 404s in the future), and exposes an async `__renderNotFound()` that pushes it through the same `renderWithHead` pipeline as regular paths — so styler tag, `@pyreon/head` meta, and asset preload links land on the rendered 404 exactly like every other prerendered page. The outer plugin reads both, renders, runs the result through the shared `injectIntoTemplate` helper (factored out of the per-path render loop in this PR — single source of truth for placeholder/fallback injection), and writes to `dist/404.html` (NOT `dist/__pyreon_404__/index.html`). Static hosts (Netlify, Cloudflare Pages, GitHub Pages, S3+CloudFront) serve `404.html` automatically for unmatched URLs — convention every major SSG framework uses. Gated by `config.ssg.emit404 !== false` (default `true`); skipped silently when no `_404.tsx` exists. The runtime's not-found handler wrapper short-circuits BEFORE the router for unmatched URLs and renders the component directly via `h(NotFound, null)`, so the SSG path mirrors that — no probe URL, no router preload. Bisect-verified at TWO layers: unit (`packages/zero/zero/src/tests/ssg-plugin.test.ts` — `walks recursively into route children` fails when the `r.children` recursion is removed) AND verify-modes (`scripts/verify-modes.ts` — `ssr-showcase × ssg` cells fail with `expected file: dist/404.html` when `findNotFoundComponent` is stubbed to return null).

  **Limitations of PR C** (most closed by PR L5 below): (1) **Host routing is required.** SSG writes `dist/404.html` but the static host (or your own reverse proxy) is responsible for SERVING it when an incoming URL doesn't match a prerendered file. Most managed hosts (Netlify / Cloudflare Pages / GitHub Pages / Vercel static) wire this by convention; S3+CloudFront / nginx / Caddy need explicit config. See `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md:_404.tsx convention` for per-platform deploy snippets. Without host routing, the framework emits the file but unmatched URLs return 404 with empty/default body — the carefully-rendered 404 HTML never reaches the user. (2) **Layout chrome was missing pre-L5** — that limitation is closed by PR L5 below: 404s now render WITH parent layout chrome (headers, footers, navigation).

  **PR L5 — 404 layout chrome via router-driven render.** Pre-L5, both PR C (default-locale 404) and PR K (per-locale 404) bypassed the router and rendered the not-found component via `h(NotFound, null)` standalone. The matched chain was empty, so parent `_layout.tsx` components didn't wrap the rendered 404 HTML — apps with branded chrome (sticky headers, sidebars, navigation, PyreonUI provider) saw a bare 404 page instead. Users had to inline the relevant markup into `_404.tsx` itself.

  L5 closes the gap by extending `@pyreon/router`'s `resolveRoute`. When a URL doesn't match any route, the resolver walks the route tree finding the deepest layout record (one with `children`) that has a `notFoundComponent` AND whose path is a prefix of the requested URL. It builds a synthetic chain `[...ancestorLayouts, syntheticLeaf]` where the synthetic leaf is a `RouteRecord` with `component = parent.notFoundComponent` and `path = '__pyreon_not_found_leaf__'`. The returned `ResolvedRoute` carries `isNotFound: true` so SSR handlers can set HTTP status 404 downstream.

  The SSG entry's `__renderNotFound(locale)` was rewritten to leverage this. Instead of standalone `h(component, null)`, it navigates the router to a synthetic non-matching probe URL per locale (`/__pyreon_not_found_probe__` or `/{locale}/__pyreon_not_found_probe__`) and runs the SAME `renderPath` pipeline that produces regular pages. `resolveRoute` returns the synthetic chain, `<RouterView />` at depth 0 renders the layout (which uses its inner `<RouterView />` to render the synthetic leaf at depth 1, producing the not-found component INSIDE the layout's chrome). Locale-aware: the probe URL's locale prefix ensures the right per-locale layout subtree matches.

  **Filter to layout records (records with `children`).** fs-router attaches `notFoundComponent` to BOTH the parent layout AND every page record under that layout. Page records have no `<RouterView />` to render the synthetic leaf at the next depth, so picking a page as the fallback parent produces a chain `[Layout, Page, syntheticLeaf]` where `Page` swallows the leaf. The walker filters to records with `Array.isArray(r.children) && r.children.length > 0` so the synthetic leaf always lands at a depth a `<RouterView />` will actually render. Discovered during integration: without this filter, the ssr-showcase 404 rendered the HOME page (deepest page with notFoundComponent → home record with path `/`) instead of the 404 component.

  **`pathPrefixApplies` segment-boundary semantics.** `/de` applies to `/de/unknown` and `/de` itself but NOT to `/encyclopedia` — full segment boundary required at the prefix's end. Root `/` applies to every URL. Deeper matches win, ties broken by path specificity (segment count). Wildcard catch-all routes (`(.*)`) still take precedence — they fire before the notFound fallback.

  **Bisect-verified at THREE layers**: (1) **router unit tests** — 9 specs in `packages/core/router/src/tests/match.test.ts` (`resolveRoute — notFoundComponent fallback` describe block), 5 of which fail when the fallback is disabled. (2) **verify-modes** `ssr-showcase × ssg` cell asserts `dist/404.html` contains BOTH `data-testid="not-found-page"` AND `data-testid="nav-home"` / `data-testid="nav-about"` — the layout chrome (nav links) and the 404 content co-occur in the rendered file. Reverting `findNotFoundFallback` → cell fails with `expected dist/404.html to contain "data-testid=\"not-found-page\""` (the empty router-view renders only layout chrome, no leaf). (3) **e2e** at `e2e/ssg-i18n.spec.ts` (per-locale 404 spec) — real-Chromium asserts both the testid AND nav links visible on `/de/404.html` AND `/404.html`. Companion `ssr-showcase × ssg` matrix cell covers default-locale 404.

  **Closes the doc limitation from L4.** L4 documented "no layout chrome" prominently in `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md:_404.tsx convention`.
