L5's update inverts the note: layouts DO wrap the 404 now. Host routing (the second L4 limitation) is unchanged — static hosts still need explicit per-locale 404 routing for unmatched URLs under locale prefixes.

  **noindex auto-injection (claim-3 from the render-modes audit).** The framework injects `<meta name="robots" content="noindex, nofollow">` into every emitted 404 HTML — at runtime (`render404Page` in `not-found.ts`) AND at build time (the SSG plugin's per-locale `__renderNotFound` writeFile path wraps the result of `injectIntoTemplate`). The `<Meta>` component's default of `'index, follow'` is correct for regular pages but actively wrong on a 404 — and most `_404.tsx` examples don't override it, so a stock build silently emitted `<meta name="robots" content="index, follow">` on every 404 page. Shared helper `ensureNoindexMeta(html)` is the single contract: it INJECTS the noindex tag when no robots meta is present, and OVERRIDES an index-permitting robots meta (the `<Meta>` default `'index, follow'`, an explicit `'index, follow'`, or the `'all'` shorthand) → a 404 is never indexable, so any index-positive value is rewritten to `noindex, nofollow`. A deliberate non-indexing directive (`noindex` / `none`) passes through UNCHANGED — which preserves a sophisticated app's `<Meta robots="noindex, nofollow, noarchive">` and keeps the helper idempotent against its own inject. **The original "bail if ANY robots meta exists — user override always wins" contract was too permissive**: the `<Meta>` component emits its `'index, follow'` default whenever the user doesn't pass an explicit `robots`, so every `_404.tsx` that used `<Meta>` (the common case — for title/canonical) silently shipped `<meta name="robots" content="index, follow">` on the 404. This was the bokisch.com 0.27.1 regression (Lighthouse confirmed `index, follow` on the live `/404.html`). Index-positive override is a strictly-better contract — the only value it clobbers is one that says "index this 404," which is never intended; a genuinely-deliberate `noindex…` still wins. Override case-insensitive across both quote styles; tokens split on `,` and matched exactly so `noindex` is never confused with another directive. Safe on body-only fragments (returns input unchanged when no robots meta AND no `</head>` is found). Bisect-verified at TWO layers: (1) unit specs in `ssr.test.ts` "render404Page" describe — reverting the helper to the old bail-on-any behavior fails the two `… is OVERRIDDEN …` specs (the `<Meta>` default `index, follow` case + the single-quote `all` case) with `expected … to contain '<meta name="robots" content="noindex,…'`, while the inject + deliberate-noindex-preserve specs still pass; restored → 14/14, AND (2) verify-modes `ssr-showcase × ssg` cell asserts `dist/404.html` contains `<meta name="robots" content="noindex, nofollow">` — stubbing the helper makes that cell fail with the missing-string error while every other cell stays green. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/not-found.ts:ensureNoindexMeta` (+ `robotsPreventsIndexing` directive parser) + the SSG call site at `ssg-plugin.ts` (`ensureNoindexMeta(injectIntoTemplate(template, result))`).

  **Limitations / known gaps** (after L5 + M1.2 + the 2026-05-13 layout-less-app fallback + the 2026-05-13 loader-skip-on-404 fix): (a) ~~**`notFoundComponent` is attached to layouts only.**~~ **Closed by the layout-less-app fallback (PR B follow-up to M1).** `findNotFoundFallback` (`packages/core/router/src/match.ts`) runs a two-pass walk: first the original layout pass (records with non-empty `children`), then a fallback for page records with `notFoundComponent` (records WITHOUT children — the layout-less single-page-app shape). When the second pass fires, the resolver synthesizes the chain as `[DefaultChromeLayout, syntheticLeaf]` where `DefaultChromeLayout` is a built-in `components.tsx` component rendering `<main data-pyreon-default-chrome><RouterView /></main>` — semantic-HTML landmark + a CSS hook for user-side styling, no prescribed visual design. The render pipeline produces 404 HTML wrapped in `<main>` instead of bare component output, accessibility / SEO improved. Layout-with-`notFoundComponent` precedence is preserved (layout pass wins; page-record fallback only fires when no layout matches). The `DefaultChromeLayout` wires through the setter pattern `_setDefaultChromeLayout()` in `match.ts` (registered at module load from `components.tsx`) to avoid a `components.tsx → match.ts` circular import — graceful degradation: if no consumer ever imports anything from `./components.tsx`, the setter doesn't fire and the fallback returns `null` (back to the standalone-render path). (b) ~~**Loaders on parent layouts run during 404 render.**~~ **Closed by the 2026-05-13 loader-skip-on-404 fix.** `router.preload(path, request?, options?)` now accepts a third arg with `skipLoaders: true` that bypasses the loader-running step entirely while keeping lazy-component resolution intact (so the synthetic chain still renders cleanly). The SSG plugin's `renderPath` forwards `{ isNotFound: true }` from `__renderNotFound` → `router.preload(probePath, undefined, { skipLoaders: true })`. Auth-touching layout loaders (`fetchUser`, session reads, private APIs) no longer fire during static 404 generation — the build has no real request context to drive them. Runtime SSR (`@pyreon/server`'s `createHandler` + dev-mode `renderSsr`) intentionally still runs loaders for 404 paths: analytics / audit-logging hooks that fire per-request should keep firing even when the request resolves to a not-found, and consumers may have wired loaders that are robust to the missing request context. The skip is opt-in at the call site; the framework only applies it for SSG build paths. Bisect-verified: reverting the `if (options?.skipLoaders) return` gate in router.ts:preload fails 2 specs in `router.preload — PR C — skipLoaders option for 404 build paths`. Public API surface change: `Router.preload` signature gained an optional third `options` parameter — back-compat (positional arg, no breakage for existing 2-arg callers). (c) ~~Runtime SSR (mode: 'ssr') still uses the old URL-pattern wrapper.~~ **Closed by M1.2.** Both production SSR (`@pyreon/server`'s `createHandler` in `packages/core/server/src/handler.ts`) AND the dev-mode `renderSsr` in `packages/zero/zero/src/vite-plugin.ts` now route unmatched URLs through the router's `resolveRoute` → `findNotFoundFallback` synthetic chain, so runtime SSR 404s render WITH layout chrome and emit real HTTP status 404. `entry-server.ts`'s legacy URL-pattern wrapper is preserved as a fallback only for apps that pass `notFoundComponent` to `createServer` WITHOUT having `_404.tsx` in the routes tree (backward-compat path; new apps should use the routes-tree convention). Bisect-verified at three layers: (1) per-package unit (`resolveRoute — notFoundComponent fallback` describe block, 9 specs), (2) verify-modes (ssr-showcase × ssg cell asserts layout chrome co-occurs in `dist/404.html`), (3) real-Chromium e2e (`e2e/ssr-showcase.spec.ts` — `runtime SSR 404 wraps not-found in layout chrome (M1.2)` spec hits an unmatched URL through the dev SSR pipeline + asserts both `data-testid="not-found-page"` AND nav-home / nav-about testids visible + HTTP 404 status). Reverting `findNotFoundFallback` in match.ts → unit specs fail; reverting handler.ts's `isNotFound` read → SSG cell still produces chrome HTML but emits status 200; reverting vite-plugin.ts's URL-pattern bailout removal → dev e2e fails with `element(s) not found` for `not-found-page` testid (handle404's static fallback fires instead).

  Reference: `packages/core/router/src/match.ts:findNotFoundFallback` + `resolveRoute`, `packages/core/router/src/types.ts:RouteRecord.notFoundComponent` + `ResolvedRoute.isNotFound`, `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:__renderNotFound` (probe-URL render path).

  **M1 correctness fixes (single PR closing four typed-but-incomplete behaviors).** Surfaces after the SSG roadmap completed; each one independently bisect-verified.

  - **M1.1 — ISR `cacheKey` opt-in + auth-incompatibility warning.** `createISRHandler(handler, config)` (`packages/zero/zero/src/isr.ts`) used to key the cache by `url.pathname` ONLY — cookies / query strings / headers were silently stripped. For auth-gated pages a single user's cached HTML was served to every other user, including anonymous visitors. The behaviour was correct for public sites but a privacy footgun for any logged-in surface. M1.1 added `ISRConfig.cacheKey?: (req: Request) => string` (opt-in) and prominently documented the auth caveat in `ISRConfig` JSDoc + `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md` ISR section + `llms-full.txt`. Companion fix in `revalidate()`: the background re-render now uses `deriveKey(originalReq, url)` so cookie-varied entries get re-rendered against the SAME cookies that produced them — pre-fix the revalidation issued a no-cookie request and stomped the user's cached entry with anonymous content. Drive-by: the cache-miss path now routes through the LRU helper `set()` (previously called `cache.set` directly, bypassing the `maxEntries` cap). Tests: `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/isr.test.ts` (3 cacheKey specs covering default pathname-only, cookie-varied, query-varied). **Default cacheKey changed to `pathname + search` (v0.27 follow-up).** M1.1's opt-in was a band-aid — the unsafe `pathname`-only default still shipped, so apps that didn't read the JSDoc still silently served `/posts?id=42` HTML for `/posts?id=99` requests. Visibly wrong content, structurally invisible to tests that probe one URL per route. The default is now `url.pathname + url.search` (matches Next.js ISR + RSC convention). Cookies / Authorization headers are still NOT included by default — that still requires an explicit `cacheKey` and the auth caveat survives. A one-time dev-mode `console.warn` fires at handler init when no `cacheKey` is configured (gated on bare `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` for bundler-agnostic tree-shake; deduped via module-level `WeakSet<deriveKey>` so a busy CMS doesn't spam logs; per-handler-instance contract so multiple handlers each surface their own warning). The warning names BOTH trade-offs explicitly: AUTH-UNSAFE for loaders reading cookies (supply `cacheKey: (req) => `${pathname}::${session}``), and HIGH-CARDINALITY for routes with analytics params like `utm_*` / `fbclid` (use `cacheKey: (req) => new URL(req.url).pathname` to strip the query). **Breaking default change in a minor bump** (pre-1.0 framework): apps relying on `pathname`-only caching with high-cardinality URLs will see cache growth proportional to unique query strings — the warning at handler init names the fix. Bisect-verified: reverting `deriveKey` to `url.pathname` makes the new default-behaviour test fail with `Expected "call 2 (q=99)" / Received "call 1 (q=42)"` (proves the test is load-bearing). Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/isr.ts:deriveKey` + `_warnedDefaultCacheKeyHandlers`.

  - **Pluggable ISR backing store (multi-instance production unlock).** `createISRHandler` was previously hard-wired to `new Map<string, CacheEntry>` — per-process, never shared. Multi-instance deploys (load-balanced Node, autoscaled containers, edge functions) needed sticky sessions or external cache plumbing the framework didn't provide. New: `ISRConfig.store?: ISRStore` accepts any backing matching `{ get(key), set(key, entry), delete?(key) }` with sync OR async returns. Default unchanged: `createMemoryStore({ maxEntries })` (extracted from the previous in-place `Map` logic) — drop-in pass-through, behaviour-identical for existing callers. Exports from `@pyreon/zero/server`: `ISRStore`, `ISRCacheEntry` (types), `createMemoryStore` (factory). The handler `await`s every store call — for the in-memory default this is a same-tick microtask (no real cost; `await` on a non-Promise returns the value); for Redis / Vercel KV / Cloudflare KV / Upstash adapters the awaits hit the real network promises. `config.maxEntries` is ignored when a custom store is supplied (the custom store owns its eviction/TTL policy). Tests: `tests/isr.test.ts` "pluggable store" describe (6 specs: default backwards-compat, `createMemoryStore` LRU bump on `get`, fake-Redis call sequence, async store roundtrip, cache-hit short-circuit, non-cacheable response does NOT call `set`). 19/19 ISR specs pass total.
  - **M1.2 — runtime SSR 404 layout chrome.** Production SSR (`@pyreon/server`'s `createHandler`) reads `router.currentRoute().isNotFound` after render and emits HTTP status 404 when the synthetic chain fired. `entry-server.ts` (zero) defers to the handler for any app whose routes tree contains `notFoundComponent` (the canonical `_404.tsx` shape) — the legacy URL-pattern wrapper stays only as a backward-compat fallback for `createServer({ notFoundComponent })` callers with no `_404.tsx` in the tree. Dev-mode parity: `vite-plugin.ts:renderSsr` drops its URL-pattern bailout AND returns `{ html, status }`; unmatched URLs route through `routerInst.preload(pathname)` → `resolveRoute` builds the synthetic chain → the renderer produces 404 HTML INSIDE the layout's chrome. Returns null (falls through to the static `handle404` fallback) only when the routes tree has no reachable `notFoundComponent` AND `resolveRoute` returned an empty `matched` chain. Bisect-verified at the dev-e2e layer: reverting `renderSsr`'s pattern-bailout removal causes `[ssr-showcase] navigation › runtime SSR 404 wraps not-found in layout chrome (M1.2)` to fail with `element(s) not found` for `getByTestId('not-found-page')`. The companion `404 page for unknown route` spec was tightened to assert ONLY the testid (the prior `.or('text=404')` fallback was for the static `render404Page(undefined)` shape which is no longer reached when `_404.tsx` is in the routes tree). Reference: `packages/core/server/src/handler.ts:170-172` (production status 404), `packages/zero/zero/src/entry-server.ts:158-184` (handler-delegation + legacy-fallback split), `packages/zero/zero/src/vite-plugin.ts:renderSsr` (dev-mode router-driven render).
  - **M1.3 — build-time ISR docs.** PR I shipped the runtime adapter hook + manifest format but `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md` covered runtime ISR only. M1.3 replaced the ~10-line ISR section with a ~135-line section covering BOTH runtime ISR (`mode: 'isr'`) AND build-time ISR (per-route `revalidate` export + `Adapter.revalidate(path)`), with the per-platform env-var table, cacheKey auth-gated warning + two examples, per-adapter caveats (Vercel POSTs to `/api/_pyreon-revalidate`, Cloudflare hits Cache API delete with rate-limit caveats, Netlify needs a Build Hook URL, static adapters are no-op), and composition guidance for mixing both layers. Drive-by markdown lint fix on the manifest table separator (`|---|` → `| --- |`).
  - **M1.4 — SSG path collision detection.** `ssgPlugin`'s `closeBundle` (`packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts`) used to silently deduplicate path collisions via the `writtenPaths` Set — a user error (two `getStaticPaths` enumerators producing the same URL, or a static route overlapping a dynamic-route enumeration) appeared as "missing pages" with no diagnostic. M1.4 adds `detectPathCollisions(paths) → string[]` + `formatPathCollisionError(duplicates) → string` and wires them into `resolvePaths` so the build aborts loudly with `[Pyreon] SSG path collision — N URL(s) resolved by multiple routes: ...` listing every collision sorted. Both helpers exposed via `_internal` for unit-testability; 6 specs in `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/ssg-plugin.test.ts` cover empty, unique, deduplication, canonical collision shape, error-message format, and single-element edge cases.

  **M2 scale + observability fixes (single PR closing five operational gaps).** Surfaces after M1 + the SSG roadmap completed; each one independently bisect-verified.

  - **M2.1 — atomic manifest writes.** `closeBundle` writes 5 underscore-prefixed manifests sequentially: `_redirects`, `_redirects.json`, `_pyreon-ssg-paths.json`, `_pyreon-revalidate.json`, `_pyreon-ssg-errors.json`. Pre-M2.1, a `SIGINT` during the flush chain (or any I/O failure mid-write) left partial state: half the manifests pointing at the new build, half the old. Adapters reading these at deploy time would see inconsistent state. M2.1 adds `writeFileAtomic(target, content)` — writes to a sibling `<target>.tmp.<pid>.<seq>` first, then `rename`s into place. `rename` is atomic on POSIX (and Windows same-volume); readers see either the OLD content or the FULL new content, never a half-written file. Best-effort cleanup unlinks the tmp file on rename failure. Per-page HTML writes (`dist/<path>/index.html`) intentionally stay plain-`writeFile` — they're individually-readable (no cross-file invariants) and the rename-per-page cost on 10k-path sites would be significant. Exposed via `_internal.writeFileAtomic`; 3 specs lock the contract.
  - **M2.2 — safe loader-data serializer.** Four call sites (`html.ts` `buildScripts` / `buildScriptsFast`, ssg-plugin SSR entry source, vite-plugin dev SSR) previously did bare `JSON.stringify(loaderData).replace(/<\//g, '<\\/')`. A loader returning `{ data, fn: () => {} }` worked by accident (JSON.stringify drops function values), but a loader returning a Mongo / Prisma model with back-references intact threw `Converting circular structure to JSON` — opaque, didn't name which loader. M2.2 adds `stringifyLoaderData(data)` to `@pyreon/router` with a custom replacer + WeakSet cycle detector. Strips functions/symbols silently, throws `[Pyreon] Loader returned circular reference at "<path>". Loaders must return JSON-serializable data...` naming the offending key, escapes `</script>` for safe inline embedding. All 4 call sites updated; 7 specs cover function-drop, symbol-drop, circular-ref error shape, `</script>` escape, plain pass-through, shared-ref treatment, empty record.
  - **M2.3 — SSG perf counters.** 5 new counters under the `ssg.*` namespace, emitted from `ssg-plugin.ts:closeBundle`: `ssg.pathRender` (per-attempt), `ssg.pathWrite` (successful HTML emit), `ssg.pathRedirect` (loader-thrown redirect), `ssg.pathError` (render error), `ssg.404Emit` (per-locale 404). Standard `globalThis.__pyreon_count__?.()` sink contract — zero cost without a consumer, zero cross-package coupling. `packages/zero/zero/src` added to `INSTRUMENTED_PACKAGE_ROOTS` in catalog-drift; `zero → ssg` mapping added to `LAYER_PREFIX_OVERRIDE`. COUNTERS.md gets 5 new rows. Drift test enforces both directions: every emit must have a catalog row, every catalog row must have ≥1 emit. Useful for CI plugins tracking SSG perf over time, future `vite build --profile`, or dev-time investigation via `bun --eval 'import {perfHarness} from "@pyreon/perf-harness"; perfHarness.install(); import("./vite.config.ts")...'`.
  - **M2.4 — adapter env-var warnings in production.** Pre-M2.4 the env-var-missing warn in all 3 platform adapters (`vercelAdapter`, `cloudflareAdapter`, `netlifyAdapter`) was gated on `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` — exactly the env condition that DEPLOYED apps run under, where users would most need the signal. Symptom: a CMS triggers `adapter.revalidate(path)`, nothing happens, no console output, no failure mode reported back. M2.4 introduces a shared `warnMissingEnv(adapterName, missingVars, hint)` helper that ALWAYS warns on the FIRST invocation per `(adapterName + missingVarSet)` (regardless of NODE_ENV), deduped via a module-level Set so a busy revalidation handler doesn't spam logs. Returns the canonical `{ regenerated: false }` shape so adapters write `return warnMissingEnv(...)` as a one-liner. 4 specs lock the contract: warns in production, dedupes across multiple calls, names every missing var, returns regenerated:false.
  - **M2.5 — build summary breakdown.** The `[zero:ssg] Prerendered N page(s)...` log line at end of closeBundle now includes: (a) revalidate-manifest entry count (`+ R revalidate path(s)`) so users see at a glance whether `_pyreon-revalidate.json` actually landed; (b) per-locale breakdown when i18n is configured (`[en: 100, de: 100, cs: 100]`) so shape mismatches like `[en: 100, de: 90, cs: 100]` (10 paths skipped for de) surface immediately instead of requiring `ls dist/<locale>/ | wc -l`. The `buildLocaleSummary` helper handles both i18n strategies — `prefix-except-default` counts unprefixed paths into the default locale; `prefix` skips them (unexpected under prefix). Exposed via `_internal.buildLocaleSummary`; 5 specs.

  **M3.A DX signals (single PR shipping three independent surfaces).** Follow-up to M1 + M2 — the analysis surfaced three DX gaps that aren't correctness or observability issues but cause silent author confusion when learning the SSG / ISR APIs. Each one independently bisect-verified.

  - **M3.1 — `vercelRevalidateHandler()` scaffold.** Pre-M3.1 `vercelAdapter.revalidate(path)` (PR I) POSTed to `/api/_pyreon-revalidate?path=…&secret=…` — a CONVENTION users had to implement themselves. M3.1 adds the drop-in handler at `@pyreon/zero/server`: `export { vercelRevalidateHandler as default } from '@pyreon/zero/server'`. Validates POST + path + secret query params, reads the build-time `_pyreon-revalidate.json` manifest, refuses revalidation for paths NOT in the manifest (closes "secret-leaks-once → attacker revalidates anything" footgun), then dispatches to a user-supplied `onRevalidate` callback OR returns success. Handler caches the manifest read on first call (process lifetime) so high-throughput webhooks don't re-stat the file. Returns Web-standard `Response` so it works in Vercel Edge functions, Node serverless via `@vercel/node` bridge, and the in-process `mode: 'ssr'` runtime. Options: `manifestPath` (default `./dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json`), `secretEnvVar` (default `VERCEL_REVALIDATE_TOKEN`), `onRevalidate(path)` (user callback). 13 specs lock the contract.

  - **M3.4 — `pyreon doctor --check-ssg` project-wide audit.** Three syntactic detectors in `@pyreon/compiler:auditSsg` (mirrors `auditIslands` shape — no type-check pass, no module resolution): (a) `404-outside-layout-dir` catches `_404.tsx` / `_not-found.tsx` NOT co-located with `_layout.tsx`, which falls outside PR L5's `findNotFoundFallback` filter and renders standalone without layout chrome; (b) `dynamic-route-missing-get-static-paths` catches `[id].tsx` / `[...slug].tsx` files without `export const getStaticPaths`, which the SSG auto-detect silently skips; (c) `non-literal-revalidate-export` catches `export const revalidate = TTL` (variable refs, arithmetic) which PR I's `extractLiteralExport` silently drops from the build-time ISR manifest. Each finding ships with file path + line/column + actionable fix. Wired through the doctor pipeline as the third opt-in audit alongside `--check-islands` and `--audit-tests`. CLI: `pyreon doctor --check-ssg [--json]`. 18 specs (per-finding broken/fixed pairs + discovery + formatter).

  - **M3.5 — three `@pyreon/lint` rules under a new `ssg` category** (65 rules / 13 categories total): `pyreon/revalidate-not-pure-literal` (error) catches the same shape as M3.4's detector at lint time; `pyreon/missing-get-static-paths` (warn) catches `[id].tsx` without `getStaticPaths` (warn-level because dynamic routes in `mode: 'ssr'` / `'isr'` legitimately don't need the enumerator); `pyreon/invalid-loader-export` (error) catches `export const loader = { data: 1 }` / `export const loader = "string"` etc. — non-callable exports that crash the SSR runtime with `TypeError: loader is not a function`. All three are route-scoped via `ROUTES_PATH_RE` on `context.getFilePath()` — the conventions only have meaning under `src/routes/`. 22 specs (per-rule broken/fixed pairs).

  Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/vercel-revalidate-handler.ts`, `packages/core/compiler/src/ssg-audit.ts`, `packages/tools/lint/src/rules/ssg/*.ts`.

  **M3.B docs + canonical example (single PR landing the SSG docs + showcase).** Follow-up to M3.A — extracts the SSG reference into a dedicated docs page AND extends the canonical blog example to exercise M3.A's three features end-to-end. Also closes a false-positive in `pyreon/missing-get-static-paths` that the example surfaced on first run.

  - **M3.2 — dedicated `docs/src/content/docs/ssg.md` page.** SSG content previously lived inside `zero.md` as a ~220-line subsection. The new dedicated page is ~580 lines covering: when-to-use SSG vs SSR/SPA/ISR, static + dynamic routes, `_404.tsx` with host-routing reference, loader-thrown redirects, per-route `revalidate` exports + the platform adapter table, `vercelRevalidateHandler` scaffold (M3.1) with security rationale, concurrency + progress reporting, subpath / base-path deploys, i18n route duplication + per-locale 404 + hreflang sitemap, sitemap auto-emit, render-error handling, path-collision detection (M1.4), the `pyreon doctor --check-ssg` audit (M3.4), the three SSG lint rules (M3.5), full manifests reference, per-platform deployment snippets (Netlify / Cloudflare Pages / GitHub Pages / Vercel / S3+CloudFront / nginx / Caddy), Next.js / Astro migration cheatsheet. Cross-referenced from `zero.md` (which is now slimmed to a quick-start overview) and wired into the docs sidebar under "Meta-Framework" right after Zero. Total doc-page count bumped to 77 (1 new).
  - **M3.3 — `examples/cpa-pw-blog` becomes the canonical SSG reference.** The existing blog example already exercised `getStaticPaths`, `_404.tsx`, sitemap auto-emit, RSS feed via API route, theme. Two M3.A-feature additions land here: (a) `export const revalidate = 3600` on `blog/[slug].tsx` — produces `dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json` entries for the 3 enumerated post URLs at build time; (b) new API route at `src/routes/api/_pyreon-revalidate.ts` using the M3.1 `vercelRevalidateHandler` scaffold with a `onRevalidate(path)` callback stub. Companion README documents what the example showcases + maps each feature to a deployable file. The verify-modes `cpa-pw-blog × ssg` cell was extended to assert `dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json` exists AND contains `"/blog/welcome": 3600` / `"/blog/why-signals": 3600` / `"/blog/static-vs-ssr": 3600` — bisect-verified by removing the `revalidate` export → cell fails with `expected file: dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json`.
  - **M3.5 false-positive fix — `pyreon/missing-get-static-paths` skips API routes.** Surfaced when running `bunx pyreon-lint .` against the showcase: the rule fired on `examples/cpa-pw-blog/src/routes/api/echo/[...path].ts` (a streaming API route with bracket filename). API routes are runtime-only by definition; `getStaticPaths` doesn't apply. Two complementary skips added: (a) **path-based** — files under `src/routes/api/` always skipped (fs-router convention); (b) **export-shape** — files without `export default` skipped wherever they sit (page routes structurally require a default-exported component; method-handler-only files are API routes by structure). Same fix mirrored in the `auditSsg` compiler detector at `packages/core/compiler/src/ssg-audit.ts:detectDynamicRouteMissingGetStaticPaths` so `pyreon doctor --check-ssg` doesn't false-positive either. Bisect-verified: removing the export-shape skip → `does NOT fire on files without export default outside api/` test fails with `expected [...] not to contain 'pyreon/missing-get-static-paths'`. 4 new lint specs + 3 new audit specs lock the contract.

  Reference: `docs/src/content/docs/ssg.md` (new), `examples/cpa-pw-blog/{src/routes/blog/[slug].tsx, src/routes/api/_pyreon-revalidate.ts, README.md}`, `packages/tools/lint/src/rules/ssg/missing-get-static-paths.ts` (API-route skip), `packages/core/compiler/src/ssg-audit.ts:detectDynamicRouteMissingGetStaticPaths` (parallel skip).

  **Dev-server bisect gotcha (M1-discovered).** The `vite-plugin.ts` source path runs through Vite's own config bundler, which uses the `node` condition → reads from `packages/zero/zero/lib/`, NOT the `bun` condition's `src/`. So reverting `src/vite-plugin.ts` alone is INVISIBLE to the running dev server — the lib was built from source as-of the last `bun install` / `bun scripts/bootstrap.ts` / `bun run --filter='@pyreon/zero' build` invocation. To bisect-verify dev-server-driven e2e specs (anything under the `examples/{ssr-showcase,…} dev` webServer), you MUST: (1) revert the source, (2) `bun run --filter='@pyreon/zero' build` to rebuild the lib, (3) kill the dev server (`lsof -ti tcp:5175 | xargs -r kill -9`), (4) re-run playwright. The user-side runtime code (`@pyreon/zero/server`, `@pyreon/runtime-server`, etc.) IS loaded via `ssrLoadModule` against the workspace `bun` condition — so `src/` changes there hot-reload — but the plugin chain is different. Same trap applies to any package whose code path lives in a Vite plugin (`@pyreon/vite-plugin`, `@pyreon/zero`). See `.claude/rules/testing.md` "Dev-server bisect" entry for the recipe.

  **Loader-redirect handling at SSG (PR B of the SSG roadmap).** Loaders that throw `redirect('/login')` for auth-gates used to silently disappear during SSG — `router.preload(path)` rejected, the path landed in `errors[]`, no HTML emitted, no redirect manifest, the user got no signal that the loader ran a redirect. Now: the SSG entry catches the redirect via `getRedirectInfo(err)` BEFORE rendering (rendering past a redirect would produce HTML for the wrong page AND leak auth-gated layout structure to unauthenticated users — same reason `@pyreon/server`'s SSR handler short-circuits on redirect-throw). The discriminated union `{ kind: 'redirect', from, to, status }` flows back to the outer plugin, which writes `dist/_redirects` (Netlify / Cloudflare Pages format: `<from> <to> <status>` per line) AND `dist/_redirects.json` (Vercel format: `{ redirects: [{ source, destination, permanent, statusCode }] }`). Both files ship together so adapters pick whichever they read; `permanent: true` for 301/308, `false` for 302/307. Optional `ssg.redirectsAsHtml: 'meta-refresh'` ALSO emits a static `<source>/index.html` with `<meta http-equiv="refresh" content="0; url=<target>">` + `<link rel="canonical">` for hosts without redirect manifest support (plain S3, GitHub Pages). Default `ssg.emitRedirects` is `true`; setting `false` restores the pre-PR-B behaviour where redirects fall into the error path. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:renderNetlifyRedirects` / `renderVercelRedirectsJson` / `renderMetaRefreshHtml`.

  **PR F — sitemap auto-emit from resolved SSG paths.** Pre-PR-F, `seoPlugin({ sitemap })` walked the file-system route tree directly and silently skipped dynamic routes (`[id]` / `[...slug]`) — their concrete values aren't knowable without running each route's enumerator. After PR A merged `getStaticPaths`, the SSG plugin now produces real concrete URLs at build time, so the sitemap should include them. The wiring: `ssgPlugin` writes `dist/_pyreon-ssg-paths.json` after the path loop with every path that produced an `index.html` (errored + redirected paths intentionally excluded). `seoPlugin({ sitemap: { useSsgPaths: true } })` flips its sitemap-emission hook from `generateBundle` (where the SSG manifest doesn't exist yet) to `closeBundle` with `enforce: 'post'` so it runs AFTER ssgPlugin, reads the manifest, merges paths into `additionalPaths`, writes `dist/sitemap.xml` via `fs.writeFile`, and cleans up the manifest (internal artifact — not for the published static host). Falls back gracefully when the manifest doesn't exist (mode is not `ssg`, or the SSG step was skipped) — sitemap still walks the file-system routes. Default `useSsgPaths: false` preserves prior behaviour. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/seo.ts:seoPlugin` + `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:writtenPaths` collector. Real-app coverage: `examples/cpa-pw-blog` + `verify-modes cpa-pw-blog × ssg` cell asserts `dist/sitemap.xml` contains `/blog/welcome` / `/blog/why-signals` / `/blog/static-vs-ssr` (the dynamic blog post URLs from `getStaticPaths`).

  **Per-route `<link rel="modulepreload">` (islands-safe) — issue #1355.** Vite already modulepreloads the single ENTRY's static graph (preserved in SSG output via `injectIntoTemplate`), but a route's own component chunk is lazy-imported, so the browser discovers it LATE in the network waterfall. The SSG plugin now injects the **per-route delta** into each prerendered page's `<head>`: the matched route chain's chunk(s) + their STATIC import closure, minus the entry graph. **Islands-safe by construction** — the closure (`ssg-modulepreload.ts:collectStaticChunkClosure`) follows ONLY the Vite manifest's `imports` (static), NEVER `dynamicImports`. A route's `dynamicImports` are exactly the deferred chunks (islands `hydrate:'never'|'visible'`, `lazy()`, heavy-module-in-handler); preloading them would pull deferred code onto the first-paint critical path and defeat the islands model. Verified end-to-end against `examples/ssr-showcase`: `/island-demo` preloads its own chunk + the `island()` runtime, but the deferred `IslandProbe` component chunk is NEVER preloaded. Mechanics: a `config()` hook enables Vite `build.manifest` on the OUTER client build (skipped for the inner SSR sub-build via `isInnerBuild` + `env.isSsrBuild`); `closeBundle` reads `dist/.vite/manifest.json`, maps each matched record's `_hmrId` (the lazy COMPONENT's source path — `record.component._hmrId`, NOT `record._hmrId`) → manifest key (`relative(root, _hmrId)` posix, with `src`-field + suffix fallbacks) → static chunk closure, subtracts the entry closure (`computeEntryHrefs` — real manifests list `index.html` inside each route's `imports`, so this subtraction is load-bearing) + the template's existing modulepreloads, injects `<link rel=modulepreload href=… crossorigin>` into `result.head` per path, then DELETES the manifest (internal artifact — unless the user enabled it themselves). Renderer emit format `href=… crossorigin` is distinct from Vite's `crossorigin href=…`, so build-artifact greps match only per-route links. Graceful at every step (missing/malformed manifest or unresolvable route → no preload, page still works — `modulepreload` is a non-load-bearing hint). Default-on for `mode:'ssg'`; opt out `zero({ ssg: { modulePreload: false } })`. Gated by `verify-modes ssr-showcase × ssg` (per-route delta present + per-route specificity + IslandProbe NEVER preloaded + manifest cleaned up; bisect-verified — making the closure follow `dynamicImports` fails the IslandProbe negative gate) + 19 resolver unit specs (`ssg-modulepreload.test.ts`). The companion "route-critical font preload" was already shipped (`font.ts` emits `<link rel=preload as=font crossorigin>`); this is modulepreload only. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-modulepreload.ts` + `ssg-plugin.ts` (`config()` manifest enable, `renderSsgEntrySource` routeModules collection, `closeBundle` injection + cleanup).

  **Render-error fallback hook + JSON artifact (PR G of the SSG roadmap).** Render exceptions used to land silently in `PrerenderResult.errors`, get logged to `console.error`, and the build continued — CI had no machine-readable signal beyond the exit code, and there was no way to emit a per-path fallback HTML so static hosts could serve something other than a 404 at the failed URL. Now two new `ssg` config fields close both gaps:

  - `ssg.onPathError?: (path, error) => string | null | Promise<string | null>` — invoked once per failed path. Returns a string → written as the path's HTML in place of the failed render (use this for "this content is temporarily unavailable" templates, branded fallbacks, etc.). Returns null → skip; the path produces no HTML output and the error stays in `errors[]` for the post-build summary. Async callbacks are awaited. The original error is ALWAYS recorded BEFORE the callback runs, so the artifact / summary catches the failure regardless of what the callback does. Callback throws are captured as a SEPARATE entry with the path suffix `(onPathError)` — a buggy callback can't take down the whole build, AND the bug surfaces instead of being swallowed.
  - `ssg.errorArtifact?: 'json' | 'none'` (default `'json'`) — when `'json'`, writes `dist/_pyreon-ssg-errors.json` after the render loop summarising every error encountered (path traversal, render exception, getStaticPaths throw, onPathError throw, 404 render fail). Each entry has `{ path, message, name, stack? }`. Wrapped in `{ errors: [...] }` (forward-compatible — future fields like `buildId` / `timing` can be added without breaking existing consumers). The file is ONLY written when `errors.length > 0` — successful builds don't leak an empty manifest. Set to `'none'` to opt out entirely (matches pre-PR-G behaviour where errors were console-only).

  CI consumption is now structural: `cat dist/_pyreon-ssg-errors.json | jq '.errors | length' | grep -q '^0$' || exit 1` gates on render failures without parsing console output. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:renderErrorArtifact` (serializer) + the `catch` block of the per-path render loop (the `onPathError` invocation).

  **PR E — subpath / base-path single-source-of-truth wiring.** Pre-PR-E, zero shipped THREE disconnected `base` settings: (a) `vite.config.base` controlled asset URL rewriting in built HTML/JS; (b) `zero({ base })` was typed in `ZeroConfig` and exposed to the client as `__ZERO_BASE__` — but **nothing read it**, the global was a typed-but-unimplemented surface; (c) `createRouter({ base })` controlled RouterLink href prefixing and route matching but was never wired from zero's config. Apps deployed to `/blog/` had to manually set ALL THREE in sync, and silently broke when any drifted (assets prefixed but RouterLinks weren't, or vice-versa). Now `zero({ base: '/blog/' })` is the canonical single source of truth and propagates through three coordination points:

  - **Vite's `base`**: `vite-plugin.ts`'s `config()` hook returns `base: config.base`. Vite's config-merge semantics make plugin-returned config the BASE — user's explicit `vite.config.base` still overrides if both are set, so the user's manual override wins. Asset URLs in built HTML get the prefix automatically.
  - **`createApp({ base })` → `createRouter({ base })`**: a new `base?: string` field on `CreateAppOptions` flows through to the router. RouterLink hrefs render with the prefix (`<a href="/blog/about">` not `<a href="/about">`), and `stripBase` correctly handles incoming URLs at request time.
  - **Three call sites forward base to createApp**: (1) `entry-server.ts` `createServer()` reads `config.base` from `resolveConfig`. (2) `client.ts` `startClient()` reads the Vite-defined `__ZERO_BASE__` global. (3) `ssg-plugin.ts`'s SSR_ENTRY_SOURCE template captures `__ZERO_BASE__` at module-eval time and passes through on every per-path render call.

  **Dist filesystem layout deliberately stays unprefixed.** `dist/about/index.html`, NOT `dist/blog/about/index.html`. Static hosts (Netlify, Cloudflare Pages, GitHub Pages, S3+CloudFront) serve `dist/` mounted at `/blog/`, mapping `/blog/about` → `dist/about/index.html`. The base belongs in URL contracts (asset paths in HTML, router hrefs), not in the on-disk layout. This matches how every major SSG framework handles subpath deploys.

  **`__ZERO_BASE__` fallback safety**: `typeof __ZERO_BASE__ !== 'undefined' && __ZERO_BASE__ !== '/'` — both client.ts and the SSG entry handle the no-Vite-define edge case (test environments, etc.) by treating the constant as undefined. The fallback is never hit in real Vite builds because the plugin's `config()` hook always declares the define.

  Real-app coverage gates the contract at THREE layers: (1) **build artifact** — `verify-modes ssr-showcase × ssg-subpath` cell with `zero({ base: '/blog/' })` asserts BOTH (a) asset URLs in `dist/index.html` start with `/blog/assets/` AND (b) RouterLink hrefs in `dist/about/index.html` resolve to `/blog/about` / `/blog/posts`. Bisect-verified: removing `base: config.base` from `vite-plugin.ts:config()` fails the asset-URL assertion; removing the `base: __ssgBase` forward in `ssg-plugin.ts:SSR_ENTRY_SOURCE` fails the RouterLink-href assertion. (2) **runtime navigation** — `e2e/ssg-subpath.spec.ts` (`bun run test:e2e:ssg-subpath`) builds the same dist + serves via `vite preview` on port 5198 and runs 4 specs in real Chromium: initial load + no-console-error sanity, asset URLs return 200 under base, RouterLink click triggers client-side navigation to `/blog/about` with no full page reload (asserted via window-sentinel preservation across the click), post-hydration counter increment patches DOM under base. Bisect-verified at this layer: removing the `__ZERO_BASE__` read in `client.ts startClient` → 2/4 specs fail (RouterLink-click and post-hydration-counter). (3) **API surface** — per-API unit tests in `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/app.test.ts` (`createApp — base option (PR E)` describe block, 4 specs covering forward + nested + default-`/` + undefined). The verify-modes layer covers SSR-emitted output, the e2e layer covers post-hydration runtime, and the unit layer covers the API contract directly. **Direct-link navigation to `/blog/about` (no trailing slash) is intentionally NOT covered** — that's a static-host directory-rewrite concern (Netlify / Cloudflare Pages / GitHub Pages do it; `vite preview` doesn't), not a framework concern.

  **PR D — concurrent rendering + progress reporting (SSG roadmap).** The pre-PR-D loop was fully sequential — `for (const p of paths) { await renderPath(p) }` — meaning a 1000-path site at ~50ms/page took 50 seconds, with 9× of every CPU core idle. Now: a worker-pool drains the path list `concurrency` workers at a time (default `4`, configurable via `ssg.concurrency`). Per-path semantics are preserved (timeout, redirect handling, error capture, onPathError fallback, 404 emission); only the schedule changes.

  Two new `ssg` config fields:

  - `ssg.concurrency?: number` (default `4`) — paths in flight. Set to `1` for the pre-PR-D fully-sequential shape (useful when loaders share a non-pooled resource — single in-process database connection, third-party API with strict serial rate-limits). Higher values land in the multi-core CI build sweet spot; the practical ceiling is your data layer's concurrent-connection tolerance. Clamped to `Math.max(1, value)` then to `min(value, paths.length)` so a misconfigured `0` or oversized value never silently hangs or spawns pointless idle workers.
  - `ssg.onProgress?: (info) => void | Promise<void>` — per-path settle callback invoked with `{ completed, total, currentPath, elapsed }`. Fires AFTER each path's render settles (success / redirect / error). Useful for build-tool progress bars, CI heartbeat lines on long builds (silent stretches on 10k-path sites look hung), and build-time timing instrumentation. Async callbacks are awaited PER WORKER before the same worker pulls its next item — across workers there is NO serialization, so callbacks may run in parallel; document this clearly (downstream consumer can wrap to a single-consumer queue if they need strict serial output). Callback throws captured as `(onProgress)`-suffixed entries in `errors[]` so a buggy callback can't take down the build.

  Generic worker-pool primitive `runWithConcurrency(items, concurrency, processItem, onSettled?)` is exported via `_internal` and tested in isolation (10 specs in `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/ssg-plugin.test.ts` — `runWithConcurrency (PR D)` describe block). Cap-clamping bisect-verified: removing the `max(1, …) + min(…, items.length)` clamps fails the `concurrency=0 → clamped to 1` spec with `expected [] to have a length of 3 but got 0`. The summary log includes a `(concurrency: N)` suffix when N > 1 so build output documents the actual schedule used. Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:runWithConcurrency` + the SSG closeBundle's worker pool that calls it.

  **PR H — i18n route duplication (SSG roadmap).** Pre-PR-H, the `i18nRouting()` Vite plugin handled request-time locale detection (Accept-Language, cookies, root redirect) but routes themselves were never duplicated per locale — `expandRoutesForLocales` didn't exist, the docstring at `i18n-routing.ts:179-182` falsely claimed fs-router consumed the i18n config, and SSG outputs / SSR matchers had no `/de/about` / `/cs/about` records to render against. Now: `zero({ i18n: { locales: ['en','de','cs'], defaultLocale: 'en' } })` (or `{ strategy: 'prefix' | 'prefix-except-default' }`) propagates through both build-time route generation (`vite-plugin.ts`'s virtual-routes load) AND SSG path expansion (`ssg-plugin.ts:autoDetectStaticPaths`) via the new `expandRoutesForLocales` helper.

  Two strategies:

  - **`prefix-except-default`** (default): default locale keeps unprefixed URLs (`/about` stays `/about`), non-default locales get explicit prefixes (`/de/about`, `/cs/about`). Best for SEO-on-default-locale apps — search engines see canonical URLs at `/about` while non-default speakers get explicit prefixes.
  - **`prefix`**: every locale prefixed including default (`/en/about`, `/de/about`, `/cs/about`). Root `/` becomes `/en` / `/de` / `/cs`. Better when no locale is "primary".

  Layouts, error boundaries, loading components, and 404 pages duplicate along with their pages — same source `filePath` (same component module), new locale-prefixed `urlPath` / `dirPath` / `depth`. The route tree built from the expanded array therefore has one fully-formed subtree per locale, so layout matching, dynamic params (`[id]` → `:id`), and catch-all routes (`[...slug]` → `:slug*`) all compose naturally with the locale prefix — no special cases.

  **`getStaticPaths` composition**: each duplicate route inherits the same `exports.getStaticPaths`. The SSG plugin's `expandUrlPattern` step then expands `/blog/[slug]` × locales × enumerator output into the cross-product (`/blog/a`, `/blog/b`, `/de/blog/a`, `/de/blog/b`, … under `prefix-except-default` with 2 slugs × 3 locales = 6 paths). Cardinality compounds, by design — `ssg.concurrency` (PR D) limits in-flight renders independent of route count.

  No-op safety: empty `locales` returns input unchanged; `[en] + prefix-except-default` short-circuits to identity (no other locales to prefix). The `i18nRouting()` Vite plugin (request-time middleware) is unchanged and orthogonal — both can be used together.

  Bisect-verified at TWO layers:

  - **Unit** (`packages/zero/zero/src/tests/i18n-routing.test.ts` — `expandRoutesForLocales` describe block, 18 specs): covers prefix vs prefix-except-default, catch-all routes (`[...slug]`), dynamic params (`[id]`), root index, layouts (per-locale subtree wrapping), `getStaticPaths` exports inheritance, depth recomputation, no-op cases, default-strategy fallback, multi-route trees.
  - **Real-app build** (`scripts/verify-modes.ts` — `ssr-showcase × ssg-i18n` cell with `locales: ['en','de','cs']`): asserts `dist/about/index.html`, `dist/de/about/index.html`, `dist/cs/about/index.html` all exist (per-locale variants); asserts `dist/en/about/index.html` does NOT exist (default-locale unprefixed under prefix-except-default). Bisect-verified by reverting the `expandRoutesForLocales` calls in BOTH `ssg-plugin.ts:autoDetectStaticPaths` AND `vite-plugin.ts`'s virtual-routes load — cell fails with `expected file: dist/de/index.html` (de-locale variant never enumerated, SSG didn't render it). Restore → 6/6 ssr-showcase cells pass.

  Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/i18n-routing.ts:expandRoutesForLocales` + the new `i18n?: I18nRoutingConfig` field on `ZeroConfig`.

  **PR H follow-up — root-layout skip + e2e gate + dynamic-route × locale cross-product.** Three additions on top of PR H's core route duplication:

  1. **Root-layout skip under `prefix-except-default`** — the original duplication produced a `/de/_layout` and `/cs/_layout` from the source root `_layout.tsx` (urlPath `/`). The route tree's hierarchical matching then wraps `/de/about` under BOTH the unprefixed `/_layout` (matches all paths as the root) AND the duplicated `/de/_layout` (matches `/de/*`). Result: layout component mounts twice, two navbars, two PyreonUI providers, two `<main>`. The fix in `expandRoutesForLocales` skips duplication ONLY for root-level layouts (`isLayout && urlPath === '/'`) under `prefix-except-default`. The unprefixed default-locale root layout already wraps locale-prefixed children via hierarchical matching — duplicating it is double-counting. **Non-root layouts** (e.g. `/dashboard/_layout` at urlPath `/dashboard`) MUST still be duplicated because the unprefixed `/dashboard/_layout` doesn't match `/de/dashboard/users` (path patterns don't intersect). **Under `prefix` strategy** the skip does NOT apply: there is no unprefixed default to inherit from, so every locale needs its own root layout. The bug was invisible at the unit + verify-modes layers (both check route enumeration + dist filesystem; neither inspects rendered HTML structure for nested layouts) — only surfaced via the real-Chromium e2e gate, which then drove the fix back into `expandRoutesForLocales` AND the unit-test suite (3 new specs covering the skip rule and its inverse under `prefix`). Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/i18n-routing.ts:expandRoutesForLocales` (the `route.isLayout && route.urlPath === '/'` guard).

  2. **Real-Chromium e2e gate** at `e2e/ssg-i18n.spec.ts` (own [`e2e-configs/ssg-i18n.config.ts`](e2e-configs/ssg-i18n.config.ts), separate webServer boot on port 5199 — same isolation rationale as ssg-subpath / ui-regression / compat-layers / app-showcase). Builds `examples/ssr-showcase` with `vite.config.i18n.ts` (sets `zero({ i18n: { locales: ['en','de','cs'], defaultLocale: 'en' } })`), serves the prerendered `dist/` via `scripts/serve-ssg.ts` (directory-rewriting static server — see "Directory-rewriting test server" below), and runs 4 specs: (a) default-locale unprefixed `/about` renders + zero console errors, (b) non-default `/de/about` renders the duplicated route, (c) third-locale `/cs/posts` renders with hydrated loader data — asserts 3 post-items AND the `window.__PYREON_LOADER_DATA__` global carries `/cs/posts` as a key, (d) RouterLink click from `/de/about` does client-side push (not full reload — window-sentinel preservation gates this). Companion to the build-artifact `verify-modes ssr-showcase × ssg-i18n` cell. The verify-modes cell asserts the dist filesystem layout; this gate asserts the runtime contract (router matches the duplicated record, hydration succeeds under the locale prefix, in-app navigation works between locale subtrees). Bisect-verified at TWO layers: (1) reverting the root-layout-skip → spec (d) fails with "matches more than one element" because two `nav-home` testids exist in the doubled layout DOM; (2) reverting the playwright config from `serve-ssg.ts` back to `vite preview` → spec (c) fails on `await expect(items).toHaveCount(3)` with `Expected: 3, Received: 0` because vite preview serves `dist/index.html` (the home page — zero post-items) for `/cs/posts` instead of `dist/cs/posts/index.html`. CI runs as a separate step in the `E2E` job: `bun run test:e2e:ssg-i18n`.

  **Test-environment artifact, NOT a framework bug.** PR #516 originally documented spec (c)'s loader-data assertion as a "known gap" — the SSG'd HTML carried 3 post-items but `useLoaderData()` returned `undefined` post-hydration. The hypothesis was "zero's dehydrated cache key doesn't include locale prefix." Investigation in this PR proved the framework was correct all along: `record.path === '/cs/posts'` on the duplicated route record (PR H sets `urlPath` to the locale-prefixed pattern), `serializeLoaderData` correctly keys the dehydrated payload as `{"/cs/posts": [...]}`, and `hydrateLoaderData` correctly walks the matched chain on the client. The bug was that `vite preview` does SPA fallback for SSG output — every URL that doesn't map to a literal file in `dist/` gets served `dist/index.html`. So `/cs/posts` was actually served the HOME page HTML, which has no loader-data inline script (the home page didn't load `/cs/posts`'s data at SSG time). `window.__PYREON_LOADER_DATA__` was `undefined` because the test was reading the home page, not the prerendered Posts page. With directory-rewriting service (real static hosts: Netlify / Cloudflare Pages / GitHub Pages / S3+CloudFront), `/cs/posts` correctly maps to `dist/cs/posts/index.html`, the inline data is present, and hydration works as designed.

  **Directory-rewriting test server**: `scripts/serve-ssg.ts` — minimal Bun static server (~80 lines, zero deps) that mirrors how real static hosts serve SSG output. `URL` without extension → `<path>/index.html`; URL ending with `/` → `<path>/index.html`; URL with extension → literal file. 404 falls back to `dist/404.html` (then plain text). Path-traversal guarded. **Honors `dist/_redirects`** (Netlify/Cloudflare format — PR L3) — `loadRedirects` parses the file at startup, `matchRedirect` short-circuits BEFORE directory rewriting and returns 301/302/etc with `Location` header. Real static hosts apply `_redirects` before any file lookup; serve-ssg matches that ordering so e2e gates exercising loader-thrown redirects (PR B) see the production shape locally. Used by `e2e-configs/ssg-i18n.config.ts` (port 5199) + `e2e-configs/ssg-i18n-prefix.config.ts` (port 5200); ssg-subpath e2e gate still uses `vite preview` because its specs don't exercise per-route prerendered HTML (only RouterLink-href and asset-URL prefixing, both of which `vite preview` serves correctly). Future SSG e2e gates that need to read the prerendered HTML for a non-index path should use `serve-ssg.ts` — `vite preview`'s SPA fallback masks the genuine production shape. Unit tests for `parseRedirects` / `loadRedirects` / `matchRedirect` / `createServeHandler` live at `packages/internals/test-utils/src/tests/serve-ssg.test.ts` (16 specs).

  3. **Dynamic-route × locale cross-product gate** — `examples/ssr-showcase/src/routes/posts/[id].ts` now exports `getStaticPaths()` enumerating 3 IDs. Combined with `zero({ i18n: { locales: ['en','de','cs'] } })`, the SSG plugin produces 9 concrete post HTML files (3 IDs × 3 locales) in addition to the static routes. The `verify-modes ssr-showcase × ssg-i18n` cell now asserts every cross-product file exists at `dist/posts/<id>/index.html` (en, unprefixed) and `dist/{de,cs}/posts/<id>/index.html` (per-locale). Locks the cross-product at the dist filesystem level — the unit test in `i18n-routing.test.ts` covers `exports.getStaticPaths` inheritance at the function level, but only this build-artifact gate catches the regression where `getStaticPaths` resolution is silently skipped for duplicated routes (e.g. if `expandUrlPattern` lost the `exports` reference somewhere in the duplication path). Reference: `examples/ssr-showcase/src/routes/posts/[id].ts:getStaticPaths` + the cross-product block in `scripts/verify-modes.ts:ssr-showcase × ssg-i18n` cell.

  **PR I — build-time ISR (per-route `revalidate` + `Adapter.revalidate(path)`).** Closes the 10-PR SSG roadmap. Two-layer design:

  **Layer 1 — build-time metadata.** Route files export `export const revalidate = <number>` (seconds, e.g. `60` / `3600`) OR `export const revalidate = false` (never revalidate). The fs-router scanner detects the export at scan time AND captures the literal value via `extractLiteralExport` (same pure-literal extraction shape as `meta` / `renderMode`); `RouteFileExports.hasRevalidate` + `revalidateLiteral` carry it through into `FileRoute.exports`. The SSG plugin's `closeBundle` emits `dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json` mapping `{ concretePath: revalidateValue }` for every prerendered path whose source route has a `revalidate` literal — including dynamic-route children (a single `posts/[id].tsx` with `revalidate = 60` and 3 enumerated IDs produces 3 manifest entries). Static hosts and adapter-driven deploys read the manifest to wire platform ISR. Filename starts with `_` so static-host publish steps don't expose it as a public asset (matches `_redirects` / `_pyreon-ssg-paths.json` convention). NOT inlined onto the route record at runtime — `revalidate` is purely a build-time deploy-config concern.

  **Layer 2 — runtime adapter hook.** New optional `Adapter.revalidate?(path: string): Promise<{ regenerated: boolean }>` on the `Adapter` interface. Each shipped adapter implements platform-specific ISR:
  - **`vercelAdapter`**: POSTs to `<deployment-url>/api/_pyreon-revalidate?path=…&secret=…` with `VERCEL_DEPLOYMENT_URL` + `VERCEL_REVALIDATE_TOKEN` env vars. User-side webhook handler reads the manifest + calls `adapter.revalidate(path)` for each entry.
  - **`cloudflareAdapter`**: POSTs to Cloudflare's `zones/<zone-id>/purge_cache` API with the full URL — Cloudflare invalidates the edge cache, next request triggers fresh origin fetch + rebuild. Needs `CLOUDFLARE_ZONE_ID` + `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN` + `CLOUDFLARE_SITE_URL` env vars.
  - **`netlifyAdapter`**: POSTs to a Build Hook URL (configured per-site) with `trigger_title=revalidate:<path>` for audit-log traceability. Netlify queues a partial rebuild. Needs `NETLIFY_BUILD_HOOK_URL` env var.
  - **`staticAdapter`** / **`nodeAdapter`** / **`bunAdapter`**: no-op fallback returning `{ regenerated: false }` + dev-mode warning. Static hosts + self-hosted Node/Bun have no platform-driven ISR; users wanting cache-with-TTL need `mode: 'isr'` (runtime LRU caching) instead.

  **Distinct from runtime ISR (`mode: 'isr'`).** Runtime ISR is on-demand SSR caching with TTL via `createISRHandler` in `@pyreon/zero/server` — pages are rendered on the FIRST request, cached for `cacheTtl` ms, served stale until expiry. Build-time ISR (this PR) is static prerender + platform-driven rebuild-on-stale. They can coexist: a `mode: 'isr'` app with per-route `revalidate` exports gets BOTH runtime caching AND deploy-time ISR config.

  **Real-app coverage** at the `verify-modes ssr-showcase × ssg` autodetect cell. `examples/ssr-showcase/src/routes/posts/[id].ts` ships `revalidate = 60`; the cell asserts `dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json` exists and contains `{ '/posts/1': 60, '/posts/2': 60, '/posts/3': 60 }` AND that `/about` (no revalidate export) is NOT in the manifest. Bisect-verified: reverting the manifest-emit block in `ssg-plugin.ts:closeBundle` → cell fails with `expected file: dist/_pyreon-revalidate.json`. Restored → 6/6 ssr-showcase cells pass.

  **Per-platform unit tests** at `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/adapters.test.ts` use a stubbed `globalThis.fetch` to assert each adapter (a) returns `regenerated: false` when env vars are missing (no-credential setup), (b) issues the right HTTP request to the platform's revalidation endpoint when env vars are set, (c) returns `regenerated: false` on platform 4xx/5xx. Bisect-verified at the unit layer too: reverting Vercel's URL-builder → the URL-shape assertion fails with `expected calls[0]?.url === <full URL>`.

  **No e2e gate** for this PR — build-time ISR has no runtime UI surface to drive Playwright against. The platform-side revalidation requires real Vercel/Cloudflare/Netlify credentials + test deployments. Closest equivalent is the verify-modes cell (real Vite build, real route file with `revalidate` export, real SSG plugin chain emits the artifact) + the per-adapter stubbed-fetch unit tests (proves each adapter calls the right platform API with the right shape).

  **Limitations / known gaps**:
  - The literal-capture path skips re-export forms (`const x = 60; export { x as revalidate }`) and non-literal expressions (`export const revalidate = TTL`). `hasRevalidate` is still `true` in those cases — the export exists — but `revalidateLiteral` is undefined and the manifest skips the entry. Documented as a limitation in the unit tests; users who want the manifest entry should export inline (`export const revalidate = 60`).
  - Netlify's Build Hook is a full-site rebuild trigger, not per-page revalidation — Netlify doesn't expose a per-page ISR API. The path arg flows into `trigger_title` for audit-log traceability but doesn't scope the rebuild.
  - Vercel's revalidation endpoint (`/api/_pyreon-revalidate`) is a convention this PR introduces — user-side serverless function code that reads the request, validates the secret, and calls Vercel's `res.revalidate()` API. Future work could ship a `@pyreon/zero/vercel-revalidate-handler` helper to scaffold it.

  Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/fs-router.ts:detectRouteExports` (literal extraction), `packages/zero/zero/src/types.ts:RouteFileExports` (`hasRevalidate` + `revalidateLiteral`) and `Adapter.revalidate?` + `AdapterRevalidateResult`, `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:buildRevalidateManifest` + the manifest-emit block in `closeBundle`, `packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/*.ts:revalidate` per-platform implementations.

  **PR J — adapter.build() wired into SSG closeBundle + per-platform SSG branches.** Pre-PR-J `Adapter.build()` was implemented for all 6 adapters (`vercel`, `cloudflare`, `netlify`, `node`, `bun`, `static`) BUT no production code path called the methods. Apps configured for `adapter: 'vercel' | 'cloudflare' | 'netlify'` got their dist directory built but no platform routing config emitted — `.vercel/output/config.json` / `_routes.json` / `netlify.toml` were absent, forcing users to write those files by hand or accept platform-default behaviour (which on Cloudflare meant invoking the Pages function for every URL even when the site was fully prerendered, wasting compute / cost on paid plans).

  PR J wires `adapter.build()` into `ssgPlugin`'s `closeBundle` AFTER the path render loop. The build pipeline is now:

  1. Render all paths (PR D worker pool)
  2. Emit `_redirects` / `_redirects.json` (PR B redirect manifests)
  3. Emit `dist/404.html` (PR C)
  4. Emit `_pyreon-ssg-paths.json` (PR F sitemap manifest)
  5. Emit `_pyreon-ssg-errors.json` if any errors (PR G)
  6. **Call `adapter.build({ kind: 'ssg', outDir, config })`** (PR J — new step)
  7. Cleanup SSR build artifacts

  **`AdapterBuildOptions` is now a discriminated union** on the new `kind` field. Pre-PR-J it was a single SSR-shaped struct with `serverEntry` / `clientOutDir` required. SSG callers couldn't supply a server entry (every page is prerendered) so they couldn't invoke `build()`. The discriminated union splits into:

  - `{ kind: 'ssr', serverEntry, clientOutDir, outDir, config }` — for SSR mode (unchanged shape; existing adapter SSR branches keep working with no behavior change)
  - `{ kind: 'ssg', outDir, config }` — new SSG variant; `outDir` IS the rendered dist directory the SSG plugin produced

  Each platform adapter's SSG branch:

  - **`vercelAdapter`**: writes `.vercel/output/config.json` v3 STATIC variant (no functions, just routes for `/assets/*` long-cache headers). Does NOT copy files into `.vercel/output/static/` — Vercel's CLI deploy auto-detects the dist root, and copying would break user post-build steps (sourcemap upload, perf scripts).
  - **`cloudflareAdapter`**: writes `_routes.json` with `version: 1, include: [], exclude: ['/*']` — i.e. "every URL is static, never invoke a Pages Function". Without this file, Cloudflare Pages defaults to running the worker on every request, wasting compute. No `_worker.js` emitted (zero-function deploy). ALSO writes `dist/_headers` (Cloudflare Pages + Netlify format) pinning `/assets/*` to `public, max-age=31536000, immutable` — without it, hashed chunks inherit the host's short default and re-fetch needlessly (the `/assets/*` rule vercel.json / netlify.toml already emit; closes the cloudflare cache-headers gap). Shared helper `adapters/cache-headers.ts:writeAssetCacheHeaders(outDir, assetsDir)` respects a user-provided `_headers` — if one already declares a policy for this `/<assetsDir>/` prefix it's untouched, otherwise the framework block is appended so user + framework rules coexist. (The `staticAdapter` deliberately stays a no-op — it's host-agnostic; emitting a Netlify/CF-specific `_headers` would be scope-creep. node/bun runtime handlers gate immutable on the `/<assetsDir>/` PATH, not file extension — see "node/bun cached immutable by extension" anti-pattern.) **`<base><assetsDir>`-aware:** the CDN adapters scope their immutable rule to the SERVED URL prefix — `base` (Vite `build.base`, default `/`) + the RESOLVED `build.assetsDir` (default `'assets'`) — NOT a hardcoded `/assets/`. The plugins capture `assetsDir` in `configResolved` and thread it into `adapter.build(options)` via `AdapterBuildOptions.assetsDir` (alongside `options.config.base`); the shared `adapters/cache-headers.ts:assetUrlPrefix(base, assetsDir)` helper computes the prefix (`/assets`, `/static`, `/blog/assets`, `/blog/static`, …) used by vercel (`config.json` `src: '<prefix>/(.*)'`), netlify (`for = "<prefix>/*"`), and cloudflare (`_headers` + `_routes.json` exclude). So a custom `build: { assetsDir: 'static' }` AND a subpath `zero({ base: '/blog/' })` deploy both keep immutable caching on their hashed chunks (pre-fix they fell to the host's short default and re-fetched every release). **node/bun stay `assetsDir`-only — base is deliberately NOT threaded** (their self-hosted handler serves files by raw `url.pathname` with no base-stripping, so a subpath deploy isn't supported there regardless; the cache check would imply support that doesn't exist). Bisect-locked by `adapters.test.ts` (`custom build.assetsDir scoping` + `base (subpath) cache-rule scoping`: custom `static` AND `base: '/blog/'` each scope every CDN adapter; node/bun honor `assetsDir` but NOT `base`; default stays `/assets/`) + two end-to-end ssr-showcase builds (`assetsDir: 'static'` → `/static/(.*)`; `base: '/blog/'` + `assetsDir: 'static'` → `/blog/static/(.*)` matching the rendered HTML's asset URLs).
  - **`netlifyAdapter`**: writes `netlify.toml` with `publish = "."` (the dist root) + `Cache-Control` headers for `/assets/*`. No functions/redirects directives — PR B's `dist/_redirects` already covers loader-redirect manifests, and the `netlify.toml` declares the static-site shape.
  - **`staticAdapter`**, **`nodeAdapter`**, **`bunAdapter`**: SSG no-op. Static dist is already at `outDir` (nothing to copy); node/bun adapters are SSR runners (irrelevant for prerendered output). The validateBuildInputs helper early-returns for `kind: 'ssg'` so SSG-mode users don't see misleading "server entry not found" errors.

  **Adapter throws are caught in the SSG closeBundle wiring** so a buggy adapter can't take down a successful render — the error lands in `errors[]` with path `(adapter:<name>)` and surfaces in the post-build summary. The summary log gains `[adapter: <name>]` when adapter is non-default (i.e. anything other than `node`).

  Bisect-verified: removing the SSG branch from `cloudflareAdapter` → 2/2 cloudflare-SSG specs fail with `TypeError: The "src" argument must be of type string ... Received undefined` (the SSR branch tries to read undefined `clientOutDir` / `serverEntry`). Restored → 9/9 PR-J SSG specs pass + all 14 pre-existing SSR specs pass. **What's NOT in PR J**: serverless adapters in SSR mode still aren't auto-invoked because zero doesn't run a separate Vite SSR build for `mode: 'ssr'` apps — that's separate infra (a future PR can wire it). Direct deploy of SSR mode requires the user to handle their own server bundle. References: `packages/zero/zero/src/types.ts:AdapterBuildOptions`, `packages/zero/zero/src/adapters/{vercel,cloudflare,netlify,static,node,bun}.ts`, `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts` (closeBundle adapter.build invocation).

  **PR K — per-locale 404 emission + hreflang sitemap cross-references (i18n follow-up).** PR H landed i18n route duplication; PR K closes the remaining SEO gaps for multi-locale SSG sites: (a) every locale subtree gets its own `dist/{locale}/404.html` rendered through that locale's `notFoundComponent` (not just the default-locale `dist/404.html`); (b) `sitemap.xml` emits `<xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang>` cross-references between locale variants per the Google-recommended shape, with an `x-default` entry pointing at the default-locale URL.

  **Per-locale 404 walker.** The synthetic SSG entry's `findNotFoundComponent` (single result) became `findNotFoundComponentsByLocale(routes, currentLocale)` returning a `Map<string | null, Component>` keyed by detected locale (`null` = default / no-i18n). Locale detection: a RouteRecord serves locale `X` when its `path` matches `/${X}` or starts with `/${X}/`. The walker carries an ambient `locale` parameter through `r.children` recursion so per-locale `_404.tsx` duplicates (PR H fans `isNotFound` records the same way it fans pages) land in the right Map entry. The locale list is baked into the SSG entry source at build time — the outer plugin passes `config.i18n?.locales ?? []` as a JSON literal to `renderSsrEntrySource(locales)` (replacing the prior `SSR_ENTRY_SOURCE` const), so the walker has structural knowledge of which path prefixes count as locale roots without needing to import the i18n config inside the SSR sub-build.

  **`__renderNotFound(locale)`** accepts an optional locale and renders that variant from the Map; the outer plugin's closeBundle iterates `[...handlerMod.__notFoundComponentsByLocale.keys()]`, calls the renderer per locale, and writes to `dist/404.html` (null locale) or `dist/{locale}/404.html` (string locale). Static hosts (Netlify per-directory `errors_404`, Cloudflare Pages, GitHub Pages, nginx `try_files`) serve the right per-prefix 404 for unmatched URLs under each locale prefix. Back-compat: `__notFoundComponent` is kept as a derived const reading the null-locale entry so downstream code that imports it directly keeps working; closeBundle falls back to single-shot mode if a stale SSR entry doesn't expose the Map.

  **Hreflang sitemap (`seoPlugin`).** New `sitemap.hreflang` field accepts `true` (auto-detect from SSG manifest) OR `I18nRoutingConfig` (explicit) OR `false`/omitted (no hreflang). The SSG plugin now embeds `i18n` into `_pyreon-ssg-paths.json` alongside `paths`, so `hreflang: true` becomes zero-config: declare `zero({ i18n: { ... } })` once, both route duplication (PR H) AND sitemap hreflang pick it up. `generateSitemap` accepts an optional `i18n` arg; when set, `clusterPathsByLocale` groups URLs by their un-prefixed (default-locale) form via the new `stripLocalePrefix` helper. Each cluster emits ONE `<url>` with hreflang siblings per locale variant + an `x-default` entry pointing at the default-locale URL:

  ```xml
  <url>
    <loc>https://example.com/about</loc>
    <changefreq>weekly</changefreq>
    <priority>0.7</priority>
    <xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang="en" href="https://example.com/about"/>
    <xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang="de" href="https://example.com/de/about"/>
    <xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang="cs" href="https://example.com/cs/about"/>
    <xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang="x-default" href="https://example.com/about"/>
  </url>
  ```

  Three locale URLs collapse into ONE `<url>` (matches Google's "use one URL set per page, cross-reference via xhtml:link" guidance, not three separate entries). The `xmlns:xhtml` namespace declaration on `<urlset>` is conditional — only emitted when hreflang is active so plain-sitemap output stays unchanged. Single-variant clusters (URLs that exist in only one locale, e.g. a locale-specific asset page) skip xhtml:link entirely — there's nothing to alternate to. Dynamic-route × locale cross-products (PR A's `getStaticPaths` × PR H's locales) flow through the same clustering naturally: `/posts/1`, `/de/posts/1`, `/cs/posts/1` cluster as one `<url>` with three hreflang siblings.

  **`stripLocalePrefix` semantics under both strategies.** Under `prefix-except-default`, an un-prefixed path belongs to the default locale by convention (`/about` → locale `en`, `unPrefixed: /about`). Under `prefix` strategy, an un-prefixed URL doesn't fit any locale subtree (every locale should carry an explicit prefix) and is treated as standalone with `locale: null` — those URLs end up in single-variant clusters and don't get hreflang siblings. Edge case: partial-match guard — `/encyclopedia` is NOT detected as locale `en` because matching requires exact `/${locale}` or `/${locale}/` prefix, not substring containment.

  **Real-app coverage** at THREE layers: (1) **unit** — `generateSitemap` / `clusterPathsByLocale` / `stripLocalePrefix` / `resolveHreflangI18n` (19 specs in `packages/zero/zero/src/tests/seo.test.ts`); SSR entry source assertions for the per-locale walker (6 specs updated in `ssg-plugin.test.ts`). (2) **verify-modes** `ssr-showcase × ssg-i18n` cell now also asserts `dist/{de,cs}/404.html` exist + `sitemap.xml` carries the full hreflang cross-reference matrix including the `/posts/{id}` dynamic-route × locale cross-product. (3) **e2e** at `e2e/ssg-i18n.spec.ts` — 2 new specs (`per-locale 404` + `hreflang sitemap.xml`) hit `/de/404.html` + `/sitemap.xml` through `scripts/serve-ssg.ts` and validate the static-host-served output structure.

  **Bisect-verified at TWO layers.** (a) Reverting the closeBundle's per-locale `localeEntries` walker to single-shot mode → verify-modes ssg-i18n cell fails with `expected file: dist/de/404.html`. Restored → 6/6 ssr-showcase cells pass. (b) Reverting the SSG plugin's manifest-emit to omit the `i18n` field → verify-modes ssg-i18n cell fails on the hreflang assertion (`<xhtml:link rel="alternate" hreflang="en" href="https://example.com/about"/>` absent from the rendered sitemap — seoPlugin's `hreflang: true` auto-detect path returns undefined when the manifest doesn't carry i18n). Restored → cell passes.

  **Limitations / known gaps** (after PR L5 closed the layout-chrome gap): (a) **Host routing is required for unmatched URLs.** SSG writes `dist/{locale}/404.html` per locale BUT the static host must be configured to route `/de/unknown-page` → `dist/de/404.html`. Most managed hosts only serve the ROOT `dist/404.html` by convention; per-prefix 404 routing needs explicit declarations (Netlify `[[redirects]]`, Cloudflare Pages `_redirects`, nginx `try_files`, Caddy `handle_errors` per-locale matcher). GitHub Pages does NOT support per-directory 404 customization at all. Documented in `docs/src/content/docs/zero.md` `_404.tsx convention` section with per-platform snippets. (b) **One `_404.tsx` source = identical rendered HTML across locales** (now WITH layout chrome thanks to L5, but the testid + 404 content text are still byte-identical). ssr-showcase ships a single `_404.ts`; the per-locale variants all render byte-identical 404 BODY content. Real i18n apps with `useI18n()` in `_404` would see locale-specific text via the hydration-time t-call — server-side i18n context flows through the router-driven render path L5 introduced (the synthetic chain runs through `router.preload(probeUrl)` which DOES run the parent layout's loaders), so server-side `useI18n()` works correctly under L5 if the layout's loader populates the locale context. (c) **`x-default` always uses the default locale's URL** — no `hreflangXDefault: false` opt-out yet; can be added when a real app needs it. (d) **No per-locale sitemap shards** (single sitemap with hreflang clusters chosen as the Google-canonical shape; sitemap-index + per-locale sharding can be added when a site outgrows the single-file size limit ~50k URLs).

  Reference: `packages/zero/zero/src/ssg-plugin.ts:renderSsrEntrySource` + `findNotFoundComponentsByLocale` + the per-locale closeBundle loop, `packages/zero/zero/src/seo.ts:clusterPathsByLocale` + `stripLocalePrefix` + `resolveHreflangI18n` + the updated `generateSitemap`, `examples/ssr-showcase/vite.config.i18n.ts` (the e2e build config wiring both surfaces).

## Testing

```bash
bun run test                          # all package tests (via workspace filter)
bun run test:browser                  # all real-browser smoke tests (Chromium via @vitest/browser)
cd packages/<name> && bun run test    # single package
cd packages/<name> && bun run test -- --coverage  # with coverage
```

DOM-dependent packages (runtime-dom, router, head, compat layers) use `environment: "happy-dom"` in vitest config.

Real-browser smoke tests run under `@vitest/browser` with Playwright Chromium — files named `*.browser.test.ts(x)`, opt in per-package via `vitest.browser.config.ts` + `test:browser` script. Reference: `packages/internals/test-utils/src/browser/sanity.browser.test.ts`. See `.claude/rules/test-environment-parity.md` for the setup recipe.

### Test environment parity

Tests must run in the same environment as production. happy-dom is a Node-based DOM polyfill, NOT a real browser — it does not catch `typeof process` dead code, real `IntersectionObserver` timing, real CSS rendering, Vite's `import.meta.env` browser behavior, or other environment-divergence bugs. See `.claude/rules/test-environment-parity.md` for the categorization (browser packages, server packages, universal packages) and the rules for each.

The recurring failure mode this prevents: tests pass because vitest provides something (`process`, hand-constructed vnodes, mocked APIs) that production does not. PR #197 (mock-vnode silent metadata drop) and PR #200 (typeof process dead in browser) were both this shape. Both bugs were invisible until a real-world consumer hit them.

**Key rules**:

- **Browser packages** must have at least one Playwright/browser smoke test in addition to vitest tests (enforced by lint rule `pyreon/require-browser-smoke-test`).
- **Mock-vnode tests must have a parallel real-`h()` test** for any contract assertion. The mock test is the fast path; the real-`h()` test is the safety net. Always have both.
- **Dev-mode warnings must use bare `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`** — the bundler-agnostic library convention. Pyreon publishes libraries; consumers compile with Vite, Webpack/Next.js, esbuild, Rollup, Parcel, or Bun. Every modern bundler auto-replaces `process.env.NODE_ENV` at consumer build time. Do NOT use `typeof process !== 'undefined' && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'` (dead in Vite browser builds) or `import.meta.env.DEV` (Vite/Rolldown-only). Reference: `flow/src/layout.ts:warnIgnoredOptions`. Enforced by `pyreon/no-process-dev-gate`.
- **Bisect-verify regression tests** before merge: revert the fix → run the test → assert it fails with the right error message → restore the fix → assert it passes. PR #200's first regression test passed even with the broken pattern, because esbuild's minifier folds dead code regardless. The bisect verification caught it.

## CI / Lint / Typecheck

```bash
bun run lint                          # lint all packages + examples (via workspace filter)
bun run typecheck                     # typecheck all packages + examples (via workspace filter)
oxlint .                              # lint (400+ rules, Rust-powered)
oxfmt --write .                       # auto-format
oxfmt --check .                       # check formatting
```

Every package and example must have `"lint": "oxlint ."` and `"typecheck": "tsc --noEmit"` in scripts.
Examples use `noEmit: true` in tsconfig (not `rootDir`) since they include vite.config.ts.

### CI architecture (post-speedup, 2026-05)

PR pipeline wall-clock: **~8.3 min** (was ~13 min pre-speedup). Five-PR plan landed via PRs #948 / #954 / #964 / #968 / #972; the architecture is non-obvious in a few places — if you're about to edit `.github/workflows/ci.yml` read this first.

**Job-DAG shape**:

```text
Install (~25s, bun install only — postinstall bootstrap SKIPPED via PYREON_BOOTSTRAP_SKIP=1)
├── lib-free jobs (start at T+25s, save ~150s critical-path):
│     typecheck-cell (8-cell matrix) → Typecheck (aggregator)
│     lint, lint-ratchet, audit-types, coverage (floor), check-doc-claims,
│     check-manifest-depth, docs-sync, audit, test-rust-binary,
│     e2e-decide
│
```
